## Purpose and Scope

The Asset Pipeline is RavEngine's system for converting source assets (3D models, textures, shaders, audio, animations, skeletons) from common formats into optimized runtime formats, packaging them into archives, and loading them at runtime. This document covers the build-time compilation tools, asset formats, packaging system, and runtime loading mechanisms.

For information about using specific asset types at runtime, see:
- Meshes and geometry: [Mesh and Geometry Processing](#9.5)
- Animation playback: [Animation Components and Assets](#6.1)
- Material creation: [Materials and Shaders](#4.2)
- Audio playback: [Audio Sources and Playback](#7.1)

---

## Architecture Overview

RavEngine's asset pipeline operates in two distinct phases: **build-time compilation** and **runtime loading**.

```mermaid
graph TB
    subgraph "Build Phase - Host Machine"
        SourceAssets["Source Assets<br/>.obj .fbx .png .ogg .glsl"]
        HostTools["Host Tools<br/>rvemc rveskc rveac rvesc"]
        IntermediateAssets["Intermediate Assets<br/>.rvem .rves .rvea<br/>Compiled Shaders"]
        PackageSystem["pack_resources.cmake"]
        Archive["TARGET.rvedata<br/>ZIP Archive"]
        
        SourceAssets --> HostTools
        HostTools --> IntermediateAssets
        IntermediateAssets --> PackageSystem
        PackageSystem --> Archive
    end
    
    subgraph "Runtime Phase - Target Device"
        VFS["PhysFS Virtual Filesystem"]
        AssetClasses["Asset Classes<br/>MeshAsset SkeletonAsset<br/>AnimationAsset Texture"]
        Managers["Asset Managers<br/>Weak Read-Through Cache"]
        
        Archive -.->|deployed with app| VFS
        VFS --> AssetClasses
        AssetClasses --> Managers
    end
    
    style SourceAssets fill:#f9f9f9
    style Archive fill:#f9f9f9
```

**Sources:** [Diagram 4 from high-level architecture]()

At build-time, source assets are processed by specialized compiler tools into intermediate formats optimized for GPU consumption. These intermediate files are then packaged into a single `.rvedata` archive. At runtime, the PhysFS virtual filesystem mounts this archive, and assets are lazily loaded on-demand through strongly-typed asset classes and manager caches.

**Sources:** [CMakeLists.txt:1-850](), [cmake/pack_resources.cmake:1-326]()

---

## Build-Time Asset Compilation

### Host Tools Architecture

RavEngine provides four specialized command-line tools for asset compilation:

| Tool | Purpose | Input | Output | Dependencies |
|------|---------|-------|--------|--------------|
| `rvemc` | Mesh compiler | .obj, .fbx + config.json | .rvem | Assimp, meshoptimizer |
| `rveskc` | Skeleton compiler | .fbx + config.json | .rves | Assimp |
| `rveac` | Animation compiler | .fbx + config.json | .rvea | Assimp |
| `rvesc` | Shader compiler | .vsh, .fsh, .csh | Platform bytecode | librglc |

**Sources:** [cmake/importers.cmake:1-37](), [cmake/rvesc.cmake:1-17]()

```mermaid
graph LR
    subgraph "Import Library"
        ImportLib["rve_importlib<br/>Assimp Integration<br/>Format Conversion"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Mesh Pipeline"
        MeshJSON["config.json"]
        MeshSource[".obj .fbx"]
        RVEMC["rvemc<br/>Vertex Optimization"]
        MeshOut[".rvem<br/>SerializedMeshDataHeader<br/>Packed Vertex Data"]
        
        MeshJSON --> RVEMC
        MeshSource --> RVEMC
        RVEMC --> MeshOut
    end
    
    subgraph "Skeleton Pipeline"
        SkelJSON["config.json"]
        SkelSource[".fbx"]
        RVESKC["rveskc<br/>Bone Hierarchy"]
        SkelOut[".rves<br/>SerializedSkeletonDataHeader<br/>Bone Transforms"]
        
        SkelJSON --> RVESKC
        SkelSource --> RVESKC
        RVESKC --> SkelOut
    end
    
    subgraph "Animation Pipeline"
        AnimJSON["config.json"]
        AnimSource[".fbx"]
        RVEAC["rveac<br/>Keyframe Extraction"]
        AnimOut[".rvea<br/>SerializedJointAnimationHeader<br/>Track Data"]
        
        AnimJSON --> RVEAC
        AnimSource --> RVEAC
        RVEAC --> AnimOut
    end
    
    subgraph "Shader Pipeline"
        ShaderSource[".vsh .fsh .csh .glsl"]
        RVESC["rvesc<br/>librglc Cross-Compilation"]
        ShaderOut["Platform Bytecode<br/>Metal: .metallib<br/>DX12: DXIL<br/>Vulkan: SPIRV"]
        
        ShaderSource --> RVESC
        RVESC --> ShaderOut
    end
    
    ImportLib --> RVEMC
    ImportLib --> RVESKC
    ImportLib --> RVEAC
```

**Sources:** [cmake/importers.cmake:11-37](), [deps/host-tools/CMakeLists.txt:1-76]()

Each tool is built from source in the `tools/` directory and uses the shared `rve_importlib` library, which wraps Assimp for 3D format support. The mesh compiler additionally integrates meshoptimizer for vertex cache optimization.

**Sources:** [cmake/importers.cmake:1-10](), [tools/importlib/]()

### Cross-Compilation Support

When cross-compiling (e.g., building for Android from Windows, or iOS from macOS), RavEngine builds the host tools natively for the build machine in a separate build tree:

```mermaid
graph TB
    subgraph "Cross-Compilation Detection"
        CMakeDetect["CMAKE_CROSSCOMPILING<br/>VS_CROSSCOMP<br/>RVE_CROSSCOMP"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Host Tools Build"
        HostToolsDir["host-tools/<br/>Separate CMake Context"]
        HostCMake["cmake -G Native Generator<br/>deps/host-tools/"]
        HostBuild["Build protoc rglc flatc<br/>rvesc rvemc rveskc rveac"]
        HostBinaries["TOOLS_DIR/Release/<br/>Native Executables"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Target Build"
        TargetBuild["Main Build<br/>Cross-Compiler Toolchain"]
        UseHostTools["Reference Host Binaries<br/>PROTOC_CMD rglc_path<br/>RVESC_PATH RVEMC_PATH"]
    end
    
    CMakeDetect -->|if cross-compiling| HostToolsDir
    HostToolsDir --> HostCMake
    HostCMake --> HostBuild
    HostBuild --> HostBinaries
    HostBinaries --> UseHostTools
    UseHostTools --> TargetBuild
```

**Sources:** [CMakeLists.txt:90-181]()

The detection logic sets `RVE_CROSSCOMP` when `CMAKE_CROSSCOMPILING` or `VS_CROSSCOMP` (Visual Studio cross-compilation) is true. In this case, the build system executes a separate CMake configuration in `${CMAKE_BINARY_DIR}/host-tools` pointing to `deps/host-tools/CMakeLists.txt`, which builds only the necessary tools using the host's native compiler.

**Sources:** [CMakeLists.txt:95-99](), [CMakeLists.txt:142-169](), [deps/host-tools/CMakeLists.txt:1-76]()

The host tool paths are cached as CMake variables (`RVEMC_PATH`, `RVESKC_PATH`, `RVEAC_PATH`, `RVESC_PATH`, `PROTOC_CMD`, `rglc_path`) and referenced during the main build when processing assets.

**Sources:** [CMakeLists.txt:108-125](), [cmake/pack_resources.cmake:122-180]()

---

## Asset Formats

### Mesh Format (.rvem)

The `.rvem` format is a binary serialized mesh format with a fixed header followed by packed vertex attribute arrays and an index buffer.

```mermaid
graph TB
    subgraph "SerializedMeshDataHeader"
        Header["header[4]: 'rvem'<br/>version<br/>numVertices<br/>numIndicies<br/>attributes: bitfield"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Vertex Attributes - Sequential"
        Positions["positions[numVertices]<br/>vec3"]
        Normals["normals[numVertices]<br/>vec3"]
        Tangents["tangents[numVertices]<br/>vec4"]
        Bitangents["bitangents[numVertices]<br/>vec3"]
        UV0["uv0[numVertices]<br/>vec2"]
        LightmapUV["lightmapUVs[numVertices]<br/>vec2"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Index Buffer"
        Indices["indices[numIndicies]<br/>uint32_t"]
    end
    
    Header --> Positions
    Positions --> Normals
    Normals --> Tangents
    Tangents --> Bitangents
    Bitangents --> UV0
    UV0 --> LightmapUV
    LightmapUV --> Indices
```

**Sources:** [src/MeshAsset.cpp:18-80](), [include/RavEngine/MeshAsset.hpp:27-145]()

The `attributes` bitfield in the header indicates which attributes are present:
- `hasPositionsBit`
- `hasNormalsBit`
- `hasTangentsBit`
- `hasBitangentsBit`
- `hasUV0Bit`
- `hasLightmapUVBit`

Only the attributes marked as present are serialized. Deserialization occurs in `MeshAsset::DeserializeMeshFromMemory()`, which reads the header, then iterates through each enabled attribute, reading `numVertices` entries for each.

**Sources:** [src/MeshAsset.cpp:23-80]()

For skinned meshes, the `.rvem` format is extended with a `VertexWeights` section appended after the indices:

```
[SerializedMeshDataHeader][Vertex Attributes][Indices][VertexWeights[numVertices]]
```

Each `VertexWeights` entry contains bone indices and weights for skeletal animation.

**Sources:** [src/MeshAssetSkinned.cpp:25-72]()

### Skeleton Format (.rves)

The `.rves` format encodes a skeleton's bone hierarchy with bind poses:

```mermaid
graph TB
    subgraph "SerializedSkeletonDataHeader"
        SkelHeader["header[4]: 'rves'<br/>numBones"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Bone Data Arrays"
        Transforms["BoneTransform[numBones]<br/>translation: vec3<br/>rotation: quat<br/>scale: vec3"]
        Names["Bone Names<br/>uint16_t length<br/>char name[length]<br/>Ã— numBones"]
        Children["Child Indices<br/>uint16_t numChildren<br/>uint16_t childIdx[numChildren]<br/>Ã— numBones"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Runtime Conversion"
        OzzSkeleton["ozz::animation::Skeleton<br/>SoA Optimized<br/>Joint Rest Poses"]
        BindPoses["Inverse Bind Poses<br/>mat4[numBones]<br/>GPU Buffer"]
    end
    
    SkelHeader --> Transforms
    Transforms --> Names
    Names --> Children
    Children --> OzzSkeleton
    OzzSkeleton --> BindPoses
```

**Sources:** [src/SkeletonAsset.cpp:23-88]()

Deserialization in `DeserializeSkeleton()` reads the three arrays sequentially, then reconstructs the hierarchical bone tree. The engine converts this into an `ozz::animation::Skeleton` for runtime use, which stores bones in SoA (Structure of Arrays) layout for SIMD efficiency.

**Sources:** [src/SkeletonAsset.cpp:90-128]()

The bind poses are computed by running Ozz's `LocalToModelJob` on the skeleton's rest poses, then inverting each matrix (because shaders need the inverse bind pose):

**Sources:** [src/SkeletonAsset.cpp:129-152]()

On non-server builds, bind poses are uploaded to a GPU buffer for use in the skinning compute shader.

**Sources:** [src/SkeletonAsset.cpp:155-175]()

### Animation Format (.rvea)

The `.rvea` format stores keyframe animation data:

```mermaid
graph TB
    subgraph "SerializedJointAnimationHeader"
        AnimHeader["header[4]: 'rvea'<br/>duration<br/>ticksPerSecond<br/>numTracks<br/>nameLength"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Track Data"
        Name["Animation Name<br/>char[nameLength]"]
        TracksArray["For each track:<br/>SerializedJointAnimationTrackHeader<br/>numTranslations<br/>numRotations<br/>numScales"]
        Keyframes["Keyframe Arrays:<br/>VectorKey[numTranslations]<br/>QuatKey[numRotations]<br/>VectorKey[numScales]"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Runtime Conversion"
        OzzRawAnim["ozz::animation::offline::RawAnimation<br/>Per-Track Keyframes"]
        OzzAnim["ozz::animation::Animation<br/>Compressed SoA<br/>Optimized Sampling"]
    end
    
    AnimHeader --> Name
    Name --> TracksArray
    TracksArray --> Keyframes
    Keyframes --> OzzRawAnim
    OzzRawAnim --> OzzAnim
```

**Sources:** [src/AnimationAsset.cpp:61-94](), [src/AnimationAsset.cpp:96-144]()

Each keyframe is a `(time, value)` pair. Translations and scales are `vec3`, rotations are `quat`. The deserialization function `DeserializeJointAnimation()` reads the header, then iterates through each track, reading its keyframes.

After deserialization, the engine converts the data into Ozz's compressed format using `ozz::animation::offline::AnimationBuilder`. This performs temporal compression and SoA layout transformation for efficient runtime sampling.

**Sources:** [src/AnimationAsset.cpp:103-143]()

### Shader Compilation

Shader compilation differs from other assets because shaders must target specific graphics APIs. The `rvesc` tool wraps `librglc` (RGL Compiler) to cross-compile GLSL to platform-specific bytecode:

```mermaid
graph LR
    subgraph "Input"
        VSH[".vsh<br/>Vertex Shader"]
        FSH[".fsh<br/>Fragment Shader"]
        CSH[".csh<br/>Compute Shader"]
        GLSL[".glsl<br/>Common Code"]
    end
    
    subgraph "rvesc + librglc"
        Parse["Parse Material JSON<br/>Extract Entry Points<br/>Include Paths"]
        Compile["librglc Cross-Compile"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Platform Output"
        MetalLib["macOS/iOS/tvOS:<br/>.metallib<br/>Metal Library"]
        DXIL["Windows:<br/>DXIL Bytecode<br/>DirectX 12"]
        SPIRV["Vulkan/Android:<br/>SPIRV Bytecode"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Embedding"
        CMRC["Non-Apple:<br/>CMRC Resource Compiler<br/>Compile-time Embed"]
        Bundle["Apple:<br/>App Bundle<br/>.metallib in Resources"]
    end
    
    VSH --> Parse
    FSH --> Parse
    CSH --> Parse
    GLSL --> Parse
    Parse --> Compile
    
    Compile --> MetalLib
    Compile --> DXIL
    Compile --> SPIRV
    
    MetalLib --> Bundle
    DXIL --> CMRC
    SPIRV --> CMRC
```

**Sources:** [cmake/shaders.cmake](), [cmake/pack_resources.cmake:186-238]()

On Apple platforms, shaders are compiled to Metal libraries (`.metallib`) and included in the app bundle's Resources directory. On other platforms, compiled bytecode is embedded directly into the executable using CMRC (CMake Resource Compiler), which generates C++ source code with the shader bytes as static data.

**Sources:** [cmake/pack_resources.cmake:206-238]()

The `pack_resources()` function iterates through all provided shaders and invokes `declare_shader()` for each, which sets up the appropriate build commands based on the target platform.

**Sources:** [cmake/pack_resources.cmake:189-204]()

---

## Runtime Packaging

### The pack_resources() Function

The `pack_resources()` CMake function is the entry point for integrating assets into a RavEngine application:

```cmake
pack_resources(
    TARGET YourGame
    OUTPUT_FILE DATA_PACK
    MESHES ${mesh_configs}
    SKELETONS ${skeleton_configs}
    ANIMATIONS ${animation_configs}
    SHADERS ${shader_files}
    TEXTURES ${texture_files}
    SOUNDS ${audio_files}
    UIS ${ui_files}
    FONTS ${font_files}
    DATA_ASSETS ${data_files}
    STREAMING_ASSETS ${streaming_files}
    STREAMING_INPUT_ROOT "${streaming_root}"
)
```

**Sources:** [cmake/pack_resources.cmake:2-12](), [README.md:50-64]()

The function performs several key tasks:

1. **Copies assets to staging directory** - Assets are copied to `${CMAKE_CURRENT_BINARY_DIR}/${TARGET}/` organized by type (meshes/, textures/, sounds/, etc.)

**Sources:** [cmake/pack_resources.cmake:99-109]()

2. **Invokes asset compilers** - For each mesh/skeleton/animation config JSON, `pack_resources()` adds custom commands to invoke the appropriate compiler tool, generating `.rvem`/`.rves`/`.rvea` files in the staging directory.

**Sources:** [cmake/pack_resources.cmake:122-180]()

3. **Compiles shaders** - Invokes `declare_shader()` for each shader, setting up per-platform compilation. On non-Apple platforms, creates a CMRC resource library.

**Sources:** [cmake/pack_resources.cmake:186-238]()

4. **Creates .rvedata archive** - After all assets are in the staging directory, a custom POST_BUILD command zips everything into `${RAVENGINE_ASSETS_DIR}/${TARGET}.rvedata`.

**Sources:** [cmake/pack_resources.cmake:290-297]()

5. **Platform-specific deployment** - On Apple, adds the `.rvedata` to the app bundle's Resources. On Windows/UWP, sets deployment properties. On Linux/Windows, copies to the executable directory.

**Sources:** [cmake/pack_resources.cmake:300-322]()

### Asset Staging and Archiving

The staging process ensures deterministic builds and handles cross-compilation:

```mermaid
graph TB
    subgraph "Staging Phase"
        Source["Source Assets<br/>Project Directory"]
        Staging["Staging Directory<br/>${CMAKE_CURRENT_BINARY_DIR}/${TARGET}/"]
        
        Source -->|copy_helper| Staging
    end
    
    subgraph "Compilation Phase"
        Configs["Config Files<br/>meshes.json<br/>skeletons.json<br/>anims.json"]
        Compilers["Host Tools<br/>rvemc rveskc rveac"]
        Compiled["Compiled Assets<br/>.rvem .rves .rvea"]
        
        Configs --> Compilers
        Compilers --> Compiled
        Compiled --> Staging
    end
    
    subgraph "Packaging Phase"
        ShaderLib["Shader Library<br/>CMRC or .metallib"]
        Archive["ZIP Archive<br/>${TARGET}.rvedata"]
        
        Staging --> Archive
        ShaderLib -.->|non-Apple only| Archive
    end
    
    subgraph "Deployment"
        ExeDir["Executable Directory<br/>Windows/Linux"]
        AppBundle["App Bundle Resources<br/>macOS/iOS"]
        
        Archive -->|copy| ExeDir
        Archive -->|bundle| AppBundle
    end
```

**Sources:** [cmake/pack_resources.cmake:42-109](), [cmake/pack_resources.cmake:273-322]()

The `copy_helper()` and `copy_helper_impl()` functions handle copying source assets to the staging directory, tracking dependencies via the global `COPY_DEPENDS` property. This ensures CMake rebuilds the archive only when source assets change.

**Sources:** [cmake/pack_resources.cmake:42-97]()

Streaming assets (large files that shouldn't be packed into the archive) receive special treatment - on Apple they go directly into the app bundle, on Windows/UWP they use VS deployment properties, and on other platforms they're copied alongside the executable.

**Sources:** [cmake/pack_resources.cmake:68-97]()

---

## Runtime Loading

### PhysFS Virtual Filesystem

At runtime, RavEngine uses PhysFS to mount the `.rvedata` archive as a virtual filesystem:

```mermaid
graph LR
    subgraph "Application Startup"
        AppInit["App::App()"]
        VFSInit["VirtualFilesystem::Init()"]
        MountArchive["PHYSFS_mount()<br/>${TARGET}.rvedata"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Asset Access"
        AssetLoad["Asset Constructor<br/>e.g., MeshAsset()"]
        VFSQuery["GetApp()->GetResources()<br/>.FileContentsAt()"]
        PhysFSRead["PHYSFS_openRead()<br/>PHYSFS_read()"]
        MemorySpan["std::span<uint8_t>"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Deserialization"
        Deserialize["Deserialize Function<br/>DeserializeMeshFromMemory()<br/>DeserializeSkeleton()<br/>DeserializeJointAnimation()"]
        RuntimeFormat["Runtime Asset<br/>GPU Upload<br/>CPU Structures"]
    end
    
    AppInit --> VFSInit
    VFSInit --> MountArchive
    
    AssetLoad --> VFSQuery
    VFSQuery --> PhysFSRead
    PhysFSRead --> MemorySpan
    MemorySpan --> Deserialize
    Deserialize --> RuntimeFormat
```

**Sources:** [src/App.cpp](), [src/VirtualFileSystem.cpp](), [src/MeshAsset.cpp:82-88]()

The `VirtualFilesystem` class provides the `FileContentsAt()` method, which returns a `std::span<uint8_t>` containing the file's bytes. Asset constructors pass paths relative to the archive root (e.g., `"meshes/player.rvem"`), and PhysFS transparently reads from the mounted archive.

**Sources:** [src/MeshAsset.cpp:82-87](), [src/SkeletonAsset.cpp:90-96](), [src/AnimationAsset.cpp:96-100]()

### Asset Deserialization

Each asset type implements a deserialization function that converts the binary format into runtime structures:

| Asset Type | Deserialize Function | Runtime Class |
|------------|---------------------|---------------|
| Mesh | `DeserializeMeshFromMemory()` | `MeshAsset` |
| Skeleton | `DeserializeSkeleton()` | `SkeletonAsset` |
| Animation | `DeserializeJointAnimation()` | `AnimationAsset` |

**Sources:** [src/MeshAsset.cpp:23-80](), [src/SkeletonAsset.cpp:23-88](), [src/AnimationAsset.cpp:61-94]()

Deserialization is a two-step process:

1. **Parse Binary Format** - Read the serialized format into intermediate structures (e.g., `SerializedMeshDataHeader`, `SerializedSkeleton`, `JointAnimation`)

**Sources:** [src/MeshAsset.cpp:25-79]()

2. **Convert to Runtime Format** - Transform intermediate data into runtime-optimized structures. For skeletal data, this involves converting to Ozz's compressed SoA format. For meshes, this uploads to GPU buffers.

**Sources:** [src/SkeletonAsset.cpp:99-128](), [src/MeshAsset.cpp:147-180]()

### GPU Upload

Non-server builds upload asset data to GPU memory during initialization:

```mermaid
graph TB
    subgraph "Mesh Upload"
        MeshData["MeshPart<br/>positions, normals, etc."]
        RenderEngine["RenderEngine<br/>.AllocateMesh()"]
        MeshRange["MeshRange<br/>Offset into Global Buffers"]
        
        MeshData --> RenderEngine
        RenderEngine --> MeshRange
    end
    
    subgraph "Skeleton Upload"
        BindPoses["Inverse Bind Poses<br/>mat4[]"]
        BoneHierarchy["Parent Indices<br/>int16_t[]"]
        CreateBuffer["Device->CreateBuffer()<br/>StorageBuffer"]
        GPUBuffers["RGLBufferPtr<br/>bindpose, boneHierarchy"]
        
        BindPoses --> CreateBuffer
        BoneHierarchy --> CreateBuffer
        CreateBuffer --> GPUBuffers
    end
    
    subgraph "Skinned Mesh Upload"
        VertexWeights["VertexWeights<br/>boneIndices, weights"]
        WeightsBuffer["RGLBufferPtr<br/>weightsBuffer"]
        
        VertexWeights --> CreateBuffer
        CreateBuffer --> WeightsBuffer
    end
```

**Sources:** [src/MeshAsset.cpp:171-179](), [src/SkeletonAsset.cpp:155-175](), [src/MeshAssetSkinned.cpp:54-70]()

The `RenderEngine::AllocateMesh()` function appends mesh data to the engine's global vertex/index buffers, returning a `MeshRange` describing the offset and count. This allows efficient batched rendering using GPU-driven techniques.

**Sources:** [src/MeshAsset.cpp:177](), [include/RavEngine/MeshAllocation.hpp]()

Skeleton bind poses and hierarchy are uploaded as storage buffers for use in the skinning compute shader. Skinned meshes additionally upload vertex weights.

**Sources:** [src/SkeletonAsset.cpp:155-175](), [src/MeshAssetSkinned.cpp:62-69]()

### Asset Managers

RavEngine provides manager classes that implement weak read-through caching for asset loading:

```mermaid
graph LR
    subgraph "Asset Manager Pattern"
        Request["User Code<br/>Request Asset by Path"]
        Manager["Asset::Manager<br/>GenericWeakReadThroughCache"]
        CheckCache{"In Cache?"}
        LoadNew["Load from VFS<br/>Deserialize<br/>GPU Upload"]
        Return["Return Ref<Asset>"]
        
        Request --> Manager
        Manager --> CheckCache
        CheckCache -->|Yes| Return
        CheckCache -->|No| LoadNew
        LoadNew --> Return
    end
    
    subgraph "Available Managers"
        MeshMgr["MeshAsset::Manager"]
        SkelMgr["SkeletonManager"]
        AnimMgr["AnimationAssetManager"]
        TexMgr["Texture::Manager"]
    end
```

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/MeshAsset.hpp:82](), [include/RavEngine/SkeletonAsset.hpp:68](), [include/RavEngine/AnimationAsset.hpp:198]()

Each manager uses weak references (`std::weak_ptr`) to track loaded assets. When an asset is no longer referenced by game code, it's automatically unloaded. If requested again, the manager reloads it from the VFS.

Example usage:

```cpp
// First load - loads from VFS
auto mesh = MeshAsset::Manager::Get("player_model");

// Subsequent loads - returns cached reference
auto mesh2 = MeshAsset::Manager::Get("player_model");

// When all references drop, asset is freed
// Next Get() will reload from VFS
```

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/Manager.hpp](), [include/RavEngine/MeshAsset.hpp:82]()

---

## Integration Example

To integrate the asset pipeline into a RavEngine application:

```cmake
cmake_minimum_required(VERSION 3.25)
project(MyGame)

add_subdirectory("RavEngine")

add_executable("MyGame" "src/main.cpp")
target_link_libraries("MyGame" PUBLIC "RavEngine")
target_compile_features("MyGame" PRIVATE cxx_std_23)

# Configure meshes with JSON
file(GLOB meshes "assets/meshes/*.json")
file(GLOB skeletons "assets/skeletons/*.json")
file(GLOB animations "assets/animations/*.json")

# Shader sources
file(GLOB shaders "shaders/*.vsh" "shaders/*.fsh" "shaders/*.csh")

# Other assets (copied directly)
file(GLOB textures "assets/textures/*.png")
file(GLOB sounds "assets/audio/*.ogg")
file(GLOB uis "assets/ui/*.rml" "assets/ui/*.rcss")

pack_resources(
    TARGET "MyGame"
    OUTPUT_FILE DATA_PACK
    MESHES ${meshes}
    SKELETONS ${skeletons}
    ANIMATIONS ${animations}
    SHADERS ${shaders}
    TEXTURES ${textures}
    SOUNDS ${sounds}
    UIS ${uis}
)
```

**Sources:** [README.md:29-75](), [cmake/pack_resources.cmake:1-326]()

The mesh/skeleton/animation JSON files reference source files and provide import options:

```json
{
    "file": "models/player.fbx",
    "scale": 1.0,
    "importNormals": true,
    "importTangents": true,
    "generateLightmapUV": false
}
```

At build time, the asset compilers process these configs and output `.rvem`/`.rves`/`.rvea` files. The `pack_resources()` function orchestrates compilation, shader cross-compilation, and packaging into `MyGame.rvedata`.

At runtime, load assets using their paths relative to the asset type directory:

```cpp
// Load mesh from "meshes/player.rvem"
auto mesh = MeshAsset::Manager::Get("player");

// Load skeleton from "skeletons/player.rves"  
auto skeleton = SkeletonManager::Get("player");

// Load animation from "animations/walk.rvea"
auto walkAnim = AnimationAssetManager::Get("walk");
```

**Sources:** [src/MeshAsset.cpp:82-88](), [src/SkeletonAsset.cpp:90-96](), [src/AnimationAsset.cpp:96-100]()

The manager classes automatically handle VFS access, deserialization, GPU upload, and caching.1b:T465c,# Creating Your First Application

## Purpose and Scope

This page walks through creating a minimal RavEngine application from scratch. It covers subclassing the `App` class, implementing lifecycle hooks, creating a `World`, and spawning entities with components. 

For information about building RavEngine and configuring your project, see [Building RavEngine](#2.1). For details about preparing assets for use in your application, see [Asset Pipeline](#2.2). For comprehensive documentation of the `App` class and main loop architecture, see [Application Lifecycle](#3.1).

---

## The App Class Architecture

Every RavEngine application begins by subclassing `App` and implementing its virtual lifecycle hooks. The `App` class manages the main loop, window creation, rendering initialization, audio setup, and world management.

### App Class Hierarchy

```mermaid
classDiagram
    class App {
        +App()
        +int run(int argc, char** argv)
        #virtual AppConfig OnConfigure(int argc, char** argv)
        #virtual void OnStartup(int argc, char** argv)
        #virtual int OnShutdown()
        #virtual bool NeedsAudio()
        #virtual bool NeedsNetworking()
        +void AddWorld(Ref~World~ world)
        +void SetRenderedWorld(Ref~World~ world)
        +void RemoveWorld(Ref~World~ world)
        +Ref~InputManager~ inputManager
        +NetworkManager networkManager
        -void Tick()
        -Ref~World~ renderWorld
        -locked_hashset~Ref~World~~ loadedWorlds
    }
    
    class YourApp {
        +YourApp()
        #AppConfig OnConfigure(int argc, char** argv)
        #void OnStartup(int argc, char** argv)
        #int OnShutdown()
    }
    
    class World {
        +World()
        +Entity Instantiate()
        +void Tick(float scale)
    }
    
    class Entity {
        +EmplaceComponent~T~(args...)
        +GetTransform()
        +Destroy()
    }
    
    YourApp --|> App : inherits
    App "1" --> "*" World : manages
    World "1" --> "*" Entity : contains
```

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/App.hpp:49-366](), [src/App.cpp:99-121]()

---

## Application Lifecycle Hooks

The `App` class provides three virtual methods that define your application's lifecycle:

### Lifecycle Method Overview

| Method | Purpose | Called When | Return Value |
|--------|---------|-------------|--------------|
| `OnConfigure` | Configure rendering backend and settings | Before initialization | `AppConfig` struct |
| `OnStartup` | Initialize game state, create worlds, load assets | After engine initialization | void |
| `OnShutdown` | Cleanup resources, save state | Before application exit | int (exit code) |

### Lifecycle Execution Flow

```mermaid
flowchart TD
    Start["main() calls app.run()"] --> Init["App::App() constructor<br/>- Initialize PhysFS<br/>- Create VirtualFilesystem"]
    Init --> Configure["OnConfigure(argc, argv)<br/>User returns AppConfig"]
    Configure --> RGLInit["Initialize RGL graphics<br/>- Create Device<br/>- Create RenderEngine<br/>- Create Window"]
    RGLInit --> RMLInit["Initialize RmlUi<br/>- Set interfaces<br/>- Load fonts"]
    RMLInit --> AudioInit{"NeedsAudio()"}
    AudioInit -->|true| CreateAudio["Create AudioPlayer<br/>player->Init()"]
    AudioInit -->|false| NetInit
    CreateAudio --> NetInit{"NeedsNetworking()"}
    NetInit -->|true| InitNet["Initialize GameNetworkingSockets"]
    NetInit -->|false| DefaultTex
    InitNet --> DefaultTex["Create default textures<br/>- defaultTexture white<br/>- defaultNormalTexture<br/>- zeroTexture"]
    DefaultTex --> Startup["OnStartup(argc, argv)<br/>User creates worlds/entities"]
    Startup --> MainLoop["Main Loop<br/>while !exit"]
    MainLoop --> PollEvents["Poll SDL events<br/>- Window resize<br/>- Input<br/>- Quit"]
    PollEvents --> TickAll["App::Tick()<br/>- Tick all worlds<br/>- Process main tasks<br/>- Render frame"]
    TickAll --> CheckExit{"exit?"}
    CheckExit -->|no| MainLoop
    CheckExit -->|yes| Shutdown["OnShutdown()<br/>User cleanup"]
    Shutdown --> Destroy["App::~App()<br/>- Wait for GPU<br/>- Clear managers<br/>- Shutdown systems"]
    Destroy --> End["Return exit code"]
    
    style Startup fill:#e1f5ff
    style MainLoop fill:#ffe1e1
    style Shutdown fill:#fff5e1
```

**Sources:** [src/App.cpp:123-352](), [include/RavEngine/App.hpp:333-348]()

---

## Creating Your Application Class

### Minimal Application Structure

A minimal RavEngine application requires:

1. A custom `App` subclass
2. Implementation of `OnStartup()` to create a `World`
3. A `main()` function that instantiates and runs the app

### Code Entity Mapping

```mermaid
graph LR
    subgraph "Your Code"
        MyApp["class MyApp : public App"]
        Main["int main(int argc, char** argv)"]
        Startup["OnStartup() override"]
    end
    
    subgraph "RavEngine Core - App.hpp"
        AppBase["class App"]
        AppRun["App::run(int, char**)"]
        VirtualStartup["virtual OnStartup()"]
        AddWorldMethod["AddWorld(Ref<World>)"]
        SetRenderedMethod["SetRenderedWorld(Ref<World>)"]
    end
    
    subgraph "RavEngine Core - World"
        WorldClass["class World"]
        Instantiate["World::Instantiate()"]
        WorldTick["World::Tick(float)"]
    end
    
    Main --> MyApp
    MyApp -.inherits.-> AppBase
    Main --> AppRun
    Startup -.overrides.-> VirtualStartup
    Startup --> AddWorldMethod
    Startup --> SetRenderedMethod
    AddWorldMethod --> WorldClass
    AppRun --> WorldTick
```

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/App.hpp:49-366](), [src/App.cpp:514-542]()

---

## World and Entity Creation

### World Management

The `App` class maintains two collections of worlds:

- **`loadedWorlds`**: All worlds that are currently active and being ticked
- **`renderWorld`**: The single world that is rendered to the main window

```mermaid
flowchart LR
    subgraph AppState["App Internal State"]
        LoadedSet["loadedWorlds<br/>locked_hashset<Ref<World>>"]
        RenderPtr["renderWorld<br/>Ref<World>"]
    end
    
    subgraph API["App Public API"]
        AddWorld["AddWorld(world)"]
        SetRendered["SetRenderedWorld(world)"]
        RemoveWorld["RemoveWorld(world)"]
    end
    
    AddWorld -->|"inserts into"| LoadedSet
    AddWorld -->|"if first world"| SetRendered
    SetRendered -->|"assigns to"| RenderPtr
    SetRendered -->|"calls OnActivate()"| World1
    RemoveWorld -->|"removes from"| LoadedSet
    RemoveWorld -->|"if is renderWorld"| RenderPtr
    
    LoadedSet --> World1["World instance 1"]
    LoadedSet --> World2["World instance 2"]
    RenderPtr -.points to.-> World1
    
    TickLoop["App::Tick() loop"] -->|"ticks all"| LoadedSet
    Rendering["RenderEngine::Draw()"] -->|"renders only"| RenderPtr
```

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/App.hpp:307-311](), [src/App_priv.hpp:514-565]()

### Entity and Component Creation

Entities are created through the `World::Instantiate()` method. Every entity automatically receives a `Transform` component:

```mermaid
flowchart TD
    WorldInst["world->Instantiate()"] --> CreateEntity["Creates Entity ID"]
    CreateEntity --> AddTransform["Automatically emplaces<br/>Transform component"]
    AddTransform --> ReturnEntity["Returns Entity handle"]
    
    ReturnEntity --> UserCode{"User adds<br/>more components?"}
    UserCode -->|yes| EmplaceComp["entity.EmplaceComponent<T>(args)"]
    EmplaceComp --> StoreComp["Component stored in<br/>World's ComponentStore"]
    UserCode -->|no| Done["Entity ready"]
    StoreComp --> Done
    
    Done --> Tick["World::Tick() processes<br/>components via systems"]
```

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/Transform.hpp:20-158]()

---

## Minimal Application Example

### Complete Walkthrough

Here is a minimal application that creates a world with a single entity:

#### Step 1: Define Your App Class

```cpp
// MyApp.hpp
#include <RavEngine/App.hpp>
#include <RavEngine/World.hpp>

class MyApp : public RavEngine::App {
protected:
    void OnStartup(int argc, char** argv) override;
};
```

Your application class inherits from `RavEngine::App` and overrides `OnStartup()` to perform initialization.

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/App.hpp:49-366]()

#### Step 2: Implement OnStartup

```cpp
// MyApp.cpp
#include "MyApp.hpp"
#include <RavEngine/Entity.hpp>

void MyApp::OnStartup(int argc, char** argv) {
    // Create a world
    auto world = RavEngine::New<RavEngine::World>();
    
    // Create an entity with Transform
    auto entity = world->Instantiate();
    
    // Modify the transform
    auto& transform = entity.GetTransform();
    transform.SetLocalPosition({0, 5, 0});
    
    // Add world to the application
    AddWorld(world);
    SetRenderedWorld(world);
}
```

This code:
1. Creates a `World` instance using `RavEngine::New<World>()`
2. Instantiates an `Entity` (automatically gets a `Transform`)
3. Modifies the entity's transform position
4. Adds the world to the app's `loadedWorlds` collection
5. Sets it as the `renderWorld` for rendering

**Sources:** [src/App_priv.hpp:532-542](), [include/RavEngine/Transform.hpp:77-82]()

#### Step 3: Create Main Entry Point

```cpp
// main.cpp
#include "MyApp.hpp"

int main(int argc, char** argv) {
    MyApp app;
    return app.run(argc, argv);
}
```

The `main()` function instantiates your app and calls `run()`, which:
- Invokes `OnConfigure()` 
- Initializes all engine systems (graphics, audio, input)
- Calls `OnStartup()`
- Enters the main loop
- Calls `OnShutdown()` on exit

**Sources:** [src/App.cpp:123-352]()

---

## The Main Loop Structure

### Tick Execution Flow

```mermaid
flowchart TD
    TickEntry["App::Tick() called each frame"] --> GetSwapchain["Acquire next swapchain image<br/>from window"]
    GetSwapchain --> TickAxes["inputManager->TickAxes()<br/>Process buffered input"]
    TickAxes --> TickWorlds["for each world in loadedWorlds"]
    
    TickWorlds --> WorldTick["world->Tick(currentScale)"]
    WorldTick --> UpdateGUI["Update GUI components<br/>Set dimensions, process events"]
    UpdateGUI --> NextWorld{"More worlds?"}
    NextWorld -->|yes| TickWorlds
    NextWorld -->|no| MainTasks["Process main thread tasks<br/>from main_tasks queue"]
    
    MainTasks --> GetCameras["Get all CameraComponent<br/>from renderWorld"]
    GetCameras --> CheckCameras{"Has cameras?"}
    CheckCameras -->|no| Fatal["Debug::Fatal:<br/>World needs camera"]
    CheckCameras -->|yes| BuildViews["Build RenderViewCollection<br/>for each camera"]
    
    BuildViews --> CallDraw["RenderEngine::Draw()<br/>allViews, renderWorld"]
    CallDraw --> Commit["CommandBuffer->Commit()"]
    Commit --> Present["swapchain->Present()"]
    Present --> EndProfile["Profile::EndTick()"]
    EndProfile --> UpdateAudio["player->SetWorld(renderWorld)"]
    UpdateAudio --> Return["Return to main loop"]
```

**Sources:** [src/App.cpp:354-503](), [src/App_priv.hpp:375-397]()

---

## Adding More Components

Once you have created an entity, you can add additional components using `EmplaceComponent<T>()`:

### Component Addition Pattern

```mermaid
graph TD
    Entity["Entity entity = world->Instantiate()"] --> HasTransform["âœ“ Has Transform component"]
    
    HasTransform --> AddStatic["entity.EmplaceComponent<StaticMeshComponent>(meshAsset)"]
    AddStatic --> AddPhysics["entity.EmplaceComponent<RigidBodyDynamic>()"]
    AddPhysics --> AddCollider["entity.EmplaceComponent<BoxCollider>()"]
    AddCollider --> AddAudio["entity.EmplaceComponent<AudioSourceComponent>(audioAsset)"]
    
    AddAudio --> ComponentStores["Components stored in<br/>World::ComponentStores"]
    
    ComponentStores --> Render["RenderEngine accesses<br/>StaticMeshComponent"]
    ComponentStores --> Physics["PhysicsSolver accesses<br/>RigidBodyDynamic + BoxCollider"]
    ComponentStores --> Audio["AudioPlayer accesses<br/>AudioSourceComponent"]
```

**Example:**

```cpp
void MyApp::OnStartup(int argc, char** argv) {
    auto world = RavEngine::New<RavEngine::World>();
    auto entity = world->Instantiate();
    
    // Entity now has Transform automatically
    entity.GetTransform().SetLocalPosition({0, 0, 0});
    
    // Add a static mesh for rendering
    auto mesh = RavEngine::New<MeshAsset>("my_mesh.rvem");
    entity.EmplaceComponent<StaticMeshComponent>(mesh);
    
    // Add physics components
    entity.EmplaceComponent<RigidBodyDynamic>();
    entity.EmplaceComponent<BoxCollider>();
    
    AddWorld(world);
    SetRenderedWorld(world);
}
```

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/Transform.hpp:20-158]()

---

## Optional Configuration

### Configuring the Render Backend

Override `OnConfigure()` to customize engine settings:

```cpp
AppConfig MyApp::OnConfigure(int argc, char** argv) {
    AppConfig config;
    config.preferredBackend = AppConfig::RenderBackend::Vulkan;
    return config;
}
```

The `AppConfig` struct allows you to specify:
- `preferredBackend`: Choose between Metal, DirectX12, Vulkan, or AutoSelect
  
If not overridden, the engine uses `RenderBackend::AutoSelect` which picks the platform default.

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/App.hpp:26-34](), [src/App.cpp:132-162]()

### Disabling Audio or Networking

Override these methods to disable subsystems:

```cpp
bool MyApp::NeedsAudio() const {
    return false;  // Disable audio system
}

bool MyApp::NeedsNetworking() const {
    return false;  // Disable networking
}
```

Returning `false` from `NeedsAudio()` prevents `AudioPlayer` initialization. Returning `false` from `NeedsNetworking()` skips `GameNetworkingSockets` initialization.

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/App.hpp:77-87](), [src/App.cpp:217-229]()

---

## Input Manager Setup

To receive input events, create an `InputManager` and bind it to your app:

```cpp
void MyApp::OnStartup(int argc, char** argv) {
    // Create input manager
    inputManager = RavEngine::New<RavEngine::InputManager>();
    
    // Create action mappings
    inputManager->AddActionMap("Jump", SDL_SCANCODE_SPACE);
    inputManager->AddAxisMap("MoveForward", SDL_SCANCODE_W, 1.0f);
    inputManager->AddAxisMap("MoveForward", SDL_SCANCODE_S, -1.0f);
    
    // Create world and entities...
    auto world = RavEngine::New<RavEngine::World>();
    AddWorld(world);
    SetRenderedWorld(world);
}
```

The `App` class has a member `inputManager` of type `Ref<InputManager>` which, when set, is automatically processed during the main loop.

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/App.hpp:171](), [src/App_priv.hpp:320-326](), [src/InputManager.cpp:15-18]()

---

## Camera Setup for Rendering

For the engine to render your world, you must create at least one `CameraComponent`:

```mermaid
flowchart LR
    CreateEntity["entity = world->Instantiate()"] --> AddCamera["entity.EmplaceComponent<CameraComponent>()"]
    AddCamera --> SetTransform["entity.GetTransform()<br/>.SetLocalPosition(0, 0, -10)"]
    
    SetTransform --> TickLoop["App::Tick() main loop"]
    TickLoop --> GetCameras["allCameras = renderWorld<br/>->GetAllComponentsOfType<CameraComponent>()"]
    GetCameras --> CheckNull{"allCameras != null?"}
    CheckNull -->|no| Fatal["Debug::Fatal:<br/>World needs camera"]
    CheckNull -->|yes| BuildViewData["For each active camera:<br/>Generate view/projection matrices"]
    BuildViewData --> Render["RenderEngine::Draw(renderWorld, allViews)"]
```

**Example:**

```cpp
void MyApp::OnStartup(int argc, char** argv) {
    auto world = RavEngine::New<RavEngine::World>();
    
    // Create camera entity
    auto cameraEntity = world->Instantiate();
    cameraEntity.EmplaceComponent<CameraComponent>();
    cameraEntity.GetTransform().SetLocalPosition({0, 0, -10});
    
    AddWorld(world);
    SetRenderedWorld(world);
}
```

Without an active `CameraComponent`, the application will terminate with `Debug::Fatal("Cannot render: World does not have a camera!")`.

**Sources:** [src/App_priv.hpp:400-442]()

---

## Summary

To create a RavEngine application:

1. **Subclass `App`** and override lifecycle methods
2. **Implement `OnStartup()`** to create your `World` and entities
3. **Create a `main()`** function that instantiates your app and calls `run()`
4. **Add a camera** to your world for rendering
5. **(Optional)** Override `OnConfigure()` for custom settings
6. **(Optional)** Set up `InputManager` for input handling

### Key API Methods Reference

| Class | Method | Purpose |
|-------|--------|---------|
| `App` | `int run(int, char**)` | Main entry point, starts engine loop |
| `App` | `void AddWorld(Ref<World>)` | Adds world to tick list |
| `App` | `void SetRenderedWorld(Ref<World>)` | Sets world to render |
| `World` | `Entity Instantiate()` | Creates new entity with Transform |
| `Entity` | `Transform& GetTransform()` | Access entity's transform |
| `Entity` | `EmplaceComponent<T>(args...)` | Add component to entity |
| `Transform` | `SetLocalPosition(vector3)` | Set position in local space |
| `InputManager` | `AddActionMap(name, scancode)` | Create input action mapping |

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/App.hpp:49-366](), [src/App.cpp:99-675](), [include/RavEngine/Transform.hpp:20-346](), [include/RavEngine/InputManager.hpp:136-413]()1c:T532e,# Core Systems

## Purpose and Scope

This page documents the foundational systems that form RavEngine's architecture: the **Application Lifecycle** (`App`), **Entity Component System** (`World`), **Transform hierarchy**, and **Input Management** (`InputManager`). These systems coordinate to provide the engine's core execution loop, entity management, scene graph, and user input handling.

For detailed rendering documentation, see [Rendering](#4). For physics simulation, see [Physics](#5). For animation, see [Animation](#6). For audio, see [Audio](#7).

---

## System Overview

RavEngine's core architecture consists of four primary systems that work together to manage application execution:

```mermaid
graph TB
    App["App<br/>Application Lifecycle"]
    World["World<br/>ECS Container"]
    InputMgr["InputManager<br/>Input Processing"]
    Transform["Transform<br/>Scene Hierarchy"]
    
    subgraph "Execution Flow"
        AppRun["App::run()<br/>Main Entry"]
        AppTick["App::Tick()<br/>Frame Update"]
        WorldTick["World::Tick()<br/>ECS Update"]
        TickECS["World::TickECS()<br/>System Execution"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Managed Resources"
        LoadedWorlds["locked_hashset<br/>loadedWorlds"]
        RenderWorld["Ref<World><br/>renderWorld"]
    end
    
    App --> AppRun
    AppRun --> AppTick
    AppTick --> WorldTick
    WorldTick --> TickECS
    
    App --> LoadedWorlds
    App --> RenderWorld
    App --> InputMgr
    
    World --> Transform
    WorldTick --> Transform
    
    InputMgr -.->|events| App
```

**Sources:** [src/App.cpp:123-352](), [src/App_priv.hpp:1-98](), [include/RavEngine/App.hpp:1-368](), [src/World.cpp:54-74]()

## Application Lifecycle

The `App` class manages the application's lifetime, coordinating all major systems through a central main loop.

### Key Components

| Component | Type | Purpose |
|-----------|------|---------|
| `executor` | `tf::Executor` | Global thread pool for parallel task execution |
| `loadedWorlds` | `locked_hashset<Ref<World>>` | All worlds being ticked |
| `renderWorld` | `Ref<World>` | Currently rendered world |
| `inputManager` | `Ref<InputManager>` | Input processing system |
| `currentScale` | `float` | Frame time scale factor |
| `tickMode` | `TickMode` | `DynamicRate` or `FixedRate` |

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/App.hpp:49-368](), [src/App_priv.hpp:49-98]()

### Main Loop Structure

```mermaid
graph TD
    Start["App::run()"]
    Init["Initialize SDL,<br/>RGL, RenderEngine"]
    MainLoop{"Main Loop<br/>!exit"}
    
    PollEvents["SDL_PollEvent()<br/>Process Events"]
    CalcDelta["Calculate deltaTime<br/>from lastFrameTime"]
    AppTick["App::Tick()"]
    TickWorlds["Tick All Worlds<br/>in loadedWorlds"]
    ProcessMainThread["Process main_tasks<br/>ConcurrentQueue"]
    Render["Render renderWorld"]
    Present["Present Swapchain"]
    
    Shutdown["OnShutdown()"]
    
    Start --> Init
    Init --> MainLoop
    MainLoop -->|true| PollEvents
    PollEvents --> CalcDelta
    CalcDelta --> AppTick
    AppTick --> TickWorlds
    TickWorlds --> ProcessMainThread
    ProcessMainThread --> Render
    Render --> Present
    Present --> MainLoop
    MainLoop -->|false| Shutdown
```

**Sources:** [src/App_priv.hpp:123-352](), [src/App_priv.hpp:354-497]()

### Frame Time Calculation

The engine calculates frame timing to support both dynamic and fixed tick rates:

```cpp
// Dynamic rate: scale based on actual frame time
auto now = clocktype::now();
deltaTimeMicroseconds = std::min(duration_cast<timeDiff>(now - lastFrameTime), maxTimeStep);
float deltaSeconds = std::chrono::duration<float>(deltaTimeMicroseconds).count();
currentScale = deltaSeconds * evalNormal;  // evalNormal = 60

// Fixed rate: constant scale
if (tickMode == TickMode::FixedRate) {
    currentScale = 1;
    deltaSeconds = 1.0s / evalNormal;
}
```

**Sources:** [src/App_priv.hpp:281-295]()

---

## World and Entity Component System

The `World` class implements RavEngine's Entity Component System (ECS), managing entities, components, and systems using sparse set data structures.

### ECS Architecture

```mermaid
graph LR
    subgraph "World Container"
        WorldClass["World"]
        AvailableIDs["Queue<entity_id_t><br/>available"]
        Versions["Vector<uint8_t><br/>versions"]
        ComponentMap["locked_node_hashmap<br/>ctti_t, AnySparseSet>"]
        PolyMap["locked_node_hashmap<br/>ctti_t, SparseSetForPolymorphic>"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Entity Storage"
        EntityID["entity_t<br/>{id, version}"]
        EntityHandle["Entity<br/>ComponentHandle"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Component Storage"
        AnySparseSet["AnySparseSet<br/>Type-erased wrapper"]
        EntitySparseSet["EntitySparseSet<T><br/>dense_set: unordered_vector<T><br/>aux_set: entity_id_t[]<br/>sparse_set: entity_id_t[]"]
    end
    
    subgraph "System Execution"
        MasterTasks["tf::Taskflow<br/>masterTasks"]
        ECSTasks["tf::Taskflow<br/>ECSTasks"]
        PhysicsTask["PhysicsLinkSystem"]
        AnimatorTask["AnimatorSystem"]
        ScriptTask["ScriptSystem"]
    end
    
    WorldClass --> AvailableIDs
    WorldClass --> Versions
    WorldClass --> ComponentMap
    WorldClass --> PolyMap
    WorldClass --> MasterTasks
    
    ComponentMap --> AnySparseSet
    AnySparseSet --> EntitySparseSet
    
    EntityHandle -.->|references| EntityID
    EntitySparseSet -.->|stores| EntityID
    
    MasterTasks --> ECSTasks
    ECSTasks --> PhysicsTask
    ECSTasks --> AnimatorTask
    ECSTasks --> ScriptTask
```

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/World.hpp:156-284](), [include/RavEngine/World.hpp:286-325](), [src/World.cpp:150-202]()

### Entity Management

Entities are identified by a `entity_t` structure containing an ID and version number:

```cpp
struct entity_t {
    entity_id_t id;      // sparse set index
    uint8_t version;      // for detecting stale references
};
```

When an entity is destroyed, its ID is added to `available` queue for reuse, and its version is incremented to invalidate old handles.

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/Types.hpp]() (referenced), [include/RavEngine/World.hpp:160-165]()

### Component Storage: EntitySparseSet

Components are stored in type-specific sparse sets for efficient iteration and random access:

| Member | Type | Purpose |
|--------|------|---------|
| `dense_set` | `unordered_vector<T>` | Tightly packed components for iteration |
| `aux_set` | `UnorderedVector<entity_id_t>` | Owner entity IDs (parallel to dense_set) |
| `sparse_set` | `Vector<entity_id_t>` | Maps entity ID â†’ dense index |

This provides O(1) component lookup and O(n) dense iteration without fragmentation.

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/World.hpp:188-284]()

### System Execution with Taskflow

Systems execute in parallel using Taskflow, with dependency management ensuring correct ordering:

```mermaid
graph TB
    subgraph "World::SetupTaskGraph()"
        MasterTask["masterTasks<br/>tf::Taskflow"]
        ECSModule["ECSTasks<br/>Composed Module"]
        
        UpdateAsync["Update async_begin/end<br/>iterators"]
        DoAsync["Execute async_tasks"]
        CleanupAsync["Remove completed tasks"]
        
        PhysicsRoot["Physics Root Task"]
        PhysicsWrite["PhysicsLinkSystemWrite"]
        RunPhysics["PhysicsSolver::Tick()"]
        PhysicsRead["PhysicsLinkSystemRead"]
        
        AnimatorSys["AnimatorSystem"]
        ScriptSys["ScriptSystem"]
        SocketSys["SocketSystem"]
    end
    
    MasterTask --> ECSModule
    ECSModule --> UpdateAsync
    UpdateAsync --> DoAsync
    DoAsync --> CleanupAsync
    
    ECSModule --> PhysicsRoot
    PhysicsRoot --> PhysicsWrite
    PhysicsRoot --> PhysicsRead
    PhysicsWrite --> RunPhysics
    RunPhysics --> PhysicsRead
    
    PhysicsRead --> AnimatorSys
    PhysicsWrite --> ScriptSys
    ScriptSys --> AnimatorSys
    AnimatorSys --> SocketSys
```

**Sources:** [src/World.cpp:150-202](), [include/RavEngine/World.hpp:150-157]()

### World Tick Execution

```cpp
void World::Tick(float scale) {
    if (graphWasModified) {
        CheckSystems();  // Rebuild task graph if systems changed
    }
    
    PreTick(scale);      // Pre-simulation hooks
    TickECS(scale);      // Execute taskflow
    PostTick(scale);     // Post-simulation hooks
    
    // Sync render data (async)
    executor.run(renderTasks).wait();
}
```

**Sources:** [src/World.cpp:54-74]()

## Transform System and Scene Hierarchy

The `Transform` component implements a parent-child scene graph with local and world space transformations.

### Transform Data Structure

```mermaid
graph TB
    subgraph "Transform Component"
        TransformClass["Transform"]
        
        Position["vector3 position<br/>(local space)"]
        Rotation["quaternion rotation<br/>(local space)"]
        Scale["vector3 scale<br/>(local space)"]
        
        ParentMatrix["matrix4 matrix<br/>(parent world transform)"]
        Parent["ComponentHandle<Transform><br/>parent"]
        Children["UnorderedVector<br/>ComponentHandle<Transform>>"]
        
        IsDirty["bool isDirty<br/>(hierarchy changed)"]
        IsTickDirty["bool isTickDirty<br/>(needs render sync)"]
    end
    
    TransformClass --> Position
    TransformClass --> Rotation
    TransformClass --> Scale
    TransformClass --> ParentMatrix
    TransformClass --> Parent
    TransformClass --> Children
    TransformClass --> IsDirty
    TransformClass --> IsTickDirty
    
    Parent -.->|points to| TransformClass
    Children -.->|contains| TransformClass
```

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/Transform.hpp:20-71]()

### Local vs World Space Transformations

Transforms maintain both local (parent-relative) and world (absolute) representations:

| Method | Space | Formula |
|--------|-------|---------|
| `GenerateLocalMatrix()` | Local | `translate(position) * toMat4(rotation) * scale(scale)` |
| `GetWorldMatrix()` | World | `matrix * GenerateLocalMatrix()` |
| `GetParentSpaceMatrix()` | Parent | `matrix` |

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/Transform.hpp:120-134](), [include/RavEngine/Transform.hpp:164-166]()

### Dirty Flag Propagation

When a transform changes, dirty flags propagate through the hierarchy:

```cpp
void Transform::UpdateChildren() {
    MarkAsDirty();  // Set isDirty and isTickDirty
    
    if (children.size() > 0) {
        auto newParentMatrix = GetWorldMatrix();
        for (auto& child : children) {
            child->matrix = newParentMatrix;  // Update cached parent matrix
            child->UpdateChildren();          // Recursive propagation
        }
    }
}
```

This ensures world matrices stay synchronized without recomputing the entire hierarchy every frame.

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/Transform.hpp:54-70]()

### Parenting Operations

```mermaid
graph LR
    subgraph "AddChild()"
        SaveWorld["Save child's<br/>world pos/rot"]
        SetParent["Set child.parent<br/>Add to children list"]
        UpdateMatrix["child.matrix =<br/>GetWorldMatrix()"]
        RestoreWorld["Restore child's<br/>world pos/rot"]
    end
    
    subgraph "RemoveChild()"
        SaveWorld2["Save child's<br/>world pos/rot"]
        ClearParent["Clear child.parent<br/>Remove from children"]
        ResetMatrix["child.matrix =<br/>identity"]
        RestoreWorld2["Restore child's<br/>world pos/rot"]
    end
    
    SaveWorld --> SetParent
    SetParent --> UpdateMatrix
    UpdateMatrix --> RestoreWorld
    
    SaveWorld2 --> ClearParent
    ClearParent --> ResetMatrix
    ResetMatrix --> RestoreWorld2
```

**Sources:** [src/Transform.cpp:10-36]()

---

## Input Management System

The `InputManager` processes SDL events and dispatches them to registered listeners via action/axis bindings.

### Input Processing Architecture

```mermaid
graph TB
    subgraph "SDL Event Layer"
        SDLEvents["SDL_Event"]
        KeyDown["SDL_EVENT_KEY_DOWN"]
        KeyUp["SDL_EVENT_KEY_UP"]
        MouseMove["SDL_EVENT_MOUSE_MOTION"]
        GamepadButton["SDL_EVENT_GAMEPAD_BUTTON"]
        GamepadAxis["SDL_EVENT_GAMEPAD_AXIS"]
    end
    
    subgraph "InputManager Processing"
        ProcessInput["ProcessInput()"]
        ProcessActionID["ProcessActionID()<br/>Action dispatching"]
        ProcessAxisID["ProcessAxisID()<br/>Axis buffering"]
        TickAxes["TickAxes()<br/>Axis consumption"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Binding Storage"
        CodeToAction["locked_hashmap<int,<br/>UnorderedSet<string>>"]
        CodeToAxis["locked_hashmap<int,<br/>UnorderedSet<AxisIdentifier>>"]
        ActionBindings["locked_hashmap<string,<br/>List<ActionBinding>>"]
        AxisBindings["locked_hashmap<string,<br/>AxisData>"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Listeners"
        IInputListener["IInputListener<br/>AnyActionDown/Up"]
        ActionCallbacks["ActionBinding<br/>Function<void(ActionState,CID)>"]
        AxisCallbacks["AxisBinding<br/>Function<void(float,CID)>"]
    end
    
    SDLEvents --> ProcessInput
    KeyDown --> ProcessActionID
    KeyUp --> ProcessActionID
    MouseMove --> ProcessAxisID
    GamepadButton --> ProcessActionID
    GamepadAxis --> ProcessAxisID
    
    ProcessActionID --> CodeToAction
    ProcessAxisID --> CodeToAxis
    
    CodeToAction --> ActionBindings
    CodeToAxis --> AxisBindings
    
    ActionBindings --> ActionCallbacks
    TickAxes --> AxisCallbacks
    
    ProcessActionID -.->|also notifies| IInputListener
```

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/InputManager.hpp:16-247](), [src/InputManager.cpp:14-245]()

### Action Bindings

Actions represent discrete button press/release events:

```cpp
// Binding creation
inputManager->AddActionMap("Jump", SDL_SCANCODE_SPACE);
inputManager->AddActionMap("Jump", ControllerButton::SDL_CONTROLLER_BUTTON_A);

// Listener registration
struct MyListener : public IInputListener {
    void AnyActionDown(int charcode) override {
        // Called for any key press
    }
};
```

When an input occurs, `ProcessActionID()` looks up actions in `CodeToAction` and invokes all registered callbacks.

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/InputManager.hpp:89-126](), [src/InputManager.cpp:30-53]()

### Axis Bindings

Axes represent continuous input values (analog sticks, mouse movement):

```cpp
// Axis inputs are buffered during event processing
void InputManager::ProcessAxisID(int ID, float value, CID controller) {
    for (const auto& axisName : CodeToAxis[ID]) {
        AxisBindings[axisName.identifier].bufferedInputs[ID] = {
            value * axisName.scale, 
            controller
        };
    }
}

// Consumed once per frame in TickAxes()
void InputManager::TickAxes() {
    for (auto& binding : AxisBindings) {
        for (const auto& axis : binding.second.bindings) {
            for (const auto& buffered_value : binding.second.bufferedInputs) {
                axis(buffered_value.second.value, 
                     buffered_value.second.source_controller);
            }
        }
    }
    // Clear mouse velocity inputs
    // ...
}
```

**Sources:** [src/InputManager.cpp:56-97]()

### Controller Support

Controllers use special ID offsets to distinguish from keyboard/mouse:

| Input Type | ID Range |
|------------|----------|
| Keyboard/Mouse | `0` to `SDL_SCANCODE_COUNT` |
| Controller Buttons | `Special::CONTROLLER_BUTTON_OFFSET` (-10000) |
| Controller Axes | `Special::CONTROLLER_AXIS_OFFSET` (-8000) |
| Mouse Movement | `Special::MOUSEMOVE_*` (-500 range) |

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/InputManager.hpp:23-71]()

## System Integration and Data Flow

### Main Execution Flow

```mermaid
sequenceDiagram
    participant AppRun as App::run()
    participant AppTick as App::Tick()
    participant WorldTick as World::Tick()
    participant Taskflow as tf::Executor
    participant RenderEngine as RenderEngine::Draw()
    
    AppRun->>AppRun: Initialize SDL, RGL
    AppRun->>AppRun: Create RenderEngine
    
    loop Main Loop
        AppRun->>AppRun: SDL_PollEvent()
        AppRun->>InputManager: ProcessInput(event)
        AppRun->>AppRun: Calculate deltaTime
        AppRun->>AppTick: Tick()
        
        AppTick->>WorldTick: Tick(currentScale)
        WorldTick->>WorldTick: PreTick()
        WorldTick->>WorldTick: TickECS()
        WorldTick->>Taskflow: executor.run(masterTasks)
        Taskflow->>Taskflow: Execute systems in parallel
        WorldTick->>WorldTick: PostTick()
        WorldTick->>Taskflow: executor.run(renderTasks)
        
        AppTick->>AppTick: Process main_tasks queue
        AppTick->>RenderEngine: Draw(renderWorld, targets)
        AppTick->>AppTick: Present swapchain
    end
```

**Sources:** [src/App_priv.hpp:123-497](), [src/World.cpp:54-74]()

### Render Data Synchronization

The `World` maintains parallel GPU-friendly data structures synchronized asynchronously:


**Sources:** [src/World.cpp:309-521](), [include/RavEngine/World.hpp:419-449]()

### Thread Safety

The engine uses several concurrency mechanisms:

| Mechanism | Usage |
|-----------|-------|
| `tf::Executor` | Parallel system execution with dependency ordering |
| `SpinLock` | Lightweight locks for component maps |
| `ConcurrentQueue` | Lock-free queues for main thread tasks |
| `std::atomic` | Atomic operations for flags and indices |
| `locked_hashmap<T, SpinLock>` | Thread-safe hash maps |

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/App.hpp:112-118](), [include/RavEngine/World.hpp:327]()

This document details the `App` class, which serves as the entry point and main orchestrator for RavEngine applications. The `App` class manages initialization, the main loop, world management, and shutdown procedures.

For information about the Entity Component System and World management, see [Entity Component System](#3.2). For rendering pipeline details, see [Rendering Architecture](#4.1). For input handling specifics, see [Input System](#3.4).

---

## Purpose and Scope

The `App` class is the root object that:
- Initializes core engine subsystems (graphics, audio, input, networking)
- Manages the main application loop with configurable tick modes
- Coordinates world loading, ticking, and rendering
- Provides lifecycle hooks for application-specific logic
- Handles graceful shutdown and resource cleanup

Users create their own application by inheriting from `App` and implementing virtual methods to customize behavior.

---

## Core App Class Structure

The `App` class provides the following key components:

| Component | Type | Purpose |
|-----------|------|---------|
| `device` | `RGLDevicePtr` | GPU device handle |
| `window` | `std::unique_ptr<Window>` | Main application window |
| `Renderer` | `std::unique_ptr<RenderEngine>` | Rendering pipeline manager |
| `Resources` | `std::unique_ptr<VirtualFilesystem>` | Asset access via PhysFS |
| `player` | `std::unique_ptr<AudioPlayer>` | Audio playback system |
| `inputManager` | `Ref<InputManager>` | Input handling and bindings |
| `executor` | `tf::Executor` | Global thread pool (Taskflow) |
| `networkManager` | `NetworkManager` | Client/server networking |
| `loadedWorlds` | `locked_hashset<Ref<World>>` | Active worlds being ticked |
| `renderWorld` | `Ref<World>` | Currently rendered world |
| `main_tasks` | `ConcurrentQueue` | Main thread task queue |

## Tick Modes

RavEngine supports two tick modes via the `tickMode` member:

### DynamicRate (Default)

In `TickMode::DynamicRate`, the engine runs as fast as possible, with `deltaTimeMicroseconds` measuring actual elapsed time. The `currentScale` factor adjusts to maintain consistent physics and animation speeds regardless of frame rate:

```cpp
currentScale = deltaSeconds * evalNormal;  // evalNormal = 60
time += deltaSeconds;
```

If the frame rate drops below 1 FPS, the engine clamps `deltaTimeMicroseconds` to `maxTimeStep` (1000ms) to prevent physics explosions.

### FixedRate

In `TickMode::FixedRate`, the engine ticks at exactly 60 Hz regardless of rendering speed:

```cpp
currentScale = 1;
auto deltaSeconds = 1.0s / evalNormal;  // Always 1/60 second
deltaTimeMicroseconds = duration_cast<timeDiff>(deltaSeconds);
time += std::chrono::duration<float>(deltaTimeMicroseconds).count();
```

This mode is useful for deterministic simulations and server builds.

**Sources:** [src/App.cpp:287-295](), [include/RavEngine/App.hpp:36-39,120]()

---

## World Management

The `App` class maintains a set of active worlds and designates one as the "render world". Multiple worlds can be ticked simultaneously, but only the render world is visible.

```mermaid
graph LR
    App["App"]
    LoadedWorlds["loadedWorlds<br/>locked_hashset&lt;Ref&lt;World&gt;&gt;<br/>All worlds being ticked"]
    RenderWorld["renderWorld<br/>Ref&lt;World&gt;<br/>World being rendered"]
    
    AddWorld["AddWorld(world)<br/>Add to loadedWorlds<br/>Auto-set as renderWorld if first"]
    RemoveWorld["RemoveWorld(world)<br/>Remove from loadedWorlds<br/>Clear renderWorld if matched"]
    SetRenderedWorld["SetRenderedWorld(world)<br/>Call OnDeactivate() on old<br/>Call OnActivate() on new"]
    AddReplaceWorld["AddReplaceWorld(old, new)<br/>Transfer render state<br/>Remove old, add new"]
    
    App --> LoadedWorlds
    App --> RenderWorld
    LoadedWorlds --> AddWorld
    LoadedWorlds --> RemoveWorld
    RenderWorld --> SetRenderedWorld
    App --> AddReplaceWorld
```

### Key World Management Methods

| Method | Parameters | Behavior |
|--------|-----------|----------|
| `AddWorld(world)` | `Ref<World>` | Adds world to tick list. If first world, automatically sets as render world. Synchronizes with network if client. |
| `RemoveWorld(world)` | `Ref<World>` | Removes world from tick list. If render world, calls `OnDeactivate()` and clears render world pointer. |
| `SetRenderedWorld(world)` | `Ref<World>` | Changes which world is rendered. Calls `OnDeactivate()` on old, `OnActivate()` on new. World must already be in `loadedWorlds`. |
| `AddReplaceWorld(old, new)` | `Ref<World>`, `Ref<World>` | Replaces old world with new, transferring render state if applicable. |
| `RemoveAllWorlds()` | None | Removes all worlds from the tick list. |

**Sources:** [src/App.cpp:514-580](), [include/RavEngine/App.hpp:174-214]()

---

## Virtual Lifecycle Hooks

Applications customize behavior by overriding these virtual methods:

### Configuration Hook

```cpp
virtual AppConfig OnConfigure(int argc, char** argv);
```

Called during `run()` before subsystem initialization. Returns an `AppConfig` specifying the preferred graphics backend:

```cpp
struct AppConfig {
    enum class RenderBackend {
        Metal, DirectX12, Vulkan, WebGPU, AutoSelect
    } preferredBackend = RenderBackend::AutoSelect;
};
```

The engine can override this via the `RGL_BACKEND` environment variable.

### Startup Hook

```cpp
virtual void OnStartup(int argc, char** argv);
```

Called after all subsystems are initialized but before entering the main loop. Use this to:
- Create and load initial worlds
- Set up input mappings
- Load assets
- Initialize gameplay state

### Shutdown Hook

```cpp
virtual int OnShutdown();
```

Called after exiting the main loop but before the destructor. Use this to:
- Save game state
- Clean up custom resources
- Return an exit code

### Other Hooks

| Hook | Purpose |
|------|---------|
| `virtual void OnFatal(std::string_view msg)` | Custom fatal error handler |
| `virtual void OnDropAudioWorklets(uint32_t nDropped)` | Called when audio buffer overruns occur |
| `virtual bool NeedsAudio() const` | Return `false` to disable audio subsystem |
| `virtual bool NeedsNetworking() const` | Return `true` to enable networking subsystem |

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/App.hpp:68-87,333-348](), [src/App.cpp:132,265,351]()

---

## Audio Snapshot System

The `App` manages triple-buffered audio snapshots for lock-free communication between the main thread and audio thread:

```mermaid
graph TD
    MainThread["Main Thread<br/>Creating AudioSnapshot"]
    AudioThread["Audio Thread<br/>Rendering Audio"]
    
    Snapshot0["audioSnapshots[0]"]
    Snapshot1["audioSnapshots[1]"]
    Snapshot2["audioSnapshots[2]"]
    
    Bitset["audioswapbitset (atomic uint8_t)<br/>Encodes 3 indices + available flag"]
    CurrentIdx["Current index (bits 0-1)<br/>Main thread writes here"]
    InactiveIdx["Inactive index (bits 2-3)<br/>Staging area"]
    RenderIdx["Render index (bits 4-5)<br/>Audio thread reads here"]
    AvailableFlag["Available flag (bit 6)<br/>Signals new data"]
    
    SwapCurrent["SwapCurrentAudioSnapshot()<br/>Atomically swap current â†” inactive<br/>Set available flag"]
    SwapRender["SwapRenderAudioSnapshotIfNeeded()<br/>Check available flag<br/>Atomically swap inactive â†” render"]
    
    GetCurrent["GetCurrentAudioSnapshot()<br/>Returns audioSnapshots[current]"]
    GetRender["GetRenderAudioSnapshot()<br/>Returns audioSnapshots[render]"]
    
    MainThread --> GetCurrent
    GetCurrent --> CurrentIdx
    MainThread --> SwapCurrent
    SwapCurrent --> Bitset
    
    AudioThread --> SwapRender
    SwapRender --> Bitset
    AudioThread --> GetRender
    GetRender --> RenderIdx
    
    Bitset --> CurrentIdx
    Bitset --> InactiveIdx
    Bitset --> RenderIdx
    Bitset --> AvailableFlag
    
    CurrentIdx --> Snapshot0
    InactiveIdx --> Snapshot1
    RenderIdx --> Snapshot2
```

The snapshot system uses a packed bitfield in an atomic `uint8_t` to avoid locks:

| Bits | Field | Purpose |
|------|-------|---------|
| 0-1 | Current | Index main thread writes to |
| 2-3 | Inactive | Staging index for swap |
| 4-5 | Render | Index audio thread reads from |
| 6 | Available | Flag indicating new data ready |

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/App.hpp:222-299,313-323](), [src/App_priv.hpp:1-19]()

---

## Main Thread Task Queue

The `App` provides a thread-safe queue for dispatching work to the main thread from any thread:

```cpp
template<typename T>
constexpr inline void DispatchMainThread(const T& f) {
    main_tasks.enqueue(f);
}
```

Tasks are processed during `App::Tick()` before rendering:

```cpp
Function<void(void)> front;
while (main_tasks.try_dequeue(front)) {
    front();
}
```

**Important:** When capturing variables in the lambda, always capture by value (`[=]`), not by reference. The lambda executes at a different time on a different thread:

```cpp
int x = 5;
GetApp()->DispatchMainThread([=]{
    std::cout << x << std::endl;  // Correct: captured by value
});
```

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/App.hpp:147-161](), [src/App.cpp:390-397]()

---

## Shutdown Sequence

When `App::Quit()` is called or the window is closed, the destructor executes a comprehensive cleanup:

```mermaid
graph TD
    Quit["App::Quit() or Window Close"]
    ExitLoop["Exit main loop"]
    OnShutdownHook["Call OnShutdown()<br/>Virtual hook, return exit code"]
    Destructor["App::~App()"]

    ShutdownAudio{"GetAudioActive()?"}

    ClearInput["inputManager = nullptr"]
    ClearRenderWorld["renderWorld = nullptr"]
    ClearWorlds["loadedWorlds.clear()"]
    
    KillNetworking["GameNetworkingSockets_Kill()"]
    DeinitPhysFS["PHYSFS_deinit()"]
    
    GetFileInterface["Get RmlUi file interface"]
    ShutdownRmlUi["Rml::Shutdown()"]
    DeleteFileInterface["delete file interface"]
    ResetRenderer["Renderer.reset()"]
    
    ClearGlobalApp["currentApp = nullptr"]
    
    Quit --> ExitLoop
    ExitLoop --> OnShutdownHook
    OnShutdownHook --> Destructor
    Destructor --> WaitGPU
    WaitGPU --> DeactivateDebug
    DeactivateDebug --> ClearMeshes
    ClearMeshes --> ClearSkinnedMeshes
    ClearSkinnedMeshes --> ClearDefaultTextures
    ClearDefaultTextures --> ClearTextureManager
    ClearTextureManager --> ShutdownAudio
    
    ShutdownAudio -->|Yes| ShutdownPlayer
    ShutdownAudio -->|No| ClearNetwork
    ShutdownPlayer --> ClearNetwork
    
    ClearNetwork --> ClearInput
    ClearInput --> ClearRenderWorld
    ClearRenderWorld --> ClearWorlds
    ClearWorlds --> KillNetworking
    KillNetworking --> DeinitPhysFS
    DeinitPhysFS --> GetFileInterface
    GetFileInterface --> ShutdownRmlUi
    ShutdownRmlUi --> DeleteFileInterface
    DeleteFileInterface --> ResetRenderer
    ResetRenderer --> ClearGlobalApp
```

**Sources:** [src/App.cpp:582-637](), [src/App.cpp:351]()

---

## Global App Access

The engine maintains a global pointer to the current `App` instance, accessible via:

```cpp
App* RavEngine::GetApp();
```

This allows subsystems to access application-level resources like the device, render engine, or virtual filesystem:

```cpp
auto device = GetApp()->GetDevice();
auto& renderer = GetApp()->GetRenderEngine();
auto& vfs = GetApp()->GetResources();
```

The global pointer is set in the constructor and cleared in the destructor. Only one `App` instance should exist at a time.

**Sources:** [src/App.cpp:53,101,636,671-674](), [include/RavEngine/GetApp.hpp]()

---

## Platform-Specific Initialization

### Windows

- Sets process DPI awareness via `SetProcessDPIAware()` (except on ARM64)
- DPI scaling is handled at the OS level, not by the engine

### Android

- Passes `SDL_GetAndroidJNIEnv()` and `SDL_GetAndroidActivity()` to PhysFS for accessing APK assets
- Special initialization struct: `PHYSFS_AndroidInit`

### Apple Platforms

- Enables smooth scrolling via `enableSmoothScrolling()`
- Uses `@autoreleasepool` blocks around main loop and tick to manage Objective-C memory

### Server Builds (`RVE_SERVER`)

- Skips SDL, RGL, RenderEngine, Window, and AudioPlayer initialization
- Uses `min_tick_time` (1/60 second) with manual delay to maintain tick rate
- No swapchain or rendering

**Sources:** [src/App.cpp:107-117,204-206,233-236,276-278,330-344,355-357](), [src/App_priv.hpp:1-46]()

---
