## Purpose and Scope

This document describes RavEngine's Entity Component System (ECS) architecture, centered on the `World` class. It covers entity creation and lifecycle management, component storage using sparse sets, component queries and filtering, system execution via task graphs, and polymorphic component support. For information about the Transform hierarchy specifically, see [Transform and Scene Hierarchy](#3.3). For physics integration, see [Physics](#5). For rendering integration details, see [Rendering Architecture](#4.1).

---

## Architecture Overview

RavEngine implements a data-oriented ECS where:
- **Entities** are lightweight handles (`entity_t`) consisting of an ID and version number
- **Components** are stored in type-specific `EntitySparseSet<T>` containers within the `World`
- **Systems** are organized into a task graph using the Taskflow library for parallel execution
- **The World** serves as the central container managing all entities, components, and systems

```mermaid
graph TB
    World["World<br/>ECS Container"]
    EntityPool["Entity Pool<br/>available queue<br/>versions vector"]
    ComponentMap["componentMap<br/>locked_node_hashmap&lt;ctti_t, AnySparseSet&gt;"]
    TaskGraph["Task Graph<br/>masterTasks (Taskflow)<br/>ECSTasks, renderTasks"]
    
    World --> EntityPool
    World --> ComponentMap
    World --> TaskGraph
    
    EntitySparseSet1["EntitySparseSet&lt;Transform&gt;<br/>dense_set, sparse_set, aux_set"]
    EntitySparseSet2["EntitySparseSet&lt;StaticMesh&gt;"]
    EntitySparseSet3["EntitySparseSet&lt;PhysicsBodyComponent&gt;"]
    
    ComponentMap --> EntitySparseSet1
    ComponentMap --> EntitySparseSet2
    ComponentMap --> EntitySparseSet3
    
    RenderData["RenderData<br/>GPU-friendly buffers<br/>worldTransforms, lights, meshes"]
    
    World --> RenderData
    
    Systems["Systems<br/>ScriptSystem<br/>AnimatorSystem<br/>PhysicsLinkSystem"]
    
    TaskGraph --> Systems
    
    style World fill:#f9f9f9
    style ComponentMap fill:#f9f9f9
    style EntitySparseSet1 fill:#f9f9f9
```

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/World.hpp:156-285](), [src/World.cpp:54-74]()

---

## Entity Management

### Entity Structure

Entities are represented by the `entity_t` type (alias for `EntityHandle`), a packed structure containing:

| Field | Bits | Purpose |
|-------|------|---------|
| `id` | 24 | Unique entity identifier within the world |
| `version` | 8 | Incremented on reuse to detect stale handles |

```mermaid
graph LR
    Entity["Entity<br/>entity_t id<br/>World* world"]
    
    EntityHandle["EntityHandle<br/>id: 24 bits<br/>version: 8 bits"]
    
    EntityPool["Entity Pool<br/>Queue&lt;entity_id_t&gt; available<br/>Vector&lt;uint8_t&gt; versions"]
    
    Entity --> EntityHandle
    Entity -.references.-> EntityPool
    
    Create["World::Spawn&lt;T&gt;()"]
    Destroy["World::DestroyEntity()"]
    
    Create -->|allocates from| EntityPool
    Destroy -->|returns to| EntityPool
    
    Version["Version Tracking<br/>CorrectVersion(entity_t)"]
    
    EntityPool --> Version
```

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/Types.hpp:10-22](), [include/RavEngine/Entity.hpp:11-92]()

### Entity Creation

Entities are created through `World::Spawn<T>()` which returns an `Entity` handle:

```cpp
// From World.hpp
template<typename T, typename ... A>
Entity Spawn(A&& ... args);
```

The process:

1. **Allocate ID**: Dequeue from `available` queue or increment `numEntities` ([include/RavEngine/World.hpp:687-703]())
2. **Version Assignment**: Assign version from `versions` vector
3. **Component Initialization**: Call `T::Create()` with the entity handle
4. **Render Data Setup**: For non-server builds, initialize per-entity render data ([src/World.cpp:531-541]())

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/World.hpp:687-720](), [src/World.cpp:531-541]()

### Entity Destruction

Entities are destroyed via `DestroyEntity(entity_t)`:

1. **Component Cleanup**: Iterate all component sparse sets and destroy matching components ([include/RavEngine/World.hpp:722-730]())
2. **Version Increment**: Increment version to invalidate existing handles
3. **ID Return**: Enqueue ID to `available` queue for reuse

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/World.hpp:722-736]()

---

## Component Storage Architecture

### Sparse Set Implementation

Each component type is stored in an `EntitySparseSet<T>` with three internal containers:

```mermaid
graph TB
    subgraph "EntitySparseSet&lt;Transform&gt;"
        Dense["dense_set<br/>unordered_vector&lt;Transform&gt;<br/>Contiguous component data"]
        Aux["aux_set<br/>UnorderedVector&lt;entity_id_t&gt;<br/>Owner IDs (parallel to dense)"]
        Sparse["sparse_set<br/>Vector&lt;entity_id_t&gt;<br/>Maps entity ID to dense index"]
    end
    
    EntityID["Entity ID: 42"]
    
    EntityID -->|lookup| Sparse
    Sparse -->|"sparse[42] = 3"| Dense
    Sparse -->|index 3| Aux
    Dense -->|"dense[3]"| Component["Transform Component"]
    Aux -->|"aux[3] = 42"| OwnerID["Owner ID"]
    
    Add["Emplace(entity_id, args...)"]
    Remove["Destroy(entity_id)"]
    Query["GetComponent(entity_id)"]
    
    Add -.->|O(1) amortized| Dense
    Remove -.->|O(1) swap-and-pop| Dense
    Query -.->|O(1) lookup| Sparse
    
    style Dense fill:#f9f9f9
    style Sparse fill:#f9f9f9
    style Aux fill:#f9f9f9
```

**Implementation Details:**

- **Sparse Lookup**: `sparse_set[entity_id]` yields dense index (O(1))
- **Dense Iteration**: `dense_set` provides cache-friendly iteration
- **Auxiliary Data**: `aux_set` maintains owner mapping parallel to `dense_set`
- **Removal**: Swap-and-pop with sparse set update ([include/RavEngine/World.hpp:210-228]())

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/World.hpp:188-284]()

### Component Operations

| Operation | Method | Time Complexity |
|-----------|--------|-----------------|
| Add | `World::EmplaceComponent<T>(entity_t, args...)` | O(1) amortized |
| Remove | `World::DestroyComponent<T>(entity_t)` | O(1) |
| Query | `World::GetComponent<T>(entity_t)` | O(1) |
| Has | `World::HasComponent<T>(entity_t)` | O(1) |
| Iterate All | `World::GetAllComponentsOfType<T>()` | O(n) over components |

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/World.hpp:738-841]()

### Type-Erased Storage

Components are stored in `AnySparseSet` wrappers within a hash map keyed by compile-time type ID (CTTI):

```cpp
locked_node_hashmap<RavEngine::ctti_t, AnySparseSet, SpinLock> componentMap;
```

Each `AnySparseSet` contains:
- Fixed-size buffer holding the `EntitySparseSet<T>` instance
- Type-erased destruction and deallocation functions

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/World.hpp:286-325](), [include/RavEngine/World.hpp:327]()

---

## Component Queries and Filtering

### Filter Method

The primary query mechanism is `World::Filter()` which accepts a lambda with component parameters:

```cpp
// From World.hpp
template<typename func_t>
inline void Filter(const func_t& function);
```

**Example Usage:**
```cpp
world->Filter([](const Transform& transform, StaticMesh& mesh) {
    // Called for each entity with both Transform AND StaticMesh
});
```

**Query Resolution Process:**

```mermaid
graph TD
    Start["Filter(lambda)"]
    ExtractTypes["Extract parameter types<br/>using callable_traits"]
    
    Start --> ExtractTypes
    
    FindSmallest["Find smallest component set<br/>iterate all parameter types"]
    ExtractTypes --> FindSmallest
    
    IterateSmallest["Iterate smallest set<br/>for each dense index"]
    FindSmallest --> IterateSmallest
    
    CheckOthers["Check entity has all other types<br/>HasComponent&lt;T&gt;() for each"]
    IterateSmallest --> CheckOthers
    
    Invoke{All present?}
    CheckOthers --> Invoke
    
    InvokeYes["Invoke lambda with<br/>GetComponent&lt;T&gt;() results"]
    InvokeNo["Skip entity"]
    
    Invoke -->|Yes| InvokeYes
    Invoke -->|No| InvokeNo
    
    InvokeYes --> IterateSmallest
    InvokeNo --> IterateSmallest
    
    style FindSmallest fill:#f9f9f9
    style CheckOthers fill:#f9f9f9
```

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/World.hpp:931-1005]()

### Query Optimization

The `Filter` implementation optimizes by:
1. **Smallest Set First**: Iterates the smallest component set to minimize checks
2. **Early Exit**: Skips entities missing any required component
3. **Cache-Friendly**: Dense iteration maintains spatial locality

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/World.hpp:931-1005]()

---

## System Execution and Task Graph

### Task Graph Structure

`World` organizes systems into a Taskflow graph with three main task groups:

```mermaid
graph TB
    MasterTasks["masterTasks<br/>tf::Taskflow"]
    
    ECSTasks["ECSTasks<br/>System execution"]
    RenderTasks["renderTasks<br/>Render data sync"]
    AudioTasks["audioTasks<br/>Audio snapshot"]
    
    MasterTasks --> ECSTasks
    MasterTasks --> RenderTasks
    MasterTasks --> AudioTasks
    
    subgraph "ECS Systems (Parallel)"
        Script["ScriptSystem"]
        Animator["AnimatorSystem"]
        PhysicsWrite["PhysicsLinkSystemWrite"]
        PhysicsRead["PhysicsLinkSystemRead"]
        PhysicsExec["PhysX Execute"]
        Socket["SocketSystem"]
    end
    
    ECSTasks --> Script
    ECSTasks --> Animator
    ECSTasks --> PhysicsWrite
    ECSTasks --> PhysicsRead
    ECSTasks --> PhysicsExec
    ECSTasks --> Socket
    
    PhysicsWrite --> PhysicsExec
    PhysicsExec --> PhysicsRead
    PhysicsRead --> Animator
    Animator --> Script
    Animator --> Socket
    
    subgraph "Render Tasks (Parallel)"
        ResizeBuffer["Resize worldTransforms buffer"]
        UpdateStatic["Update StaticMesh transforms"]
        UpdateSkinned["Update SkinnedMesh transforms"]
        UpdateLights["Update light data"]
    end
    
    RenderTasks --> ResizeBuffer
    ResizeBuffer --> UpdateStatic
    ResizeBuffer --> UpdateSkinned
    ResizeBuffer --> UpdateLights
    
    AudioTasks -.->|runs after| ECSTasks
    
    style ECSTasks fill:#f9f9f9
    style RenderTasks fill:#f9f9f9
```

**Sources:** [src/World.cpp:150-303](), [include/RavEngine/World.hpp:1186-1269]()

### System Registration

Systems are registered using `EmplaceSystem<T>()` or `EmplacePolymorphicSystem<T>()`:

```cpp
// From World.cpp
EmplacePolymorphicSystem<ScriptSystem>();
EmplaceSystem<AnimatorSystem>();
CreateDependency<AnimatorSystem, ScriptSystem>();  // Animator runs before Script
```

**System Types:**

| Method | Purpose | Example |
|--------|---------|---------|
| `EmplaceSystem<T>()` | Concrete system with known query types | `AnimatorSystem` |
| `EmplacePolymorphicSystem<T>()` | System querying polymorphic components | `ScriptSystem` |
| `EmplaceSerialSystem<T>()` | System that must run serially | `SocketSystem` |

**Sources:** [src/World.cpp:77-86](), [include/RavEngine/World.hpp:1186-1269]()

### Tick Execution

The `World::Tick()` method executes the task graph each frame:

1. **PreTick**: Prepare frame (check systems graph)
2. **TickECS**: Execute ECS systems via Taskflow
3. **PostTick**: Cleanup operations
4. **RenderTasks**: Synchronize render data (parallel)

**Sources:** [src/World.cpp:54-74]()

---

## Polymorphic Components

### Polymorphic Component System

RavEngine supports component inheritance through `PolymorphicIndirection`:

```mermaid
graph TB
    Entity["Entity<br/>ID: 42"]
    
    PolyMap["SparseSetForPolymorphic<br/>Maps entity to PolymorphicIndirection"]
    
    PolyIndirection["PolymorphicIndirection<br/>entity: 42<br/>world: ptr"]
    
    Entity --> PolyMap
    PolyMap --> PolyIndirection
    
    Elt1["elt<br/>full_id: CTTI&lt;BoxCollider&gt;<br/>getfn: lambda"]
    Elt2["elt<br/>full_id: CTTI&lt;SphereCollider&gt;<br/>getfn: lambda"]
    
    PolyIndirection --> Elt1
    PolyIndirection --> Elt2
    
    BoxSet["EntitySparseSet&lt;BoxCollider&gt;"]
    SphereSet["EntitySparseSet&lt;SphereCollider&gt;"]
    
    Elt1 -.->|retrieves from| BoxSet
    Elt2 -.->|retrieves from| SphereSet
    
    Query["GetAllComponentsPolymorphic&lt;PhysicsCollider&gt;()"]
    Query --> PolyIndirection
    
    style PolyIndirection fill:#f9f9f9
```

**Usage Example:**
```cpp
// Entity has both BoxCollider and SphereCollider (both inherit PhysicsCollider)
auto colliders = entity.GetAllComponentsPolymorphic<PhysicsCollider>();
for (auto& elt : colliders) {
    auto* collider = elt.Get<PhysicsCollider>(entity.GetID());
    // Use polymorphic interface
}
```

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/World.hpp:474-557](), [include/RavEngine/World.hpp:560-625]()

### Queryable System

Components can be made queryable by inheriting from `Queryable<T>` or `QueryableDelta<Base, Derived>`:

```cpp
// From PhysicsBodyComponent.hpp
class PhysicsBodyComponent : public Queryable<PhysicsBodyComponent> { ... };
class RigidBodyDynamicComponent : public QueryableDelta<PhysicsBodyComponent, RigidBodyDynamicComponent> { ... };
```

This enables polymorphic queries while maintaining type information.

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/PhysicsBodyComponent.hpp:38-48](), [include/RavEngine/PhysicsBodyComponent.hpp:236-243]()

## Render Data Synchronization

The `World::RenderData` structure maintains GPU-friendly copies of component data for rendering:

```mermaid
    Transforms["worldTransforms<br/>BufferedVRAMVector&lt;matrix4&gt;<br/>Indexed by entity ID"]
    DirLights["directionalLightData<br/>BufferedVRAMSparseSet&lt;DirLightUploadData&gt;"]
    PointLights["pointLightData<br/>BufferedVRAMSparseSet&lt;PointLightUploadData&gt;"]
    SpotLights["spotLightData<br/>BufferedVRAMSparseSet&lt;SpotLightDataUpload&gt;"]
    AmbientLights["ambientLightData<br/>BufferedVRAMSparseSet&lt;AmbientLightUploadData&gt;"]
    
    RenderData --> Transforms
    RenderData --> DirLights
    RenderData --> PointLights
    RenderData --> SpotLights
    RenderData --> AmbientLights

    style RenderData fill:#f9f9f9

```

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/World.hpp:419-449]()

### Synchronization Process

Render data synchronization occurs in the `renderTasks` task graph:

**Transform Synchronization:**
```mermaid
graph LR
    Component["Transform Component<br/>isTickDirty = true"]
    
    Check{Transform dirty?}
    
    Component --> Check
    
    Update["renderData.worldTransforms<br/>SetValueAt(entityID, matrix)"]
    ClearFlag["transform.ClearTickDirty()"]
    Skip["Skip update"]
    
    Check -->|Yes| Update
    Check -->|No| Skip
    Update --> ClearFlag
    
    BufferSync["BufferedVRAMVector::EncodeSync()<br/>Copy staging to GPU buffer"]
    
    Update -.->|later| BufferSync
    
    style Update fill:#f9f9f9
```

**Sources:** [src/World.cpp:311-391](), [src/World.cpp:392-520]()

### Dirty Flag Tracking

Components use dirty flags to minimize synchronization overhead:

- `Transform::isTickDirty` - Set when transform changes during current tick
- Cleared after synchronization to render data
- Lights use `isInvalidated()` for color/intensity changes

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/Transform.hpp:32-52](), [src/World.cpp:392-427]()

---

## Component Lifecycle Hooks

### Destroy Hook

Components can implement a `Destroy()` method called during component removal:

```cpp
// From World.hpp EntitySparseSet::Destroy
if constexpr(HasDestroy<T>::value){
    auto& oldvalue = GetComponent(local_id);
    oldvalue.Destroy();
}
```

**Example: PhysicsBodyComponent**
```cpp
void PhysicsBodyComponent::Destroy(){
    if (rigidActor != nullptr) {
        e.GetWorld()->Solver->Destroy(*this);
        rigidActor->release();
        // Notify receivers
        for (auto& receiver : receivers) {
            receiver->OnUnregisterBody(otherwayHandle);
        }
    }
}
```

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/World.hpp:213-217](), [src/PhysicsBodyComponent.cpp:36-49]()

---

## World Tick Phases

The `World::Tick()` method executes in four distinct phases:

| Phase | Method | Purpose | Threading |
|-------|--------|---------|-----------|
| **PreTick** | `PreTick(float)` | Check system graph, prepare frame | Serial |
| **TickECS** | `TickECS(float)` | Execute all ECS systems | Parallel (Taskflow) |
| **PostTick** | `PostTick(float)` | Cleanup operations | Serial |
| **Render Sync** | Execute `renderTasks` | Synchronize GPU data | Parallel (Taskflow) |

**Sources:** [src/World.cpp:54-74]()

---

## Best Practices

### Component Design
- Keep components data-focused with minimal logic
- Implement `Destroy()` for cleanup requiring world access
- Use `ComponentWithOwner` base class for entity reference
- Mark components as `Queryable<T>` for polymorphic queries

### System Design
- Use `CreateDependency<A, B>()` to define execution order
- Prefer parallel systems over serial when possible
- Keep system `Tick()` methods stateless
- Use `Filter()` for efficient component queries

### Performance
- Minimize component size for cache efficiency
- Batch entity creation/destruction when possible
- Use dirty flags to avoid unnecessary updates
- Leverage sparse set O(1) lookups

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/World.hpp:1186-1269](), [src/World.cpp:150-303]()1f:T3d1f,# Transform and Scene Hierarchy

</details>



## Purpose and Scope

This document covers the **Transform** component system in RavEngine, which manages the spatial properties (position, rotation, scale) of entities and their hierarchical relationships within a scene graph. The Transform system provides both local (parent-relative) and world (absolute) coordinate space operations, implements efficient dirty flag propagation for render synchronization, and maintains parent-child relationships for complex object hierarchies.

For information about the broader Entity Component System architecture, see [Entity Component System](#3.2). For Transform integration with physics simulation, see [Physics Simulation and Events](#5.2). For skeletal animation's use of Transform hierarchies, see [Animation Components and Assets](#6.1).

**Sources**: [include/RavEngine/Transform.hpp:1-346]()

---

## Transform Component Fundamentals

The `Transform` component ([include/RavEngine/Transform.hpp:20]()) is the fundamental spatial representation for entities in RavEngine. It inherits from `ComponentWithOwner` to maintain entity ownership and `Queryable<Transform>` to enable efficient queries.

### Data Structure

The Transform stores the following core data members:

| Member | Type | Purpose |
|--------|------|---------|
| `position` | `vector3` | Local (parent-relative) position |
| `rotation` | `quaternion` | Local (parent-relative) rotation |
| `scale` | `vector3` | Local (parent-relative) scale |
| `matrix` | `matrix4` | Cached parent's world-space transformation matrix |
| `parent` | `ComponentHandle<Transform>` | Non-owning reference to parent transform |
| `children` | `UnorderedVector<ComponentHandle<Transform>>` | Non-owning references to child transforms |
| `isDirty` | `bool` (bitfield) | Indicates hierarchy changes requiring recalculation |
| `isTickDirty` | `bool` (bitfield) | Indicates changes within current tick requiring GPU sync |

The struct is carefully ordered for optimal memory layout on 64-bit architectures, with static assertions verifying padding efficiency ([include/RavEngine/Transform.hpp:36-41]()).

```mermaid
graph TB
    subgraph Transform["Transform Component Structure"]
        Owner["Entity owner<br/>(ComponentWithOwner)"]
        LocalData["Local Properties:<br/>vector3 position<br/>quaternion rotation<br/>vector3 scale"]
        Hierarchy["Hierarchy Data:<br/>ComponentHandle&lt;Transform&gt; parent<br/>UnorderedVector&lt;...&gt; children"]
        Cache["Cached Data:<br/>matrix4 matrix<br/>(parent's world matrix)"]
        DirtyFlags["Dirty Flags:<br/>bool isDirty<br/>bool isTickDirty"]
    end
    
    Owner --> LocalData
    LocalData --> Hierarchy
    Hierarchy --> Cache
    Cache --> DirtyFlags
```

**Diagram**: Transform Component Memory Layout

**Sources**: [include/RavEngine/Transform.hpp:20-41]()

---

## Coordinate Spaces

RavEngine distinguishes between **local (parent-relative)** and **world (absolute)** coordinate spaces, providing API methods for both.

### Local Space

Local space properties define a transform's position, rotation, and scale relative to its parent. If a transform has no parent, local space is equivalent to world space.

**Key methods**:
- `SetLocalPosition(const vector3&)` ([include/RavEngine/Transform.hpp:221-226]())
- `SetLocalRotation(const quaternion&)` ([include/RavEngine/Transform.hpp:251-255]())
- `SetLocalScale(const vector3&)` ([include/RavEngine/Transform.hpp:291-295]())
- `GetLocalPosition()` ([include/RavEngine/Transform.hpp:303-306]())
- `GetLocalRotation()` ([include/RavEngine/Transform.hpp:308-311]())
- `GetLocalScale()` ([include/RavEngine/Transform.hpp:313-316]())

### World Space

World space properties represent absolute positions and rotations in the scene. Setting world properties when a parent exists requires inverse transformation calculations.

**Key methods**:
- `SetWorldPosition(const vector3&)` ([include/RavEngine/Transform.hpp:232-245]())
- `SetWorldRotation(const quaternion&)` ([include/RavEngine/Transform.hpp:272-285]())
- `GetWorldPosition()` ([include/RavEngine/Transform.hpp:327-334]())
- `GetWorldRotation()` ([include/RavEngine/Transform.hpp:336-345]())

```mermaid
graph LR
    subgraph LocalSpace["Local Space"]
        LP["position"]
        LR["rotation"]
        LS["scale"]
    end
    
    subgraph MatrixGen["Matrix Generation"]
        GLM["GenerateLocalMatrix():<br/>T * R * S"]
    end
    
    subgraph ParentMatrix["Parent Transform"]
        PM["matrix<br/>(parent world matrix)"]
    end
    
    subgraph WorldSpace["World Space"]
        WM["GetWorldMatrix():<br/>parent.matrix *<br/>GenerateLocalMatrix()"]
        WP["GetWorldPosition()"]
        WR["GetWorldRotation()"]
    end
    
    LP --> GLM
    LR --> GLM
    LS --> GLM
    
    PM --> WM
    GLM --> WM
    
    WM --> WP
    WM --> WR
```

**Diagram**: Local to World Space Transformation

The `GenerateLocalMatrix()` method ([include/RavEngine/Transform.hpp:164-166]()) constructs a transformation matrix using standard **Translation Ã— Rotation Ã— Scale** composition:

```
matrix = translate(position) * toMat4(rotation) * scale(scale)
```

The `GetWorldMatrix()` method ([include/RavEngine/Transform.hpp:128-130]()) multiplies the parent's cached world matrix by the local matrix:

```
worldMatrix = matrix * GenerateLocalMatrix()
```

**Note**: The `matrix` member variable stores the **parent's world transformation**, not this transform's world transformation. This design optimizes hierarchy updates.

**Sources**: [include/RavEngine/Transform.hpp:128-130](), [include/RavEngine/Transform.hpp:164-166](), [include/RavEngine/Transform.hpp:221-245](), [include/RavEngine/Transform.hpp:272-285](), [include/RavEngine/Transform.hpp:327-345]()

---

## Scene Hierarchy Management

The Transform system implements a parent-child hierarchy where children maintain references to their parent and parents maintain lists of children. This bidirectional relationship enables efficient traversal and update propagation.

### Adding Children

The `AddChild(ComponentHandle<Transform>)` method ([src/Transform.cpp:10-23]()) establishes a parent-child relationship while preserving the child's world-space position and rotation:

1. Captures child's current world position and rotation
2. Sets child's `parent` reference to this transform
3. Inserts child into this transform's `children` list
4. Updates child's cached `matrix` to this transform's world matrix
5. Restores child's world position and rotation (adjusting local values accordingly)

```mermaid
sequenceDiagram
    participant Parent as "Parent Transform"
    participant Child as "Child Transform"
    
    Parent->>Child: "AddChild(child)"
    activate Parent
    
    Child->>Child: "worldPos = GetWorldPosition()"
    Child->>Child: "worldRot = GetWorldRotation()"
    
    Parent->>Child: "child.parent = this"
    Parent->>Parent: "children.insert(child)"
    Parent->>Child: "child.matrix = GetWorldMatrix()"
    
    Child->>Child: "SetWorldPosition(worldPos)"
    Child->>Child: "SetWorldRotation(worldRot)"
    
    deactivate Parent
```

**Diagram**: AddChild Operation Sequence

### Removing Children

The `RemoveChild(ComponentHandle<Transform>)` method ([src/Transform.cpp:25-36]()) performs the inverse operation:

1. Captures child's world position and rotation
2. Clears child's `parent` reference
3. Removes child from this transform's `children` list
4. Resets child's cached `matrix` to identity
5. Restores child's world position and rotation (now as local values)

**Sources**: [src/Transform.cpp:10-36]()

---

## Dirty Flag Propagation System

The Transform system uses two distinct dirty flags to optimize synchronization with rendering and other systems:

| Flag | Purpose | Cleared By |
|------|---------|-----------|
| `isDirty` | Indicates hierarchy structure changes requiring matrix recalculation | Never cleared (used for recalculation checks) |
| `isTickDirty` | Indicates changes within current tick requiring GPU buffer update | World's render data synchronization ([include/RavEngine/Transform.hpp:50-52]()) |

### Update Propagation

Any modification to a transform's position, rotation, or scale triggers `UpdateChildren()` ([include/RavEngine/Transform.hpp:54-70]()), which:

1. Calls `MarkAsDirty()` ([include/RavEngine/Transform.hpp:45-48]()) to set both dirty flags
2. If children exist, recursively updates all descendants
3. For each child:
   - Marks child as dirty
   - Recalculates this transform's world matrix
   - Updates child's cached parent matrix
   - Recursively processes child's children

```mermaid
graph TD
    Modify["Transform Modification<br/>(SetLocalPosition, etc)"]
    UpdateChildren["UpdateChildren()"]
    MarkDirty["MarkAsDirty():<br/>isDirty = true<br/>isTickDirty = true"]
    HasChildren{"children.size() > 0?"}
    RecursiveUpdate["For each child:<br/>1. child.MarkAsDirty()<br/>2. newMatrix = GetWorldMatrix()<br/>3. child.matrix = newMatrix<br/>4. Recurse into child"]
    Done["Complete"]
    
    Modify --> UpdateChildren
    UpdateChildren --> MarkDirty
    MarkDirty --> HasChildren
    HasChildren -->|Yes| RecursiveUpdate
    HasChildren -->|No| Done
    RecursiveUpdate --> RecursiveUpdate
    RecursiveUpdate --> Done
```

**Diagram**: Dirty Flag Propagation Flow

The recursive update uses a lambda function with self-reference ([include/RavEngine/Transform.hpp:58-68]()) to traverse the hierarchy efficiently.

### Tick Dirty Flag Usage

The `isTickDirty` flag enables the World to identify transforms that have been modified during the current frame and require GPU buffer synchronization. The `getTickDirty()` accessor ([include/RavEngine/Transform.hpp:73-75]()) exposes this state, while `ClearTickDirty()` ([include/RavEngine/Transform.hpp:50-52]()) resets it after synchronization.

**Sources**: [include/RavEngine/Transform.hpp:45-75]()

---

## Common Transform Operations

### Delta Operations

Delta methods apply incremental changes to existing values:

- `LocalTranslateDelta(const vector3&)` ([include/RavEngine/Transform.hpp:205-210]()): Adds offset to local position
- `WorldTranslateDelta(const vector3&)` ([include/RavEngine/Transform.hpp:212-215]()): Adds offset to world position
- `LocalRotateDelta(const quaternion&)` ([include/RavEngine/Transform.hpp:261-266]()): Multiplies local rotation
- `LocalScaleDelta(const vector3&)` ([include/RavEngine/Transform.hpp:297-301]()): Adds offset to local scale

### Directional Vectors

Transforms provide convenience methods to retrieve directional vectors in both local and world space:

**Local space** (relative to parent):
- `Forward()` ([include/RavEngine/Transform.hpp:171-173]()): Returns local forward direction (`rotation * vector3_forward`)
- `Right()` ([include/RavEngine/Transform.hpp:185-187]()): Returns local right direction (`rotation * vector3_right`)
- `Up()` ([include/RavEngine/Transform.hpp:178-180]()): Returns local up direction (`rotation * vector3_up`)

**World space**:
- `WorldForward()` ([include/RavEngine/Transform.hpp:189-191]()): Returns world forward direction
- `WorldRight()` ([include/RavEngine/Transform.hpp:193-195]()): Returns world right direction
- `WorldUp()` ([include/RavEngine/Transform.hpp:197-199]()): Returns world up direction

These methods are particularly useful for character controllers, camera systems, and physics forces.

**Sources**: [include/RavEngine/Transform.hpp:171-199](), [include/RavEngine/Transform.hpp:205-301]()

---

## Hierarchy Query and Destruction

### Parent Checking

The `HasParent()` method ([include/RavEngine/Transform.hpp:108-110]()) checks if the transform has a valid parent reference:

```
bool hasParent = transform.HasParent();  // Returns parent.IsValid()
```

### Child Access

The `GetChildren()` method ([include/RavEngine/Transform.hpp:148-150]()) provides read-only access to the children collection:

```
const auto& children = transform.GetChildren();
```

### Recursive Destruction

The `Destroy()` method ([include/RavEngine/Transform.hpp:153-157]()) recursively destroys all child entities:

```cpp
void Transform::Destroy() {
    for(auto& child : children) {
        child.GetOwner().Destroy();  // Destroys child entity and all its components
    }
}
```

This enables easy cleanup of entire object hierarchies.

**Sources**: [include/RavEngine/Transform.hpp:108-157]()

---

## Integration with Other Systems

### Rendering System Integration

The `isTickDirty` flag integrates with the World's render data structures (see [Render Data Synchronization](#9.3)) to minimize GPU buffer updates. Only transforms marked as tick-dirty require synchronization to the `worldTransforms` buffer.

```mermaid
graph LR
    Transform["Transform Component"]
    TickDirty["isTickDirty flag"]
    WorldRenderData["World::RenderData"]
    WorldTransforms["BufferedVRAMVector<br/>worldTransforms"]
    GPU["GPU Buffers"]
    
    Transform --> TickDirty
    TickDirty -->|"if true"| WorldRenderData
    WorldRenderData --> WorldTransforms
    WorldTransforms --> GPU
    TickDirty -->|"ClearTickDirty()"| Transform
```

**Diagram**: Transform to Render Data Pipeline

### Physics System Integration

Physics bodies (see [Physics Bodies and Colliders](#5.1)) read Transform positions and rotations during simulation. After physics simulation, the `PhysicsSolver` writes back updated positions to Transform components, triggering dirty flag propagation.

### Animation System Integration

The `AnimatorComponent` is declared as a friend of Transform ([include/RavEngine/Transform.hpp:21]()) to enable direct matrix manipulation during skeletal animation. Socket attachments use the hierarchy system to bind entities to specific bones in animated skeletons (see [Animation Components and Assets](#6.1)).

The `_SetMatrix()` protected method ([include/RavEngine/Transform.hpp:24-27]()) allows AnimatorComponent to directly update the parent matrix cache without triggering normal update paths:

```cpp
void Transform::_SetMatrix(const matrix4& m) {
    matrix = m;
    UpdateChildren();
}
```

**Sources**: [include/RavEngine/Transform.hpp:21-27](), [include/RavEngine/Transform.hpp:32-33](), [include/RavEngine/Transform.hpp:45-52]()

---

## Best Practices and Performance Considerations

### Minimize Hierarchy Depth

Deep hierarchies amplify update costs during dirty propagation. Each level multiplies the number of matrix recalculations. Consider flattening hierarchies where possible or caching intermediate results for frequently-queried transforms.

### Batch Modifications

When setting multiple properties (position, rotation, scale), consider the order of operations to minimize dirty propagation overhead. Each setter triggers `UpdateChildren()`, so batching related changes can reduce redundant traversals.

### World vs Local Space

Use local space operations when working with parented objects to maintain expected behavior. Use world space operations when dealing with absolute positioning (e.g., teleportation, camera placement).

### Constructor Defaults

The default Transform constructor ([include/RavEngine/Transform.hpp:82]()) initializes to origin position (0,0,0), identity rotation, and unit scale (1,1,1). A parameterized constructor ([include/RavEngine/Transform.hpp:77-81]()) allows explicit initialization.

**Sources**: [include/RavEngine/Transform.hpp:77-82]()20:T5b3a,# Input System

The Input System provides cross-platform input handling for keyboard, mouse, and gamepad devices. It implements an action/axis mapping system that allows decoupling hardware input codes from game logic through named bindings. The system processes SDL3 events each frame, routes them through user-defined mappings, and invokes bound callbacks.

For information about GUI-specific input handling, see [User Interface](#8). For general application lifecycle and event processing, see [Application Lifecycle](#3.1).

## Architecture Overview

The Input System consists of three primary components: `InputManager` for binding management and event routing, `IInputListener` for global input observation, and SDL3 integration for cross-platform device abstraction.

```mermaid

        Gamepad["Gamepad Events<br/>SDL_EVENT_GAMEPAD_*"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Core Input System"
        InputMgr["InputManager<br/>include/RavEngine/InputManager.hpp"]
        ProcessInput["ProcessInput()<br/>src/InputManager.cpp:130"]
        ProcessActionID["ProcessActionID()<br/>Maps codes to actions"]
        ProcessAxisID["ProcessAxisID()<br/>Buffers axis values"]
        TickAxes["TickAxes()<br/>Dispatches buffered axes"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Mapping Tables"
        CodeToAction["CodeToAction<br/>locked_hashmap<int, set<string>>"]
        CodeToAxis["CodeToAxis<br/>locked_hashmap<int, set<AxisID>>"]
        ActionBindings["ActionBindings<br/>locked_hashmap<string, list<ActionBinding>>"]
```

## Input Processing Flow

Each frame, the `App` main loop polls SDL3 events and forwards them to `InputManager::ProcessInput`. The system distinguishes between **actions** (binary pressed/released states) and **axes** (continuous float values). Actions execute callbacks immediately, while axes buffer their values and dispatch them during `TickAxes` to accumulate multiple inputs per frame.

```mermaid
graph TD
    Start["App::Tick<br/>src/App_priv.hpp:354"]
    PollEvents["SDL_PollEvent loop<br/>src/App_priv.hpp:300"]
    
    KeyEvent{Event Type?}
    
    ProcessInputCall["inputManager->ProcessInput()<br/>src/App_priv.hpp:321"]
    TickAxesCall["inputManager->TickAxes()<br/>src/App_priv.hpp:367"]
    
    ProcessInput["ProcessInput()<br/>src/InputManager.cpp:130"]
    
    KeyDown["SDL_EVENT_KEY_DOWN/UP<br/>scancode event"]
    MouseButton["SDL_EVENT_MOUSE_BUTTON_*<br/>button event"]
    MouseMotion["SDL_EVENT_MOUSE_MOTION<br/>position + velocity"]
    MouseWheel["SDL_EVENT_MOUSE_WHEEL<br/>scroll delta"]
    GamepadButton["SDL_EVENT_GAMEPAD_BUTTON_*<br/>button + controller ID"]
    GamepadAxis["SDL_EVENT_GAMEPAD_AXIS_MOTION<br/>axis value + controller ID"]
    TextInput["SDL_EVENT_TEXT_INPUT<br/>UTF-8 string"]
    
    ProcessActionID["ProcessActionID()<br/>src/InputManager.cpp:30"]
    ProcessAxisID["ProcessAxisID()<br/>src/InputManager.cpp:56"]
    ProcessTextInput["ProcessTextInput()<br/>src/InputManager.cpp:99"]
    
    LookupAction["CodeToAction lookup<br/>Find action names"]
    LookupAxis["CodeToAxis lookup<br/>Find axis names"]
    
    BufferAxis["Buffer to AxisData<br/>bufferedInputs map"]
    ExecuteAction["Execute ActionBinding<br/>Invoke callbacks"]
    
    TickAxes["TickAxes()<br/>src/InputManager.cpp:67"]
    DispatchAxes["Dispatch buffered axes<br/>Execute AxisBinding"]
    ClearVelocity["Clear mouse velocity<br/>MOUSEMOVE_*VEL = 0"]
    
    Cleanup["CleanupBindings()<br/>Remove invalid bindings"]

    PollEvents --> KeyEvent

    KeyEvent -->|Mouse Button| MouseButton

    ProcessInput --> ProcessAxisID
    ProcessInput --> ProcessTextInput

    TickAxesCall --> TickAxes

```

## Action Mapping System

Actions represent discrete button presses and releases. Users create **action maps** that associate human-readable names with raw input codes, then **bind** member functions to those named actions with state and controller filters.

### Action Mapping Workflow

| Step | Method | Description |
|------|--------|-------------|
| 1. Create Mapping | `AddActionMap(name, ID)` | Associate name with SDL scancode/button ID |
| 2. Bind Callback | `BindAction(name, thisptr, &Class::method, state, controllers)` | Register member function for action |
| 3. Process Input | Automatic via `ProcessActionID` | System invokes callbacks when conditions match |
| 4. Unbind | `UnbindAction(name, thisptr, &Class::method, state, controllers)` | Remove binding |
| 5. Remove Mapping | `RemoveActionMap(name, ID)` | Delete action map entry |

### Action Binding Internals

The `ActionBinding` class stores callbacks with filtering criteria:

```mermaid
graph LR
    subgraph "ActionBinding Class"
        ActionBinding["ActionBinding<br/>include/RavEngine/InputManager.hpp:139"]
        FuncPtr["actionCallback func<br/>Function<void()>"]
        FuncAddr["void* func_addr<br/>For equality checks"]
        ID["size_t id<br/>Owner validity"]
        Controller["CID controller<br/>Bitmask filter"]
        State["ActionState state<br/>Pressed/Released"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Invocation Filter"
        OpCall["operator()<br/>line 161"]
        CheckState{"state_in == state?"}
        CheckController{"controller & c_in != NONE?"}
        CheckValid{"IsValid()?"}
        Execute["func()"]
    end
    
    ActionBinding --> FuncPtr
    ActionBinding --> FuncAddr
    ActionBinding --> ID
    ActionBinding --> Controller
    ActionBinding --> State
    
    OpCall --> CheckState
    CheckState -->|Yes| CheckController
    CheckState -->|No| Skip["Return"]
    CheckController -->|Yes| CheckValid
    CheckController -->|No| Skip
    CheckValid -->|Yes| Execute
    CheckValid -->|No| Skip
```

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/InputManager.hpp:139-179](), [src/InputManager.cpp:30-53]()

### Controller ID System

`CID` (Controller ID) is a bitmask enum supporting up to 16 simultaneous controllers. Each bit represents one controller, with `CID::ANY` matching all controllers. The system uses bitwise operations to filter inputs.

| CID Value | Bit Position | Usage |
|-----------|--------------|-------|
| `CID::C0` | `1 << 0` | Keyboard/Mouse (primary) |
| `CID::C1` | `1 << 1` | Gamepad slot 1 |
| `CID::C2` | `1 << 2` | Gamepad slot 2 |
| ... | ... | ... |
| `CID::C15` | `1 << 15` | Gamepad slot 15 |
| `CID::ANY` | `~0` | All controllers |

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/InputManager.hpp:80-131](), [src/InputManager.cpp:137-190]()

## Axis Mapping System

Axes represent continuous input values (mouse position, analog sticks, triggers). Unlike actions, axis values are **buffered** per frame and dispatched together during `TickAxes`, allowing accumulation of multiple sources (e.g., WASD keys mapped to movement axes).

### Axis Processing Pipeline

```mermaid
graph TB
    subgraph "Frame N Input Processing"
        Input1["Mouse Motion Event<br/>MOUSEMOVE_X = 0.5"]
        Input2["Gamepad Axis Event<br/>LEFT_AXIS_X = -0.3"]
        ProcessAxis1["ProcessAxisID(MOUSEMOVE_X)"]
        ProcessAxis2["ProcessAxisID(LEFT_AXIS_X)"]
        
        Lookup1["CodeToAxis[MOUSEMOVE_X]<br/>Returns {'CameraRotation', scale=1}"]
        Lookup2["CodeToAxis[LEFT_AXIS_X]<br/>Returns {'Movement', scale=1}"]
        
        Buffer1["AxisBindings['CameraRotation']<br/>bufferedInputs[MOUSEMOVE_X] = {0.5, C0}"]
        Buffer2["AxisBindings['Movement']<br/>bufferedInputs[LEFT_AXIS_X] = {-0.3, C1}"]
    end
    
    subgraph "TickAxes Dispatch"
        TickStart["TickAxes()<br/>src/InputManager.cpp:67"]
        ForEachBinding["for binding in AxisBindings"]
        ForEachBuffered["for buffered in bufferedInputs"]
        
        ApplyDeadzone{"abs(value) >= deadzone?"}
        InvokeCallback["AxisBinding::operator()<br/>Pass value to user callback"]
        PassZero["Pass 0.0"]
        
        ClearVelocities["Clear MOUSEMOVE_*VEL<br/>Clear MOUSEWHEEL_*"]
    end
    
    Input1 --> ProcessAxis1
    Input2 --> ProcessAxis2
    
    ProcessAxis1 --> Lookup1
    ProcessAxis2 --> Lookup2
    
    Lookup1 --> Buffer1
    Lookup2 --> Buffer2
    
    Buffer1 --> TickStart
    Buffer2 --> TickStart
    
    TickStart --> ForEachBinding
    ForEachBinding --> ForEachBuffered
    ForEachBuffered --> ApplyDeadzone
    ApplyDeadzone -->|Yes| InvokeCallback
    ApplyDeadzone -->|No| PassZero
    InvokeCallback --> ClearVelocities
    PassZero --> ClearVelocities
```

**Sources:** [src/InputManager.cpp:56-97](), [include/RavEngine/InputManager.hpp:181-219]()

### Axis Binding Configuration

The `AxisBinding` class supports deadzones and scale factors:

| Field | Type | Purpose |
|-------|------|---------|
| `func` | `axisCallback` | Lambda capturing member function |
| `func_addr` | `void*` | Original function pointer for equality |
| `id` | `size_t` | Owner object ID for validity checking |
| `controller` | `CID` | Controller bitmask filter |
| `deadzone` | `float` | Minimum absolute value to trigger callback |

The `CodeToAxis` map stores `AxisID` structs with per-mapping scale factors, allowing input inversion (e.g., `scale = -1` for inverted Y axis).

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/InputManager.hpp:227-243](), [include/RavEngine/InputManager.hpp:356-364]()

## Special Input Codes

The system defines special input codes for inputs that don't map directly to SDL scancodes. These use negative integer values to avoid collision with SDL constants.

### Mouse Input Processing

Mouse events receive special handling to provide both absolute position (normalized to `[0,1]`) and velocity (frame delta):

- `SDL_EVENT_MOUSE_MOTION` generates 4 axis events:
  - `MOUSEMOVE_X/Y`: Position divided by window dimensions and DPI scale
  - `MOUSEMOVE_XVEL/YVEL`: Raw delta multiplied by inverse framerate scale
  
Mouse velocity axes are **automatically cleared** each frame during `TickAxes` to prevent stale velocity values.

**Sources:** [src/InputManager.cpp:140-152](), [src/InputManager.cpp:80-94](), [include/RavEngine/InputManager.hpp:23-34]()

### Gamepad Input Remapping

SDL3 provides gamepad axis values in different ranges depending on the axis type. The system normalizes these to consistent ranges:

| SDL Axis Type | SDL Range | Normalized Range |
|---------------|-----------|------------------|
| Left/Right Stick X/Y | `[SDL_JOYSTICK_AXIS_MIN, SDL_JOYSTICK_AXIS_MAX]` | `[-1, 1]` |
| Left/Right Trigger | `[0, SDL_JOYSTICK_AXIS_MAX]` | `[0, 1]` |

The controller ID offset is computed as: `Make_CID(event.gdevice.which + 1)`, mapping SDL device index to `CID` bitmask.

**Sources:** [src/InputManager.cpp:165-184](), [include/RavEngine/InputManager.hpp:60-71]()

## Input Listener Interface

The `IInputListener` interface provides global input observation without creating specific bindings. This is used internally by the GUI system to forward all inputs to RmlUi contexts.

The GUI system uses `AnyActionDown/Up` to maintain a modifier state bitmask (Ctrl, Shift, Alt, etc.) and forwards keyboard events to RmlUi. Mouse button events are also forwarded through this interface.

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/IInputListener.hpp:1-20](), [src/GUI.cpp:162-249](), [src/InputManager.cpp:41-52](), [src/InputManager.cpp:99-106]()

## Integration with Application Loop

The `App` class manages the `InputManager` lifecycle and invokes its methods each frame. Input processing occurs early in the frame, before world ticking.

### App Integration Points

| File | Line Range | Purpose |
|------|------------|---------|
| `include/RavEngine/App.hpp` | 171 | `Ref<InputManager> inputManager` member |
| `src/App_priv.hpp` | 298-327 | Event loop: SDL polling and input forwarding |
| `src/App_priv.hpp` | 320-325 | Forward SDL events to `inputManager->ProcessInput()` |
| `src/App_priv.hpp` | 364-368 | `inputManager->TickAxes()` after event processing |
| `src/App_priv.hpp` | 621 | `inputManager = nullptr` on shutdown |

### Frame Execution Order

1. **SDL Event Processing**: `SDL_PollEvent` loop retrieves platform events
2. **Input Processing**: `ProcessInput` routes events to action/axis systems
3. **Axis Dispatching**: `TickAxes` executes axis callbacks with accumulated values
4. **World Ticking**: User game logic executes with current input state
5. **Rendering**: Visual feedback for input-driven changes

**Sources:** [src/App_priv.hpp:298-370](), [include/RavEngine/App.hpp:171]()

## Example Usage Patterns

### Basic Action Binding

```cpp
// In World::OnActivate or similar initialization code
auto inputManager = GetApp()->inputManager;

// Create action map: "Jump" -> Spacebar
inputManager->AddActionMap("Jump", SDL_SCANCODE_SPACE);

// Bind to member function for keyboard/mouse (C0)
inputManager->BindAction("Jump", GetWeakThis(), &MyWorld::OnJump, 
                         ActionState::Pressed, CID::C0);

// Member function in MyWorld class
void OnJump() {
    // Jump logic here
}
```

### Axis Binding with Deadzone

```cpp
// Create axis map: "MoveForward" -> W/S keys with inversion
inputManager->AddAxisMap("MoveForward", SDL_SCANCODE_W, 1.0f);
inputManager->AddAxisMap("MoveForward", SDL_SCANCODE_S, -1.0f);

// Add gamepad left stick Y axis
inputManager->AddAxisMap("MoveForward", 
    ControllerAxis::SDL_CONTROLLER_AXIS_LEFTY, -1.0f);

// Bind with 0.15 deadzone for any controller
inputManager->BindAxis("MoveForward", GetWeakThis(), &MyWorld::OnMoveForward,
                       CID::ANY, 0.15f);

// Member function receives accumulated value
void OnMoveForward(float value) {
    // value ranges from -1 to 1, 0 if in deadzone
    characterSpeed = value * maxSpeed;
}
```

### Mouse Input Binding

```cpp
// Normalized mouse position
inputManager->AddAxisMap("MouseX", Special::MOUSEMOVE_X);
inputManager->AddAxisMap("MouseY", Special::MOUSEMOVE_Y);

// Mouse velocity (cleared each frame)
inputManager->AddAxisMap("CameraYaw", Special::MOUSEMOVE_XVEL, 0.5f);
inputManager->AddAxisMap("CameraPitch", Special::MOUSEMOVE_YVEL, -0.5f);

// Mouse wheel for zoom
inputManager->AddAxisMap("Zoom", Special::MOUSEWHEEL_Y);

// Bind callbacks
inputManager->BindAxis("CameraYaw", GetWeakThis(), &MyWorld::RotateCamera,
                       CID::C0, 0.0f);
```

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/InputManager.hpp:296-411]()

## Cleanup and Memory Management

The system uses weak pointers and automatic cleanup to prevent dangling references when bound objects are destroyed. `CleanupBindings` is called each frame after axis dispatch to remove invalid bindings.

### Cleanup Process

```mermaid
graph TD
    TickAxes["TickAxes() completes"]
    CleanupCall["CleanupBindings()<br/>src/InputManager.cpp:108"]
    
    CleanupActions["Clean ActionBindings"]
    ActionCheck{"binding.IsValid()?"}
    RemoveAction["remove_if() deletes binding"]
    
    CleanupAxes["Clean AxisBindings"]
    AxisCheck{"binding.IsValid()?"}
    RemoveAxis["remove_if() deletes binding"]
    
    CleanupAny["Clean AnyEventBindings"]
    AnyCheck{"weak_ptr.expired()?"}
    RemoveAny["remove_if() deletes listener"]
    
    TickAxes --> CleanupCall
    CleanupCall --> CleanupActions
    CleanupActions --> ActionCheck
    ActionCheck -->|Invalid| RemoveAction
    ActionCheck -->|Valid| CleanupAxes
    RemoveAction --> CleanupAxes
    
    CleanupAxes --> AxisCheck
    AxisCheck -->|Invalid| RemoveAxis
    AxisCheck -->|Valid| CleanupAny
    RemoveAxis --> CleanupAny
    
    CleanupAny --> AnyCheck
    AnyCheck -->|Expired| RemoveAny
    AnyCheck -->|Valid| Done["Complete"]
    RemoveAny --> Done
```

**Sources:** [src/InputManager.cpp:108-128]()

## Thread Safety

The `InputManager` uses `locked_hashmap` and `locked_hashset` with `SpinLock` for thread-safe concurrent access to mapping tables. However, input processing itself is **single-threaded** and occurs only on the main thread during `App::Tick`.

| Data Structure | Thread Safety Mechanism |
|----------------|-------------------------|
| `CodeToAction` | `locked_hashmap<int, locked_hashset<string, SpinLock>, SpinLock>` |
| `CodeToAxis` | `locked_hashmap<int, locked_hashset<AxisID, SpinLock>, SpinLock>` |
| `ActionBindings` | `locked_hashmap<string, LinkedList<ActionBinding>, SpinLock>` |
| `AxisBindings` | Not locked (single-threaded access) |
| `AnyEventBindings` | Not locked (single-threaded access) |

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/InputManager.hpp:223-258]()

## Platform-Specific Considerations

### DPI Scaling

On macOS, mouse position is automatically scaled by DPI factor. On Windows, DPI scaling is disabled (`dpiScale = 1`) to avoid double-scaling issues with Windows' per-monitor DPI awareness.

**Sources:** [src/InputManager.cpp:131-133]()

### SDL3 Event Types

The system handles the following SDL3 event types:

- `SDL_EVENT_KEY_DOWN/UP`: Keyboard input using scancodes (not keycodes)
- `SDL_EVENT_MOUSE_BUTTON_DOWN/UP`: Mouse buttons (1=left, 2=middle, 3=right)
- `SDL_EVENT_MOUSE_MOTION`: Position and velocity
- `SDL_EVENT_MOUSE_WHEEL`: Scroll wheel delta
- `SDL_EVENT_GAMEPAD_BUTTON_DOWN/UP`: Standardized gamepad buttons
- `SDL_EVENT_GAMEPAD_AXIS_MOTION`: Analog sticks and triggers
- `SDL_EVENT_GAMEPAD_ADDED/REMOVED`: Controller hotplugging
- `SDL_EVENT_TEXT_INPUT`: UTF-8 text input for GUI text fields

**Sources:** [src/InputManager.cpp:134-205]()21:T7642,# Rendering

RavEngine's rendering system is a GPU-driven, multi-pass renderer built on top of the RGL graphics abstraction layer. It manages the entire rendering pipeline from entity data synchronization to final frame presentation, supporting Vulkan, DirectX 12, and Metal backends. The system implements advanced techniques including clustered forward+ lighting, GPU-based culling, skeletal animation skinning, order-independent transparency, and optional screen-space effects (SSAO/GTAO/SSGI).

For information about materials and shaders, see [Materials and Shaders](#4.2). For lighting configuration, see [Lighting System](#4.3). For particle rendering, see [Particle Systems](#4.4). For camera setup, see [Cameras and Render Targets](#4.5). For post-processing, see [Post-Processing and Effects](#4.6).

---

## Architecture Overview

The rendering system is centered on the `RenderEngine` class, which orchestrates all rendering operations. It consumes data from the `World`'s parallel render data structures and produces rendered frames through a series of GPU passes.

**Rendering Architecture - Core Components**

## RenderEngine Class

The `RenderEngine` class ([include/RavEngine/RenderEngine.hpp:63]()) is the main rendering coordinator. It is constructed once per application with a device and configuration, and owns all render passes, pipelines, and shared GPU resources.

### Key Responsibilities

| Responsibility | Implementation |
|----------------|----------------|
| Command buffer management | `mainCommandBuffer`, `transformSyncCommandBuffer`, `transientCommandBuffer` ([RenderEngine.hpp:73]()) |
| Render pass definitions | `litRenderPass`, `shadowRenderPass`, `depthPrepassRenderPass`, etc. ([RenderEngine.hpp:78]()) |
| Pipeline compilation | Material pipelines, compute pipelines ([RenderEngine.hpp:80-82]()) |
| Shared geometry buffers | `sharedPositionBuffer`, `sharedIndexBuffer` ([RenderEngine.hpp:84]()) |
| Mesh allocation | `AllocateMesh()`, `DeallocateMesh()` ([RenderEngine.hpp:317-318]()) |
| Transient memory | 32MB scratch buffer for per-frame data ([RenderEngine.hpp:324-333]()) |

### Initialization

The `RenderEngine` constructor ([src/RenderEngine.cpp:296]()) creates:
- Command queues and buffers ([RenderEngine.cpp:304-307]())
- Samplers (texture, clamp, shadow, depth pyramid) ([RenderEngine.cpp:308-331]())
- Render passes with specific load/store operations ([RenderEngine.cpp:337-626]())
- Compute pipelines for skinning, culling, clustering ([RenderEngine.cpp:973-1224]())
- Shared vertex/index buffers with initial capacity ([RenderEngine.cpp:1061-1062]())

**Sources:** [src/RenderEngine.cpp:296-1224](), [include/RavEngine/RenderEngine.hpp:63-252]()

---

## Render Pipeline Execution

The main rendering entry point is `RenderEngine::Draw()` ([src/RenderEngine_Draw.cpp:98]()), which executes the multi-pass pipeline for all cameras in the provided `RenderViewCollection` views.

**Multi-Pass Pipeline Flow**

### Depth Prepass and Early-Z Optimization

For opaque materials, the pipeline uses a depth prepass with `depthFunction = Greater` (reverse-Z for better precision) ([src/RenderEngine_Draw.cpp:818-942]()). This writes depth and view-space normals. The main opaque pass then uses `depthFunction = Equal` ([src/RenderEngine_Draw.cpp:1390]()) to leverage early-Z rejection, preventing fragment shader execution for occluded pixels.

Materials create three pipeline variants: main, shadow, and depth prepass ([src/Material.cpp:165-180]()).

**Sources:** [src/RenderEngine_Draw.cpp:818-942, 1390-1533](), [src/Material.cpp:165-180]()

### Clustered Forward+ Lighting

The renderer implements clustered forward+ shading by dividing the view frustum into a 3D grid of clusters (12Ã—12Ã—24 by default, [include/RavEngine/RenderEngine.hpp:48-51]()).

**Clustering Process:**

1. **Grid Build** ([src/RenderEngine_Draw.cpp:982-1002]()): `clusterBuildGridPipeline` compute shader initializes cluster bounds in view space
2. **Light Assignment** ([src/RenderEngine_Draw.cpp:1004-1070]()): `clusterPopulatePipeline` assigns point lights and spot lights to overlapping clusters
3. **Fragment Shading** ([tools/rvesc/lit_mesh.fsh:260-353]()): Fragments determine their cluster index and iterate only lights in that cluster

The `Cluster` structure ([include/RavEngine/RenderEngine.hpp:53-60]()) stores indices of affecting lights:

```cpp
struct Cluster {
    glm::vec3 minPoint;
    glm::vec3 maxPoint;
    uint32_t pointLightCount;
    uint32_t spotLightCount;
    uint32_t pointLightIndices[CLUSTER_MAX_POINTS];
    uint32_t spotLightIndices[CLUSTER_MAX_SPOTS];
};
```

**Sources:** [src/RenderEngine_Draw.cpp:982-1070](), [tools/rvesc/lit_mesh.fsh:260-353](), [include/RavEngine/RenderEngine.hpp:48-60]()

---

## GPU-Driven Culling and Rendering

RavEngine uses GPU-driven culling to reduce CPU overhead and improve scalability. Objects are culled on the GPU using compute shaders, which directly write Multi-Draw Indirect (MDI) commands.

**GPU Culling Data Flow**

```mermaid
graph LR
    subgraph "CPU Input Data"
        CUBO["CUBO Structures<br/>(defaultcull.csh:7-17)<br/>Per-material metadata"]
        ModelMatrices["modelBuffer<br/>World transform matrices<br/>(defaultcull.csh:34)"]
        RenderLayers["renderLayerBuffer<br/>Layer bitmasks<br/>(defaultcull.csh:46)"]
        EntityIDs["entityIDBuffer<br/>Entity references<br/>(defaultcull.csh:59)"]
        PerObjectFlags["perObjectFlags<br/>Culling attributes<br/>(defaultcull.csh:50)"]
    end
    
    subgraph "GPU Culling Compute Shader"
        CullShader["defaultcull.csh<br/>defaultCullingComputePipeline<br/>(RenderEngine_Draw.cpp:1074)"]
        FrustumCull["Frustum Culling<br/>CullSphere() against planes<br/>(defaultcull.csh:71-78)"]
        OcclusionCull["Occlusion Culling<br/>Depth pyramid sampling<br/>(defaultcull.csh:221-246)"]
        LODSelect["LOD Selection<br/>Distance-based<br/>(defaultcull.csh:250-263)"]
    end
    
    subgraph "GPU Output Data"
        IndirectCommands["IndirectCommand Buffer<br/>MDI draw calls<br/>(defaultcull.csh:38)"]
        VisibleIDs["entityIDsToRender<br/>Visible entity list<br/>(defaultcull.csh:56)"]
    end
    
    subgraph "GPU Rendering"
        DrawIndirect["DrawIndexedIndirect()<br/>RenderEngine_Draw.cpp:1471"]
    end
    
    CUBO --> CullShader
    ModelMatrices --> CullShader
    RenderLayers --> CullShader
    EntityIDs --> CullShader
    PerObjectFlags --> CullShader
    
    CullShader --> FrustumCull
    FrustumCull --> OcclusionCull
    OcclusionCull --> LODSelect
    
    LODSelect --> IndirectCommands
    LODSelect --> VisibleIDs
    
    IndirectCommands --> DrawIndirect
    VisibleIDs --> DrawIndirect
```

**Sources:** [shaders/defaultcull.csh:1-283](), [src/RenderEngine_Draw.cpp:1074-1175, 1471]()

### CUBO (Culling Buffer Object)

The `CUBO` structure ([shaders/defaultcull.csh:7-17]()) groups rendering metadata per material:

```glsl
struct CUBO {
    uint indirectBufferOffset;
    uint numObjects;
    uint cullingBufferOffset;
    float radius;  // bounding sphere radius
    uint numLODs;
    uint idOutputBufferBindlessHandle;
    uint entityIDInputBufferBindlessHandle;
    uint indirectOutputBufferBindlessHandle;
    uint lodDistanceBufferBindlessHandle;
};
```

For each draw call, a CUBO is created describing the objects using that material ([src/RenderEngine_Draw.cpp:1074-1175]()). The compute shader processes entities in parallel, performing per-object culling tests.

**Sources:** [shaders/defaultcull.csh:7-17](), [src/RenderEngine_Draw.cpp:1074-1175]()

### Depth Pyramid Occlusion Culling

After the depth prepass, a hierarchical depth pyramid is generated ([src/RenderEngine_Draw.cpp:944-964]()) using `depthPyramidPipeline`. Each mip level stores the minimum depth of the 2Ã—2 texels below it.

During culling ([shaders/defaultcull.csh:221-246]()):
1. Object's bounding sphere is projected to screen space
2. Appropriate mip level is selected based on screen-space size
3. Depth is sampled from pyramid using `depthPyramidSampler` with min reduction
4. Object's depth is compared; if occluded, it's culled

This technique is disabled on some platforms via `OCCLUSION_CULLING_UNAVAILABLE` ([src/RenderEngine_Draw.cpp:35]()).

**Sources:** [src/RenderEngine_Draw.cpp:944-964](), [shaders/defaultcull.csh:221-246]()

### Per-Object Attributes

Each entity has a `perObjectFlags` bitmask ([shaders/defaultcull.csh:50]()) controlling culling behavior:

| Bit | Meaning | Code Reference |
|-----|---------|----------------|
| 0 | Frustum culling enabled | [defaultcull.csh:181]() |
| 1 | Occlusion culling enabled | [defaultcull.csh:182]() |
| 2 | Casts shadows | [defaultcull.csh:183]() |
| 3 | Receives shadows | [lit_mesh.fsh:165]() |

These are set via `World::SetEntityAttributes()` ([include/RavEngine/World.hpp:547-555]()).

**Sources:** [shaders/defaultcull.csh:50, 181-183](), [tools/rvesc/lit_mesh.fsh:165](), [include/RavEngine/World.hpp:547-555]()

---

## Render Data Synchronization

The `World` maintains parallel render-friendly data structures that are asynchronously synchronized to GPU buffers.

**World Render Data to GPU Flow**

```mermaid
graph TB
    subgraph "World ECS Components"
        StaticMeshComp["StaticMesh Component<br/>(StaticMesh.hpp:14)"]
        SkinnedMeshComp["SkinnedMeshComponent<br/>(SkinnedMeshComponent.hpp:12)"]
        TransformComp["Transform Component<br/>Hierarchical transforms"]
        LightComps["Light Components<br/>DirectionalLight<br/>PointLight<br/>SpotLight<br/>AmbientLight"]
    end
    
    subgraph "World::RenderData (World.hpp:419)"
        WorldTransforms["BufferedVRAMVector&lt;matrix4&gt;<br/>worldTransforms"]
        
        StaticMeshRD["OrderedMap&lt;MaterialSort, MDIICommand&gt;<br/>staticMeshRenderData"]
        SkinnedMeshRD["OrderedMap&lt;MaterialSort, MDIICommandSkinned&gt;<br/>skinnedMeshRenderData"]
        
        DirLightData["BufferedVRAMSparseSet<br/>directionalLightData"]
        PointLightData["BufferedVRAMSparseSet<br/>pointLightData"]
        SpotLightData["BufferedVRAMSparseSet<br/>spotLightData"]
        AmbientLightData["BufferedVRAMSparseSet<br/>ambientLightData"]
        
        RenderLayers["BufferedVRAMVector&lt;renderlayer_t&gt;<br/>renderLayers"]
        PerObjectAttrs["BufferedVRAMVector&lt;perobject_t&gt;<br/>perObjectAttributes"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Render Tasks (World.cpp:311-521)"
        ResizeBuffer["resizeBuffer task<br/>Allocate for all entities"]
        UpdateStaticMesh["updateRenderDataStaticMesh<br/>Write dirty transforms"]
        UpdateSkinnedMesh["updateRenderDataSkinnedMesh<br/>Write dirty transforms"]
        UpdateDirLights["updateInvalidatedDirs<br/>Write light properties"]
        UpdatePointLights["updateInvalidatedPoints"]
        UpdateSpotLights["updateInvalidatedSpots"]
        UpdateAmbientLights["updateInvalidatedAmbients"]
    end

        GPUWorldTransforms["worldTransforms<br/>Private Buffer"]
        GPULightBuffers["Light SSBOs<br/>Private Buffers"]
        GPUMeshBuffers["MDI Command Buffers<br/>Indirect + Entity IDs"]
    end
    
    StaticMeshComp --> StaticMeshRD
    SkinnedMeshComp --> SkinnedMeshRD
    TransformComp --> WorldTransforms
    LightComps --> DirLightData
    LightComps --> PointLightData
    LightComps --> SpotLightData
    LightComps --> AmbientLightData
    
    ResizeBuffer --> WorldTransforms
    UpdateStaticMesh --> WorldTransforms
    UpdateSkinnedMesh --> WorldTransforms
    UpdateDirLights --> DirLightData
    UpdatePointLights --> PointLightData
    UpdateSpotLights --> SpotLightData
    UpdateAmbientLights --> AmbientLightData
    
    WorldTransforms -.->|"EncodeSync()"| GPUWorldTransforms
    DirLightData -.->|"EncodeSync()"| GPULightBuffers
    PointLightData -.->|"EncodeSync()"| GPULightBuffers
    SpotLightData -.->|"EncodeSync()"| GPULightBuffers
    AmbientLightData -.->|"EncodeSync()"| GPULightBuffers
    StaticMeshRD -.->|"EncodeSync()"| GPUMeshBuffers
    SkinnedMeshRD -.->|"EncodeSync()"| GPUMeshBuffers
```

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/World.hpp:419-449](), [src/World.cpp:311-521]()

### BufferedVRAMVector and BufferedVRAMSparseSet

These template classes ([include/RavEngine/VRAMSparseSet.hpp]() - not shown but referenced) maintain host-side data and GPU-side private buffers. Changes are tracked via dirty flags, and `EncodeSync()` ([src/RenderEngine_Draw.cpp:120-147]()) copies modified data to staging buffers and records copy commands.

The synchronization happens early in `RenderEngine::Draw()` ([src/RenderEngine_Draw.cpp:110-304]()) using a dedicated `transformSyncCommandBuffer` that executes before the main rendering commands.

**Sources:** [src/RenderEngine_Draw.cpp:110-304]()

### MDIICommand Structures

Static and skinned meshes are grouped by material into `MDIICommand` ([include/RavEngine/World.hpp:339-349]()) and `MDIICommandSkinned` ([include/RavEngine/World.hpp:351-362]()) structures:

```cpp
struct MDIICommand : public MDICommandBase {
    struct command {
        WeakRef<MeshCollectionStatic> mesh;
        BufferedVRAMSparseSet<entity_id_t, entity_id_t> entities;
        command(decltype(mesh) mesh, set_t::index_type index, 
                const set_t::value_type& first_value);
    };
    unordered_vector<command> commands;
};
```

Each `command` represents a mesh with a list of entities using it. These are stored in `World::renderData.staticMeshRenderData` ([include/RavEngine/World.hpp:443]()) as an `OrderedMap<MaterialSort, MDIICommand>`, sorted by material priority for state-change minimization.

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/World.hpp:334-362, 443-444]()

### Render Tasks Execution

The `World` sets up render synchronization tasks ([src/World.cpp:311-521]()) that run asynchronously after ECS tick:

1. **resizeBuffer** ([World.cpp:316-328]()): Ensures capacity for all entities
2. **updateRenderDataStaticMesh** ([World.cpp:354-365]()): Writes world matrices for dirty static meshes
3. **updateRenderDataSkinnedMesh** ([World.cpp:367-378]()): Writes matrices for dirty skinned meshes
4. **updateInvalidatedDirs/Points/Spots/Ambients** ([World.cpp:392-520]()): Writes light parameters

These tasks leverage the taskflow executor and run concurrently where dependencies allow. After completion, `EncodeSync()` transfers data to GPU.

**Sources:** [src/World.cpp:311-521](), [src/World.cpp:69-73]()

---

## Material System Overview

Materials define the shader programs and pipeline state for rendering. See [Materials and Shaders](#4.2) for full details.

**Material Class Hierarchy**

```mermaid
graph TB
    Material["Material<br/>(Material.hpp:45)<br/>Base shader interface"]
    LitMaterial["LitMaterial<br/>(Material.hpp:136)<br/>Clustered lighting support"]
    UnlitMaterial["UnlitMaterial<br/>(Material.hpp:146)<br/>No lighting calculations"]
    PBRMaterial["PBRMaterial<br/>(BuiltinMaterials.hpp:17)<br/>Metallic-roughness workflow"]
    
    MaterialInstance["MaterialInstance<br/>(Material.hpp:184)<br/>Per-object settings"]
    PBRMaterialInstance["PBRMaterialInstance<br/>(BuiltinMaterials.hpp:39)<br/>Texture/tint bindings"]
    
    Material --> LitMaterial
    Material --> UnlitMaterial
    LitMaterial --> PBRMaterial
    
    MaterialInstance -.->|"references"| Material
    PBRMaterialInstance --> MaterialInstance
    PBRMaterialInstance -.->|"uses"| PBRMaterial
```

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/Material.hpp:45-219](), [include/RavEngine/BuiltinMaterials.hpp:1-96]()

### Pipeline Variants

Each material compiles multiple pipeline variants ([src/Material.cpp:135-195]()):
- **Main render pipeline**: For lit/unlit passes, with `depthFunction = Equal` for opaques
- **Depth prepass pipeline**: Writes depth/normals, `depthFunction = Greater`
- **Shadow pipeline**: Depth-only, backface culling, depth clamping enabled

Vertex attributes are trimmed based on `MaterialConfig::requiredAttributes` ([src/Material.cpp:94-132]()) to reduce bandwidth.

**Sources:** [src/Material.cpp:30-196]()

---

## Lighting System Overview

RavEngine supports four light types, managed as ECS components. See [Lighting System](#4.3) for full configuration details.

| Light Type | Component | Shadow Support | Use Case |
|------------|-----------|----------------|----------|
| Directional | `DirectionalLight` ([Light.hpp:134]()) | Yes, CSM up to 4 cascades | Sunlight |
| Point | `PointLight` ([Light.hpp:157]()) | Yes, cube shadowmap | Omnidirectional |
| Spot | `SpotLight` ([Light.hpp:189]()) | Yes, single shadowmap | Flashlight, cone |
| Ambient | `AmbientLight` ([Light.hpp:119]()) | No | Indirect/IBL |

### Shadow Rendering

Shadow-casting lights render to depth textures before the main pass ([src/RenderEngine_Draw.cpp:1179-1383]()):

1. **Directional lights** use Cascaded Shadow Maps (CSM) with view-dependent split calculation ([RenderEngine_Draw.cpp:180-287]())
2. **Point lights** render 6 cube faces ([RenderEngine_Draw.cpp:1235-1328]())
3. **Spot lights** render a single frustum ([RenderEngine_Draw.cpp:1330-1383]())

Shadow sampling uses PCF (Percentage-Closer Filtering) implemented in shader ([tools/rvesc/lit_mesh.fsh:229-257]()).

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/Light.hpp:1-230](), [src/RenderEngine_Draw.cpp:1179-1383, 180-287](), [tools/rvesc/lit_mesh.fsh:229-257]()

---

## Render Target Management

`RenderTargetCollection` ([include/RavEngine/RenderTargetCollection.hpp:20]()) encapsulates all framebuffer targets for a viewport:

```cpp
struct RenderTargetCollection {
    RGLTexturePtr depthStencil;
    RGLTexturePtr lightingTexture;        // Main color output
    RGLTexturePtr radianceTexture;        // Direct lighting
    RGLTexturePtr viewSpaceNormalsTexture; // For SSAO/SSGI
    RGLTexturePtr ssaoOutputTexture1;     // Ping-pong AO
    RGLTexturePtr ssaoOutputTexture2;
    RGLTexturePtr ssgiOutputTexture;
    std::array<RGLTexturePtr, 4> mlabAccum; // MLAB transparency
    RGLTexturePtr mlabDepth;
    DepthPyramid depthPyramid;            // Hierarchical-Z
    Function<RGL::ITexture*()> finalFramebufferFn; // Swapchain image
};
```

Collections are created via `RenderEngine::CreateRenderTargetCollection()` ([src/RenderEngine.cpp:1270]()) and resized dynamically ([src/RenderEngine.cpp:1353]()).

`RenderViewCollection` ([include/RavEngine/RenderTargetCollection.hpp:42]()) pairs targets with camera data for multi-view rendering (split-screen, VR).

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/RenderTargetCollection.hpp:20-60](), [src/RenderEngine.cpp:1270-1432]()

---

## Transparency Rendering (MLAB)

RavEngine implements Multi-Layer Alpha Blending (MLAB) for order-independent transparency on tile-based GPUs. On traditional GPUs, a simpler interlock-based approach is used.

**MLAB Storage** ([include/RavEngine/RenderTargetCollection.hpp:23-25]()):
```cpp
std::array<RGLTexturePtr, 4> mlabAccum;  // 4 layers
RGLTexturePtr mlabDepth;
```

During transparent rendering ([src/RenderEngine_Draw.cpp:1628-1738]()), fragments write to storage images via `writeTransparency()` ([tools/rvesc/lit_mesh.fsh:362]()). The resolve pass ([src/RenderEngine_Draw.cpp:1742-1771]()) composites layers front-to-back.

On non-TBDR platforms, fragment interlocks (`beginInvocationInterlockARB()`/`endInvocationInterlockARB()`) synchronize access ([tools/rvesc/lit_mesh.fsh:360-365]()).

**Sources:** [src/RenderEngine_Draw.cpp:1628-1771](), [tools/rvesc/lit_mesh.fsh:358-368](), [include/RavEngine/RenderTargetCollection.hpp:23-25]()

---

## Graphics Abstraction Layer (RGL)

All rendering is abstracted through RGL (RavEngine Graphics Library), providing a unified API over Vulkan, DirectX 12, and Metal. See [RGL Graphics Abstraction Layer](#9.1) for details.

RGL types used throughout rendering:
- `RGLDevicePtr`: GPU device
- `RGLCommandBufferPtr`: Command recording
- `RGLTexturePtr`: Images and framebuffers
- `RGLBufferPtr`: Vertex, index, uniform buffers
- `RGLRenderPipelinePtr`: Graphics pipeline state
- `RGLComputePipelinePtr`: Compute pipeline state
- `RGLSamplerPtr`: Texture sampling configuration

The `RenderEngine` holds a `device` ([RenderEngine.hpp:71]()) and creates all RGL objects from it.

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/RenderEngine.hpp:71](), [src/RenderEngine.cpp:296]()

---

## Performance Considerations

### Mesh Allocation

Static geometry is allocated from shared vertex/index buffers ([RenderEngine.hpp:84]()) using a free-list allocator. `AllocateMesh()` ([src/RenderEngine.cpp:1434]()) returns a `MeshRange` describing the allocation. Buffers auto-resize when capacity is exceeded ([src/RenderEngine.cpp:1622-1707]()).

### Transient Data

Per-frame CPUâ†’GPU data (push constants, scratch data) uses a 32MB ring buffer ([RenderEngine.hpp:324-333]()). `WriteTransient()` ([src/RenderEngine.cpp:1257]()) appends data and returns an offset. The buffer resets each frame ([src/RenderEngine_Draw.cpp:99]()).

### Resource Garbage Collection

Deleted GPU resources are queued in concurrent queues (`gcBuffers`, `gcTextures`, etc. [RenderEngine.hpp:311-314]()) and freed in `DestroyUnusedResources()` ([src/RenderEngine.cpp:2161]()) after GPU sync.

**Sources:** [src/RenderEngine.cpp:1434-1707, 1257-1268, 2161-2176](), [include/RavEngine/RenderEngine.hpp:84, 311-333]()

---

## Shader Interface

### Engine Bindings

Shaders receive engine data through fixed bindings ([shaders/lit_mesh_shared.glsl:16-22]()):

```glsl
layout(std430, binding = MODEL_MATRIX_BINDING) readonly buffer modelMatrixBuffer {
    mat4 model[];
};
layout(scalar, binding = 11) readonly buffer lightAuxDataSSBO {
    EngineData_Internal engineConstants[];
};
```

Light data is bound to slots 12-17 ([tools/rvesc/lit_mesh.fsh:63-110]()). Bindless textures and shadow maps use sets 1-2 ([lit_mesh.fsh:115-117]()).

### User Shader Functions

Lit materials implement a `frag()` function returning `LitOutput` ([tools/rvesc/lit_mesh.fsh:13-21, 131]()):

```glsl
struct LitOutput {
    vec4 color;
    vec3 normal;
    vec3 emissiveColor;
    float roughness;
    float specular;
    float metallic;
    float ao;
};
LitOutput frag(EnvironmentData envData);
```

The engine applies lighting calculations using the returned material properties ([lit_mesh.fsh:161-374]()).

**Sources:** [tools/rvesc/lit_mesh.fsh:13-374](), [shaders/lit_mesh_shared.glsl:1-23]()

## Purpose and Scope

This document describes RavEngine's rendering architecture, focusing on the `RenderEngine` class, the multi-pass GPU-driven rendering pipeline, and how frame execution flows from the ECS `World` to the GPU. It covers the high-level rendering pipeline structure, GPU-driven culling and indirect rendering, render data synchronization, and command buffer management.

For information about specific rendering subsystems:
- Material system and shader pipelines: see [Materials and Shaders](#4.2)
- Lighting techniques and shadow mapping: see [Lighting System](#4.3)
- GPU particle effects: see [Particle Systems](#4.4)
- Camera setup and render targets: see [Cameras and Render Targets](#4.5)
- Post-processing passes: see [Post-Processing and Effects](#4.6)

For lower-level graphics API abstraction: see [RGL Graphics Abstraction Layer](#9.1)

---

## RenderEngine Class Overview

The `RenderEngine` class is the primary interface for all rendering operations in RavEngine. It orchestrates multi-pass rendering, manages GPU resources, and translates ECS component data into GPU-friendly formats for efficient rendering.

### Key Responsibilities

| Responsibility | Description | Implementation |
|---------------|-------------|----------------|
| **Frame Orchestration** | Executes the complete rendering pipeline for one frame | `RenderEngine::Draw()` |
| **Pass Management** | Creates and manages render passes (depth prepass, opaque, transparent, shadows, etc.) | Multiple `RGLRenderPassPtr` members |
| **GPU Resource Management** | Allocates and manages vertex/index buffers, textures, and pipelines | `sharedPositionBuffer`, `sharedIndexBuffer`, etc. |
| **Compute Pipeline Execution** | Dispatches compute shaders for culling, skinning, particles | `defaultCullingComputePipeline`, `skinnedMeshComputePipeline` |
| **Command Buffer Creation** | Encodes GPU commands for submission to the graphics queue | `mainCommandBuffer`, `transformSyncCommandBuffer` |
| **Mesh Allocation** | Manages a unified vertex/index buffer for all meshes | `vertexFreeList`, `indexFreeList` |
| **RGL Abstraction** | Interfaces with RGL for cross-platform graphics | `RGLDevicePtr device` |

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/RenderEngine.hpp:63-364]()

```mermaid
graph TB
    subgraph "Application Layer"
        App["App"]
        World["World<br/>ECS Container"]
    end
    
    subgraph "RenderEngine Core"
        RE["RenderEngine<br/>Main Orchestrator"]

        RE --> Draw
    end
```
