
**Push Constants:**

Material instances override `SetPushConstantData()` ([include/RavEngine/ParticleMaterial.hpp:166-168]()) to provide shader-specific uniform data. The method returns the number of bytes written.

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/ParticleMaterial.hpp:154-209]()

## GPU Lifecycle Management

Particle creation and death are managed entirely on the GPU using compute shaders and atomic operations.

### Particle Creation Pipeline

```mermaid
graph TD
    Start["ParticleEmitter::GetNextParticleSpawnCount()"]
    
    CreateShader["create_particle.csh<br/>Compute Dispatch"]
    
    subgraph "create_particle.csh Operations"
        C1["atomicAdd(aliveParticleCount, 1)<br/>Reserve slot"]
        C2{"Slot < maxTotalParticles?"}
        C3["atomicAdd(freeListCount, -1)<br/>Try freelist"]
        C4{"Freelist available?"}
        C5["particleID = particleFreelist[freelistSize-1]<br/>Reuse dead particle"]
        C6["particleID = particleBufferSlot<br/>Create new particle"]
        C7["aliveParticleIndexBuffer[slot] = particleID"]
        C8["particlesCreatedThisFrameBuffer[idx] = particleID"]
        C9["atomicAdd(createdThisFrame, 1)"]
    end
    
    InitShader["User Init Shader<br/>Initialize new particles"]
    
    Start --> CreateShader
    CreateShader --> C1
    C1 --> C2
    C2 -->|No| End1["atomicAdd(aliveParticleCount, -1)<br/>Abort"]
    C2 -->|Yes| C9
    C9 --> C3
    C3 --> C4
    C4 -->|Yes| C5
    C4 -->|No| C6
    C5 --> C7
    C6 --> C7
    C7 --> C8
    C8 --> InitShader
```

**create_particle.csh** ([shaders/create_particle.csh:1-76]()):
- Dispatched with `particlesToSpawn` threads (64 threads per workgroup)
- Each thread attempts to create one particle
- Uses freelist to reuse dead particle slots when available
- Falls back to allocating new slots from the linear buffer
- Writes created particle IDs to `particlesCreatedThisFrameBuffer` for init shader

**User Init Shader:**
- Reads `particlesCreatedThisFrameBuffer` and `emitterStateBuffer.createdThisFrame`
- Initializes custom particle data in `particleDataBuffer`
- Sets initial lifetime in `particleLifeBuffer`

**Sources:** [shaders/create_particle.csh:1-76](), [src/ParticleMaterial.cpp:158-200]()

### Particle Update Pipeline

```mermaid
graph LR
    UpdateShader["User Update Shader<br/>Dispatched per alive particle"]
    
    subgraph "Update Responsibilities"
        U1["Read particleDataBuffer[particleID]<br/>via activeParticleIndexBuffer"]
        U2["Update simulation state<br/>(position, velocity, etc)"]
        U3["Decrement particleLifeBuffer[particleID]<br/>by fpsScale * deltaTime"]
        U4["Write updated data back<br/>to particleDataBuffer"]
        U5["Optional: Update indirectDrawBuffer<br/>for mesh selection"]
    end
    
    UpdateShader --> U1
    U1 --> U2
    U2 --> U3
    U3 --> U4
    U4 --> U5
```

The update shader receives `ParticleUpdateUBO` with `fpsScale` ([include/RavEngine/ParticleMaterial.hpp:21-23]()) to perform frame-rate independent updates. It is dispatched with `aliveParticleCount` threads.

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/ParticleMaterial.hpp:21-23](), [src/ParticleMaterial.cpp:203-245]()

### Particle Death Pipeline

```mermaid
graph TD
    KillShader["kill_particle.csh<br/>Dispatched per alive particle"]
    
    subgraph "kill_particle.csh Operations"
        K1["Thread 0: particleState.createdThisFrame = 0"]
        K2["particleID = aliveParticleIndexBuffer[invocationID]"]
        K3{"particleLifeBuffer[particleID] > 0?"}
        K4["Return (keep alive)"]
        K5["freelistIdx = atomicAdd(freeListCount, 1)"]
        K6["particleFreelist[freelistIdx] = particleID"]
        K7["prevAlive = atomicAdd(aliveParticleCount, -1)"]
        K8["aliveParticleIndexBuffer[invocationID] =<br/>aliveParticleIndexBuffer[prevAlive-1]<br/>(Swap with last alive)"]
    end
    
    KillShader --> K1
    K1 --> K2
    K2 --> K3
    K3 -->|Yes| K4
    K3 -->|No| K5
    K5 --> K6
    K6 --> K7
    K7 --> K8
```

**kill_particle.csh** ([shaders/kill_particle.csh:1-63]()):
- Thread 0 resets `createdThisFrame` counter ([shaders/kill_particle.csh:36-39]())
- Each thread checks if its particle's lifetime is <= 0
- Dead particles are added to freelist for reuse
- Alive particle array is compacted by swapping dead particle with last alive particle

This swap-and-pop approach ensures the alive particle array remains contiguous for efficient rendering.

**Sources:** [shaders/kill_particle.csh:1-63]()

### Indirect Rendering

Particles use indirect draw calls to avoid CPU-GPU synchronization:

**indirectDrawBuffer** ([src/ParticleEmitter.cpp:36-45]()):
```cpp
RGL::IndirectCommand {
    .vertexCount = 4,        // For billboards (quad strip)
    .instanceCount = 0,      // Updated by GPU
    .firstVertex = 0,
    .firstInstance = 0,
}
```

The update shader or a separate compute pass updates `instanceCount` based on `aliveParticleCount`, enabling fully GPU-driven rendering without CPU readback.

**Sources:** [src/ParticleEmitter.cpp:36-45]()

## Built-in Materials

### SpritesheetParticleRenderMaterial

`SpritesheetParticleRenderMaterial<LightingMode>` ([include/RavEngine/ParticleMaterial.hpp:218-246]()) provides billboard rendering with spritesheet animation support.

**Bindings:**

| Binding | Type | Purpose |
|---------|------|---------|
| 0 (`SamplerBindingSlot`) | Sampler | Texture sampler |
| 1 (`SpritesheetBindingSlot`) | SampledImage | Spritesheet texture |

**Push Constants (ParticleBillboardUBO):**

| Field | Type | Purpose |
|-------|------|---------|
| `spritesheetDim` | `vector2i` | Texture dimensions (width, height) |
| `numSprites` | `vector2i` | Sprite grid (numSpritesWidth, numSpritesHeight) |
| `bytesPerParticle` | `uint32_t` | Size of custom particle struct |
| `particlePositionOffset` | `uint32_t` | Byte offset to position field |
| `particleScaleOffset` | `uint32_t` | Byte offset to scale field |
| `particleFrameOffset` | `uint32_t` | Byte offset to frame index field |

The vertex shader uses these offsets to extract particle data from the untyped `particleDataBuffer`. The fragment shader samples the spritesheet based on the particle's frame index.

**Instance Setup:**

```cpp
SpritesheetParticleRenderMaterialInstance instance(material, 
    bytesPerParticle, 
    particlePositionOffset, 
    particleScaleOffset, 
    particleFrameOffset);
instance.spriteDim = {numSpritesWidth, numSpritesHeight};
instance.SetSpritesheet(spritesheetTexture);
```

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/ParticleMaterial.hpp:218-269](), [src/ParticleMaterial.cpp:247-270]()

### PBRMeshParticleRenderMaterial

`PBRMeshParticleRenderMaterial` ([include/RavEngine/ParticleMaterial.hpp:271-273]()) provides physically-based mesh particle rendering with full PBR texture support.

**Texture Bindings:**

| Binding | Texture Type |
|---------|--------------|
| 0 | Sampler |
| 1 (`kDiffuseBinding`) | Albedo/Diffuse |
| 2 (`kNormalBinding`) | Normal map |
| 3 (`kSpecularBinding`) | Specular map |
| 4 (`kMetallicBinding`) | Metallic map |
| 5 (`kRoughnessBinding`) | Roughness map |
| 6 (`kAOBinding`) | Ambient occlusion map |
| 7 (`kEmissiveBinding`) | Emissive map |

**Push Constants (PBRUBO):**

| Field | Type | Purpose |
|-------|------|---------|
| `colorTint` | `glm::vec4` | Base color multiplier |
| `metallicTint` | `float` | Metallic multiplier |
| `roughnessTint` | `float` | Roughness multiplier |
| `specularTint` | `float` | Specular multiplier |
| `bytesPerParticle` | `uint32_t` | Size of custom particle struct |
| `positionOffset` | `uint32_t` | Byte offset to position field |
| `scaleOffset` | `uint32_t` | Byte offset to scale field |
| `rotationOffset` | `uint32_t` | Byte offset to rotation field |

The vertex shader uses these offsets to extract transformation data and instance each mesh per particle.

**Instance Setup:**

```cpp
PBRMeshParticleRenderMaterialInstance instance(material, 
    meshCollection,
    bytesPerParticle, 
    positionOffsetBytes, 
    scaleOffsetBytes, 
    rotationOffsetBytes);
instance.SetAlbedoTexture(albedo);
instance.SetNormalTexture(normal);
// ... other textures
```

**Default Textures:**

The constructor ([src/ParticleMaterial.cpp:392-402]()) sets default textures from `Texture::Manager`:
- Most textures default to `defaultTexture` (white)
- Normal map defaults to `defaultNormalTexture` (flat normal)
- Emissive defaults to `zeroTexture` (black)

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/ParticleMaterial.hpp:271-318](), [src/ParticleMaterial.cpp:272-415]()

## Custom Material Creation

### Creating Custom Update Materials

1. **Define Particle Structure:** Design your custom particle data layout (position, velocity, color, etc.)

2. **Write Init Shader:** Compute shader to initialize new particles
   - Access bindings 0-4 as defined in [src/ParticleMaterial.cpp:158-192]()
   - Read `particlesCreatedThisFrameBuffer` to find new particle IDs
   - Initialize `particleDataBuffer` and `particleLifeBuffer`

3. **Write Update Shader:** Compute shader to update particles each frame
   - Access bindings 0-3 as defined in [src/ParticleMaterial.cpp:204-236]()
   - Read `ParticleUpdateUBO.fpsScale` from push constants
   - Update simulation state and decrement lifetime

4. **Subclass ParticleUpdateMaterial:**
```cpp
struct MyUpdateMaterial : public ParticleUpdateMaterial {
    MyUpdateMaterial() : ParticleUpdateMaterial("my_init_shader", "my_update_shader") {}
};
```

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/ParticleMaterial.hpp:38-54](), [src/ParticleMaterial.cpp:153-245]()

### Creating Custom Render Materials

#### Custom Billboard Materials

1. **Write Shaders:** Vertex shader expands billboards, fragment shader applies effects
   - Vertex shader receives `ParticleQuadVert` ([include/RavEngine/ParticleMaterial.hpp:34-36]())
   - Access standard particle bindings 18-22

2. **Subclass BillboardRenderParticleMaterial:**
```cpp
template<LightingMode mode>
struct MyBillboardMaterial : public BillboardRenderParticleMaterial<mode> {
    MyBillboardMaterial() : BillboardRenderParticleMaterial<mode>(
        "my_billboard_vs", 
        "my_billboard_fs",
        {
            .bindings = { /* custom texture/sampler bindings */ },
            .pushConstantSize = sizeof(MyUBO),
            .opacityMode = OpacityMode::Transparent,
            .zTestEnabled = true,
            .zWriteEnabled = false
        }) {}
};
```

3. **Subclass Material Instance:**
```cpp
struct MyBillboardInstance : public BillboardParticleRenderMaterialInstance {
    MyBillboardInstance(Ref<MyBillboardMaterial<LightingMode::Lit>> mat) 
        : BillboardParticleRenderMaterialInstance(mat) {}
    
    virtual uint8_t SetPushConstantData(std::span<std::byte, 128> data) const override {
        MyUBO ubo{ /* fill data */ };
        std::memcpy(data.data(), &ubo, sizeof(ubo));
        return sizeof(ubo);
    }
};
```

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/ParticleMaterial.hpp:112-121,172-183](), [src/ParticleMaterial.cpp:440-452]()

#### Custom Mesh Materials

1. **Write Shaders:** Vertex shader instances meshes, fragment shader applies materials
   - Vertex shader receives `defaultVertexConfig` mesh vertices
   - Access binding 21 for mesh geometry data

2. **Subclass MeshParticleRenderMaterial:**
```cpp
template<LightingMode mode>
struct MyMeshMaterial : public MeshParticleRenderMaterial<mode> {
    MyMeshMaterial() : MeshParticleRenderMaterial<mode>(
        "my_mesh_particle_vs", 
        "my_mesh_particle_fs",
        {
            .bindings = { /* custom bindings */ },
            .pushConstantSize = sizeof(MyMeshUBO),
            .opacityMode = OpacityMode::Opaque
        }) {}
};
```

3. **Optional: Custom Mesh Selection:**
```cpp
struct MyMeshSelectionMaterial : public MeshParticleMeshSelectionMaterial {
    MyMeshSelectionMaterial() : MeshParticleMeshSelectionMaterial("my_selection_shader") {}
};
```

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/ParticleMaterial.hpp:128-136,186-209](), [src/ParticleMaterial.cpp:421-439]()

### Lighting Modes

Both billboard and mesh materials support two lighting modes via template parameter:

- `LightingMode::Lit`: Participates in clustered forward+ lighting (see [Lighting System](#4.3))
- `LightingMode::Unlit`: No lighting calculations, emissive only

The lighting mode determines which augmentation function is called:
- `augmentLitMaterialBindings()` ([src/ParticleMaterial.cpp:425-426]())
- `augmentUnlitMaterialBindings()` ([src/ParticleMaterial.cpp:428-429]())

These functions add engine-required bindings for light data, shadow maps, and environment maps.

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/ParticleMaterial.hpp:64-67](), [src/ParticleMaterial.cpp:417-431]()26:T5404,# Cameras and Render Targets

## Purpose and Scope

This page documents the camera system and render target management in RavEngine. It covers the `CameraComponent` class used to define viewpoints, the `RenderTargetCollection` structure that holds rendering textures, and the `RenderViewCollection` that links cameras to render targets. This page focuses on how cameras are configured and how they output to different render targets, including the main window and render textures.

For information about the rendering pipeline that consumes camera data, see [Rendering Architecture](#4.1). For post-processing effects applied to camera output, see [Post-Processing and Effects](#4.6). For the World and Entity systems that manage camera components, see [Entity Component System](#3.2).

---

## Camera Component Overview

The `CameraComponent` is an ECS component that defines a viewpoint into the world. Each camera generates projection and view matrices used by the rendering pipeline to determine what is visible and how it should be projected onto a 2D surface.

### Key Camera Properties

| Property | Type | Purpose |
|----------|------|---------|
| `nearClip` | `float` | Near clipping plane distance |
| `farClip` | `float` | Far clipping plane distance |
| `FOV` | `float` | Field of view angle (degrees) |
| `renderLayers` | `renderlayer_t` | Bitmask of which render layers this camera sees |
| `target` | `Ref<RenderTexture>` | Optional render texture target (if null, renders to main window) |
| `viewportOverride` | `ViewportOverride` | Optional viewport sub-region within render target |
| `postProcessingEffects` | `PostProcessEffectStack` | Stack of post-processing effects |
| `tonemap` | `Ref<TonemapMaterialInstance>` | Tone mapping operator |
| `indirectLightingSettings` | `IndirectLightingSettings` | SSAO, SSGI configuration |

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/RenderTargetCollection.hpp:15-59]()

### Camera Activation and Targeting

Cameras can be in an active or inactive state. Only active cameras participate in rendering. Cameras determine their output destination through the `target` property:

- **Main Window Rendering**: If `target` is `nullptr`, the camera renders to the main application window's swapchain
- **Render Texture Rendering**: If `target` is set to a `RenderTexture`, the camera renders to that texture's internal `RenderTargetCollection`

Multiple cameras can target the same `RenderTargetCollection`, enabling split-screen rendering where each camera occupies a different viewport region.

**Sources:** [src/App_priv.hpp:400-442]()

---

## Render Target Collections

The `RenderTargetCollection` structure encapsulates all textures required for multi-pass rendering. It contains color attachments, depth buffers, intermediate textures for effects, and transparency accumulation buffers.

### RenderTargetCollection Structure

```mermaid
graph TB
    RTC["RenderTargetCollection"]
    
    subgraph "Primary Attachments"
        Depth["depthStencil<br/>D32SFloat<br/>Main depth buffer"]
        Color["lightingTexture<br/>RGBA16_Sfloat<br/>Final lit output"]
        Radiance["radianceTexture<br/>RGBA16_Sfloat<br/>HDR radiance"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Transparency (MLAB)"
        MLAB0["mlabAccum[0]<br/>RGBA16_Sfloat"]
        MLAB1["mlabAccum[1]<br/>RGBA8_Unorm"]
        MLAB2["mlabAccum[2]<br/>RGBA8_Unorm"]
        MLAB3["mlabAccum[3]<br/>RGBA8_Unorm"]
        MLABDepth["mlabDepth<br/>RGBA16_Sfloat"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Post-Processing"
        Scratch["lightingScratchTexture<br/>Ping-pong buffer"]
        ViewNormals["viewSpaceNormalsTexture<br/>RGBA16_Sfloat"]
        SSAO["ssaoOutputTexture1/2<br/>R16_Float<br/>Ambient occlusion"]
        SSGI["ssgiOutputTexture<br/>RGBA16_Sfloat<br/>Global illumination"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Depth Pyramid"
        DepthPyramid["depthPyramid<br/>Mipmap chain for<br/>occlusion culling"]
    end
    
    FinalFB["finalFramebufferFn<br/>Function returns<br/>swapchain or texture"]
    
    RTC --> Depth
    RTC --> Color
    RTC --> Radiance
    RTC --> MLAB0
    RTC --> MLAB1
    RTC --> MLAB2
    RTC --> MLAB3
    RTC --> MLABDepth
    RTC --> Scratch
    RTC --> ViewNormals
    RTC --> SSAO
    RTC --> SSGI
    RTC --> DepthPyramid
    RTC --> FinalFB
```

**Diagram: RenderTargetCollection Texture Layout**

### Texture Purposes

- **depthStencil**: Primary depth buffer using reversed-Z depth (`D32SFloat`), values range from 1.0 (near) to 0.0 (far)
- **lightingTexture**: Main HDR color output after lighting calculations
- **radianceTexture**: Stores emissive and reflected radiance before tone mapping
- **mlabAccum[0-3]**: Four accumulation buffers for Multi-Layer Alpha Blending (order-independent transparency)
- **mlabDepth**: Depth values for transparency sorting
- **lightingScratchTexture**: Temporary buffer for multi-pass post-processing (blur, etc.)
- **viewSpaceNormalsTexture**: View-space normals output from depth prepass, used for SSAO/SSGI
- **ssaoOutputTexture1/2**: Ping-pong buffers for SSAO/GTAO computation and upsampling
- **ssgiOutputTexture**: Screen-space global illumination result
- **depthPyramid**: Hierarchical depth mipmap chain for GPU occlusion culling
- **finalFramebufferFn**: Function pointer that resolves to either swapchain image or render texture

The collection is created via `RenderEngine::CreateRenderTargetCollection()` and can be resized using `RenderEngine::ResizeRenderTargetCollection()`.

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/RenderTargetCollection.hpp:20-40](), [src/RenderEngine.cpp:254-256]()

---

## Render View Collections

The `RenderViewCollection` structure pairs a `RenderTargetCollection` with an array of camera data, enabling multiple cameras to render to the same target with different viewpoints.

### RenderViewCollection Architecture

```mermaid
graph LR
    subgraph "RenderViewCollection"
        Collection["collection<br/>RenderTargetCollection<br/>Shared render targets"]
        CamDataArray["camDatas<br/>Vector&lt;camData&gt;<br/>Per-camera matrices/settings"]
        PixelDims["pixelDimensions<br/>dim_t&lt;int&gt;<br/>Target size"]
    end
    
    subgraph "camData Structure"
        ViewProj["viewProj: mat4<br/>Combined matrix"]
        ProjOnly["projOnly: mat4<br/>Projection matrix"]
        ViewOnly["viewOnly: mat4<br/>View matrix"]
        CamPos["camPos: vec3<br/>Camera position"]
        ZNearFar["zNearFar: vec2<br/>Clip planes"]
        ViewportOvr["viewportOverride<br/>Viewport region"]
        Layers["layers: renderlayer_t<br/>Visibility mask"]
        FOVVal["fov: float<br/>Field of view"]
        Dimensions["targetWidth/Height<br/>Resolution"]
        PostFX["postProcessingEffects*<br/>Effect stack"]
        Tonemap["tonemap*<br/>Tone mapper"]
        IndirectSettings["indirectSettings<br/>SSAO/SSGI config"]
    end
    
    Collection --> CamDataArray
    CamDataArray --> ViewProj
    CamDataArray --> ProjOnly
    CamDataArray --> ViewOnly
    CamDataArray --> CamPos
    CamDataArray --> ZNearFar
    CamDataArray --> ViewportOvr
    CamDataArray --> Layers
    CamDataArray --> FOVVal
    CamDataArray --> Dimensions
    CamDataArray --> PostFX
    CamDataArray --> Tonemap
    CamDataArray --> IndirectSettings
```

**Diagram: RenderViewCollection and Camera Data Structure**

### Camera Data Generation

The `MakeCamData` lambda in `App_priv.hpp` constructs camera data from a `CameraComponent`:

```cpp
// Pseudo-code representation of camData construction
camData {
    viewProj = camera.GenerateProjectionMatrix(width, height) * camera.GenerateViewMatrix(),
    projOnly = camera.GenerateProjectionMatrix(width, height),
    viewOnly = camera.GenerateViewMatrix(),
    camPos = camera.GetOwner().GetTransform().GetWorldPosition(),
    zNearFar = {camera.nearClip, camera.farClip},
    viewportOverride = camera.viewportOverride,
    layers = camera.renderLayers,
    fov = camera.FOV,
    targetWidth = width,
    targetHeight = height,
    postProcessingEffects = &camera.postProcessingEffects,
    tonemap = camera.tonemap.get(),
    indirectSettings = camera.indirectLightingSettings
}
```

This data is consumed by the rendering pipeline to configure GPU state, compute frustum planes for culling, and apply per-camera settings.

**Sources:** [src/App_priv.hpp:409-418](), [include/RavEngine/RenderTargetCollection.hpp:44-57]()

---

## Camera Collection and Rendering Flow

The application collects active cameras each frame and organizes them into `RenderViewCollection` instances based on their targets. The rendering engine then iterates over these collections to produce final images.

### Camera Collection Process

```mermaid
graph TD
    Start["App::Tick<br/>Frame begins"] --> GetCameras["GetAllComponentsOfType&lt;CameraComponent&gt;<br/>Query all cameras in renderWorld"]
    
    GetCameras --> FilterActive{"For each camera:<br/>Is Active?"}
    FilterActive -->|No| Skip["Skip camera"]
    FilterActive -->|Yes| CheckTarget{"Has target?"}
    
    CheckTarget -->|"Yes (RenderTexture)"| RTGroup["Create RenderViewCollection<br/>collection = target->GetCollection()<br/>Add to allViews"]
    CheckTarget -->|"No (Main Window)"| MainGroup["Add to mainWindowView.camDatas<br/>collection = main window targets"]
    
    RTGroup --> XRCheck{"XR Enabled?"}
    MainGroup --> XRCheck
    
    XRCheck -->|Yes| AddXR["Add xrRenderViewCollections<br/>to allViews<br/>Copy camera settings to XR views"]
    XRCheck -->|No| FinalizeViews["allViews.push_back(mainWindowView)<br/>Complete view list"]
    
    AddXR --> FinalizeViews
    FinalizeViews --> RenderAll["RenderEngine::Draw(world, allViews)<br/>Render all view collections"]
    
    RenderAll --> IterateViews["For each RenderViewCollection:<br/>For each camData:<br/>Execute rendering passes"]
```

**Diagram: Camera Collection and Rendering Flow**

### Split-Screen and Multi-View Rendering

Multiple cameras can render to the same `RenderTargetCollection` by adding multiple entries to `camDatas`. Each camera can specify a `ViewportOverride` to occupy a sub-region of the render target:

```cpp
struct ViewportOverride {
    glm::vec2 originFactor {0, 0};    // Normalized [0,1] viewport origin
    glm::vec2 sizeFactor {1, 1};      // Normalized [0,1] viewport size
};
```

For example, two-player split-screen:
- **Player 1**: `originFactor = {0, 0}`, `sizeFactor = {0.5, 1}` (left half)
- **Player 2**: `originFactor = {0.5, 0}`, `sizeFactor = {0.5, 1}` (right half)

The rendering pipeline respects viewport overrides when setting scissor regions and viewport dimensions for each camera pass.

**Sources:** [src/App_priv.hpp:419-474](), [include/RavEngine/RenderTargetCollection.hpp:15-18]()

---

## Render-to-Texture

The `RenderTexture` class provides user-facing functionality for rendering camera output to a texture instead of the main window. This enables effects like mirrors, security cameras, portals, and picture-in-picture displays.

### RenderTexture Implementation

```mermaid
graph TB
    RT["RenderTexture"]
    
    Create["RenderTexture(width, height)"] --> CreateRTC["RenderEngine::CreateRenderTargetCollection<br/>Allocate internal textures"]
    CreateRTC --> CreateFinalFB["Create Texture(width, height)<br/>BGRA8_Unorm render target<br/>enableRenderTarget = true"]
    CreateFinalFB --> SetupCallback["Set collection.finalFramebufferFn<br/>Return finalFB texture pointer"]
    
    RT --> CollectionRef["collection<br/>RenderTargetCollection<br/>Full rendering buffers"]
    RT --> FinalFBRef["finalFB<br/>Ref&lt;Texture&gt;<br/>User-accessible result"]
    
    SetupCallback --> Ready["RenderTexture ready for use"]
    
    subgraph "Usage in CameraComponent"
        CameraSetTarget["camera.target = renderTexture"]
        CameraSetTarget --> CameraRenders["Camera renders to<br/>renderTexture->GetCollection()"]
        CameraRenders --> UserSamples["User samples finalFB texture<br/>in materials, GUI, etc."]
    end
    
    Ready --> CameraSetTarget
```

**Diagram: RenderTexture Creation and Usage**

### Accessing Render Texture Output

After a camera renders to a `RenderTexture`, the output is available in the `finalFB` texture, which can be retrieved via `GetTexture()`. This texture can then be:

- Bound to a material and displayed on a mesh in the world
- Used as a source for GUI elements
- Sampled in custom shaders for advanced effects

The `RenderTexture` manages the lifecycle of its internal `RenderTargetCollection` and ensures proper cleanup via the garbage collection system when destroyed.

**Sources:** [src/Texture.cpp:252-259](), [include/RavEngine/Texture.hpp:83-94]()

---

## Integration with Rendering Pipeline

The rendering pipeline iterates over all `RenderViewCollection` instances provided to `RenderEngine::Draw()`. For each collection and each camera within it, the engine executes the full multi-pass rendering sequence.

### Per-Camera Rendering Sequence

```mermaid
graph TD
    StartRender["RenderEngine::Draw(world, screenTargets)"]
    
    StartRender --> SyncBuffers["Sync GPU Buffers<br/>Transforms, lights, mesh data"]
    SyncBuffers --> SkeletalSkinning["Compute: Skeletal Animation<br/>skinning_cs_csh"]
    SkeletalSkinning --> ParticleUpdate["Compute: Particle Update<br/>User update shaders"]
    
    ParticleUpdate --> CameraLoop["For each screenTarget:<br/>For each camData in target"]
    
    CameraLoop --> SetViewport["Set Viewport<br/>Apply viewportOverride<br/>or use full dimensions"]
    SetViewport --> SetMatrices["Set Camera Matrices<br/>viewProj, projOnly, viewOnly<br/>camPos, zNearFar"]
    
    SetMatrices --> SetLayers["Set Render Layers<br/>cameraRenderLayers = camData.layers"]
    SetLayers --> DepthPrepass["Pass 1: Depth Prepass<br/>Write depth + view normals<br/>depthFunction = Greater"]
    
    DepthPrepass --> BuildDepthPyramid["Compute: Build Depth Pyramid<br/>depthpyramid_csh<br/>For occlusion culling"]
    BuildDepthPyramid --> AssignLightClusters["Compute: Assign Light Clusters<br/>cluster_assign_lights_csh<br/>Using camera frustum"]
    
    AssignLightClusters --> CullOpaque["Compute: Cull Opaque Objects<br/>defaultcull.csh<br/>Frustum + Occlusion + LOD<br/>Using camera matrices"]
    
    CullOpaque --> ShadowMaps["Pass 2: Shadow Maps<br/>(If lights cast shadows)"]
    ShadowMaps --> OpaqueMain["Pass 3: Main Opaque<br/>Lit/Unlit materials<br/>depthFunction = Equal<br/>Using camera viewProj"]
    
    OpaqueMain --> Skybox["Pass 4: Skybox<br/>Using camera rotation"]
    Skybox --> CullTransparent["Compute: Cull Transparent"]
    CullTransparent --> Transparent["Pass 5: Transparent<br/>MLAB accumulation"]
    
    Transparent --> ResolveTransparency["Resolve Transparency<br/>Composite MLAB"]
    ResolveTransparency --> AO["Compute: SSAO/GTAO<br/>(If enabled in indirectSettings)"]
    AO --> SSGI["Compute: SSGI<br/>(If enabled in indirectSettings)"]
    
    SSGI --> ApplyIndirect["Apply Indirect Lighting<br/>AO/SSGI/IBL"]
    ApplyIndirect --> PostProcess["Pass 6: Post-Processing<br/>Apply postProcessingEffects stack"]
    PostProcess --> Tonemap["Tonemap<br/>Apply camera.tonemap<br/>HDR to LDR"]
    
    Tonemap --> NextCam{"More cameras<br/>in this target?"}
    NextCam -->|Yes| SetViewport
    NextCam -->|No| NextTarget{"More screenTargets?"}
    NextTarget -->|Yes| CameraLoop
    NextTarget -->|No| GUIPass["Pass 7: GUI Rendering<br/>For main window target"]
    
    GUIPass --> DebugPass["Pass 8: Debug Rendering<br/>Im3d overlays"]
    DebugPass --> Submit["Submit Command Buffer<br/>to GPU Queue"]
```

**Diagram: Per-Camera Rendering Pipeline Integration**

### Camera-Specific Culling

The `defaultcull.csh` compute shader uses camera data from the `CullingUBO` structure to perform GPU-driven frustum and occlusion culling:

```cpp
struct CullingUBO {
    glm::mat4 viewProj;              // Combined view-projection matrix
    glm::vec3 camPos;                // Camera world position
    uint32_t numCubos;               // Number of culling batches
    renderlayer_t cameraRenderLayers; // Visibility layer mask
    uint32_t singleInstanceModeAndShadowMode;
};
```

Each object's bounding sphere is tested against the camera's frustum planes (derived from `viewProj`) and the depth pyramid (generated from the camera's depth buffer). Objects on non-matching render layers are also culled.

**Sources:** [src/RenderEngine_Draw.cpp:98-258](), [shaders/defaultcull.csh:19-178](), [include/RavEngine/RenderEngine.hpp:224-230]()

---

## Main Window vs Render Texture Targets

The camera system distinguishes between two output modes based on the `target` property:

### Main Window Target Path

When `camera.target == nullptr`:

1. Camera data is added to `mainWindowView.camDatas`
2. `mainWindowView.collection` is sized to match window dimensions
3. `collection.finalFramebufferFn` is set to return swapchain images from `Window::BlockGetNextSwapchainImage()`
4. Rendering outputs directly to the presentation surface
5. GUI and debug overlays are rendered on top

**Sources:** [src/App_priv.hpp:433-442](), [src/App_priv.hpp:467-474]()

### Render Texture Target Path

When `camera.target != nullptr`:

1. A new `RenderViewCollection` is created with `collection = target->GetCollection()`
2. Camera data is added to this dedicated collection
3. `collection.finalFramebufferFn` returns the render texture's internal `finalFB` texture
4. Rendering outputs to the render texture, which can be sampled later
5. No GUI or debug overlays are applied

**Sources:** [src/App_priv.hpp:420-431]()

---

## XR Multi-View Support

RavEngine supports OpenXR stereo rendering by creating additional `RenderViewCollection` instances for each XR eye view. The XR integration generates camera matrices for each eye and pairs them with dedicated render targets.

```mermaid
graph LR
    subgraph "XR Frame Begin"
        BeginXR["OpenXRIntegration::BeginXRFrame"] --> GetViews["Retrieve XrView array<br/>One per eye (typically 2)"]
        GetViews --> UpdateTargets["UpdateXRTargetCollections<br/>Resize/create RenderTargetCollections"]
    end
    
    subgraph "XR Camera Data"
        RefCam["Reference CameraComponent<br/>Last non-RT camera<br/>Provides settings"] --> CopySettings["Copy to XR camDatas:<br/>postProcessingEffects<br/>zNearFar<br/>layers<br/>tonemap<br/>indirectSettings"]
        CopySettings --> XRMatrices["XR-provided matrices:<br/>viewProj from XrView<br/>Position from XrView"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Rendering"
        XRMatrices --> AddToAllViews["xrRenderViewCollections<br/>added to allViews"]
        AddToAllViews --> RenderEyes["Render each eye view<br/>using XR matrices"]
        RenderEyes --> EndXRFrame["OpenXRIntegration::EndXRFrame<br/>Submit to XR runtime"]
    end
    
    UpdateTargets --> RefCam
```

**Diagram: XR Multi-View Rendering Flow**

XR views reuse the post-processing and rendering settings from a reference camera but use XR-specific projection matrices and eye positions provided by the OpenXR runtime.

**Sources:** [src/App_priv.hpp:448-464]()

---

## Summary

The camera and render target system in RavEngine provides flexible, multi-view rendering capabilities:

- **CameraComponent** defines viewpoints with configurable FOV, clipping planes, render layers, and post-processing settings
- **RenderTargetCollection** encapsulates all textures needed for multi-pass rendering, including depth, lighting, transparency, and post-processing buffers
- **RenderViewCollection** links cameras to render targets, supporting multiple cameras per target for split-screen
- **RenderTexture** enables render-to-texture for mirrors, portals, and dynamic textures
- **Viewport management** allows precise control over sub-regions of render targets
- **Integration with the rendering pipeline** uses camera data for culling, lighting, and view-dependent effects
- **XR support** enables stereo rendering with per-eye camera matrices

The system is designed for efficient GPU-driven rendering with minimal CPU overhead, supporting advanced features like order-independent transparency, screen-space effects, and multi-view rendering.

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/RenderTargetCollection.hpp](), [src/App_priv.hpp:398-489](), [src/RenderEngine_Draw.cpp:98-1500](), [src/Texture.cpp:252-265]()27:T6057,# Post-Processing and Effects

</details>



## Overview

The post-processing and effects system provides GPU-accelerated image-space effects applied after the main 3D scene rendering. RavEngine implements multiple post-processing passes including **Screen-Space Ambient Occlusion (SSAO)**, **Ground-Truth Ambient Occlusion (GTAO)**, **Screen-Space Global Illumination (SSGI)**, **Order-Independent Transparency (MLAB)**, and **tonemapping**. These effects enhance visual quality through indirect lighting approximations, depth-based occlusion, and HDR tone mapping.

For information about the overall rendering pipeline architecture, see [Rendering Architecture](#4.1). For material system integration, see [Materials and Shaders](#4.2). For camera configuration that affects post-processing, see [Cameras and Render Targets](#4.5).

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/RenderEngine.hpp:1-364](), [include/RavEngine/RenderTargetCollection.hpp:1-63]()

---

## Post-Processing Pipeline Integration

Post-processing effects execute as part of the main rendering pipeline's later stages, after opaque and transparent geometry has been rendered. The pipeline operates on intermediate render targets stored in the `RenderTargetCollection` structure, which maintains multiple textures for different stages of processing.

### Pipeline Sequence

```mermaid
graph TD
    OpaquePass["Pass 3: Main Opaque Rendering<br/>depthFunction = Equal<br/>Clustered lighting"]
    Skybox["Pass 4: Skybox"]
    TransparentPass["Pass 5: Transparent Rendering<br/>MLAB accumulation"]
    TransparentResolve["Resolve OIT<br/>transparencyApplyPipeline"]
    AODecision{"AO Enabled?"}
    ComputeAO["Compute Ambient Occlusion<br/>ssaoPipeline or gtaoPipeline"]
    AOUpsample["Upsample AO<br/>aoUpsamplePipeline"]
    SSGIDecision{"SSGI Enabled?"}
    ComputeSSGI["Compute SSGI<br/>ssgipipeline<br/>Downsample + Trace"]
    SSGIUpsample["Upsample SSGI<br/>ssgiUpsamplePipeline"]
    ApplyIndirect["Apply Indirect Lighting<br/>ambientSSGIApplyPipeline<br/>Combine AO/SSGI/IBL"]
    PostProcess["Pass 6: Post-Processing<br/>Custom PostProcessEffectStack"]
    Tonemap["Tonemap to Final FB<br/>HDR to LDR conversion"]
    
    OpaquePass --> Skybox
    Skybox --> TransparentPass
    TransparentPass --> TransparentResolve
    TransparentResolve --> AODecision
    AODecision -->|Yes| ComputeAO
    AODecision -->|No| SSGIDecision
    ComputeAO --> AOUpsample
    AOUpsample --> SSGIDecision
    SSGIDecision -->|Yes| ComputeSSGI
    SSGIDecision -->|No| ApplyIndirect
    ComputeSSGI --> SSGIUpsample
    SSGIUpsample --> ApplyIndirect
    ApplyIndirect --> PostProcess
    PostProcess --> Tonemap
```

**Sources:** [src/RenderEngine_Draw.cpp:1-2500](), [include/RavEngine/RenderEngine.hpp:78-82]()

### Post-Processing Execution Context

Post-processing effects execute per-camera in the `RenderEngine::Draw` method. Each camera's `RenderViewCollection::camData` structure specifies post-processing configuration through the `postProcessingEffects` pointer and indirect lighting settings.

```mermaid
graph LR
    subgraph "RenderViewCollection"
        RTCollection["RenderTargetCollection<br/>depthStencil<br/>lightingTexture<br/>ssaoOutputTexture1/2<br/>ssgiOutputTexture"]
        CamData["Vector&lt;camData&gt;<br/>viewProj matrices<br/>postProcessingEffects*<br/>indirectSettings"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Per-Camera Processing"
        CameraLoop["For Each Camera"]
        PostEffects["Execute Post-Processing"]
        Tonemap["Apply Tonemapping"]
    end
    
    RTCollection --> CameraLoop
    CamData --> CameraLoop
    CameraLoop --> PostEffects
    PostEffects --> Tonemap
```

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/RenderTargetCollection.hpp:42-60](), [src/RenderEngine_Draw.cpp:473-end]()

---

## Render Target Configuration

The `RenderTargetCollection` structure manages all intermediate textures required for post-processing. These textures use high-precision formats to preserve lighting data through multiple processing stages.

### RenderTargetCollection Structure

| Texture Member | Format | Purpose |
|----------------|--------|---------|
| `depthStencil` | `D32SFloat` | Depth buffer for depth pyramid and occlusion culling |
| `lightingTexture` | `RGBA16_Sfloat` | Main HDR color accumulation buffer |
| `lightingScratchTexture` | `RGBA16_Sfloat` | Temporary buffer for ping-pong operations |
| `radianceTexture` | `RGBA16_Sfloat` | Intermediate radiance buffer for lit pass |
| `viewSpaceNormalsTexture` | `RGBA16_Sfloat` | View-space normals for SSAO/SSGI |
| `ssaoOutputTexture1` | `R16_Float` | Primary AO output buffer |
| `ssaoOutputTexture2` | `R16_Float` | Secondary AO buffer for upsampling |
| `ssgiOutputTexture` | `RGBA16_Sfloat` | SSGI output with up to 5 mip levels |
| `mlabAccum[0-3]` | See MLAB section | Multi-layer transparency accumulation |
| `mlabDepth` | `RGBA16_Sfloat` | Transparency depth sorting |
| `depthPyramid` | `R32_Float` | Hierarchical depth mipmap chain |

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/RenderTargetCollection.hpp:20-27](), [include/RavEngine/RenderEngine.hpp:144-158]()

### Texture Format Constants

The render engine defines standard texture formats as compile-time constants:

```cpp
// From RenderEngine.hpp:151-158
constexpr static RGL::TextureFormat
    colorTexFormat = RGL::TextureFormat::RGBA16_Sfloat,
    radianceFormat = RGL::TextureFormat::RGBA16_Sfloat,
    albedoFormat = RGL::TextureFormat::RGBA16_Sfloat,
    viewSpaceNormalTextureFormat = RGL::TextureFormat::RGBA16_Sfloat,
    ssgiOutputFormat = RGL::TextureFormat::RGBA16_Sfloat,
    ssaoOutputFormat = RGL::TextureFormat::R16_Float,
    depthFormat = RGL::TextureFormat::D32SFloat;
```

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/RenderEngine.hpp:151-158](), [include/RavEngine/RenderTargetCollection.hpp:20-40]()

---

## Ambient Occlusion (SSAO/GTAO)

RavEngine supports two ambient occlusion techniques selectable at runtime: **Screen-Space Ambient Occlusion (SSAO)** and **Ground-Truth Ambient Occlusion (GTAO)**. Both techniques sample the depth buffer and view-space normals to estimate geometric occlusion.

### AO Method Selection

```cpp
// From RenderEngine.hpp:265-273
enum class AOMethod : uint8_t {
    SSAO,
    GTAO
};

static struct vs {
    bool vsync = true;
    AOMethod aoMethod = AOMethod::SSAO;
} VideoSettings;
```

The active AO method is controlled through `RenderEngine::VideoSettings::aoMethod`. The selection determines which compute pipeline executes during the AO pass.

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/RenderEngine.hpp:265-273]()

### AO Pipelines and Uniform Buffers

```mermaid
graph TB
    subgraph "AO Compute Pass"
        AODecision{"VideoSettings.aoMethod"}
        SSAO["ssaoPipeline<br/>SSAOUBO"]
        GTAO["gtaoPipeline<br/>GTAOUBO"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Input Textures"
        Depth["depthStencil"]
        Normals["viewSpaceNormalsTexture"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Output"
        AOTex1["ssaoOutputTexture1"]
        Upsample["aoUpsamplePipeline"]
        AOTex2["ssaoOutputTexture2"]
    end
    
    AODecision -->|SSAO| SSAO
    AODecision -->|GTAO| GTAO
    Depth --> SSAO
    Depth --> GTAO
    Normals --> SSAO
    Normals --> GTAO
    SSAO --> AOTex1
    GTAO --> AOTex1
    AOTex1 --> Upsample
    Upsample --> AOTex2
```

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/RenderEngine.hpp:81-82](), [include/RavEngine/RenderEngine.hpp:197-205]()

### SSAO Uniform Buffer Object

```cpp
// From RenderEngine.hpp:201-205
struct SSAOUBO {
    glm::mat4 proj;
    glm::mat4 invProj;
    glm::ivec2 screenDim;
};
```

The `SSAOUBO` provides projection matrices for reconstructing world-space positions from depth values during SSAO computation.

### GTAO Uniform Buffer Object

```cpp
// From RenderEngine.hpp:197-199
struct GTAOUBO {
    glm::ivec2 screenDim;
};
```

GTAO requires only screen dimensions, as it uses a different sampling approach than SSAO.

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/RenderEngine.hpp:197-205]()

### AO Application in Lighting

After computing ambient occlusion, the result is applied during the indirect lighting application phase through the `ambientSSGIApplyPipeline`. The `AmbientSSGIApplyUBO` controls AO strength:

```cpp
// From RenderEngine.hpp:132-138
struct AmbientSSGIApplyUBO {
    glm::mat4 invView{ 1 };
    uint32_t ambientLightCount = 0;
    float ssaoStrength = 1;
    uint32_t options = 0;
    static constexpr uint32_t SSAOBIT = 1, SSGIBIT = 1 << 1;
};
```

The `options` bitmask enables/disables SSAO and SSGI independently.

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/RenderEngine.hpp:132-138]()

---

## Screen-Space Global Illumination (SSGI)

SSGI approximates indirect lighting by tracing rays through screen-space depth buffers. RavEngine's SSGI implementation uses a **downsample-trace-upsample** pipeline with mipmap chains for efficient hierarchical ray marching.

### SSGI Pipeline Architecture

```mermaid
graph TD
    subgraph "SSGI Downsample"
        FullRes["lightingTexture<br/>Full Resolution"]
        Downsample["ssgiDownsamplePipeline<br/>Generate mip levels"]
        SSGIMips["ssgiOutputTexture<br/>5 mip levels"]
    end
    
    subgraph "SSGI Trace"
        TraceCompute["ssgipipeline<br/>Ray march through depth"]
        DepthPyramid["depthPyramid<br/>Hierarchical depth"]
        SSGIUBO["SSGIUBO:<br/>projection, sampleCount<br/>sampleRadius, hitThickness"]
    end
    
    subgraph "SSGI Upsample"
        Upsample1["ssgiUpsamplePipeline<br/>Blur + upsample pass 1"]
        Upsample2["ssgiUpsamplePipeline<br/>Blur + upsample pass 2"]
        UpsampleFinal["ssgiUpsamplePipleineFinalStep<br/>Final upsample"]
    end
    
    FullRes --> Downsample
    Downsample --> SSGIMips
    SSGIMips --> TraceCompute
    DepthPyramid --> TraceCompute
    SSGIUBO --> TraceCompute
    TraceCompute --> Upsample1
    Upsample1 --> Upsample2
    Upsample2 --> UpsampleFinal
```

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/RenderEngine.hpp:81-82](), [include/RavEngine/RenderEngine.hpp:187-195]()

### SSGI Uniform Buffer Object

```cpp
// From RenderEngine.hpp:187-195
struct SSGIUBO {
    glm::mat4 projection;
    glm::mat4 invProj;
    glm::ivec2 outputDim;
    float sampleCount;
    float sampleRadius;
    float sliceCount;
    float hitThickness;
};
```

SSGI parameters control ray marching behavior:
- `sampleCount`: Number of samples per pixel for ray tracing
- `sampleRadius`: Maximum ray length in screen space
- `sliceCount`: Number of angular slices for hemispherical sampling
- `hitThickness`: Depth threshold for ray-geometry intersection

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/RenderEngine.hpp:187-195]()

### SSGI Mipmap Chain

The `ssgiOutputTexture` maintains up to **5 mip levels** for hierarchical processing:

```cpp
// From RenderEngine.hpp:145
constexpr static uint32_t maxssgimips = 5;
```

Each mip level represents the lighting buffer downsampled by successive factors of 2, enabling efficient multi-scale processing.

### Downsample and Upsample UBOs

```cpp
// From RenderEngine.hpp:119-126
struct DownsampleUBO {
    glm::uvec4 targetDim;
};

struct UpsampleUBO {
    glm::uvec4 targetDim;
    float filterRadius;
};
```

The `filterRadius` in `UpsampleUBO` controls blur kernel size during upsampling.

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/RenderEngine.hpp:119-126]()

---

## Depth Pyramid

The depth pyramid is a hierarchical mipmap chain of the depth buffer used for occlusion culling (see [GPU-Driven Rendering Techniques](#9.2)) and screen-space effects. Each mip level stores the **minimum depth** of the level below it, enabling efficient hierarchical visibility queries.

### Depth Pyramid Structure

```mermaid
graph LR
    subgraph "DepthPyramid Encapsulation"
        DepthPyramidClass["DepthPyramid<br/>depthPyramid member<br/>in RenderTargetCollection"]
    end
    
    subgraph "GPU Resources"
        DepthTexture["Original Depth Buffer<br/>D32SFloat"]
        PyramidTexture["Depth Pyramid Texture<br/>R32_Float<br/>Multiple mip levels"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Generation Pipeline"
        DepthCopy["depthPyramidCopyPipeline<br/>Copy depth to R32 format"]
        BuildPyramid["depthPyramidPipeline<br/>Generate mip levels<br/>Reduction sampler"]
    end
    
    DepthTexture --> DepthCopy
    DepthCopy --> PyramidTexture
    PyramidTexture --> BuildPyramid
    BuildPyramid --> PyramidTexture
    PyramidTexture -.-> DepthPyramidClass
```

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/RenderTargetCollection.hpp:27](), [include/RavEngine/RenderEngine.hpp:82]()

### Depth Pyramid Format and Sampler

```cpp
// From RenderEngine.hpp:144
static constexpr RGL::TextureFormat depthPyramidFormat = RGL::TextureFormat::R32_Float;
```

The depth pyramid uses a single-channel 32-bit float format to store depth values. A specialized sampler with **reduction mode set to minimum** automatically selects the minimum depth when sampling:

```cpp
// From RenderEngine.cpp:323-331 (constructor)
depthPyramidSampler = device->CreateSampler({
    .addressModeU = RGL::SamplerAddressMode::Clamp,
    .addressModeV = RGL::SamplerAddressMode::Clamp,
    .addressModeW = RGL::SamplerAddressMode::Clamp,
    .minFilter = RGL::MinMagFilterMode::Linear,
    .magFilter = RGL::MinMagFilterMode::Linear,
    .mipFilter = RGL::MipFilterMode::Nearest,
    .reductionMode = RGL::SamplerReductionMode::Minimum,
});
```

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/RenderEngine.hpp:144](), [src/RenderEngine.cpp:323-331]()

### Depth Pyramid Pipeline

The `depthPyramidPipeline` compute shader generates mip levels by sampling the previous level with the reduction sampler, automatically computing per-pixel minimum depth values.

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/RenderEngine.hpp:82](), [shaders/defaultcull.csh:224-273]()

---

## Order-Independent Transparency (MLAB)

RavEngine implements **Multi-Layer Alpha Blending (MLAB)** for order-independent transparency. Unlike traditional alpha blending, MLAB correctly composites transparent objects regardless of draw order by accumulating multiple transparency layers in separate buffers.

### MLAB Render Target Configuration

```cpp
// From RenderTargetCollection.hpp:23-25
std::array<RGLTexturePtr, 4> mlabAccum;
constexpr static std::array<RGL::TextureFormat, 4> formats = {
    RGL::TextureFormat::RGBA16_Sfloat,  // Layer 0
    RGL::TextureFormat::RGBA8_Unorm,    // Layer 1
    RGL::TextureFormat::RGBA8_Unorm,    // Layer 2
    RGL::TextureFormat::RGBA8_Unorm     // Layer 3
};
constexpr static auto mlabDepthFormat = RGL::TextureFormat::RGBA16_Sfloat;
```

MLAB uses **4 accumulation layers** with the first layer in higher precision (16-bit float) for the closest transparent surface, and subsequent layers in 8-bit unorm for memory efficiency.

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/RenderTargetCollection.hpp:23-25]()

### MLAB Rendering Pipeline

```mermaid
graph TD
    subgraph "Transparent Object Rendering"
        TransparentCull["Cull Transparent Objects<br/>defaultcull_csh"]
        LitTransparent["litTransparentPass<br/>Lit transparent materials"]
        UnlitTransparent["unlitTransparentPass<br/>Unlit transparent materials"]
    end
    
    subgraph "MLAB Accumulation"
        ClearMLAB["transparentClearPass<br/>Clear mlabAccum[0-3]<br/>Clear mlabDepth"]
        WriteMLAB["Write to mlabAccum<br/>Depth sorting in shader"]
    end
    
    subgraph "MLAB Resolve"
        ApplyTransparency["transparencyApplyPipeline<br/>Composite MLAB layers<br/>to lightingTexture"]
    end
    
    TransparentCull --> ClearMLAB
    ClearMLAB --> LitTransparent
    ClearMLAB --> UnlitTransparent
    LitTransparent --> WriteMLAB
    UnlitTransparent --> WriteMLAB
    WriteMLAB --> ApplyTransparency
```

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/RenderEngine.hpp:78](), [src/RenderEngine.cpp:523-556]()

### Transparent Render Pass Configuration

The `litTransparentPass` and `unlitTransparentPass` render passes are configured to write to all MLAB accumulation buffers:

```cpp
// From RenderEngine.cpp:442-480
litTransparentPass = RGL::CreateRenderPass({
    .attachments = {
        { .format = RenderTargetCollection::formats[0], ... },
        { .format = RenderTargetCollection::formats[1], ... },
        { .format = RenderTargetCollection::formats[2], ... },
        { .format = RenderTargetCollection::formats[3], ... },
        { .format = RenderTargetCollection::mlabDepthFormat, ... }
    },
    .depthAttachment = ...
});
```

**Sources:** [src/RenderEngine.cpp:442-520]()

### Transparency Clear Pass

The `transparentClearPass` initializes MLAB buffers before rendering transparent objects:

```cpp
// From RenderEngine.cpp:523-556
transparentClearPass = RGL::CreateRenderPass({
    .attachments = {
        { .format = RenderTargetCollection::formats[0],
          .loadOp = RGL::LoadAccessOperation::Clear,
          .clearColor = {0,0,0,1} },  // Clear to black with full alpha
        // ... (formats[1-3] similar)
        { .format = RenderTargetCollection::mlabDepthFormat,
          .loadOp = RGL::LoadAccessOperation::Clear,
          .clearColor = {1,1,1,1} }  // Clear depth to far plane
    }
});
```

**Sources:** [src/RenderEngine.cpp:523-556]()

## Tonemapping

Tonemapping converts high-dynamic-range (HDR) lighting data to low-dynamic-range (LDR) for display. RavEngine provides a customizable tonemapping system through the `Tonemap` interface.

### Tonemap Integration

Each camera specifies its tonemapping function through the `RenderViewCollection::camData::tonemap` pointer:

```cpp
// From RenderTargetCollection.hpp:55
const void* tonemap = nullptr;  // Pointer to tonemapping material instance
```

If no tonemap is specified, the engine uses the `dummyTonemap`:

```cpp
// From RenderEngine.hpp:93
Ref<DummyTonemapInstance> dummyTonemap;
```

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/RenderTargetCollection.hpp:55](), [include/RavEngine/RenderEngine.hpp:93]()

### Tonemapping Render Pass

Tonemapping executes as the final step before GUI rendering, converting the HDR `lightingTexture` to the LDR `finalFramebuffer`:

```mermaid
graph LR
    HDR["lightingTexture<br/>RGBA16_Sfloat<br/>HDR color"]
    TonemapShader["Tonemap Shader<br/>Custom or Builtin"]
    LDR["finalFramebuffer<br/>BGRA8_Unorm<br/>LDR display output"]
    
    HDR --> TonemapShader
    TonemapShader --> LDR
```

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/RenderEngine.hpp:93](), [src/RenderEngine.cpp:51]()

### Final Render Pass Configuration

The `finalRenderPass` is configured for LDR output:

```cpp
// From RenderEngine.cpp:578-591
finalRenderPass = RGL::CreateRenderPass({
    .attachments = {
        {
            .format = RGL::TextureFormat::BGRA8_Unorm,
            .loadOp = RGL::LoadAccessOperation::Load,
            .storeOp = RGL::StoreAccessOperation::Store,
        },
    },
    .depthAttachment = RGL::RenderPassConfig::AttachmentDesc{
        .format = RGL::TextureFormat::D32SFloat,
        .loadOp = RGL::LoadAccessOperation::Load,
        .storeOp = RGL::StoreAccessOperation::Store,
    }
});
```

**Sources:** [src/RenderEngine.cpp:578-591]()

## Blur Effects

RavEngine provides separable Gaussian blur kernels for bloom and other effects requiring blurred images. The blur implementation uses a two-pass approach: horizontal blur followed by vertical blur.

### Blur Pipeline Structure

```mermaid
graph LR
    InputTex["Input Texture"]
    TempTex["Intermediate Texture"]
    OutputTex["Output Texture"]
    
    BlurX["blurKernelX<br/>Horizontal blur<br/>Compute shader"]
    BlurY["blurKernelY<br/>Vertical blur<br/>Compute shader"]
    
    InputTex --> BlurX
    BlurX --> TempTex
    TempTex --> BlurY
    BlurY --> OutputTex
```

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/RenderEngine.hpp:82]()

### Blur Kernel Pipelines

```cpp
// From RenderEngine.hpp:82
RGLComputePipelinePtr blurKernelX, blurKernelY;
```

Both pipelines share the same layout:

```cpp
// From RenderEngine.cpp:1142-1173
auto blurKernelLayout = device->CreatePipelineLayout({
    .bindings = {
        {
            .binding = 0,
            .type = RGL::BindingType::StorageImage,
            .stageFlags = RGL::BindingVisibility::Compute,
            .writable = false  // Input texture
        },
        {
            .binding = 1,
            .type = RGL::BindingType::StorageImage,
            .stageFlags = RGL::BindingVisibility::Compute,
            .writable = true   // Output texture
        },
    }
});
```

The blur kernels operate on storage images, allowing efficient compute-based filtering without render passes.

**Sources:** [src/RenderEngine.cpp:1142-1173]()

## Custom Post-Processing Stack

RavEngine supports custom post-processing effects through the `PostProcessEffectStack` system. Effects can be added per-camera and execute in sequence after built-in effects.

### PostProcessEffectStack Integration

```cpp
// From RenderTargetCollection.hpp:54
const PostProcessEffectStack* postProcessingEffects = nullptr;
```

Each camera's `camData` structure can reference a `PostProcessEffectStack` instance that defines custom shader passes.

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/RenderTargetCollection.hpp:54](), [include/RavEngine/PostProcess.hpp:1]()

### Post-Processing Render Pass

Custom effects execute using the `postProcessRenderPass`:

```cpp
// From RenderEngine.cpp:559-576
postProcessRenderPass = RGL::CreateRenderPass({
    .attachments = {
        {
            .format = colorTexFormat,  // RGBA16_Sfloat
            .loadOp = RGL::LoadAccessOperation::Load,
            .storeOp = RGL::StoreAccessOperation::Store,
        },
    }
});

postProcessRenderPassClear = RGL::CreateRenderPass({
    .attachments = {
        {
            .format = colorTexFormat,
            .loadOp = RGL::LoadAccessOperation::Clear,
            .storeOp = RGL::StoreAccessOperation::Store,
        },
    }
});
```

The `postProcessRenderPassClear` variant clears the color buffer, while `postProcessRenderPass` preserves existing content for accumulative effects.

**Sources:** [src/RenderEngine.cpp:559-576]()

### Default Post-Effect Vertex Shader

Post-processing effects typically use a fullscreen triangle. The engine provides a default vertex shader:

```cpp
// From RenderEngine.hpp:140-149
RGLShaderLibraryPtr defaultPostEffectVSH;

auto GetDefaultPostEffectVSH() const {
    return defaultPostEffectVSH;
}
```

Materials can use this shader for standard fullscreen post-processing passes.

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/RenderEngine.hpp:140-149]()

---

## Indirect Lighting Settings

Per-camera indirect lighting parameters control SSAO, SSGI, and image-based lighting behavior:

```cpp
// From RenderTargetCollection.hpp:56
IndirectLightingSettings indirectSettings;
```

The `IndirectLightingSettings` structure (defined elsewhere in the codebase) configures:
- SSAO strength and bias
- SSGI sample count and radius
- Environment map contribution
- Indirect lighting intensity scaling

These settings integrate with the `AmbientSSGIApplyUBO` during the indirect lighting application pass.

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/RenderTargetCollection.hpp:56](), [include/RavEngine/RenderEngine.hpp:132-138]()

---

## Effect Execution Summary

The following table summarizes when each post-processing effect executes in the rendering pipeline:

| Effect | Pipeline Stage | Input Textures | Output Texture | Configurable |
|--------|---------------|----------------|----------------|--------------|
| MLAB Transparency | After transparent pass | depth, MLAB accum | lightingTexture | Per-material |
| Depth Pyramid | After depth prepass | depthStencil | depthPyramid | No |
| SSAO/GTAO | After OIT resolve | depth, normals | ssaoOutputTexture | VideoSettings.aoMethod |
| SSGI | After AO | lighting, depth pyramid | ssgiOutputTexture | Per-camera |
| Indirect Lighting | After SSGI | AO, SSGI, IBL maps | lightingTexture | Per-camera |
| Custom Effects | After indirect lighting | User-defined | User-defined | Per-camera |
| Tonemapping | Before GUI | lightingTexture | finalFramebuffer | Per-camera |
| Blur | On-demand | Any texture | Any texture | Programmatic |

**Sources:** [src/RenderEngine_Draw.cpp:1-2500](), [include/RavEngine/RenderEngine.hpp:78-82]()28:T47f5,# Physics

## Purpose and Scope

This document provides a comprehensive overview of RavEngine's physics system, which integrates NVIDIA PhysX 4.x for rigid body simulation and collision detection. It covers the core architecture, component-based design, and integration with the Entity Component System (ECS). 

For detailed information on individual components and collider types, see [Physics Bodies and Colliders](#5.1). For collision callbacks and simulation lifecycle management, see [Physics Simulation and Events](#5.2). For raycasting and spatial queries, see [Scene Queries and Raycasting](#5.3).

**Sources:** [Diagram 1: Overall Engine Architecture](#), [Diagram 5: Physics and Animation Simulation Integration](#)

---

## Overview

RavEngine's physics system wraps NVIDIA PhysX to provide rigid body dynamics, collision detection, and scene queries. The system is designed around three primary concepts:

1. **PhysicsSolver** - Manages the PhysX scene and orchestrates simulation per `World`
2. **PhysicsBodyComponent** - Represents a rigid body (dynamic or static) attached to an Entity
3. **PhysicsCollider** - Defines collision geometry shapes attached to physics bodies

The physics system operates as part of the World tick cycle, updating transforms bidirectionally between the Transform component and PhysX's internal simulation state.

**Sources:** [src/PhysicsSolver.cpp:1-315](), [include/RavEngine/PhysicsSolver.hpp:1-157](), [include/RavEngine/PhysicsBodyComponent.hpp:1-362]()

---

## Architecture Overview

### Core Classes and Relationships

```mermaid
graph TB
    World["World"]
    PhysicsSolver["PhysicsSolver<br/>PxScene manager"]
    Entity["Entity<br/>ECS entity handle"]
    
    PhysicsBodyComponent["PhysicsBodyComponent<br/>Base class<br/>rigidActor: PxRigidActor*"]
    RigidBodyDynamic["RigidBodyDynamicComponent<br/>PxRigidDynamic*<br/>Movable bodies"]
    RigidBodyStatic["RigidBodyStaticComponent<br/>PxRigidStatic*<br/>Static geometry"]
    
    PhysicsCollider["PhysicsCollider<br/>Base collider<br/>collider: PxShape*"]
    BoxCollider["BoxCollider<br/>PxBoxGeometry"]
    SphereCollider["SphereCollider<br/>PxSphereGeometry"]
    CapsuleCollider["CapsuleCollider<br/>PxCapsuleGeometry"]
    MeshCollider["MeshCollider<br/>PxTriangleMesh"]
    ConvexMeshCollider["ConvexMeshCollider<br/>PxConvexMesh"]
    
    PhysicsCallback["PhysicsCallback<br/>Collision event receiver"]
    Transform["Transform<br/>World position/rotation"]
    
    World --> PhysicsSolver
    World --> Entity
    Entity --> PhysicsBodyComponent
    Entity --> Transform
    
    PhysicsBodyComponent --> RigidBodyDynamic
    PhysicsBodyComponent --> RigidBodyStatic
    
    PhysicsBodyComponent --> PhysicsCollider
    PhysicsBodyComponent --> PhysicsCallback
    
    PhysicsCollider --> BoxCollider
    PhysicsCollider --> SphereCollider
    PhysicsCollider --> CapsuleCollider
    PhysicsCollider --> MeshCollider
    PhysicsCollider --> ConvexMeshCollider
    
    PhysicsSolver -.->|"Spawn/Destroy"| PhysicsBodyComponent
    PhysicsSolver -.->|"onContact callbacks"| PhysicsBodyComponent
    PhysicsBodyComponent -.->|"sync pose"| Transform
```

**Diagram: Physics System Class Hierarchy and Relationships**

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/PhysicsBodyComponent.hpp:38-361](), [include/RavEngine/PhysicsSolver.hpp:34-156](), [include/RavEngine/PhysicsCollider.hpp:20-171]()

## Component-Based Physics

### Entity-Component Integration

Physics bodies are added to entities as components. Each `PhysicsBodyComponent` stores a pointer to its owning entity's ID in the `PxRigidActor::userData` field for bidirectional lookup during collision callbacks.

```mermaid
sequenceDiagram
    participant Entity
    participant PhysicsBodyComponent
    participant PhysicsSolver
    participant PxScene
    
    Entity->>PhysicsBodyComponent: EmplaceComponent<RigidBodyDynamicComponent>()
    activate PhysicsBodyComponent
    PhysicsBodyComponent->>PhysicsSolver: phys->createRigidDynamic()
    PhysicsSolver-->>PhysicsBodyComponent: PxRigidDynamic*
    PhysicsBodyComponent->>PhysicsBodyComponent: CompleteConstruction()
    PhysicsBodyComponent->>PhysicsSolver: Solver->Spawn(*this)
    PhysicsSolver->>PxScene: scene->addActor(*rigidActor)
    PhysicsSolver->>PhysicsBodyComponent: Store entity_t in userData
    deactivate PhysicsBodyComponent
```

**Diagram: Physics Component Creation Flow**

The entity ID is stored by copying bits directly into the `userData` pointer:

```
memcpy(&actor.rigidActor->userData, &e.id, sizeof(e.id));
```

**Sources:** [src/PhysicsBodyComponent.cpp:26-59](), [src/PhysicsSolver.cpp:218-226]()

---

### Collider Management

Colliders are attached to physics bodies via the `PhysicsBodyComponent::EmplaceCollider()` template method, which stores them in a `Colony<std::shared_ptr<PhysicsCollider>>`:

```mermaid
graph TD
    PhysicsBodyComponent["PhysicsBodyComponent"]
    Colony["Colony&lt;shared_ptr&lt;PhysicsCollider&gt;&gt;<br/>colliders"]
    
    BoxCollider["BoxCollider"]
    SphereCollider["SphereCollider"]
    CapsuleCollider["CapsuleCollider"]
    
    PxRigidActor["PxRigidActor"]
    PxShape1["PxShape* (Box)"]
    PxShape2["PxShape* (Sphere)"]
    PxShape3["PxShape* (Capsule)"]
    
    PhysicsBodyComponent --> Colony
    PhysicsBodyComponent --> PxRigidActor
    
    Colony --> BoxCollider
    Colony --> SphereCollider
    Colony --> CapsuleCollider
    
    BoxCollider --> PxShape1
    SphereCollider --> PxShape2
    CapsuleCollider --> PxShape3
    
    PxRigidActor -.->|"attachShape"| PxShape1
    PxRigidActor -.->|"attachShape"| PxShape2
    PxRigidActor -.->|"attachShape"| PxShape3
```

**Diagram: Collider Storage and Attachment**

Usage example:
```cpp
// From user code
auto handle = bodyComponent.EmplaceCollider<BoxCollider>(
    vector3(1, 1, 1),  // extent
    physicsMaterial,
    vector3(0, 0, 0),  // relative position
    quaternion(1, 0, 0, 0)  // relative rotation
);
```

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/PhysicsBodyComponent.hpp:76-90](), [src/PhysicsCollider.cpp:30-39]()

---

## Physics Simulation Lifecycle

### World Tick Integration

The physics simulation executes during the `World::Tick()` cycle, specifically during the `TickECS` phase:

```mermaid
sequenceDiagram
    participant World
    participant PhysicsSolver
    participant PxScene
    participant PhysicsLinkSystem
    participant Transform
    
    World->>World: PreTick()
    World->>World: TickECS()
    activate World
    
    World->>PhysicsLinkSystem: Read Transform -> PhysX
    PhysicsLinkSystem->>Transform: GetWorldPosition/Rotation()
    PhysicsLinkSystem->>PhysicsBodyComponent: setDynamicsWorldPose()
    
    World->>PhysicsSolver: Tick(deltaTime)
    activate PhysicsSolver
    PhysicsSolver->>PhysicsSolver: Calculate substeps
    loop nsteps times
        PhysicsSolver->>PxScene: scene->simulate(step_time)
        PhysicsSolver->>PxScene: scene->fetchResults(true)
        PxScene-->>PhysicsSolver: Collision events
        PhysicsSolver->>PhysicsSolver: onContact() / onTrigger()
    end
    deactivate PhysicsSolver
    
    World->>PhysicsLinkSystem: Write PhysX -> Transform
    PhysicsLinkSystem->>PhysicsBodyComponent: getDynamicsWorldPose()
    PhysicsLinkSystem->>Transform: SetWorldPosition/Rotation()
    
    deactivate World
    World->>World: PostTick()
```

**Diagram: Physics Simulation in World Tick Cycle**

**Sources:** [src/PhysicsSolver.cpp:242-256](), [Diagram 5: Physics and Animation Simulation Integration](#)

---

### Substepping

The `PhysicsSolver::Tick()` method implements automatic substepping to maintain simulation stability when frame times are large:

| Symbol | Description |
|--------|-------------|
| `max_step_time` | Maximum physics timestep (1/30 second) |
| `scaleFactor` | Frame delta time |
| `nsteps` | Calculated number of substeps: `ceil(step / max_step_time)` |
| `step_time` | Actual substep duration: `step / nsteps` |

**Sources:** [src/PhysicsSolver.cpp:242-256](), [include/RavEngine/PhysicsSolver.hpp:62]()

---

## Collision Filtering

### Filter Groups and Masks

RavEngine uses PhysX's layer-based collision filtering via two 32-bit integers per body:

| Field | Type | Description |
|-------|------|-------------|
| `filterGroup` | `PxU32` | Bitmask representing which layer(s) this body belongs to |
| `filterMask` | `PxU32` | Bitmask representing which layers this body can collide with |

The custom filter shader at [src/PhysicsSolver.cpp:32-49]() implements the collision rule:

```
Collision occurs if:
  (filterData0.word0 & filterData1.word1) && (filterData1.word0 & filterData0.word1)
```

Where `word0` contains the `filterGroup` and `word1` contains the `filterMask`.

**Sources:** [src/PhysicsSolver.cpp:32-49](), [include/RavEngine/PhysicsBodyComponent.hpp:64-65]()

---

### Collision Events

The `PhysicsSolver` implements `PxSimulationEventCallback` to receive collision events from PhysX:

```mermaid
graph TB
    PxScene["PxScene<br/>PhysX simulation"]
    PhysicsSolver["PhysicsSolver<br/>PxSimulationEventCallback"]
    
    onContact["onContact()<br/>Contact events"]
    onTrigger["onTrigger()<br/>Trigger events"]
    
    Body1["PhysicsBodyComponent<br/>Entity 1"]
    Body2["PhysicsBodyComponent<br/>Entity 2"]
    
    Receivers["UnorderedSet&lt;PhysicsCallback&gt;<br/>receivers"]
    
    Callback1["PhysicsCallback 1"]
    Callback2["PhysicsCallback 2"]
    
    PxScene -->|"simulate()"| PhysicsSolver
    PhysicsSolver --> onContact
    PhysicsSolver --> onTrigger
    
    onContact -->|"Resolve entity IDs"| Body1
    onContact -->|"Resolve entity IDs"| Body2
    
    Body1 --> Receivers
    Receivers --> Callback1
    Receivers --> Callback2
    
    Callback1 -.->|"OnColliderEnter"| Callback1
    Callback1 -.->|"OnColliderPersist"| Callback1
    Callback1 -.->|"OnColliderExit"| Callback1
    Callback1 -.->|"OnTriggerEnter"| Callback1
    Callback1 -.->|"OnTriggerExit"| Callback1
```

**Diagram: Collision Event Callback Flow**

Event types:
- **OnColliderEnter** - First frame of collision (`PxPairFlag::eNOTIFY_TOUCH_FOUND`)
- **OnColliderPersist** - Collision continues (`PxPairFlag::eNOTIFY_TOUCH_PERSISTS`)
- **OnColliderExit** - Collision ends (`PxPairFlag::eNOTIFY_TOUCH_LOST`)
- **OnTriggerEnter** - Entry into trigger volume
- **OnTriggerExit** - Exit from trigger volume

**Sources:** [src/PhysicsSolver.cpp:53-143](), [src/PhysicsBodyComponent.cpp:274-316]()

---

## Thread Safety and Locking

### Scene Lock Wrappers

All PhysX scene access must be properly locked. `PhysicsBodyComponent` provides helper methods:

```mermaid
graph LR
    LockWrite["LockWrite(lambda)<br/>Write operations"]
    LockRead["LockRead(lambda)<br/>Read operations"]
    
    PxScene["PxScene"]
    
    LockWrite -->|"scene->lockWrite()"| PxScene
    LockWrite -->|"Execute lambda"| Lambda1["User code"]
    LockWrite -->|"scene->unlockWrite()"| PxScene
    
    LockRead -->|"scene->lockRead()"| PxScene
    LockRead -->|"Execute lambda"| Lambda2["User code"]
    LockRead -->|"scene->unlockRead()"| PxScene
```

**Diagram: Thread-Safe Scene Access Pattern**

Example usage from the codebase:
```cpp
// Read lock example
LockRead([&] {
    auto vel = static_cast<PxRigidBody*>(rigidActor)->getLinearVelocity();
});

// Write lock example
LockWrite([&] {
    static_cast<PxRigidDynamic*>(rigidActor)->setLinearVelocity(
        PxVec3(newvel.x, newvel.y, newvel.z), autowake
    );
});
```

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/PhysicsBodyComponent.hpp:207-231](), [src/PhysicsBodyComponent.cpp:92-103](), [src/PhysicsBodyComponent.cpp:234-249]()

### RigidBodyDynamicComponent

Inherits from `PhysicsBodyComponent`. Represents movable physics bodies with mass, velocity, and forces.

Key methods:
- `SetMass(decimalType)` / `GetMass()`
- `SetLinearVelocity()` / `GetLinearVelocity()`
- `SetAngularVelocity()` / `GetAngularVelocity()`
- `AddForce()` / `AddTorque()`
- `Wake()` / `Sleep()` / `IsSleeping()`
- `SetKinematicTarget()` - For kinematic bodies

**Location:** [include/RavEngine/PhysicsBodyComponent.hpp:236-346]()

---

### RigidBodyStaticComponent

Inherits from `PhysicsBodyComponent`. Represents immovable static geometry like terrain, buildings, or level geometry. Cannot have velocity or forces applied.

**Location:** [include/RavEngine/PhysicsBodyComponent.hpp:348-360]()

## Contact Point Data

The `ContactPairPoint` struct provides detailed collision information:

| Field | Type | Description |
|-------|------|-------------|
| `position` | `vector3` | World-space contact point location |
| `normal` | `vector3` | Contact surface normal |
| `impulse` | `vector3` | Impulse applied at contact point |
| `separation` | `decimalType` | Penetration depth (negative) or separation (positive) |

Contact point extraction is controlled by `PhysicsBodyComponent::SetWantsContactData(bool)`. When disabled, collision callbacks receive `nullptr` for contact points to save performance.

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/PhysicsBodyComponent.hpp:28-36](), [src/PhysicsSolver.cpp:73-85]()

---

## Entity ID Storage

RavEngine stores entity IDs directly in PhysX's `userData` pointer field using `memcpy`:

```
entity_t id = /* entity id */;
memcpy(&rigidActor->userData, &id, sizeof(id));
```

During collision callbacks, the ID is extracted:
```
entity_t id;
memcpy(&id, &actor->userData, sizeof(id));
Entity entity(id, owner);
```

This avoids dynamic allocation and provides O(1) entity lookup during collision events.

**Sources:** [src/PhysicsSolver.cpp:63-68](), [src/PhysicsSolver.cpp:220-221]()

---

## Force Modes

The `ForceMode` enum controls how forces and torques are applied:

| Mode | Description |
|------|-------------|
| `Force` | Force dependent on mass and timestep |
| `Impulse` | Instantaneous force change, mass-dependent |
| `Acceleration` | Force independent of mass |
| `VelocityChange` | Instantaneous velocity change, mass-independent |

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/PhysicsBodyComponent.hpp:18-23](), [src/PhysicsBodyComponent.cpp:344-351]()

---

## Coordinate Conversion

RavEngine's vector types are converted to PhysX types inline:

```cpp
static inline PxVec3 convert(const vector3& v) {
    return PxVec3(v.x, v.y, v.z);
}

static inline PxQuat convertQuat(const quaternion& q) {
    return PxQuat(q.x, q.y, q.z, q.w);
}
```

**Sources:** [src/PhysicsBodyComponent.cpp:18-24]()

---

## Summary

The RavEngine physics system provides a component-based wrapper around NVIDIA PhysX with the following key characteristics:

- **Component-based design** - Physics bodies are ECS components attached to entities
- **Bidirectional synchronization** - Transforms sync between ECS and PhysX simulation
- **Collision filtering** - Layer-based filtering via `filterGroup` and `filterMask`
- **Event-driven callbacks** - `PhysicsCallback` receivers handle collision events
- **Thread-safe API** - Scene lock wrappers ensure safe concurrent access
- **Automatic substepping** - Maintains simulation stability at low framerates
- **Multiple collider shapes** - Box, sphere, capsule, mesh, and convex mesh support

For implementation details on specific components, see the child pages:
- [Physics Bodies and Colliders](#5.1) - Component usage and collider types
- [Physics Simulation and Events](#5.2) - Solver operation and callback system
- [Scene Queries and Raycasting](#5.3) - Spatial queries and overlap tests

**Sources:** All files listed in this document29:T6264,# Physics Bodies and Colliders
