This document covers the physics body components (`PhysicsBodyComponent`, `RigidBodyDynamicComponent`, `RigidBodyStaticComponent`) and collider shapes that enable rigid body simulation and collision detection in RavEngine through PhysX integration. 

For information about the physics simulation loop and collision callbacks, see [Physics Simulation and Events](#5.2). For scene queries like raycasting and overlap tests, see [Scene Queries and Raycasting](#5.3).

## Overview

RavEngine's physics system is built on NVIDIA PhysX and provides rigid body dynamics through component-based architecture. Physics bodies represent objects that participate in physics simulation, while colliders define their collision geometry. The system supports:

- Dynamic rigid bodies with forces, velocities, and mass
- Static rigid bodies for immovable geometry
- Multiple collider shapes per body
- Collision filtering and layering
- Contact point data extraction
- Trigger volumes
- Thread-safe access to PhysX simulation

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/PhysicsBodyComponent.hpp:38-234](), [src/PhysicsBodyComponent.cpp:1-394]()

## Physics Body Component Hierarchy

```mermaid
classDiagram
    class PhysicsBodyComponent {
        +PxRigidActor* rigidActor
        +PxU32 filterGroup
        +PxU32 filterMask
        +EmplaceCollider()
        +DestroyCollider()
        +AddReceiver()
        +RemoveReceiver()
        +getDynamicsWorldPose()
        +setDynamicsWorldPose()
        +SetGravityEnabled()
        +SetSimulationEnabled()
        -Colony~PhysicsCollider~ colliders
        -UnorderedSet~PhysicsCallback~ receivers
    }
    
    class RigidBodyDynamicComponent {
        +SetMass()
        +GetMass()
        +SetLinearVelocity()
        +GetLinearVelocity()
        +SetAngularVelocity()
        +GetAngularVelocity()
        +AddForce()
        +AddTorque()
        +SetAxisLock()
        +Wake()
        +Sleep()
        +IsSleeping()
        +SetKinematicTarget()
    }
    
    class RigidBodyStaticComponent {
    }
    
    class ComponentWithOwner {
        +Entity GetOwner()
    }
    
    class IDebugRenderable {
        +DebugDraw()
    }
    
    ComponentWithOwner <|-- PhysicsBodyComponent
    IDebugRenderable <|-- PhysicsBodyComponent
    PhysicsBodyComponent <|-- RigidBodyDynamicComponent
    PhysicsBodyComponent <|-- RigidBodyStaticComponent
    
    PhysicsBodyComponent o-- "0..*" PhysicsCollider
    PhysicsBodyComponent o-- "0..*" PhysicsCallback
```

**Diagram 1:** Physics body component class hierarchy and relationships

The `PhysicsBodyComponent` base class wraps PhysX's `PxRigidActor` and provides common functionality. `RigidBodyDynamicComponent` is used for movable objects affected by forces and gravity, while `RigidBodyStaticComponent` represents immovable scenery. Both types can have multiple colliders attached.

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/PhysicsBodyComponent.hpp:38-360]()

## Creating Physics Bodies

### Dynamic Bodies

Dynamic bodies respond to forces, gravity, and collisions. They are created by emplacing a `RigidBodyDynamicComponent` on an entity:

```cpp
// Entity must already have a Transform component
auto entity = world->Instantiate<Entity>();
entity.EmplaceComponent<Transform>();

// Create dynamic body
auto& body = entity.EmplaceComponent<RigidBodyDynamicComponent>();
```

The constructor creates a PhysX `PxRigidDynamic` actor and registers it with the `PhysicsSolver`. The entity's `Transform` component is required and used to initialize the physics pose.

**Sources:** [src/PhysicsBodyComponent.cpp:53-59](), [include/RavEngine/PhysicsBodyComponent.hpp:236-243]()

### Static Bodies

Static bodies do not move during simulation but can collide with dynamic bodies:

```cpp
auto entity = world->Instantiate<Entity>();
entity.EmplaceComponent<Transform>();

// Create static body
auto& staticBody = entity.EmplaceComponent<RigidBodyStaticComponent>();
```

Static bodies create a PhysX `PxRigidStatic` actor. They are optimal for level geometry and environmental objects.

**Sources:** [src/PhysicsBodyComponent.cpp:380-383](), [include/RavEngine/PhysicsBodyComponent.hpp:348-360]()

### Collision Filtering

Physics bodies support layer-based collision filtering via `filterGroup` and `filterMask` fields:

```cpp
// Constructor with filter parameters
auto& body = entity.EmplaceComponent<RigidBodyDynamicComponent>(
    entity,
    FilterLayers::L0,        // filterGroup - this object's layer
    FilterLayers::L1 | FilterLayers::L2  // filterMask - layers this can collide with
);

// Or set after construction
body.filterGroup = FilterLayers::L0;
body.filterMask = FilterLayers::L1 | FilterLayers::L2;
```

The filter shader uses bitwise operations to determine if two bodies should collide:

- Two bodies collide if `(bodyA.filterGroup & bodyB.filterMask) && (bodyB.filterGroup & bodyA.filterMask)`

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/PhysicsBodyComponent.hpp:64-65](), [include/RavEngine/PhysicsBodyComponent.hpp:239-241](), [src/PhysicsSolver.cpp:32-49]()

### Lifecycle Integration

```mermaid
sequenceDiagram
    participant Entity
    participant RigidBodyDynamicComponent
    participant PhysicsSolver
    participant PxScene
    
    Entity->>RigidBodyDynamicComponent: EmplaceComponent()
    RigidBodyDynamicComponent->>RigidBodyDynamicComponent: Create PxRigidDynamic
    RigidBodyDynamicComponent->>RigidBodyDynamicComponent: CompleteConstruction()
    RigidBodyDynamicComponent->>PhysicsSolver: Spawn(this)
    PhysicsSolver->>PxScene: addActor(rigidActor)
    
    Note over Entity,PxScene: Body is now in simulation
    
    Entity->>RigidBodyDynamicComponent: Destroy()
    RigidBodyDynamicComponent->>PhysicsSolver: Destroy(this)
    PhysicsSolver->>PxScene: removeActor(rigidActor)
    RigidBodyDynamicComponent->>RigidBodyDynamicComponent: rigidActor->release()
```

**Diagram 2:** Physics body creation and destruction lifecycle

The `CompleteConstruction()` method registers the body with the world's `PhysicsSolver`, which adds it to the PhysX scene. The entity's ID is stored in the `rigidActor->userData` field for event callbacks.

**Sources:** [src/PhysicsBodyComponent.cpp:28-30](), [src/PhysicsBodyComponent.cpp:36-49](), [src/PhysicsSolver.cpp:218-226](), [src/PhysicsSolver.cpp:232-236]()

## Collider Types

All colliders inherit from `PhysicsCollider` and are attached to physics bodies via `EmplaceCollider()`. Each collider requires a `PhysicsMaterial` that defines friction and restitution properties.

### BoxCollider

Axis-aligned box shape defined by half-extents:

```cpp
auto material = New<PhysicsMaterial>(0.5f, 0.5f, 0.3f); // static, dynamic friction, restitution

auto handle = body.EmplaceCollider<BoxCollider>(
    vector3(1.0, 2.0, 1.0),  // half-extents (box is 2x4x2 total)
    material,
    vector3(0, 1, 0),        // relative position offset
    quaternion(1, 0, 0, 0)   // relative rotation
);
```

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/PhysicsCollider.hpp:77-98](), [src/PhysicsCollider.cpp:30-39]()

### SphereCollider

Spherical shape defined by radius:

```cpp
auto handle = body.EmplaceCollider<SphereCollider>(
    1.5f,           // radius
    material,
    vector3(0, 0, 0),
    quaternion(1, 0, 0, 0)
);

// Query radius
decimalType r = sphereCollider->GetRadius();
```

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/PhysicsCollider.hpp:100-119](), [src/PhysicsCollider.cpp:41-56]()

### CapsuleCollider

Capsule shape defined by radius and half-height (distance from center to pole):

```cpp
auto handle = body.EmplaceCollider<CapsuleCollider>(
    0.5f,   // radius
    1.0f,   // half-height
    material,
    vector3(0, 1, 0),
    quaternion(1, 0, 0, 0)
);
```

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/PhysicsCollider.hpp:121-141](), [src/PhysicsCollider.cpp:59-66]()

### MeshCollider

Triangle mesh collider for complex static geometry. Uses PhysX mesh cooking:

```cpp
auto meshAsset = MeshAsset::Manager::Get("statue.rvem");
auto handle = body.EmplaceCollider<MeshCollider>(meshAsset, material);
```

The constructor extracts vertex positions and indices from the `MeshAsset`, creates a PhysX `PxTriangleMesh` via cooking, and attaches it. Mesh colliders are typically used with `RigidBodyStaticComponent` for performance.

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/PhysicsCollider.hpp:143-156](), [src/PhysicsCollider.cpp:68-114]()

### ConvexMeshCollider

Convex hull collider suitable for dynamic bodies with complex shapes:

```cpp
auto meshAsset = MeshAsset::Manager::Get("rock.rvem");
auto handle = body.EmplaceCollider<ConvexMeshCollider>(meshAsset, material);
```

Creates a PhysX `PxConvexMesh` by computing the convex hull of the mesh vertices. Better suited for dynamic bodies than triangle meshes.

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/PhysicsCollider.hpp:158-170](), [src/PhysicsCollider.cpp:116-144]()

### Collider Management

```mermaid
graph TD
    PhysicsBodyComponent["PhysicsBodyComponent"]
    Colony["Colony&lt;shared_ptr&lt;PhysicsCollider&gt;&gt;<br/>colliders"]
    
    EmplaceCollider["EmplaceCollider&lt;T&gt;(args)"]
    CreateShape["Create PxShape<br/>(Box/Sphere/etc)"]
    AttachToActor["PxRigidActorExt::createExclusiveShape"]
    UpdateFilter["UpdateFilterData()"]
    ReturnHandle["Return ColliderHandle"]
    
    DestroyCollider["DestroyCollider(handle)"]
    EraseFromColony["colliders.erase(handle.id)"]
    DetachShape["rigidActor->detachShape()"]
    
    PhysicsBodyComponent --> Colony
    
    EmplaceCollider --> CreateShape
    CreateShape --> AttachToActor
    AttachToActor --> UpdateFilter
    UpdateFilter --> ReturnHandle
    ReturnHandle --> Colony
    
    DestroyCollider --> EraseFromColony
    EraseFromColony --> DetachShape
```

**Diagram 3:** Collider emplacement and destruction workflow

The `EmplaceCollider()` method constructs the collider in-place and returns a `ColliderHandle` that can be used to destroy it later. Colliders are stored in a `Colony` for stable iteration during physics callbacks.

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/PhysicsBodyComponent.hpp:76-90](), [src/PhysicsCollider.cpp:23-28](), [src/PhysicsBodyComponent.cpp:61-64]()

## Collider Properties

### Collision Type: Collider vs Trigger

Colliders can act as solid collision shapes or as trigger volumes:

```cpp
// Default: solid collider
collider->SetType(PhysicsCollider::CollisionType::Collider);

// Trigger: detects overlaps but doesn't physically collide
collider->SetType(PhysicsCollider::CollisionType::Trigger);

auto type = collider->GetType();
```

Triggers generate `OnTriggerEnter` and `OnTriggerExit` events instead of collision events. They do not affect physical simulation.

**Sources:** [src/PhysicsCollider.cpp:146-163](), [include/RavEngine/PhysicsCollider.hpp:33-46]()

### Scene Query Participation

Control whether a collider participates in raycasts and overlap queries:

```cpp
collider->SetQueryable(true);   // participates in scene queries
collider->SetQueryable(false);  // ignored by raycasts/overlaps

bool isQueryable = collider->GetQueryable();
```

**Sources:** [src/PhysicsCollider.cpp:165-173](), [include/RavEngine/PhysicsCollider.hpp:48-59]()

### Relative Transformation

Colliders can be offset from their owning body's transform:

```cpp
collider->SetRelativeTransform(
    vector3(0, 1, 0),        // position offset
    quaternion(1, 0, 0, 0)   // rotation offset
);

Transformation relativeTransform = collider->GetRelativeTransform();
```

This is useful for placing colliders at specific locations on complex objects (e.g., a character's head or weapon).

**Sources:** [src/PhysicsCollider.cpp:175-182](), [include/RavEngine/PhysicsCollider.hpp:61-71]()

## Collision Event Handling

Physics bodies receive collision events through `PhysicsCallback` receivers. Multiple callbacks can be registered per body.

### Registering Callbacks

```cpp
struct MyCallback : public PhysicsCallback {
    void OnColliderEnter(PhysicsBodyComponent& other, 
                        const ContactPairPoint* contacts, 
                        size_t numContacts) override {
        // Handle collision start
    }
    
    void OnColliderPersist(PhysicsBodyComponent& other,
                          const ContactPairPoint* contacts,
                          size_t numContacts) override {
        // Handle ongoing collision
    }
    
    void OnColliderExit(PhysicsBodyComponent& other,
                       const ContactPairPoint* contacts,
                       size_t numContacts) override {
        // Handle collision end
    }
    
    void OnTriggerEnter(PhysicsBodyComponent& other) override {
        // Handle trigger enter
    }
    
    void OnTriggerExit(PhysicsBodyComponent& other) override {
        // Handle trigger exit
    }
};

auto callback = std::make_shared<MyCallback>();
body.AddReceiver(callback);

// Later, to remove:
body.RemoveReceiver(callback);
```

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/PhysicsBodyComponent.hpp:95-107](), [src/PhysicsBodyComponent.cpp:66-88](), [src/PhysicsBodyComponent.cpp:274-316]()

### Contact Point Data

Contact information is provided through `ContactPairPoint` structs:

```cpp
struct ContactPairPoint {
    vector3 position;   // world-space contact point
    vector3 normal;     // contact normal (points from this to other)
    vector3 impulse;    // impulse applied at this contact
    decimalType separation;  // penetration depth (negative) or separation distance
};
```

To receive contact data, enable it on the body:

```cpp
body.SetWantsContactData(true);
```

If disabled (default), `contactPoints` will be `nullptr` and `numContacts` will be 0, improving performance.

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/PhysicsBodyComponent.hpp:28-36](), [src/PhysicsBodyComponent.cpp:389-393](), [include/RavEngine/PhysicsBodyComponent.hpp:184-193]()

### Collision Event Flow

```mermaid
sequenceDiagram
    participant PxScene
    participant PhysicsSolver
    participant PhysicsBodyComponent
    participant PhysicsCallback
    
    PxScene->>PhysicsSolver: onContact(pairHeader, pairs)
    
    PhysicsSolver->>PhysicsSolver: Extract entity IDs from userData
    PhysicsSolver->>PhysicsSolver: Get PhysicsBodyComponent refs
    
    alt wantsContactData enabled
        PhysicsSolver->>PhysicsSolver: extractContacts() from PxContactPair
        PhysicsSolver->>PhysicsSolver: Convert to ContactPairPoint[]
    end
    
    alt eNOTIFY_TOUCH_FOUND
        PhysicsSolver->>PhysicsBodyComponent: OnColliderEnter(other, contacts, count)
        PhysicsBodyComponent->>PhysicsCallback: OnColliderEnter() for each receiver
    end
    
    alt eNOTIFY_TOUCH_PERSISTS
        PhysicsSolver->>PhysicsBodyComponent: OnColliderPersist(other, contacts, count)
        PhysicsBodyComponent->>PhysicsCallback: OnColliderPersist() for each receiver
    end
    
    alt eNOTIFY_TOUCH_LOST
        PhysicsSolver->>PhysicsBodyComponent: OnColliderExit(other, contacts, count)
        PhysicsBodyComponent->>PhysicsCallback: OnColliderExit() for each receiver
    end
```

**Diagram 4:** Collision event propagation from PhysX to user callbacks

The `PhysicsSolver::onContact()` method extracts entity IDs from `PxRigidActor::userData`, retrieves the corresponding `PhysicsBodyComponent` instances, and dispatches events to all registered receivers.

**Sources:** [src/PhysicsSolver.cpp:53-105](), [src/PhysicsBodyComponent.cpp:274-299]()

## Dynamic Body Properties

### Mass and Inertia

```cpp
// Set mass directly
dynamicBody.SetMass(10.0f);

decimalType mass = dynamicBody.GetMass();
decimalType invMass = dynamicBody.GetMassInverse();
```

PhysX automatically computes inertia tensors based on the attached colliders and mass distribution.

**Sources:** [src/PhysicsBodyComponent.cpp:324-342](), [include/RavEngine/PhysicsBodyComponent.hpp:305-318]()

### Velocity

Linear and angular velocity can be read or set directly:

```cpp
// Get velocities
vector3 linearVel = dynamicBody.GetLinearVelocity();
vector3 angularVel = dynamicBody.GetAngularVelocity();  // euler angles

// Set velocities
dynamicBody.SetLinearVelocity(vector3(5, 0, 0), true);  // autowake=true
dynamicBody.SetAngularVelocity(vector3(0, 1, 0), false); // autowake=false
```

The `autowake` parameter determines if the body should be woken from sleep when velocity is set.

**Sources:** [src/PhysicsBodyComponent.cpp:209-249](), [include/RavEngine/PhysicsBodyComponent.hpp:244-256]()

### Forces and Torques

Apply forces/torques with different modes:

```cpp
enum class ForceMode {
    Force,           // mass-dependent continuous force
    Impulse,         // mass-dependent instantaneous force
    Acceleration,    // mass-independent continuous acceleration
    VelocityChange   // mass-independent instantaneous velocity change
};

// Add force
dynamicBody.AddForce(vector3(100, 0, 0), ForceMode::Force);

// Add torque
dynamicBody.AddTorque(vector3(0, 50, 0), ForceMode::Impulse);

// Clear accumulated forces/torques
dynamicBody.ClearAllForces();
dynamicBody.ClearAllTorques();
```

Forces and torques accumulate and are applied during the next physics substep.

**Sources:** [src/PhysicsBodyComponent.cpp:344-377](), [include/RavEngine/PhysicsBodyComponent.hpp:18-23](), [include/RavEngine/PhysicsBodyComponent.hpp:320-340]()

### Axis Locking

Constrain motion along specific axes:

```cpp
enum AxisLock {
    Linear_X  = (1 << 0),
    Linear_Y  = (1 << 1),
    Linear_Z  = (1 << 2),
    Angular_X = (1 << 3),
    Angular_Y = (1 << 4),
    Angular_Z = (1 << 5)
};

// Lock Y-axis translation and X/Z rotation (2D platformer-style)
dynamicBody.SetAxisLock(AxisLock::Linear_Y | AxisLock::Angular_X | AxisLock::Angular_Z);

uint16_t locks = dynamicBody.GetAxisLock();
```

**Sources:** [src/PhysicsBodyComponent.cpp:251-257](), [include/RavEngine/PhysicsBodyComponent.hpp:282-302]()

### Damping

Linear and angular damping reduce velocity over time:

```cpp
// Air resistance for linear motion
dynamicBody.SetLinearDamping(0.1f);

// Rotational drag
dynamicBody.SetAngularDamping(0.05f);

float linearDamp = dynamicBody.GetLinearDamping();
float angularDamp = dynamicBody.GetAngularDamping();
```

**Sources:** [src/PhysicsBodyComponent.cpp:176-207](), [include/RavEngine/PhysicsBodyComponent.hpp:261-265]()

### Sleep Control

Physics bodies automatically sleep when inactive to save CPU:

```cpp
// Manually wake a sleeping body
dynamicBody.Wake();

// Force body to sleep
dynamicBody.Sleep();

// Check sleep state
if (dynamicBody.IsSleeping()) {
    // Body is asleep
}
```

**Sources:** [src/PhysicsBodyComponent.cpp:259-272](), [include/RavEngine/PhysicsBodyComponent.hpp:268-280]()

### Kinematic Targets

For animated objects, set kinematic targets instead of directly manipulating transform:

```cpp
// Body moves smoothly toward this target
dynamicBody.SetKinematicTarget(
    vector3(10, 0, 5),          // target position
    quaternion(1, 0, 0, 0)      // target rotation
);

auto [targetPos, targetRot] = dynamicBody.GetKinematicTarget();
```

This is preferable to teleportation for character controllers and moving platforms.

**Sources:** [src/PhysicsBodyComponent.cpp:161-174](), [include/RavEngine/PhysicsBodyComponent.hpp:258-259]()

## Common Body Properties

These properties apply to both static and dynamic bodies.

### Gravity Control

```cpp
// Disable gravity for floating objects
body.SetGravityEnabled(false);

// Re-enable gravity
body.SetGravityEnabled(true);

bool hasGravity = body.GetGravityEnabled();
```

**Sources:** [src/PhysicsBodyComponent.cpp:109-119](), [include/RavEngine/PhysicsBodyComponent.hpp:123-129]()

### Sleep Notifications

Enable callbacks when bodies sleep/wake:

```cpp
body.SetSleepNotificationsEnabled(true);

bool notificationsOn = body.GetSleepNotificationsEnabled();
```

When enabled, the `PhysicsSolver` will invoke `onWake()` and `onSleep()` callbacks (currently empty implementations).

**Sources:** [src/PhysicsBodyComponent.cpp:125-133](), [include/RavEngine/PhysicsBodyComponent.hpp:131-136]()

### Simulation Enable/Disable

Temporarily disable physics simulation for a body:

```cpp
// Disable simulation (removes constraints, clears forces, sleeps body)
body.SetSimulationEnabled(false);

// Re-enable simulation
body.SetSimulationEnabled(true);

bool isSimulating = body.GetSimulationEnabled();
```

**Sources:** [src/PhysicsBodyComponent.cpp:140-154](), [include/RavEngine/PhysicsBodyComponent.hpp:138-143]()

### World Pose

Get or set the physics world transform:

```cpp
// Get current physics pose (thread-safe)
auto [position, rotation] = body.getDynamicsWorldPose();

// Teleport to new pose (thread-safe)
body.setDynamicsWorldPose(
    vector3(0, 10, 0),
    quaternion(1, 0, 0, 0)
);
```

Setting the pose marks it as needing synchronization with the `Transform` component. The system uses internal locking to ensure thread safety when accessing the PhysX scene.

**Sources:** [src/PhysicsBodyComponent.cpp:90-103](), [include/RavEngine/PhysicsBodyComponent.hpp:109-121]()

## Integration with Transform System

```mermaid
graph LR
    subgraph "Main Thread - ECS"
        Transform["Transform Component"]
        PhysicsBodyComponent["PhysicsBodyComponent"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Physics Thread"
        PxRigidActor["PxRigidActor"]
        PxScene["PxScene::simulate()"]
    end
    
    subgraph "PhysicsLinkSystem"
        PreTick["PhysicsLinkSystemWrite<br/>Pre-Tick"]
        PostTick["PhysicsLinkSystemRead<br/>Post-Tick"]
    end
    
    Transform -->|"initial pose"| PhysicsBodyComponent
    PhysicsBodyComponent -->|"CompleteConstruction()"| PxRigidActor
    
    PreTick -->|"if setPoseNeedsSync"| PxRigidActor
    Transform -.->|"read world transform"| PreTick
    PreTick -.->|"setGlobalPose()"| PxRigidActor
    
    PxScene -->|"update poses"| PxRigidActor
    
    PostTick -->|"getGlobalPose()"| PxRigidActor
    PostTick -.->|"write world transform"| Transform
```

**Diagram 5:** Synchronization between Transform components and PhysX rigid actors

The `PhysicsLinkSystemWrite` runs before physics simulation and updates PhysX poses from `Transform` components when `setPoseNeedsSync` is true. After simulation, `PhysicsLinkSystemRead` copies updated poses back to `Transform` components for rendering.

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/PhysicsBodyComponent.hpp:53-55](), [src/PhysicsBodyComponent.cpp:98-103](), [src/PhysicsBodyComponent.cpp:318-322]()

## Thread Safety

All physics operations use scene-level locking to ensure thread safety:

```cpp
// Internal locking patterns
template<typename T>
inline void LockWrite(const T& func){
    auto scene = rigidActor->getScene();
    if (scene){
        scene->lockWrite();
        func();
        scene->unlockWrite();
    }
    else{
        func();
    }
}
```

The `LockRead()` and `LockWrite()` methods wrap PhysX's scene locking API. They gracefully handle cases where the actor hasn't been added to a scene yet.

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/PhysicsBodyComponent.hpp:207-231](), [src/PhysicsBodyComponent.cpp:92-94](), [src/PhysicsBodyComponent.cpp:100-102]()

## Debug Rendering

Physics bodies support debug visualization when `IDebugRenderable` is enabled (non-server builds):

```cpp
// Automatically called by debug rendering system
body.DebugDraw(debugDrawer, debugColor, transform);
```

Each collider type implements its own debug drawing:
- `BoxCollider`: Draws wireframe rectangular prism
- `SphereCollider`: Draws wireframe sphere
- `CapsuleCollider`: Draws wireframe capsule
- `MeshCollider`: Draws wireframe mesh (debug builds only)

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/PhysicsBodyComponent.hpp:195-203](), [src/PhysicsCollider.cpp:188-204]()

## Performance Considerations

| Feature | Performance Impact | Recommendation |
|---------|-------------------|----------------|
| Contact point data | High | Only enable with `SetWantsContactData(true)` when needed |
| Mesh colliders on dynamic bodies | Very high | Use `ConvexMeshCollider` or primitive shapes instead |
| Many small colliders | Medium | Consider combining into fewer larger shapes |
| Collision filtering | Low | Use extensively to avoid unnecessary collision checks |
| Scene queries on triggers | Low | Mark triggers as non-queryable if not needed for raycasts |

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/PhysicsBodyComponent.hpp:184-193](), [src/PhysicsSolver.cpp:76-84]()2a:T4c59,# Physics Simulation and Events

This document covers the physics simulation lifecycle managed by `PhysicsSolver`, collision and trigger event handling, physics callback registration, and contact point data extraction. For information about physics bodies and colliders themselves, see [Physics Bodies and Colliders](#5.1). For scene queries and raycasting, see [Scene Queries and Raycasting](#5.3).

## Overview

RavEngine's physics system is built on NVIDIA PhysX and provides rigid body dynamics simulation with comprehensive event handling. The `PhysicsSolver` class manages a PhysX `PxScene`, executes simulation steps with automatic sub-stepping, and dispatches collision/trigger events to registered callbacks. Each `World` owns a single `PhysicsSolver` instance that processes all physics bodies in that world.

## PhysicsSolver Architecture

The `PhysicsSolver` integrates with PhysX through static foundation objects and per-world scene management.

### Class Structure and PhysX Integration

```mermaid
graph TD
    World["World<br/>ECS Container"] -->|owns| PhysicsSolver["PhysicsSolver<br/>Per-world simulation"]
    
    PhysicsSolver -->|uses| PxScene["PxScene*<br/>PhysX scene instance"]
    PhysicsSolver -->|inherits| PxSimulationEventCallback["PxSimulationEventCallback<br/>Event interface"]
    PhysicsSolver -->|uses| PhysicsTaskDispatcher["PhysicsTaskDispatcher<br/>Multi-threaded execution"]
    
    PhysicsSolver -.->|static| PxFoundation["PxFoundation*<br/>Global PhysX foundation"]
    PhysicsSolver -.->|static| PxPhysics["PxPhysics*<br/>Global physics SDK"]
    PhysicsSolver -.->|static| PxPvd["PxPvd*<br/>Visual debugger"]
    
    PhysicsBodyComponent["PhysicsBodyComponent"] -->|contains| PxRigidActor["PxRigidActor*<br/>PhysX actor"]
    
    PxScene -->|simulates| PxRigidActor
    PxScene -->|callbacks| PhysicsSolver
    
    PhysicsSolver -->|Spawn/Destroy| PhysicsBodyComponent
```

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/PhysicsSolver.hpp:34-46](), [src/PhysicsSolver.cpp:259-296]()

The `PhysicsSolver` manages both global static PhysX objects (foundation, physics SDK, visual debugger) and per-world scene instances. Static objects are shared across all worlds in the application and initialized on first use.

| Static Member | Type | Purpose |
|--------------|------|---------|
| `foundation` | `PxFoundation*` | PhysX memory and error management |
| `phys` | `PxPhysics*` | Global PhysX SDK instance |
| `pvd` | `PxPvd*` | Connection to PhysX Visual Debugger |

| Instance Member | Type | Purpose |
|----------------|------|---------|
| `scene` | `PxScene*` | Per-world physics simulation scene |
| `owner` | `World*` | Back-reference to owning world |
| `taskDispatcher` | `PhysicsTaskDispatcher` | Multi-threaded task execution |

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/PhysicsSolver.hpp:38-46](), [src/PhysicsSolver.cpp:24-28]()

### Initialization and Configuration

The constructor configures the PhysX scene with gravity, collision filtering, and simulation callbacks:

[src/PhysicsSolver.cpp:259-296]()

Key configuration details:
- **Gravity:** Default `-9.81 m/sÂ²` on Y-axis
- **Filter Shader:** Custom `FilterShader` function implementing layer-based filtering
- **Simulation Event Callback:** `this` pointer for collision/trigger events
- **CPU Dispatcher:** `PhysicsTaskDispatcher` for multi-threaded execution
- **PhysX Extensions:** Initialized for additional functionality

**Sources:** [src/PhysicsSolver.cpp:276-295]()

## Simulation Lifecycle

The physics simulation executes during the `World::Tick` phase with automatic sub-stepping for stability.

### Tick Execution Flow

```mermaid
sequenceDiagram
    participant World
    participant PhysicsSolver
    participant PxScene
    participant PhysicsBodyComponent
    participant Callbacks
    
    World->>PhysicsSolver: Tick(deltaTime)
    
    PhysicsSolver->>PhysicsSolver: Calculate step = deltaTime / (evalNormal/2)
    PhysicsSolver->>PhysicsSolver: Calculate nsteps = ceil(step / max_step_time)
    PhysicsSolver->>PhysicsSolver: Calculate step_time = step / nsteps
    
    PhysicsSolver->>PxScene: lockWrite()
    
    loop For each substep
        PhysicsSolver->>PxScene: simulate(step_time)
        PhysicsSolver->>PxScene: fetchResults(true)
        Note over PxScene: Blocking wait for results
        
        PxScene-->>PhysicsSolver: onContact() callbacks
        PxScene-->>PhysicsSolver: onTrigger() callbacks
        
        PhysicsSolver->>PhysicsBodyComponent: OnColliderEnter/Persist/Exit
        PhysicsSolver->>PhysicsBodyComponent: OnTriggerEnter/Exit
        
        PhysicsBodyComponent->>Callbacks: Dispatch to receivers
    end
    
    PhysicsSolver->>PxScene: unlockWrite()
```

**Sources:** [src/PhysicsSolver.cpp:242-256]()

### Sub-stepping Algorithm

The simulation implements automatic sub-stepping to maintain stability when frame times exceed the maximum step time:

[src/PhysicsSolver.cpp:242-256]()

- **Maximum Step Time:** `1.0f/30` (33.33ms) - [include/RavEngine/PhysicsSolver.hpp:62]()
- **Step Calculation:** `scaleFactor / (GetApp()->evalNormal / 2)`
- **Sub-step Count:** `ceil(step / max_step_time)` ensures no single step exceeds maximum
- **Step Time:** Divided evenly across sub-steps

This ensures the simulation remains stable even during frame drops by breaking large time deltas into smaller, fixed-size steps.

**Sources:** [src/PhysicsSolver.cpp:242-256](), [include/RavEngine/PhysicsSolver.hpp:62]()

## Collision Events

Collision events fire when non-trigger shapes interact, providing detailed contact information.

### Event Types and Lifecycle

| Event | Method | Trigger Condition | Contact Points |
|-------|--------|-------------------|----------------|
| Collision Enter | `OnColliderEnter()` | First frame of contact | Available |
| Collision Persist | `OnColliderPersist()` | Ongoing contact | Available |
| Collision Exit | `OnColliderExit()` | Contact separation | Available |

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/PhysicsBodyComponent.hpp:146-167]()

### Collision Event Flow

```mermaid
graph TD
    PxScene["PxScene::simulate()"] -->|generates| ContactPairs["PxContactPair[]<br/>Contact pair data"]
    
    ContactPairs -->|callback| onContact["PhysicsSolver::onContact()"]
    
    onContact -->|extract| UserData["pairHeader.actors[].userData<br/>entity_t ID"]
    
    UserData -->|memcpy| EntityIDs["entity_t id1, id2"]
    
    EntityIDs -->|construct| Entities["Entity actor1_e, actor2_e"]
    
    Entities -->|GetAllComponentsPolymorphic| Bodies["PhysicsBodyComponent& actor1, actor2"]
    
    onContact -->|extract if needed| ContactPoints["ContactPairPoint[]<br/>Contact data"]
    
    Bodies -->|PxPairFlag::eNOTIFY_TOUCH_FOUND| OnColliderEnter["actor1.OnColliderEnter(actor2, points, count)<br/>actor2.OnColliderEnter(actor1, points, count)"]
    
    Bodies -->|PxPairFlag::eNOTIFY_TOUCH_PERSISTS| OnColliderPersist["actor1.OnColliderPersist(actor2, points, count)<br/>actor2.OnColliderPersist(actor1, points, count)"]
    
    Bodies -->|PxPairFlag::eNOTIFY_TOUCH_LOST| OnColliderExit["actor1.OnColliderExit(actor2, points, count)<br/>actor2.OnColliderExit(actor1, points, count)"]
    
    OnColliderEnter -->|dispatch| Receivers["receivers[] PhysicsCallback objects"]
    OnColliderPersist -->|dispatch| Receivers
    OnColliderExit -->|dispatch| Receivers
```

**Sources:** [src/PhysicsSolver.cpp:53-105](), [src/PhysicsBodyComponent.cpp:274-299]()

### Contact Event Implementation

The `PhysicsSolver::onContact()` callback processes collision pairs from PhysX:

[src/PhysicsSolver.cpp:53-105]()

Key implementation details:

1. **Actor Validation:** Checks `userData != nullptr` to skip destroyed actors - [src/PhysicsSolver.cpp:59-61]()
2. **Entity Reconstruction:** Uses `memcpy` to extract `entity_t` IDs from `userData` - [src/PhysicsSolver.cpp:63-68]()
3. **Component Retrieval:** Gets first polymorphic `PhysicsBodyComponent` from each entity - [src/PhysicsSolver.cpp:70-71]()
4. **Contact Point Extraction:** Conditionally extracts contact data if either body wants it - [src/PhysicsSolver.cpp:76-85]()
5. **Bidirectional Events:** Fires events on both actors - [src/PhysicsSolver.cpp:88-102]()

**Sources:** [src/PhysicsSolver.cpp:53-105]()

### Contact Point Data Structure

Contact points provide detailed information about collision geometry:

```mermaid
graph LR
    PxContactPairPoint["PxContactPairPoint<br/>PhysX structure"] -->|convert| ContactPairPoint["ContactPairPoint<br/>RavEngine wrapper"]
    
    ContactPairPoint -->|vector3| position["position<br/>World-space contact point"]
    ContactPairPoint -->|vector3| normal["normal<br/>Contact surface normal"]
    ContactPairPoint -->|vector3| impulse["impulse<br/>Collision impulse vector"]
    ContactPairPoint -->|decimalType| separation["separation<br/>Penetration depth"]
```

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/PhysicsBodyComponent.hpp:28-36](), [src/PhysicsBodyComponent.cpp:389-393]()

The `ContactPairPoint` structure is constructed from PhysX's `PxContactPairPoint`:

[src/PhysicsBodyComponent.cpp:389-393]()

Contact data extraction is controlled by the `wantsContactData` flag on each body. If neither body wants contact data, `contactPoints` is a dangling pointer and `numContactPoints` is 0.

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/PhysicsBodyComponent.hpp:184-193](), [src/PhysicsSolver.cpp:76-85]()

## Trigger Events

Trigger events fire when a trigger shape overlaps another shape, without generating collision response.

### Trigger Event Types

| Event | Method | Trigger Condition |
|-------|--------|-------------------|
| Trigger Enter | `OnTriggerEnter()` | Trigger overlap begins |
| Trigger Exit | `OnTriggerExit()` | Trigger overlap ends |

**Note:** Triggers do NOT provide contact point data. Trigger events do NOT fire between two triggers.

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/PhysicsBodyComponent.hpp:169-179]()

### Trigger Event Flow

```mermaid
graph TD
    PxScene["PxScene::simulate()"] -->|generates| TriggerPairs["PxTriggerPair[]<br/>Trigger pair data"]
    
    TriggerPairs -->|callback| onTrigger["PhysicsSolver::onTrigger()"]
    
    onTrigger -->|check| RemovedFlags["PxTriggerPairFlag::eREMOVED_SHAPE_*"]
    RemovedFlags -->|if set| Skip["continue<br/>(skip deleted shapes)"]
    
    onTrigger -->|check| UserDataValid["otherActor->userData != nullptr<br/>triggerActor->userData != nullptr"]
    UserDataValid -->|if null| Skip
    
    onTrigger -->|extract| EntityIDs["entity_t id1 (other)<br/>entity_t id2 (trigger)"]
    
    EntityIDs -->|construct| Entities["Entity other_e, trigger_e"]
    
    Entities -->|GetAllComponentsPolymorphic| Bodies["PhysicsBodyComponent& other, trigger"]
    
    Bodies -->|PxPairFlag::eNOTIFY_TOUCH_FOUND| OnTriggerEnter["other.OnTriggerEnter(trigger)<br/>trigger.OnTriggerEnter(other)"]
    
    Bodies -->|PxPairFlag::eNOTIFY_TOUCH_LOST| OnTriggerExit["other.OnTriggerExit(trigger)<br/>trigger.OnTriggerExit(other)"]
    
    OnTriggerEnter -->|dispatch| Receivers["receivers[] PhysicsCallback objects"]
    OnTriggerExit -->|dispatch| Receivers
```

**Sources:** [src/PhysicsSolver.cpp:107-143](), [src/PhysicsBodyComponent.cpp:302-316]()

### Trigger Event Implementation

The `PhysicsSolver::onTrigger()` callback processes trigger pairs:

[src/PhysicsSolver.cpp:107-143]()

Key differences from collision events:

1. **Shape Removal Check:** Skips pairs with `eREMOVED_SHAPE_TRIGGER` or `eREMOVED_SHAPE_OTHER` flags - [src/PhysicsSolver.cpp:112-114]()
2. **No Contact Data:** Triggers provide no contact point information
3. **Bidirectional Events:** Both actors receive enter/exit events - [src/PhysicsSolver.cpp:133-141]()
4. **Status Flags:** Uses `PxPairFlag::eNOTIFY_TOUCH_FOUND` and `eNOTIFY_TOUCH_LOST` - [src/PhysicsSolver.cpp:133, 138]()

**Sources:** [src/PhysicsSolver.cpp:107-143]()

## Physics Callbacks

The callback system allows game code to respond to physics events through the `PhysicsCallback` interface.

### Callback Registration

```mermaid
graph LR
    PhysicsBodyComponent["PhysicsBodyComponent"] -->|contains| receivers["receivers<br/>UnorderedSet&lt;shared_ptr&lt;PhysicsCallback&gt;&gt;"]
    
    GameCode["Game Code"] -->|AddReceiver| PhysicsBodyComponent
    GameCode -->|RemoveReceiver| PhysicsBodyComponent
    
    receivers -->|OnRegisterBody| PhysicsCallback["PhysicsCallback<br/>User implementation"]
    receivers -->|OnUnregisterBody| PhysicsCallback
    
    PhysicsBodyComponent -->|dispatch events| PhysicsCallback
    
    PhysicsCallback -->|optional| OnColliderEnter["OnColliderEnter()"]
    PhysicsCallback -->|optional| OnColliderPersist["OnColliderPersist()"]
    PhysicsCallback -->|optional| OnColliderExit["OnColliderExit()"]
    PhysicsCallback -->|optional| OnTriggerEnter["OnTriggerEnter()"]
    PhysicsCallback -->|optional| OnTriggerExit["OnTriggerExit()"]
```

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/PhysicsBodyComponent.hpp:50, 95-107](), [src/PhysicsBodyComponent.cpp:66-88]()

### Receiver Management

Bodies maintain a set of registered callback receivers:

[src/PhysicsBodyComponent.cpp:66-78]()

When a receiver is added:
1. Inserted into `receivers` set
2. `OnRegisterBody()` called with polymorphic handle to this body

When a receiver is removed:
1. Erased from `receivers` set
2. `OnUnregisterBody()` called with polymorphic handle to this body

**Sources:** [src/PhysicsBodyComponent.cpp:66-88]()

### Event Dispatch Pattern

Each event method iterates through registered receivers and conditionally calls their callbacks:

[src/PhysicsBodyComponent.cpp:274-281]()

The pattern checks if the callback function is set before calling, allowing receivers to selectively implement only needed callbacks. This is repeated for all event types: `OnColliderEnter`, `OnColliderPersist`, `OnColliderExit`, `OnTriggerEnter`, and `OnTriggerExit`.

**Sources:** [src/PhysicsBodyComponent.cpp:274-316]()

## Collision Filtering

The filter shader determines which collisions are detected and reported.

### Filter Shader Logic

```mermaid
graph TD
    FilterShader["FilterShader(attributes0, filterData0,<br/>attributes1, filterData1)"] --> CheckTrigger{"Is either<br/>object a trigger?"}
    
    CheckTrigger -->|Yes| TriggerPath["pairFlags = eTRIGGER_DEFAULT<br/>return eDEFAULT"]
    
    CheckTrigger -->|No| SetContact["pairFlags = eCONTACT_DEFAULT"]
    
    SetContact --> CheckLayers{"(filterData0.word0 & filterData1.word1)<br/>&&<br/>(filterData1.word0 & filterData0.word1)"}
    
    CheckLayers -->|Yes| EnableEvents["pairFlags |= eNOTIFY_TOUCH_FOUND<br/>| eNOTIFY_TOUCH_PERSISTS<br/>| eNOTIFY_TOUCH_LOST<br/>| eNOTIFY_CONTACT_POINTS"]
    
    CheckLayers -->|No| SkipEvents["No event flags added"]
    
    EnableEvents --> Return["return eDEFAULT"]
    SkipEvents --> Return
```

**Sources:** [src/PhysicsSolver.cpp:32-49]()

### Filter Data Layout

PhysX filter data uses a 4-word structure:

| Word | Usage | Set By |
|------|-------|--------|
| `word0` | Own filter group | `PhysicsBodyComponent::filterGroup` |
| `word1` | Filter mask (layers to collide with) | `PhysicsBodyComponent::filterMask` |
| `word2` | Unused | - |
| `word3` | Unused | - |

The filter shader performs bitwise AND checks: `(A.word0 & B.word1) && (B.word0 & A.word1)`. Both conditions must be true for collision events to fire.

**Sources:** [src/PhysicsSolver.cpp:44-46](), [include/RavEngine/PhysicsBodyComponent.hpp:64-65]()

### Filter Data Update

Colliders update their filter data when attached to a body:

[src/PhysicsCollider.cpp:23-28]()

This ensures the collider inherits the body's filter group and mask settings.

**Sources:** [src/PhysicsCollider.cpp:23-28]()

## Actor Spawning and Destruction

Bodies are registered and unregistered from the physics scene through spawn/destroy operations.

### Spawn Flow

```mermaid
sequenceDiagram
    participant Entity
    participant PhysicsBodyComponent
    participant PhysicsSolver
    participant PxScene
    
    Entity->>PhysicsBodyComponent: Constructor
    PhysicsBodyComponent->>PhysicsBodyComponent: Create PxRigidActor
    PhysicsBodyComponent->>PhysicsBodyComponent: CompleteConstruction()
    PhysicsBodyComponent->>PhysicsSolver: Spawn(*this)
    
    PhysicsSolver->>PhysicsSolver: memcpy entity_t ID into userData
    PhysicsSolver->>PxScene: lockWrite()
    PhysicsSolver->>PxScene: addActor(rigidActor)
    PhysicsSolver->>PxScene: unlockWrite()
```

**Sources:** [src/PhysicsBodyComponent.cpp:28-30, 53-59](), [src/PhysicsSolver.cpp:218-226]()

The `userData` field of `PxRigidActor` stores the `entity_t` ID (NOT a pointer) to enable entity lookup during collision callbacks. This is done via `memcpy` to avoid pointer size issues:

[src/PhysicsSolver.cpp:218-226]()

**Sources:** [src/PhysicsSolver.cpp:218-226]()

### Destroy Flow

```mermaid
sequenceDiagram
    participant PhysicsBodyComponent
    participant PhysicsSolver
    participant PxScene
    participant Receivers
    
    PhysicsBodyComponent->>PhysicsSolver: Destroy(*this)
    
    PhysicsSolver->>PxScene: lockWrite()
    PhysicsSolver->>PxScene: removeActor(rigidActor)
    PhysicsSolver->>PxScene: unlockWrite()
    
    PhysicsBodyComponent->>PhysicsBodyComponent: userData = nullptr
    PhysicsBodyComponent->>PhysicsBodyComponent: rigidActor->release()
    
    PhysicsBodyComponent->>Receivers: OnUnregisterBody() for all receivers
```

**Sources:** [src/PhysicsBodyComponent.cpp:36-49](), [src/PhysicsSolver.cpp:232-236]()

The body's destructor sets `userData` to `nullptr` before releasing the PhysX actor to prevent dangling pointer access in pending collision callbacks:

[src/PhysicsBodyComponent.cpp:36-49]()

**Sources:** [src/PhysicsBodyComponent.cpp:36-49](), [src/PhysicsSolver.cpp:232-236]()

## Thread Safety

The physics system uses PhysX's scene locking mechanisms for thread-safe access.

### Locking Helpers

`PhysicsBodyComponent` provides `LockRead` and `LockWrite` helper templates:

[include/RavEngine/PhysicsBodyComponent.hpp:207-231]()

These ensure proper scene locking when accessing PhysX state from outside the simulation thread. If the actor is not yet added to a scene, the function executes without locking.

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/PhysicsBodyComponent.hpp:207-231]()

### Pose Synchronization

The `setPoseNeedsSync` flag tracks when physics poses have been manually set:

[src/PhysicsBodyComponent.cpp:98-103, 318-322]()

This flag is used by the `PhysicsLinkSystem` to synchronize Transform components with physics state. See [Transform and Scene Hierarchy](#3.3) for details on the linking system.

**Sources:** [src/PhysicsBodyComponent.cpp:98-103, 318-322](), [include/RavEngine/PhysicsBodyComponent.hpp:55]()2b:T4a17,# Scene Queries and Raycasting

## Purpose and Scope

This document covers RavEngine's spatial query system for performing raycasts and overlap tests against the physics world. Scene queries allow you to test for intersections with physics colliders without relying on collision events, enabling gameplay features like line-of-sight checks, area-of-effect detection, and object placement validation.

For information about physics bodies and colliders themselves, see [Physics Bodies and Colliders](#5.1). For collision event callbacks, see [Physics Simulation and Events](#5.2).

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/PhysicsSolver.hpp:79-155](), [src/PhysicsSolver.cpp:156-211]()

---

## Query System Architecture

Scene queries are performed through the `PhysicsSolver` class, which wraps PhysX's scene query functionality. Queries execute synchronously and return immediately with results.

```mermaid
graph TD
    World["World"]
    PhysicsSolver["PhysicsSolver<br/>scene query methods"]
    PxScene["physx::PxScene<br/>PhysX scene"]
    
    PhysicsBody["PhysicsBodyComponent<br/>rigidActor"]
    Collider["PhysicsCollider<br/>PxShape"]
    QueryFlag["eSCENE_QUERY_SHAPE flag"]
    
    World -->|"owns"| PhysicsSolver
    PhysicsSolver -->|"owns"| PxScene
    PhysicsSolver -->|"Raycast()"| PxScene
    PhysicsSolver -->|"BoxOverlap()"| PxScene
    PhysicsSolver -->|"SphereOverlap()"| PxScene
    PhysicsSolver -->|"CapsuleOverlap()"| PxScene
    
    PhysicsBody -->|"contains"| Collider
    Collider -->|"has"| QueryFlag
    PxScene -->|"tests against"| Collider
    
    QueryFlag -->|"true = participates<br/>false = ignored"| PxScene
```

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/PhysicsSolver.hpp:34-46](), [src/PhysicsSolver.cpp:259-296]()

---

## Raycasting

### Raycast Method

The `Raycast` method performs a ray-sphere intersection test against all queryable colliders in the physics scene.

```cpp
bool PhysicsSolver::Raycast(
    const vector3& origin,          // Ray starting point
    const vector3& direction,       // Ray direction (does not need to be normalized)
    decimalType maxDistance,        // Maximum ray distance
    RaycastHit& out_hit,           // Output hit information
    uint32_t layerMask = ALL_LAYERS // Layer mask filter
);
```

**Parameters:**
| Parameter | Type | Description |
|-----------|------|-------------|
| `origin` | `vector3` | World-space starting point of the ray |
| `direction` | `vector3` | Direction vector (normalized or not) |
| `maxDistance` | `decimalType` | Maximum distance to test along the ray |
| `out_hit` | `RaycastHit&` | Output structure populated with hit data |
| `layerMask` | `uint32_t` | Bitmask for filtering by collision layers |

**Return Value:** `true` if the ray hit a collider, `false` otherwise.

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/PhysicsSolver.hpp:93-101](), [src/PhysicsSolver.cpp:156-188]()

### Raycast Execution Flow

```mermaid
graph TD
    Start["Raycast() called"]
    CreateBuffer["Create PxRaycastBuffer"]
    CreateCallback["Create RaycastCallback<br/>with layerMask"]
    SetupFilter["Setup PxQueryFilterData<br/>flags: eSTATIC | eDYNAMIC | ePREFILTER"]
    
    Execute["scene->raycast()<br/>origin, direction, maxDistance"]
    
    PreFilter{"RaycastCallback::preFilter()<br/>Check shape filterData.word1<br/>against layerMask"}
    
    Hit{"Hit found?"}
    PopulateHit["Populate RaycastHit<br/>position, normal, distance, entity"]
    ReturnTrue["Return true"]
    ReturnFalse["Return false"]
    
    Start --> CreateBuffer
    CreateBuffer --> CreateCallback
    CreateCallback --> SetupFilter
    SetupFilter --> Execute
    Execute --> PreFilter
    PreFilter -->|"layer matches"| Hit
    PreFilter -->|"layer excluded"| ReturnFalse
    Hit -->|"hasBlock == true"| PopulateHit
    Hit -->|"no hit"| ReturnFalse
    PopulateHit --> ReturnTrue
```

**Sources:** [src/PhysicsSolver.cpp:156-188](), [src/PhysicsSolver.cpp:160-178]()

### RaycastHit Structure

The `RaycastHit` structure contains detailed information about a ray intersection:

```cpp
struct PhysicsSolver::RaycastHit {
    bool hasBlocking;           // True if ray hit a blocking collider
    vector3 hitPosition;        // World-space hit point
    vector3 hitNormal;          // Surface normal at hit point
    decimalType hitDistance;    // Distance from origin to hit point
    
    Entity getEntity() const;   // Returns the Entity owning the hit collider
};
```

**Member Details:**

| Member | Type | Description |
|--------|------|-------------|
| `hasBlocking` | `bool` | Indicates if a blocking hit occurred |
| `hitPosition` | `vector3` | World-space coordinates of the hit point |
| `hitNormal` | `vector3` | Surface normal vector at the hit location |
| `hitDistance` | `decimalType` | Distance traveled along the ray to the hit |
| `getEntity()` | `Entity` | Returns the `Entity` that owns the hit `PhysicsBodyComponent` |

The `RaycastHit` constructor extracts data from PhysX's `PxRaycastBuffer` and converts entity ID from the actor's `userData` field.

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/PhysicsSolver.hpp:80-91](), [src/PhysicsSolver.cpp:298-314]()

### Usage Example

```cpp
// Perform a raycast from camera forward
auto world = entity.GetWorld();
auto& solver = world->Solver;

vector3 origin = cameraPosition;
vector3 direction = cameraForward;
decimalType maxDistance = 100.0;

PhysicsSolver::RaycastHit hit;
if (solver->Raycast(origin, direction, maxDistance, hit)) {
    // Ray hit something
    vector3 hitPoint = hit.hitPosition;
    vector3 normal = hit.hitNormal;
    Entity hitEntity = hit.getEntity();
    
    // Use hit information...
}
```

## Overlap Queries

Overlap queries test if a geometric shape intersects with any colliders in the physics scene. RavEngine provides three overlap shapes: box, sphere, and capsule.

### Box Overlap

Tests for intersections with an oriented box volume.

```cpp
bool PhysicsSolver::BoxOverlap(
    const vector3& origin,      // Center point of the box
    const quaternion& rotation, // Orientation of the box
    const vector3& half_ext,    // Half-extents (distance from center to face)
    OverlapHit& out_hit        // Output overlap information
);
```

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/PhysicsSolver.hpp:112-119](), [src/PhysicsSolver.cpp:190-193]()

### Sphere Overlap

Tests for intersections with a spherical volume.

```cpp
bool PhysicsSolver::SphereOverlap(
    const vector3& origin,   // Center point of the sphere
    decimalType radius,      // Radius of the sphere
    OverlapHit& out_hit     // Output overlap information
);
```

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/PhysicsSolver.hpp:121-128](), [src/PhysicsSolver.cpp:195-198]()

### Capsule Overlap

Tests for intersections with a capsule volume (cylinder with hemispherical caps).

```cpp
bool PhysicsSolver::CapsuleOverlap(
    const vector3& origin,       // Center point of the capsule
    const quaternion& rotation,  // Orientation of the capsule
    decimalType radius,          // Radius of the capsule
    decimalType halfheight,      // Half-height from center to pole
    OverlapHit& out_hit         // Output overlap information
);
```

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/PhysicsSolver.hpp:130-138](), [src/PhysicsSolver.cpp:200-203]()

### Overlap Query Implementation

All overlap queries funnel through the internal `generic_overlap` method:

```mermaid
graph TD
    BoxOverlap["BoxOverlap()"]
    SphereOverlap["SphereOverlap()"]
    CapsuleOverlap["CapsuleOverlap()"]
    
    GenericOverlap["generic_overlap()<br/>PhysicsTransform, PxGeometry"]
    
    CreateGeometry["Create PxGeometry<br/>PxBoxGeometry<br/>PxSphereGeometry<br/>PxCapsuleGeometry"]
    
    SceneOverlap["scene->overlap()<br/>geometry, transform"]
    
    PopulateResult["Populate OverlapHit<br/>from PxOverlapBuffer"]
    
    Return["Return bool result"]
    
    BoxOverlap --> CreateGeometry
    SphereOverlap --> CreateGeometry
    CapsuleOverlap --> CreateGeometry
    
    CreateGeometry --> GenericOverlap
    GenericOverlap --> SceneOverlap
    SceneOverlap --> PopulateResult
    PopulateResult --> Return
```

**Sources:** [src/PhysicsSolver.cpp:205-211](), [src/PhysicsSolver.cpp:190-203]()

### OverlapHit Structure

The `OverlapHit` structure contains information about overlapping objects:

```cpp
struct PhysicsSolver::OverlapHit {
    Ref<Entity> overlapObject;  // Entity that was overlapped
};
```

**Note:** The current implementation appears incomplete in the provided source files. The constructor does not fully populate the `overlapObject` field, as indicated by the TODO comment at [include/RavEngine/PhysicsSolver.hpp:106-107]().

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/PhysicsSolver.hpp:104-109]()

## Layer Filtering

### Layer Mask System

Raycasts support layer-based filtering to selectively test against specific collision layers. This is controlled by the `layerMask` parameter using bitmask operations.

```mermaid
graph TD
    Raycast["Raycast() with layerMask"]
    Callback["RaycastCallback<br/>stores layerMask"]
    
    TestShape["For each potential hit shape"]
    GetFilterData["shape->getSimulationFilterData()"]
    ExtractLayer["Extract layer from<br/>filterData.word1"]
    
    BitwiseAND["layerMask & filterData.word1"]
    
    Match{"Bitwise AND<br/>result != 0?"}
    
    Block["Return eBLOCK<br/>shape can be hit"]
    Skip["Return eNONE<br/>skip this shape"]
    
    Raycast --> Callback
    Callback --> TestShape
    TestShape --> GetFilterData
    GetFilterData --> ExtractLayer
    ExtractLayer --> BitwiseAND
    BitwiseAND --> Match
    Match -->|"yes"| Block
    Match -->|"no"| Skip
```

The filtering uses `PxFilterData.word1` which contains the collision layer bits for the shape. The raycast only hits shapes whose layer bits overlap with the provided `layerMask`.

**Sources:** [src/PhysicsSolver.cpp:160-178](), [src/PhysicsSolver.cpp:164-173]()

### Filter Data Setup

Collision filter data is configured when creating colliders through the `PhysicsBodyComponent`:

```cpp
// From PhysicsBodyComponent
physx::PxU32 filterGroup = -1;  // word0: own layer ID
physx::PxU32 filterMask = -1;   // word1: layers this object collides with
```

When a collider is attached to a physics body, its filter data is updated via `UpdateFilterData`:

```cpp
void PhysicsCollider::UpdateFilterData(PhysicsBodyComponent* owner) {
    PxFilterData filterData;
    filterData.word0 = owner->filterGroup;  // Own ID
    filterData.word1 = owner->filterMask;   // Collision mask
    collider->setSimulationFilterData(filterData);
}
```

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/PhysicsBodyComponent.hpp:63-65](), [src/PhysicsCollider.cpp:23-28]()

### Predefined Layer Constants

The `FilterLayers` enum provides common layer bit definitions:

```cpp
struct FilterLayers {
    enum Enum {
        L0 = (1 << 0),  // 0x0001
        L1 = (1 << 1),  // 0x0002
        L2 = (1 << 2),  // 0x0004
        L3 = (1 << 3),  // 0x0008
    };
};
```

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/PhysicsSolver.hpp:21-28]()

---

## Configuring Colliders for Scene Queries

### Queryable Flag

By default, colliders may not participate in scene queries. You must explicitly enable query participation using `SetQueryable`:

```cpp
void PhysicsCollider::SetQueryable(bool state);
bool PhysicsCollider::GetQueryable() const;
```

This controls the `PxShapeFlag::eSCENE_QUERY_SHAPE` flag on the underlying PhysX shape:

```mermaid
graph LR
    Collider["PhysicsCollider"]
    SetQueryable["SetQueryable(true)"]
    PxShape["PxShape"]
    Flag["eSCENE_QUERY_SHAPE flag"]
    
    SceneQuery["Scene Queries<br/>Raycast<br/>Overlap"]
    
    Collider -->|"owns"| PxShape
    SetQueryable -->|"sets"| Flag
    Flag -->|"stored in"| PxShape
    
    SceneQuery -->|"only tests shapes with<br/>eSCENE_QUERY_SHAPE = true"| PxShape
```

**Implementation:**

```cpp
void PhysicsCollider::SetQueryable(bool state) {
    collider->setFlag(PxShapeFlag::eSCENE_QUERY_SHAPE, state);
}

bool PhysicsCollider::GetQueryable() const {
    return collider->getFlags() & PxShapeFlag::eSCENE_QUERY_SHAPE;
}
```

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/PhysicsCollider.hpp:48-59](), [src/PhysicsCollider.cpp:165-173]()

### Collision vs Query Shapes

Colliders can be configured independently for collision simulation and scene queries:

| Flag | Purpose | Set By |
|------|---------|--------|
| `eSIMULATION_SHAPE` | Participates in physics simulation and collision events | `SetType(CollisionType::Collider)` |
| `eTRIGGER_SHAPE` | Acts as a trigger volume (no collision response) | `SetType(CollisionType::Trigger)` |
| `eSCENE_QUERY_SHAPE` | Participates in raycasts and overlap queries | `SetQueryable(true)` |

**Sources:** [src/PhysicsCollider.cpp:146-173]()

---

## Query Filter Flags

The raycast implementation uses `PxQueryFilterData` to control which types of objects are tested:

```cpp
PxQueryFilterData filterData;
filterData.flags = PxQueryFlag::eSTATIC | 
                   PxQueryFlag::eDYNAMIC | 
                   PxQueryFlag::ePREFILTER;
```

**Flag Meanings:**

| Flag | Description |
|------|-------------|
| `eSTATIC` | Test against static rigid bodies (`RigidBodyStaticComponent`) |
| `eDYNAMIC` | Test against dynamic rigid bodies (`RigidBodyDynamicComponent`) |
| `ePREFILTER` | Enable the prefilter callback for layer filtering |

**Sources:** [src/PhysicsSolver.cpp:180-181]()

---

## PhysX Integration Details

### Query Execution Thread Safety

Scene queries lock the PhysX scene internally for thread safety. The raycast implementation does not explicitly lock because PhysX's `scene->raycast()` handles locking internally.

However, physics bodies use explicit locking when accessing scene data:

```cpp
template<typename T>
inline void PhysicsBodyComponent::LockRead(const T& func) const {
    auto scene = rigidActor->getScene();
    if (scene) {
        scene->lockRead();
        func();
        scene->unlockRead();
    }
    else {
        func();
    }
}
```

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/PhysicsBodyComponent.hpp:220-231]()

### Entity Retrieval from Query Results

When a query hits a `PhysicsBodyComponent`, the entity ID is retrieved from the actor's `userData` field:

```cpp
PhysicsSolver::RaycastHit::RaycastHit(const physx::PxRaycastBuffer& hit, World* owner) {
    // ...
    if (hit.hasBlock) {
        entity_t id;
        memcpy(&id, &hit.block.actor->userData, sizeof(id));
        hitObject = {id, owner};
    }
}
```

The `userData` field is populated when the physics body is spawned:

```cpp
void PhysicsSolver::Spawn(PhysicsBodyComponent& actor) {
    auto e = actor.GetOwner();
    if (actor.rigidActor->userData == nullptr) {
        memcpy(&actor.rigidActor->userData, &e.id, sizeof(e.id));
    }
    // ...
}
```

**Sources:** [src/PhysicsSolver.cpp:298-309](), [src/PhysicsSolver.cpp:218-226]()

---

## Performance Considerations

### Query Cost Factors

Scene query performance depends on several factors:

1. **Number of Queryable Colliders**: Only shapes with `eSCENE_QUERY_SHAPE` are tested
2. **Spatial Partitioning**: PhysX uses internal spatial acceleration structures
3. **Layer Filtering**: Prefilter callbacks reduce unnecessary tests
4. **Geometry Complexity**: Mesh colliders are more expensive than primitives
5. **Query Shape Size**: Larger overlap volumes test more candidates

### Optimization Strategies

**Minimize Queryable Shapes:**
- Only set `SetQueryable(true)` on colliders that need to be tested
- Use layer filtering to exclude irrelevant objects

**Prefer Primitive Shapes:**
- Box, sphere, and capsule queries are faster than mesh-based queries
- Consider using simplified collision proxies for queries

**Limit Query Frequency:**
- Cache query results when appropriate
- Use spatial partitioning for frequently queried areas
- Consider throttling queries that don't need every-frame updates

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/PhysicsCollider.hpp:48-59](), [src/PhysicsSolver.cpp:156-211]()

---

## Practical Usage Patterns

### Line-of-Sight Check

```cpp
bool HasLineOfSight(Entity source, Entity target, World* world) {
    auto sourcePos = source.GetTransform().GetWorldPosition();
    auto targetPos = target.GetTransform().GetWorldPosition();
    
    vector3 direction = targetPos - sourcePos;
    decimalType distance = glm::length(direction);
    direction = glm::normalize(direction);
    
    PhysicsSolver::RaycastHit hit;
    if (world->Solver->Raycast(sourcePos, direction, distance, hit)) {
        // Check if we hit the target or something in between
        return hit.getEntity() == target;
    }
    
    return true; // No obstruction
}
```

### Ground Detection

```cpp
bool IsGrounded(Entity entity, World* world, decimalType checkDistance = 0.1) {
    auto pos = entity.GetTransform().GetWorldPosition();
    vector3 down(0, -1, 0);
    
    PhysicsSolver::RaycastHit hit;
    return world->Solver->Raycast(pos, down, checkDistance, hit);
}
```

### Area Query for Nearby Objects

```cpp
void FindObjectsInRadius(vector3 center, decimalType radius, World* world) {
    PhysicsSolver::OverlapHit hit;
    if (world->Solver->SphereOverlap(center, radius, hit)) {
        // Process overlapping entities
        // Note: Current implementation may need enhancement
    }
}
```

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/PhysicsSolver.hpp:79-155]()

---

## Summary

Scene queries in RavEngine provide essential spatial testing capabilities through:

- **Raycasting**: Line-intersection tests with detailed hit information
- **Overlap Queries**: Volume-based intersection tests (box, sphere, capsule)
- **Layer Filtering**: Selective testing using collision layer masks
- **Queryable Configuration**: Per-collider control over query participation

All queries execute through the `PhysicsSolver` accessible via `World::Solver`, using PhysX's optimized scene query system. Colliders must have `SetQueryable(true)` to participate in queries, and layer masks provide additional filtering control.

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/PhysicsSolver.hpp:34-155](), [src/PhysicsSolver.cpp:156-211](), [include/RavEngine/PhysicsCollider.hpp:48-59]()2c:T5f1f,# Animation

## Purpose and Scope

This document covers RavEngine's skeletal animation system, which enables character animation through bone-driven mesh deformation. The system integrates the Ozz-animation library to provide animation playback, state machines, blend trees, and GPU-accelerated skeletal skinning. 

For details on specific subsystems:
- Animation components and asset loading: see [Animation Components and Assets](#6.1)
- State machine implementation and transitions: see [Animation State Machines](#6.2)
- Blending techniques and blend trees: see [Animation Blending and Blend Trees](#6.3)
- GPU skinning compute pipeline: see [Skeletal Skinning Pipeline](#6.4)

For physics integration via bone sockets, see [Physics Bodies and Colliders](#5.1). For mesh rendering, see [Materials and Shaders](#4.2).

---

## System Overview

RavEngine's animation system is built on the **Ozz-animation** library, which provides compressed animation storage and efficient SIMD-optimized sampling. The system supports:

- **Multi-layer state machines** with transitions and callbacks
- **2D blend trees** for spatial animation blending
- **Custom code-driven animations** via programmable hooks
- **GPU-based vertex skinning** using compute shaders
- **Hierarchical bone sockets** for attaching objects to bones

The animation pipeline operates in three phases:
1. **CPU sampling**: AnimatorComponent evaluates animation curves and blends layers
2. **CPU pose computation**: Local-space transforms convert to model-space matrices
3. **GPU skinning**: Compute shader deforms mesh vertices using bone weights

**Key Design Philosophy**: Animation sampling occurs on the CPU using Ozz's optimized jobs, while the expensive vertex deformation work runs entirely on the GPU. This minimizes CPU overhead while maximizing GPU parallelism for skinned mesh rendering.

**Sources**: [include/RavEngine/AnimatorComponent.hpp:1-394](), [src/AnimatorComponent.cpp:1-388]()

---

## Core Classes

### AnimatorComponent

`AnimatorComponent` is the main entity component that drives skeletal animation. It owns a reference to a `SkeletonAsset` and manages multiple animation layers.

**Key Responsibilities**:
- Stores the current skeleton and pose matrices
- Manages up to 32 animation layers (`kmax_layers`)
- Blends layer outputs into a final pose
- Converts local-space bone transforms to model-space matrices
- Generates skinning matrices (pose Ã— inverse bindpose)
- Updates socket attachments for bone-parented transforms

**Important Members**:
- `skeleton`: Reference to the SkeletonAsset
- `layers`: Vector of Layer unique pointers
- `glm_pose`: World-space bone matrices
- `local_pose`: Model-space bone matrices
- `skinningmats`: Final skinning matrices for GPU
- `all_transforms`: Blended SoA transforms from all layers

**Sources**: [include/RavEngine/AnimatorComponent.hpp:132-391](), [src/AnimatorComponent.cpp:33-35]()

### AnimatorComponent::Layer

Each `Layer` represents an independent state machine with its own playback state. Layers support:
- **Additive blending**: Layer can be marked as additive for overlay animations
- **Skeleton masking**: Per-bone weights control which bones the layer affects
- **Weight control**: Layer weight scales its influence in the final blend

**Key Methods**:
- `Goto(anim_id_t newState)`: Transition to a new state
- `Play(float resetPlayhead)`: Begin playback
- `Pause()`: Stop playback without resetting time
- `InsertState(const State& state)`: Add a state to the state machine

**Sources**: [include/RavEngine/AnimatorComponent.hpp:243-331](), [src/AnimatorComponent.cpp:36-106]()

### AnimatorComponent::State

A `State` represents a node in the state machine, wrapping an `IAnimGraphable` animation source.

**Key Features**:
- **Exit transitions**: Map of target state IDs to transition definitions
- **Auto-transitions**: Automatically transition when non-looping animation completes
- **Callbacks**: BeginCallback and EndCallback for state change events
- **Speed control**: Per-state playback speed multiplier
- **Looping**: Whether the animation loops or plays once

**Transition Configuration**:
```cpp
State& SetTransition(decltype(ID) id, T interpolation, decimal duration, 
                     Transition::TimeMode mode = Transition::TimeMode::Blended)
```
Uses Tweeny library for customizable transition curves.

**Sources**: [include/RavEngine/AnimatorComponent.hpp:144-235](), [src/AnimatorComponent.cpp:46-79]()

### IAnimGraphable

The `IAnimGraphable` interface defines the contract for animation graph nodes:

```cpp
virtual bool Sample(float t, float start, float speed, bool looping,
                    ozz::vector<ozz::math::SoaTransform>& output,
                    ozz::animation::SamplingJob::Context& cache,
                    const ozz::animation::Skeleton* skeleton) const = 0;
```

**Implementations**:
- `AnimationAsset`: Pre-baked animation clip
- `AnimationAssetSegment`: Subrange of an AnimationAsset
- `AnimationClip`: Blend multiple IAnimGraphables with fixed weights
- `AnimBlendTree`: 2D spatial blending with movable control point
- `CustomSkeletonAnimation`: Code-driven bone manipulation

**Sources**: [include/RavEngine/AnimationAsset.hpp:28-52]()

### SkeletonAsset

`SkeletonAsset` stores the bone hierarchy and bindpose information:

**Data Stored**:
- `skeleton`: Ozz-optimized runtime skeleton
- `bindpose`: GPU buffer containing inverse bindpose matrices
- `boneHierarchy`: GPU buffer with parent indices for each bone
- `bindposes`: CPU copy of inverse bindpose matrices

The skeleton defines the bone structure, while bindposes represent the "neutral" pose that vertices are authored in. Skinning matrices are computed as: `skinningMatrix = currentPose Ã— inverseBindpose`.

**Sources**: [include/RavEngine/SkeletonAsset.hpp:15-69](), [src/SkeletonAsset.cpp:1-201]()

## Animation Playback Pipeline

The following diagram shows the complete data flow from assets to rendered skinned mesh:

**Animation Playback and Skinning Pipeline**

```mermaid

        AnimFile["animations/name.rvea<br/>Virtual Filesystem"]
        SkeletonFile["skeletons/name.rves<br/>Virtual Filesystem"]
        MeshFile["meshes/name.rvem<br/>(skinned variant)"]
    end
    
    subgraph "CPU - AnimatorComponent::Tick()"
        LoadAssets["Load AnimationAsset<br/>+ SkeletonAsset"]
        
        SampleLayers["For each Layer:<br/>Layer::Tick()"]
        
        SampleStates["Sample State IAnimGraphable<br/>IAnimGraphable::Sample()"]
        
        OzzSample["ozz::animation::SamplingJob<br/>Sample curves to SoaTransform"]
        
        BlendStates["If transitioning:<br/>ozz::BlendingJob<br/>Blend from/to states"]
        
        BlendLayers["ozz::BlendingJob<br/>Blend all layers<br/>Normal + Additive"]
        
        LocalToModel["ozz::LocalToModelJob<br/>Convert local to model space"]
        
        ComputeSkinning["For each bone:<br/>skinningMats[i] = pose[i] * bindpose[i]"]

    end

        ReadBindpose["Read inverse bindpose<br/>from SkeletonAsset buffer"]
        
        ReadPose["Read current pose<br/>from skinningMats SSBO"]
        
        TransformVertex["For each vertex:<br/>finalPos = Î£(weight[i] * bone[i] * pos)"]
        
        WriteOutput["Write to skinned vertex buffer"]
        
        Render["Main opaque pass<br/>Render skinned mesh"]
    end
    
    AnimFile --> LoadAssets
    SkeletonFile --> LoadAssets
    MeshFile --> LoadAssets
    
    LoadAssets --> SampleLayers
    SampleLayers --> SampleStates
    SampleStates --> OzzSample
    OzzSample --> BlendStates
    BlendStates --> BlendLayers
    BlendLayers --> LocalToModel
    LocalToModel --> ComputeSkinning
    ComputeSkinning --> UpdateSockets
    
    ComputeSkinning --> SyncMatrices
    SyncMatrices --> SkinningCS
    SkinningCS --> ReadWeights
    SkinningCS --> ReadBindpose
    SkinningCS --> ReadPose
    ReadWeights --> TransformVertex
    ReadBindpose --> TransformVertex
    ReadPose --> TransformVertex
    TransformVertex --> WriteOutput
    WriteOutput --> Render
```

**Sources**: [src/AnimatorComponent.cpp:108-169](), [include/RavEngine/AnimatorComponent.hpp:338-344](), Diagram 5 from high-level architecture
