## Animation Sampling Process

### Layer Tick Execution

When `AnimatorComponent::Tick()` is called each frame, it processes all layers:

1. **Setup Layer Arrays**: Separate normal and additive layers into Ozz BlendingJob::Layer arrays
2. **Tick Each Layer**: Call `Layer::Tick()` to sample the current state
3. **Apply Skeleton Masks**: If a layer has a SkeletonMask, set per-bone joint weights
4. **Blend Layers**: Use `ozz::animation::BlendingJob` to combine all layers into `all_transforms`
5. **Local to Model**: Use `ozz::animation::LocalToModelJob` to convert SoA transforms to model-space matrices
6. **Compute Skinning Matrices**: Multiply each pose matrix by its inverse bindpose
7. **Update World Poses**: Call `GetPose()` to multiply by entity's world transform

**Sources**: [src/AnimatorComponent.cpp:108-169]()

### State Sampling with Blending

Within `Layer::Tick()`, if the layer is transitioning between states:

1. **Sample Both States**: Call `Sample()` on both `from` and `to` states
2. **Step Transition Tween**: Advance the Tweeny tween to get blend weight
3. **Blend States**: Use `ozz::animation::BlendingJob` with two layers:
   - Layer 0: fromState transforms, weight = 1 - currentBlendingValue
   - Layer 1: toState transforms, weight = currentBlendingValue
4. **Check Completion**: When tween progress >= 1.0, end transition

**Sources**: [src/AnimatorComponent.cpp:171-238]()

### Ozz SoaTransform Format

Ozz uses Structure-of-Arrays (SoA) format for bone transforms to enable SIMD optimization:

- **SoaTransform**: Stores 4 bones' transforms in a single structure
- **SIMD Operations**: Ozz performs 4-wide SIMD math on SoaTransform
- **Conversion**: Engine converts to standard 4x4 matrices for GPU upload

This explains why skeleton joints are measured in `num_soa_joints()` (number of 4-bone groups) versus `num_joints()` (total bone count).

**Sources**: [src/AnimatorComponent.cpp:150-158](), [include/RavEngine/AnimatorComponent.hpp:2-4]()

---

## Animation Graph Node Types

### AnimationAsset

`AnimationAsset` represents a pre-baked animation clip loaded from `.rvea` files. The asset stores:
- Ozz-compressed animation data
- Duration in seconds
- Ticks per second (for subclip calculation)

**Sampling**: Converts global time to normalized ratio [0, 1] and calls `ozz::animation::SamplingJob`.

**Sources**: [include/RavEngine/AnimationAsset.hpp:57-81](), [src/AnimationAsset.cpp:96-144](), [src/AnimationAsset.cpp:157-169]()

### AnimationAssetSegment

`AnimationAssetSegment` plays a subrange of an `AnimationAsset`:

```cpp
AnimationAssetSegment(Ref<AnimationAsset> asset, float start_ticks, float end_ticks)
```

**Use Case**: Single FBX file contains multiple animations (walk, run, idle). Each segment defines a slice of the full timeline.

**Sampling**: Maps playback time to the subclip's tick range before sampling the underlying AnimationAsset.

**Sources**: [include/RavEngine/AnimationAsset.hpp:142-155](), [src/AnimationAsset.cpp:21-45]()

### AnimationClip

`AnimationClip` blends multiple `IAnimGraphable` sources with fixed weights:

```cpp
void SetAnimationInfluence(Ref<IAnimGraphable> asset, float influence = 1)
```

**Use Case**: Combine walk animation at 70% with limp animation at 30% for an injured character.

**Sampling**: Samples all registered animations and blends using `ozz::BlendingJob` with configured weights.

**Sources**: [include/RavEngine/AnimationAsset.hpp:157-196](), [src/AnimationAsset.cpp:171-204]()

### AnimBlendTree

`AnimBlendTree` performs 2D spatial blending using a movable control point:

**Structure**:
- **Nodes**: Up to 64 nodes (`kmax_nodes`), each with a 2D graph position
- **Control Point**: `blend_pos` in [-1, 1] Ã— [-1, 1] space
- **Influence Calculation**: `weight = 1.0 - distance(blend_pos, node.graph_pos) Ã— node.max_influence`

**Use Case**: 2D locomotion blending - X axis for walk/run speed, Y axis for turn angle.

```cpp
tree.InsertNode(WALK_FORWARD, AnimBlendTree::Node(walkAnim, clamped_vec2(0, 1)));
tree.InsertNode(RUN_FORWARD, AnimBlendTree::Node(runAnim, clamped_vec2(0, 1)));
tree.SetBlendPos(clamped_vec2(speedInput, turnInput));
```

**Sources**: [include/RavEngine/AnimatorComponent.hpp:42-129](), [src/AnimatorComponent.cpp:338-378]()

### CustomSkeletonAnimation

`CustomSkeletonAnimation` enables code-driven bone manipulation:

```cpp
CustomSkeletonAnimation(Function<bool(BoneTransforms, const ozz::animation::Skeleton*, 
                                      float t, float start, float speed, bool looping)> hook)
```

**BoneTransforms API**:
- `GetBone(uint32_t index)`: Returns `{quaternion rotation, vector3 translation, vector3 scale}`
- `SetBone(uint32_t index, const SingleTransform&)`: Modifies bone transform

**Use Case**: Procedural animations like aim offsets, look-at targeting, or physics-driven ragdolls.

**Sources**: [include/RavEngine/AnimationAsset.hpp:98-137](), [src/AnimationAsset.cpp:206-255]()

---

## Skeletal Skinning Pipeline

### Mesh Asset with Weights

`MeshAssetSkinned` extends `MeshAsset` with per-vertex bone weights:

```cpp
struct VertexWeights {
    uint32_t boneIndices[4];  // Indices into skeleton
    float weights[4];         // Normalized weights (sum to 1.0)
};
```

The skinned mesh stores a GPU buffer (`weightsBuffer`) containing `VertexWeights` for each vertex.

**Sources**: [include/RavEngine/MeshAssetSkinned.hpp:12-33](), [src/MeshAssetSkinned.cpp:25-72]()

### GPU Skinning Compute Shader

The `skinning_cs.csh` compute shader performs vertex deformation:

**Inputs**:
- Original vertex positions/normals from `MeshAsset`
- `VertexWeights` from `MeshAssetSkinned`
- Skinning matrices from `AnimatorComponent`
- Inverse bindpose matrices from `SkeletonAsset`

**Per-Vertex Computation**:
```glsl
vec3 skinnedPos = vec3(0);
for (int i = 0; i < 4; i++) {
    mat4 boneMatrix = skinningMats[weights.boneIndices[i]];
    skinnedPos += weights.weights[i] * (boneMatrix * vec4(pos, 1)).xyz;
}
```

**Output**: Deformed vertex buffer consumed by main rendering pass.

**Sources**: Diagram 5 from high-level architecture, [src/MeshAssetSkinned.cpp:52-69]()

### Rendering Integration

The RenderEngine executes skinning during the compute phase before the main opaque pass:

1. **Sync CPU Data**: `AnimatorComponent::Tick()` uploads `skinningmats` to GPU SSBO
2. **Dispatch Skinning Compute**: For each skinned mesh, dispatch compute shader
3. **Barrier**: Ensure skinned vertex buffer writes complete
4. **Main Opaque Pass**: Render skinned meshes using deformed vertices

This design keeps skeletal animation entirely GPU-resident after initial CPU sampling, maximizing parallelism.

**Sources**: Diagram 3 from high-level architecture (RenderEngine multi-pass execution)

---

## Bone Sockets and Transform Attachment

`AnimatorComponent::UpdateSocket()` allows attaching `Transform` components to specific bones:

```cpp
void UpdateSocket(const std::string& boneName, Transform& t) const
```

**Implementation**: Sets the Transform's matrix to the world-space matrix of the named bone. This enables:
- Weapon attachment to hand bones
- Hat attachment to head bone
- Particle effects at attachment points

**Usage Pattern**:
1. Query skeleton for bone existence: `skeleton->HasBone("LeftHand")`
2. Each frame, call `animator.UpdateSocket("LeftHand", weaponTransform)`
3. Weapon automatically follows hand animation

**Sources**: [src/AnimatorComponent.cpp:240-248](), [include/RavEngine/SkeletonAsset.hpp:63-65]()

---

## Asset Pipeline Integration

### Animation Asset Format (.rvea)

The `.rvea` format stores compressed animation data:

**Header**: `SerializedJointAnimationHeader`
- Magic bytes: "rvea"
- Duration, ticks per second
- Number of tracks (one per bone)

**Per-Track Data**:
- Translation keyframes: `{time, vec3}`
- Rotation keyframes: `{time, quaternion}`
- Scale keyframes: `{time, vec3}`

**Loading**: `AnimationAsset` constructor deserializes and converts to Ozz format using `ozz::animation::offline::AnimationBuilder`.

**Sources**: [src/AnimationAsset.cpp:61-144]()

### Skeleton Asset Format (.rves)

The `.rves` format stores skeleton hierarchy:

**Header**: `SerializedSkeletonDataHeader`
- Magic bytes: "rves"
- Number of bones

**Data**:
- Per-bone transforms (translation, rotation, scale)
- Bone names (variable length strings)
- Parent-child relationships (index arrays)

**Loading**: `SkeletonAsset` constructor deserializes into `ozz::animation::offline::RawSkeleton`, then builds runtime-optimized `ozz::animation::Skeleton`.

**Sources**: [src/SkeletonAsset.cpp:23-176]()

### Skinned Mesh Format (.rvem extension)

Skinned meshes use the same `.rvem` extension as static meshes, but append weight data:

**Layout**:
1. Standard mesh data (positions, normals, UVs, indices)
2. `VertexWeights` array (4 indices + 4 weights per vertex)

The `MeshAssetSkinned` constructor reads the base mesh, then reads the trailing weight data and uploads to `weightsBuffer`.

**Sources**: [src/MeshAssetSkinned.cpp:25-72]()

---

## Integration with Other Systems

### Transform Hierarchy

`AnimatorComponent` works with the Transform system for:
- **World Pose Calculation**: `GetPose(const Transform& t)` multiplies bone matrices by entity's world transform
- **Socket Attachments**: `UpdateSocket()` sets child Transform matrices based on bone poses

**Sources**: [src/AnimatorComponent.cpp:240-248](), [src/AnimatorComponent.cpp:299-317]()

### Rendering System

RenderEngine integrates animation through:
- **Skinned Mesh Components**: `SkinnedMeshComponent` references both `MeshAssetSkinned` and `AnimatorComponent`
- **Compute Skinning Pass**: Dispatched before main rendering
- **GPU Buffer Management**: Skinning matrices uploaded to SSBO for shader access

**Sources**: Diagram 3 and Diagram 5 from high-level architecture

### Physics System (Sockets)

While physics bodies are independent of animation, sockets enable:
- **Weapon Collision**: Attach collider to sword bone for hit detection
- **Ragdoll Transition**: Map bones to physics bodies for death animations

**Sources**: [include/RavEngine/AnimatorComponent.hpp:348-349]()

---

## Debug Visualization

`AnimatorComponent` implements `IDebugRenderable` for visual debugging:

```cpp
void DebugDraw(RavEngine::DebugDrawer& dbg, const Transform& t) const override
```

**Visualization**: Draws spheres at each bone's world position, allowing inspection of the current pose.

**Sources**: [src/AnimatorComponent.cpp:379-387](), [include/RavEngine/AnimatorComponent.hpp:132-135]()

---

## Performance Considerations

### CPU Optimization
- **Ozz SIMD**: All bone math uses 4-wide SIMD via SoaTransform
- **Sparse Updates**: Only active (playing) layers perform sampling
- **Shared Caches**: `SamplingJob::Context` reused across layers to minimize allocations

### GPU Optimization
- **Compute Skinning**: Vertex deformation fully parallelized on GPU
- **Indirect Rendering**: Skinned meshes participate in GPU-driven culling
- **Buffer Management**: Skinning matrices uploaded once per animator, shared across all meshes using that skeleton

### Memory Efficiency
- **Compressed Animations**: Ozz format significantly smaller than raw keyframe data
- **Shared Skeletons**: Multiple entities with same skeleton share `SkeletonAsset`
- **SoA Layout**: Cache-friendly bone data organization

**Sources**: [src/AnimatorComponent.cpp:108-169](), Diagram 5 from high-level architecture

---

## Usage Example

Basic animator setup:

```cpp
// Load assets
auto skeleton = SkeletonManager::Get("character_skeleton");
auto walkAnim = AnimationAssetManager::Get("character_walk");
auto runAnim = AnimationAssetManager::Get("character_run");

// Create animator component
auto animator = world.Emplace<AnimatorComponent>(entity, skeleton);

// Add a layer with two states
auto layer = animator->AddLayer();

AnimatorComponent::State walkState(0, walkAnim, true, 1.0f);
AnimatorComponent::State runState(1, runAnim, true, 1.0f);

// Configure transition with 0.3 second blend
walkState.SetTransition(1, tweeny::easing::quadraticInOut, 0.3);
runState.SetTransition(0, tweeny::easing::quadraticInOut, 0.3);

layer->InsertState(walkState);
layer->InsertState(runState);

// Start playing walk animation
layer->Goto(0, false, true);
layer->Play();

// Later: transition to run
layer->Goto(1); // Uses configured transition
```

**Sources**: [include/RavEngine/AnimatorComponent.hpp:241-391](), [src/AnimatorComponent.cpp:283-291]()2d:T7415,# Animation Components and Assets

This page documents the core animation components and asset types in RavEngine's skeletal animation system. It covers `AnimatorComponent`, `AnimationAsset`, `SkeletonAsset`, `MeshAssetSkinned`, and the animation graph node interface that enables blending and custom animations.

For information about animation state machines and transitions, see [Animation State Machines](#6.2). For details on blend trees and animation blending techniques, see [Animation Blending and Blend Trees](#6.3). For GPU-based vertex skinning implementation, see [Skeletal Skinning Pipeline](#6.4).

## Core Animation Architecture

RavEngine's animation system is built on top of **Ozz-animation**, a runtime library for skeletal animation playback. The system uses a component-based architecture where `AnimatorComponent` manages animation playback on entities, `AnimationAsset` provides animation data, `SkeletonAsset` defines bone hierarchies, and `MeshAssetSkinned` supplies vertex weights for deformation.

```mermaid
graph TB
    subgraph "Entity Components"
        Entity["Entity"]
        AnimComp["AnimatorComponent<br/>- skeleton: Ref&lt;SkeletonAsset&gt;<br/>- layers: Vector&lt;Layer&gt;<br/>- skinningmats: ozz::vector&lt;matrix4&gt;"]
        SkinnedMesh["SkinnedMeshComponent<br/>(rendering)"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Asset Types"
        SkelAsset["SkeletonAsset<br/>- skeleton: ozz::Skeleton<br/>- bindposes: Vector&lt;mat4&gt;<br/>- bindpose: RGLBufferPtr"]
        AnimAsset["AnimationAsset<br/>- anim: ozz::Animation<br/>- duration_seconds: float<br/>- tps: float"]
        MeshSkinned["MeshAssetSkinned<br/>(extends MeshAsset)<br/>- weightsBuffer: RGLBufferPtr"]
    end
    
    subgraph "File Formats"
        RVES[".rves files<br/>(skeleton data)"]
        RVEA[".rvea files<br/>(animation data)"]
        RVEM[".rvem files<br/>(skinned mesh + weights)"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Ozz-animation Library"
        OzzSkel["ozz::animation::Skeleton"]
        OzzAnim["ozz::animation::Animation"]
        OzzSample["SamplingJob"]
        OzzBlend["BlendingJob"]
        OzzL2M["LocalToModelJob"]
    end
    
    Entity --> AnimComp
    Entity --> SkinnedMesh
    
    AnimComp --> SkelAsset
    AnimComp --> AnimAsset
    SkinnedMesh --> MeshSkinned
    
    RVES --> SkelAsset
    RVEA --> AnimAsset
    RVEM --> MeshSkinned
    
    SkelAsset --> OzzSkel
    AnimAsset --> OzzAnim
    
    AnimComp --> OzzSample
    AnimComp --> OzzBlend
    AnimComp --> OzzL2M
```

**Diagram: Core animation system architecture showing component-asset relationships and Ozz-animation integration**

Sources: [include/RavEngine/AnimatorComponent.hpp:132-391](), [include/RavEngine/AnimationAsset.hpp:57-81](), [include/RavEngine/SkeletonAsset.hpp:15-66](), [include/RavEngine/MeshAssetSkinned.hpp:12-31]()

## AnimatorComponent

`AnimatorComponent` is the primary component for skeletal animation playback. It manages animation state machines, blending between animations, and calculates bone transformations for rendering. Each `AnimatorComponent` references a `SkeletonAsset` and contains one or more **Layer**s that define animation state machines.

### Component Structure

```mermaid
graph LR
    subgraph "AnimatorComponent"
        direction TB
        AC["AnimatorComponent<br/>kmax_layers = 32"]
        Skel["skeleton: Ref&lt;SkeletonAsset&gt;"]
        Layers["layers: Vector&lt;unique_ptr&lt;Layer&gt;&gt;"]
        Pose["glm_pose: ozz::vector&lt;matrix4&gt;<br/>(world-space bone matrices)"]
        LocalPose["local_pose: ozz::vector&lt;matrix4&gt;<br/>(model-space bone matrices)"]
        SkinMats["skinningmats: ozz::vector&lt;matrix4&gt;<br/>(pose * inverse_bindpose)"]
        AllTrans["all_transforms: ozz::vector&lt;SoaTransform&gt;<br/>(blended output)"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Layer Structure"
        Layer["Layer"]
        States["states: locked_node_hashmap&lt;anim_id_t, State&gt;"]
        CurrentState["currentState: anim_id_t"]
        Playing["isPlaying: bool"]
        Blending["isBlending: bool"]
        Transforms["transforms: ozz::vector&lt;SoaTransform&gt;"]
        Weight["weight: float"]
        Additive["isAdditive: bool"]
        SkMask["skeletonMask: optional&lt;Ref&lt;SkeletonMask&gt;&gt;"]
    end
    
    AC --> Skel
    AC --> Layers
    AC --> Pose
    AC --> LocalPose
    AC --> SkinMats
    AC --> AllTrans
    
    Layers --> Layer
    Layer --> States
    Layer --> CurrentState
    Layer --> Playing
    Layer --> Blending
    Layer --> Transforms
    Layer --> Weight
    Layer --> Additive
    Layer --> SkMask
```

**Diagram: AnimatorComponent internal structure with Layer organization**

The component stores multiple representations of bone transforms:
- `all_transforms`: SoA (Structure of Arrays) format used by Ozz for SIMD optimization, contains blended output from all layers
- `models`: Ozz's Float4x4 format in model space
- `local_pose`: GLM matrix4 format in model space
- `glm_pose`: GLM matrix4 format in world space (includes entity transform)
- `skinningmats`: Final matrices used by GPU skinning shader (pose Ã— inverse_bindpose)

Sources: [include/RavEngine/AnimatorComponent.hpp:132-391](), [src/AnimatorComponent.cpp:108-169]()

### Layer System

Each `Layer` maintains its own state machine with states and transitions. Layers support:
- **Weight blending**: Each layer has a `weight` value controlling its contribution to final pose
- **Additive blending**: Layers can be marked as `isAdditive` to add on top of base layers
- **Skeleton masking**: Optional `SkeletonMask` restricts which bones the layer affects
- **Independent playback**: Each layer maintains its own `isPlaying` flag and playback state

```mermaid
graph TD
    subgraph "Layer::State Structure"
        State["State"]
        ID["ID: anim_id_t (uint16_t)"]
        Clip["clip: Ref&lt;IAnimGraphable&gt;"]
        Loop["isLooping: bool"]
        Speed["speed: float"]
        LastTime["lastPlayTime: double"]
        ExitTrans["exitTransitions: UnorderedMap&lt;anim_id_t, Transition&gt;"]
        AutoTrans["hasAutoTransition: bool<br/>autoTransitionID: anim_id_t"]
        Callbacks["beginCallback: Function&lt;void(anim_id_t)&gt;<br/>endCallback: Function&lt;void(anim_id_t)&gt;"]
    end
    
    subgraph "State::Transition"
        Trans["Transition"]
        TimeMode["type: TimeMode<br/>- Blended (carry over time)<br/>- BeginNew (reset to 0)"]
        Tween["transition: tweeny::tween&lt;float&gt;"]
    end
    
    State --> ID
    State --> Clip
    State --> Loop
    State --> Speed
    State --> LastTime
    State --> ExitTrans
    State --> AutoTrans
    State --> Callbacks
    
    ExitTrans --> Trans
    Trans --> TimeMode
    Trans --> Tween
```

**Diagram: Layer State and Transition structure**

The `State` structure [include/RavEngine/AnimatorComponent.hpp:144-235]() represents a node in the animation state machine. Key features:
- Each state references an `IAnimGraphable` (can be `AnimationAsset`, `AnimBlendTree`, etc.)
- States define exit transitions to other states with configurable blending curves
- Auto-transitions trigger automatically when non-looping animations complete
- Callbacks fire when states begin or end

Sources: [include/RavEngine/AnimatorComponent.hpp:144-235](), [include/RavEngine/AnimatorComponent.hpp:243-331]()

### Component Usage

To create and configure an `AnimatorComponent`:

```cpp
// Create component with a skeleton
auto animator = entity.EmplaceComponent<AnimatorComponent>(
    Manager<SkeletonAsset>::Get("character_skeleton")
);

// Add a layer
auto layer = animator->AddLayer();

// Insert states with animations
layer->InsertState(AnimatorComponent::State(
    0, // state ID
    Manager<AnimationAsset>::Get("idle"),
    true, // looping
    1.0f  // speed
));

layer->InsertState(AnimatorComponent::State(
    1, // state ID  
    Manager<AnimationAsset>::Get("walk"),
    true,
    1.0f
));

// Configure transition from idle to walk
layer->GetNode(0).SetTransition(
    1, // target state ID
    tweeny::easing::cubicInOut,
    0.3, // duration in seconds
    AnimatorComponent::State::Transition::TimeMode::Blended
);

// Start playing
layer->Play();
layer->Goto(0); // go to idle state
```

The `AnimatorComponent::Tick` method [src/AnimatorComponent.cpp:108-169]() executes each frame to:
1. Tick each layer to sample animations and handle state transitions
2. Blend layer outputs using `ozz::animation::BlendingJob` (supports normal and additive blending)
3. Convert from local space to model space using `ozz::animation::LocalToModelJob`
4. Calculate skinning matrices by multiplying pose matrices with inverse bindposes
5. Update world-space pose for socket attachment and debug rendering

Sources: [include/RavEngine/AnimatorComponent.hpp:241-377](), [src/AnimatorComponent.cpp:33-35](), [src/AnimatorComponent.cpp:108-169](), [src/AnimatorComponent.cpp:283-291]()

## Animation Assets

### AnimationAsset

`AnimationAsset` represents a pre-computed skeletal animation. Assets are loaded from `.rvea` files produced by the `rveac` animation compiler and stored in the `.rvedata` archive. Internally, animations use Ozz-animation's compressed format for efficient storage and playback.

| Property | Type | Description |
|----------|------|-------------|
| `anim` | `ozz::unique_ptr<ozz::animation::Animation>` | Ozz-animation compressed animation data |
| `duration_seconds` | `float` | Animation duration in seconds |
| `tps` | `float` | Ticks per second (frames per second from source) |

The asset loading process [src/AnimationAsset.cpp:96-144]():
1. Load `.rvea` file from virtual filesystem
2. Deserialize to intermediate `JointAnimation` format [src/AnimationAsset.cpp:61-94]()
3. Convert to `ozz::animation::offline::RawAnimation`
4. Use `ozz::animation::offline::AnimationBuilder` to create optimized runtime animation
5. Store ticks-per-second and duration for time calculations

**Serialized Animation Format (.rvea)**:

```
SerializedJointAnimationHeader:
- header: array<char, 4> = "rvea"
- duration: float (in ticks)
- ticksPerSecond: float
- numTracks: uint32_t
- nameLength: uint16_t

Animation Name: char[nameLength]

For each track:
  SerializedJointAnimationTrackHeader:
  - numTranslations: uint32_t
  - numRotations: uint32_t
  - numScales: uint32_t
  
  Translation Keys: KeyFrame<vec3>[numTranslations]
  Rotation Keys: KeyFrame<quat>[numRotations]
  Scale Keys: KeyFrame<vec3>[numScales]
```

The number of tracks must match the number of bones in the target skeleton. Each track contains keyframes for translation, rotation, and scale at specific time points.

Sources: [include/RavEngine/AnimationAsset.hpp:57-81](), [src/AnimationAsset.cpp:96-144](), [src/AnimationAsset.cpp:61-94]()

### IAnimGraphable Interface

`IAnimGraphable` [include/RavEngine/AnimationAsset.hpp:28-52]() is the base interface for all animation graph nodes. It defines a single method for sampling animation data:

```cpp
virtual bool Sample(
    float t,        // current time
    float start,    // time when animation was started
    float speed,    // playback speed multiplier
    bool looping,   // whether to loop
    ozz::vector<ozz::math::SoaTransform>& output,  // output transforms
    ozz::animation::SamplingJob::Context& cache,   // sampling cache
    const ozz::animation::Skeleton* skeleton       // target skeleton
) const = 0;
```

The method returns `true` when a non-looping animation completes. Implementations include:

| Implementation | Purpose |
|----------------|---------|
| `AnimationAsset` | Plays a pre-computed animation |
| `AnimationAssetSegment` | Plays a time range within an `AnimationAsset` |
| `AnimationClip` | Blends multiple `IAnimGraphable` nodes with influence weights |
| `AnimBlendTree` | 2D spatial blending (see [Animation Blending and Blend Trees](#6.3)) |
| `CustomSkeletonAnimation` | Code-driven animation via user-provided function |

```mermaid
graph TB
    IAnimGraphable["IAnimGraphable<br/>(interface)<br/>+ Sample(...)"]
    
    AnimAsset["AnimationAsset<br/>- anim: ozz::Animation<br/>Plays compressed animation"]
    
    AnimSegment["AnimationAssetSegment<br/>- anim_asset: Ref&lt;AnimationAsset&gt;<br/>- start_ticks, end_ticks: float<br/>Plays sub-range of animation"]
    
    AnimClip["AnimationClip<br/>- influence: hashmap&lt;IAnimGraphable, Sampler&gt;<br/>Blends multiple animations with weights"]
    
    BlendTree["AnimBlendTree<br/>- states: hashmap&lt;anim_id_t, Node&gt;<br/>- blend_pos: clamped_vec2<br/>2D spatial blending (see page 6.3)"]
    
    CustomAnim["CustomSkeletonAnimation<br/>- mutateBonesHook: Function<br/>Code-driven animation"]
    
    IAnimGraphable --> AnimAsset
    IAnimGraphable --> AnimSegment
    IAnimGraphable --> AnimClip
    IAnimGraphable --> BlendTree
    IAnimGraphable --> CustomAnim
    
    AnimSegment --> AnimAsset
    AnimClip --> IAnimGraphable
    BlendTree --> IAnimGraphable
```

**Diagram: IAnimGraphable interface hierarchy and implementations**

Sources: [include/RavEngine/AnimationAsset.hpp:28-52](), [include/RavEngine/AnimationAsset.hpp:57-81](), [include/RavEngine/AnimationAsset.hpp:142-155](), [include/RavEngine/AnimationAsset.hpp:157-196]()

### AnimationAssetSegment

`AnimationAssetSegment` [include/RavEngine/AnimationAsset.hpp:142-155]() allows playing a sub-range of an `AnimationAsset`, similar to Unity's animation clip ranges. This is useful when a single animation file contains multiple logical animations.

```cpp
auto walkCycle = std::make_shared<AnimationAssetSegment>(
    Manager<AnimationAsset>::Get("character_anims"),
    0.0f,    // start at tick 0
    120.0f   // end at tick 120
);

auto runCycle = std::make_shared<AnimationAssetSegment>(
    Manager<AnimationAsset>::Get("character_anims"),
    120.0f,  // start at tick 120
    240.0f   // end at tick 240
);
```

The `Sample` implementation [src/AnimationAsset.cpp:21-45]() calculates the normalized time within the segment range and delegates to the underlying asset's sampling.

Sources: [include/RavEngine/AnimationAsset.hpp:142-155](), [src/AnimationAsset.cpp:21-45]()

### AnimationClip

`AnimationClip` [include/RavEngine/AnimationAsset.hpp:157-196]() blends multiple `IAnimGraphable` nodes with configurable influence weights. This enables layered animation where, for example, a walking animation can be blended with an aiming animation.

```cpp
auto clip = std::make_shared<AnimationClip>();
clip->SetAnimationInfluence(walkAnim, 0.7f);  // 70% walk
clip->SetAnimationInfluence(runAnim, 0.3f);   // 30% run
```

The `Sample` implementation [src/AnimationAsset.cpp:171-204]() samples all child animations into separate buffers, then uses `ozz::animation::BlendingJob` to combine them with the specified weights.

Sources: [include/RavEngine/AnimationAsset.hpp:157-196](), [src/AnimationAsset.cpp:171-204]()

### CustomSkeletonAnimation

`CustomSkeletonAnimation` [include/RavEngine/AnimationAsset.hpp:101-110]() enables procedural, code-driven animation. Users provide a function that receives a `BoneTransforms` wrapper and modifies bone transformations programmatically.

```cpp
auto proceduralAnim = std::make_shared<CustomSkeletonAnimation>(
    [](BoneTransforms transforms, const ozz::animation::Skeleton* skeleton,
       float t, float start, float speed, bool looping) -> bool {
        // Get and modify bones
        auto headBone = transforms.GetBone(skeleton->joint_names()["head"]);
        headBone.rotation = glm::angleAxis(sin(t) * 0.1f, glm::vec3(0,1,0));
        transforms.SetBone(skeleton->joint_names()["head"], headBone);
        return false; // never ends
    }
);
```

`BoneTransforms` [include/RavEngine/AnimationAsset.hpp:83-96]() provides `GetBone`/`SetBone` methods to manipulate individual bone transforms. The underlying data is in Ozz's SoA format, but the wrapper converts to a more intuitive per-bone structure.

Sources: [include/RavEngine/AnimationAsset.hpp:101-126](), [include/RavEngine/AnimationAsset.hpp:83-96](), [src/AnimationAsset.cpp:206-209](), [src/AnimationAsset.cpp:211-255]()

## Skeleton Assets

`SkeletonAsset` represents a hierarchical bone structure. Assets are loaded from `.rves` files produced by the `rveskc` skeleton compiler. The asset stores both CPU-side bone data and GPU buffers for shader access.

### SkeletonAsset Structure

```mermaid
graph LR
    subgraph "SkeletonAsset"
        SA["SkeletonAsset"]
        OzzSkel["skeleton: ozz::unique_ptr&lt;Skeleton&gt;<br/>Runtime-optimized bone hierarchy"]
        Bindposes["bindposes: Vector&lt;glm::mat4&gt;<br/>Inverse bindpose matrices (CPU)"]
        BindposeGPU["bindpose: RGLBufferPtr<br/>SSBO with inverse bindposes"]
        Hierarchy["boneHierarchy: RGLBufferPtr<br/>SSBO with parent indices"]
    end
    
    SA --> OzzSkel
    SA --> Bindposes
    SA --> BindposeGPU
    SA --> Hierarchy
```

**Diagram: SkeletonAsset internal structure**

The asset loading process [src/SkeletonAsset.cpp:90-176]():
1. Load `.rves` file from virtual filesystem
2. Deserialize to intermediate `SkeletonData` format with hierarchical bones [src/SkeletonAsset.cpp:23-88]()
3. Convert to `ozz::animation::offline::RawSkeleton`
4. Validate and build runtime `ozz::animation::Skeleton` using `ozz::animation::offline::SkeletonBuilder`
5. Extract rest pose and compute inverse bindpose matrices
6. Upload bindposes and hierarchy to GPU buffers for shader access

**Serialized Skeleton Format (.rves)**:

```
SerializedSkeletonDataHeader:
- header: array<char, 4> = "rves"
- numBones: uint32_t

For each bone:
  BoneTransform:
  - translation: vec3
  - rotation: quat
  - scale: vec3

For each bone:
  Name Length: uint16_t
  Name: char[length]

For each bone:
  Num Children: uint16_t
  Child Indices: uint16_t[numChildren]
```

The skeleton hierarchy is flattened during serialization with explicit child indices, then reconstructed into a tree structure during loading.

Sources: [include/RavEngine/SkeletonAsset.hpp:15-66](), [src/SkeletonAsset.cpp:90-176](), [src/SkeletonAsset.cpp:23-88]()

### Bindpose and Hierarchy Buffers

The **bindpose buffer** stores inverse bindpose matrices for GPU skinning [src/SkeletonAsset.cpp:129-162](). The skinning shader multiplies animated bone matrices by these inverse bindposes to transform vertices from bind pose to animated pose.

The **boneHierarchy buffer** [src/SkeletonAsset.cpp:164-174]() is a linear array where each index represents a bone, and the value at that index is the parent bone's index. A value of -1 indicates a root bone with no parent. This enables GPU-side traversal of the skeleton hierarchy if needed.

Both buffers are created as Storage Buffers (`StorageBuffer = true`) with `Private` access, populated once at load time:

```cpp
bindpose = device->CreateBuffer({
    uint32_t(bindposes.size()),
    {.StorageBuffer = true},
    sizeof(bindposes[0]),
    RGL::BufferAccess::Private
});
bindpose->SetBufferData({ bindposes.data(), bindposes.size() * sizeof(bindposes[0]) });
```

Sources: [src/SkeletonAsset.cpp:154-174]()

### Bone Queries

`SkeletonAsset` provides methods to query bone indices by name:

```cpp
std::optional<uint16_t> IndexForBone(const std::string_view boneName) const;
bool HasBone(const std::string_view boneName) const;
```

These iterate through Ozz's `joint_names()` array [src/SkeletonAsset.cpp:188-200]() to find matching bone names. Bone indices are used for socket attachment and per-bone manipulation in custom animations.

Sources: [include/RavEngine/SkeletonAsset.hpp:59-65](), [src/SkeletonAsset.cpp:188-200]()

## Skinned Mesh Assets

`MeshAssetSkinned` extends `MeshAsset` with bone weight data for vertex skinning. These assets are loaded from `.rvem` files that contain both standard mesh data (positions, normals, UVs) and additional per-vertex bone weights.

### MeshAssetSkinned Structure

```mermaid
graph TB
    subgraph "Inheritance"
        MeshAsset["MeshAsset<br/>- meshAllocation: MeshRange<br/>- totalVerts, totalIndices: size_t<br/>- attributes: MeshAttributes<br/>- bounds: Bounds"]
        MeshSkinned["MeshAssetSkinned<br/>- weightsBuffer: RGLBufferPtr"]
    end
    
    MeshAsset --> MeshSkinned
    
    subgraph "Vertex Weights"
        Weights["VertexWeights struct<br/>(4 bones per vertex)"]
        BoneIndices["boneIDs: uint16_t[4]<br/>Indices into skeleton"]
        BoneWeights["weights: float[4]<br/>Influence per bone<br/>Sum to 1.0"]
    end
    
    MeshSkinned --> Weights
    Weights --> BoneIndices
    Weights --> BoneWeights
```

**Diagram: MeshAssetSkinned structure and vertex weight format**

The `.rvem` file format for skinned meshes contains:
1. Standard `SerializedMeshDataHeader` with mesh geometry (see [Asset Pipeline](#2.2))
2. Vertex positions, normals, tangents, UVs (if attributes are present)
3. Index buffer
4. **Additional section**: Array of `VertexWeights` (one per vertex)

Each `VertexWeights` entry contains 4 bone indices and 4 corresponding weights. This matches the GPU skinning shader's expectations [src/MeshAssetSkinned.cpp:44-70]():

```cpp
// Validate weight count matches vertex count
auto size = ((str.data() + str.size()) - fp) / sizeof(VertexWeights);
Debug::Assert(size == GetNumVerts(), "Skin does not have vertex weights for every vertex");

// Create GPU buffer
weightsBuffer = device->CreateBuffer({
    uint32_t(weightsgpu.size()),
    {.StorageBuffer = true},
    sizeof(VertexWeights),
    RGL::BufferAccess::Private,
    {.Writable = false}
});
```

The `weightsBuffer` is bound in the skinning compute shader to read bone influences during vertex deformation. See [Skeletal Skinning Pipeline](#6.4) for details on GPU skinning.

Sources: [include/RavEngine/MeshAssetSkinned.hpp:12-31](), [src/MeshAssetSkinned.cpp:25-72]()

### Loading Skinned Meshes

To load a `MeshAssetSkinned`:

```cpp
auto skinnedMesh = Manager<MeshAssetSkinned>::Get("character_body");

// Use with SkinnedMeshComponent for rendering
entity.EmplaceComponent<SkinnedMeshComponent>(skinnedMesh, material);
```

The asset loader [src/MeshAssetSkinned.cpp:25-72]():
1. Calls parent `MeshAsset` deserialization for geometry
2. Validates weight data is present
3. Reads `VertexWeights` array from file
4. Uploads to GPU as a Storage Buffer

The mesh's geometry goes into the engine's shared mesh buffer (see [GPU-Driven Rendering Techniques](#9.2)), while the weights buffer is stored separately and bound per-mesh during skinning.

Sources: [src/MeshAssetSkinned.cpp:25-72]()

## Asset Pipeline Integration

Animation assets are processed by host tools during the build phase and packaged into the `.rvedata` archive. The pipeline supports cross-compilation, allowing assets to be built on one platform for use on another.

```mermaid
graph LR
    subgraph "Source Formats"
        FBX[".fbx / .gltf<br/>3D model files<br/>with animations"]
        JSON["animation_config.json<br/>Per-animation settings"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Host Tools"
        RVEMC["rvemc<br/>Mesh Compiler<br/>Outputs .rvem"]
        RVESKC["rveskc<br/>Skeleton Compiler<br/>Outputs .rves"]
        RVEAC["rveac<br/>Animation Compiler<br/>Outputs .rvea"]
        ImportLib["rve_importlib<br/>Assimp integration<br/>Reads FBX/glTF"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Intermediate Formats"
        RVEM[".rvem<br/>Mesh + Weights"]
        RVES[".rves<br/>Skeleton Hierarchy"]
        RVEA[".rvea<br/>Animation Tracks"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Runtime Loading"
        VFS["VirtualFilesystem<br/>PhysFS<br/>.rvedata archive"]
        AssetMgr["Asset Managers<br/>Lazy loading<br/>Weak caching"]
    end
    
    FBX --> ImportLib
    JSON --> RVEAC
    
    ImportLib --> RVEMC
    ImportLib --> RVESKC
    ImportLib --> RVEAC
    
    RVEMC --> RVEM
    RVESKC --> RVES
    RVEAC --> RVEA
    
    RVEM --> VFS
    RVES --> VFS
    RVEA --> VFS
    
    VFS --> AssetMgr
```

**Diagram: Animation asset pipeline from source files to runtime loading**

The process involves:

1. **Source Assets**: Artists create models with skeletons and animations in DCC tools (Blender, Maya, etc.), export as FBX or glTF
2. **Host Tool Compilation**: 
   - `rvemc` extracts mesh geometry and bone weights â†’ `.rvem`
   - `rveskc` extracts skeleton hierarchy â†’ `.rves`
   - `rveac` extracts animation keyframes â†’ `.rvea`
3. **Packaging**: `pack_resources.cmake` function archives all assets into `TARGET.rvedata`
4. **Runtime Loading**: Assets are lazily loaded through manager classes when first requested

Each asset type has a corresponding manager for caching:
- `SkeletonAsset`: `SkeletonManager` [include/RavEngine/SkeletonAsset.hpp:68]()
- `AnimationAsset`: `AnimationAssetManager` [include/RavEngine/AnimationAsset.hpp:198]()
- `MeshAssetSkinned`: `MeshAssetSkinned::Manager` [include/RavEngine/MeshAssetSkinned.hpp:25]()

These managers use `GenericWeakReadThroughCache` to maintain weak references, allowing assets to be unloaded when no longer used:

```cpp
auto skeleton = Manager<SkeletonAsset>::Get("character_skeleton");
auto animation = Manager<AnimationAsset>::Get("character_idle");
auto mesh = Manager<MeshAssetSkinned>::Get("character_body");
```

For details on the build system and cross-compilation, see [Cross-Platform Build System](#9.4).

Sources: [include/RavEngine/SkeletonAsset.hpp:68](), [include/RavEngine/AnimationAsset.hpp:198](), [include/RavEngine/MeshAssetSkinned.hpp:25](), [src/SkeletonAsset.cpp:90-127](), [src/AnimationAsset.cpp:96-143](), [src/MeshAssetSkinned.cpp:25-38]()

## Tick and Sampling Flow

Each frame, the `World` calls `AnimatorComponent::Tick` [src/AnimatorComponent.cpp:108-169]() for all active animators. The tick process orchestrates sampling, blending, and transform calculations.

```mermaid
graph TD
    WorldTick["World::Tick<br/>(each frame)"]
    AnimTick["AnimatorComponent::Tick(Transform&)"]
    
    LayerTick["For each Layer:<br/>Layer::Tick(skeleton)"]
    
    SampleState["If playing:<br/>Sample current State's IAnimGraphable"]
    
    BlendState["If blending:<br/>Sample both from/to states<br/>Blend with tween progress"]
    
    OzzSample["IAnimGraphable::Sample(...)<br/>Writes to layer transforms"]
    
    LayerBlend["ozz::animation::BlendingJob<br/>Blend all layer outputs<br/>Normal + Additive layers<br/>Apply weights & skeleton masks<br/>Output to all_transforms"]
    
    LocalToModel["ozz::animation::LocalToModelJob<br/>Convert SoA transforms<br/>to model-space matrices<br/>Output to models"]
    
    CalcSkinning["For each bone:<br/>skinningmats[i] = local_pose[i] * bindpose[i]"]
    
    UpdateWorld["GetPose(transform)<br/>Multiply models by entity world matrix<br/>Output to glm_pose"]
    
    WorldTick --> AnimTick
    AnimTick --> LayerTick
    
    LayerTick --> SampleState
    LayerTick --> BlendState
    
    SampleState --> OzzSample
    BlendState --> OzzSample
    
    OzzSample --> LayerBlend
    LayerBlend --> LocalToModel
    LocalToModel --> CalcSkinning
    CalcSkinning --> UpdateWorld
```

**Diagram: Frame-by-frame tick and sampling flow through AnimatorComponent**

The tick process:

1. **Layer Ticking** [src/AnimatorComponent.cpp:171-238](): Each layer samples its current state's animation
   - If **blending** between states: samples both from/to states, uses `ozz::animation::BlendingJob` to interpolate based on tween progress
   - If **not blending**: samples only the current state
   - Handles auto-transitions for completed non-looping animations

2. **Layer Blending** [src/AnimatorComponent.cpp:113-147](): Combines all layer outputs
   - Separates normal and additive layers
   - Creates `ozz::animation::BlendingJob::Layer` array with transforms, weights, and optional skeleton masks
   - Runs `BlendingJob` to produce final `all_transforms`

3. **Space Conversion** [src/AnimatorComponent.cpp:150-158](): Converts from local SoA to model-space matrices
   - Uses `ozz::animation::LocalToModelJob` with skeleton hierarchy
   - Output goes to `models` (Ozz Float4x4 format)

4. **Skinning Matrix Calculation** [src/AnimatorComponent.cpp:160-165](): Prepares matrices for GPU
   - Multiplies pose matrices by inverse bindposes
   - Result stored in `skinningmats` for upload to GPU

5. **World-Space Update** [src/AnimatorComponent.cpp:168](): Combines with entity transform
   - `GetPose` multiplies model-space bones by entity's world matrix
   - Used for socket attachment and debug rendering

The `skinningmats` buffer is uploaded to GPU during render data synchronization (see [Skeletal Skinning Pipeline](#6.4)).

Sources: [src/AnimatorComponent.cpp:108-169](), [src/AnimatorComponent.cpp:171-238](), [src/AnimatorComponent.cpp:299-316](), [src/AnimatorComponent.cpp:319-336]()2e:T44b5,# Animation State Machines

## Purpose and Scope

This page documents RavEngine's animation state machine system, which enables character animation control through states and transitions. State machines are managed per-layer within `AnimatorComponent` and allow defining animation states, transition curves, auto-progression, and state callbacks.

For information about the `AnimatorComponent` class and animation assets, see [Animation Components and Assets](#6.1). For details about blending multiple animations, see [Animation Blending and Blend Trees](#6.3).

---

## State Machine Hierarchy

RavEngine organizes animation state machines hierarchically through layers. Each `AnimatorComponent` can contain up to 32 layers, and each layer maintains its own independent state machine.

**Diagram: State Machine Architecture**
```mermaid
graph TB
    AnimatorComponent["AnimatorComponent"]
    
    subgraph Layers["Layers (max 32)"]
        Layer0["Layer 0<br/>AnimatorComponent::Layer"]
        Layer1["Layer 1<br/>AnimatorComponent::Layer"]
        LayerN["Layer N<br/>AnimatorComponent::Layer"]
    end
    
    subgraph StateMachine0["Layer 0 State Machine"]
        State0_Idle["State: Idle<br/>ID=0"]
        State0_Walk["State: Walk<br/>ID=1"]
        State0_Run["State: Run<br/>ID=2"]
        
        State0_Idle -->|"SetTransition(1, easing, duration)"| State0_Walk
        State0_Walk -->|"SetTransition(2, easing, duration)"| State0_Run
        State0_Run -->|"SetTransition(0, easing, duration)"| State0_Idle
        State0_Walk -->|"SetAutoTransition(0)"| State0_Idle
    end
    
    subgraph StateContents["State Contents"]
        StateClip["State::clip<br/>Ref&lt;IAnimGraphable&gt;"]
        StateSpeed["State::speed<br/>float"]
        StateLooping["State::isLooping<br/>bool"]
        StateTransitions["State::exitTransitions<br/>UnorderedMap&lt;anim_id_t, Transition&gt;"]
    end
    
    AnimatorComponent --> Layer0
    AnimatorComponent --> Layer1
    AnimatorComponent --> LayerN
    
    Layer0 --> State0_Idle
    Layer0 --> State0_Walk
    Layer0 --> State0_Run
    
    State0_Idle --> StateClip
    State0_Idle --> StateSpeed
    State0_Idle --> StateLooping
    State0_Idle --> StateTransitions
```

Sources: [include/RavEngine/AnimatorComponent.hpp:132-391](), [include/RavEngine/AnimatorComponent.hpp:243-331](), [include/RavEngine/AnimatorComponent.hpp:144-235]()

---

## States

### State Structure

A `State` represents a single animation node in the state machine. Each state contains:

| Property | Type | Description |
|----------|------|-------------|
| `ID` | `anim_id_t` (uint16_t) | Numeric identifier for the state |
| `clip` | `Ref<IAnimGraphable>` | Animation asset, blend tree, or custom animation |
| `isLooping` | `bool` | Whether the animation repeats |
| `speed` | `float` | Playback speed multiplier (1.0 = normal) |
| `exitTransitions` | `UnorderedMap<anim_id_t, Transition>` | Transitions to other states |
| `lastPlayTime` | `double` | Internal tracking for playback time |

Sources: [include/RavEngine/AnimatorComponent.hpp:144-175]()

### Creating States

States are created by constructing a `State` object and inserting it into a layer:

```cpp
// Create state with ID, clip, looping flag, and speed
AnimatorComponent::State idleState(0, idleAnimation, true, 1.0f);
layer->InsertState(idleState);

AnimatorComponent::State walkState(1, walkAnimation, true, 1.0f);
layer->InsertState(walkState);
```

States can reference any `IAnimGraphable` object, including:
- `AnimationAsset` - Pre-baked animation clips
- `AnimationAssetSegment` - Subsections of animations
- `AnimBlendTree` - 2D spatial blending graphs
- `AnimationClip` - Weighted animation combinations
- `CustomSkeletonAnimation` - Code-driven animations

Sources: [include/RavEngine/AnimatorComponent.hpp:175](), [include/RavEngine/AnimatorComponent.hpp:261-263]()

---

## Transitions

### Transition Configuration

Transitions define how the state machine blends from one state to another. Each state stores its exit transitions in the `exitTransitions` map, keyed by target state ID.

**Diagram: Transition System**
```mermaid
graph LR
    subgraph StateA["State A"]
        ClipA["clip: AnimationAsset"]
        ExitTrans["exitTransitions"]
    end
    
    subgraph Transition["Transition to State B"]
        TransType["TimeMode<br/>Blended / BeginNew"]
        TransTween["transition: tweeny::tween&lt;float&gt;<br/>Easing curve"]
    end
    
    subgraph StateB["State B"]
        ClipB["clip: AnimationAsset"]
    end
    
    StateA --> Transition
    Transition --> StateB
    ExitTrans --> TransType
    ExitTrans --> TransTween
```

Sources: [include/RavEngine/AnimatorComponent.hpp:153-170]()

### Setting Transitions

The `SetTransition()` method configures how a state transitions to another state:

```cpp
// Parameters: target_id, interpolation, duration, time_mode
state.SetTransition(targetStateID, 
                    tweeny::easing::cubicInOut,  // Easing function
                    0.5,                          // Duration in seconds
                    State::Transition::TimeMode::Blended);
```

The transition stores a `tweeny::tween` object that interpolates from 0.0 to 1.0 over the specified duration using the provided easing function.

Sources: [include/RavEngine/AnimatorComponent.hpp:164-170](), [src/AnimatorComponent.cpp:72-73]()

### Time Modes

Transitions support two time handling modes:

| TimeMode | Behavior |
|----------|----------|
| `Blended` | The playback time carries over from the source state to the target state |
| `BeginNew` | The target state's playback time resets to 0 when the transition begins |

Sources: [include/RavEngine/AnimatorComponent.hpp:154-157](), [src/AnimatorComponent.cpp:67-69]()

### Manual Transitions

The `Layer::Goto()` method triggers a transition to a new state:

```cpp
// Transition to state with ID=1
layer->Goto(1);

// Skip blending and jump immediately
layer->Goto(1, true);  // skipTransition=true

// Restart animation regardless of time mode
layer->Goto(1, false, true);  // restartAnimation=true
```

**Diagram: Goto() Transition Logic**
```mermaid
graph TD
    GotoCall["Layer::Goto(newState, skipTransition, restartAnimation)"]
    
    CheckSame{"newState ==<br/>currentState?"}
    CallEndCallback["currentState.DoEnd(newState)"]
    
    CheckSkip{"skipTransition<br/>|| no transition<br/>defined?"}
    
    JumpState["currentState = newState<br/>Set lastPlayTime if restartAnimation"]
    
    SetupBlend["Setup StateBlend:<br/>- stateBlend.from = currentState<br/>- stateBlend.to = newState<br/>- Copy transition tween<br/>- isBlending = true"]
    
    CheckTimeMode{"TimeMode ==<br/>BeginNew<br/>|| restartAnimation?"}
    
    ResetTime["GetStateForID(newState).lastPlayTime<br/>= GetApp()->GetCurrentTime()"]
    
    CallBeginCallback["newState.DoBegin(prevState)"]
    
    GotoCall --> CheckSame
    CheckSame -->|"No"| CallEndCallback
    CheckSame -->|"Yes"| CheckSkip
    CallEndCallback --> CheckSkip
    
    CheckSkip -->|"Yes"| JumpState
    CheckSkip -->|"No"| CheckTimeMode
    
    CheckTimeMode -->|"Yes"| ResetTime
    CheckTimeMode -->|"No"| SetupBlend
    ResetTime --> SetupBlend
    
    JumpState --> CallBeginCallback
    SetupBlend --> CallBeginCallback
```

Sources: [src/AnimatorComponent.cpp:46-79](), [include/RavEngine/AnimatorComponent.hpp:255]()

### Auto-Transitions

States can automatically transition to another state when their animation completes. This is useful for non-looping animations that should chain together.

```cpp
// When this state finishes, automatically go to state 0
state.SetAutoTransition(0);

// Clear auto-transition
state.ClearAutoTransition();
```

**Note:** Auto-transitions only trigger when the animation completes. Looping animations never complete, so they will never auto-transition.

Sources: [include/RavEngine/AnimatorComponent.hpp:200-210](), [src/AnimatorComponent.cpp:320-326]()

---

## State Callbacks

States support callbacks that execute when the state begins or ends. Callbacks receive the ID of the previous/next state as a parameter.

```cpp
// Called when this state becomes active
state.SetBeginCallback([](anim_id_t prevState) {
    Debug::Log("Entered state from state {}", prevState);
});

// Called when this state exits
state.SetEndCallback([](anim_id_t nextState) {
    Debug::Log("Exiting state to state {}", nextState);
});
```

Callbacks are invoked in the following order:
1. `currentState.DoEnd(newState)` - Exit callback for old state
2. State transition occurs
3. `newState.DoBegin(prevState)` - Enter callback for new state

Sources: [include/RavEngine/AnimatorComponent.hpp:216-226](), [include/RavEngine/AnimatorComponent.hpp:182-192](), [src/AnimatorComponent.cpp:49-51](), [src/AnimatorComponent.cpp:78]()

---

## Layer Management

### Creating Layers

Layers are created using `AnimatorComponent::AddLayer()`:

```cpp
auto animator = entity.EmplaceComponent<AnimatorComponent>(skeleton);

// Add layers
auto baseLayer = animator.AddLayer();
auto upperBodyLayer = animator.AddLayer();

// Configure layer properties
upperBodyLayer->SetWeight(0.5f);
upperBodyLayer->SetAdditive(true);
upperBodyLayer->SetSkeletonMask(armsMask);
```

Sources: [src/AnimatorComponent.cpp:283-291](), [include/RavEngine/AnimatorComponent.hpp:373-377]()

### Layer Properties

| Property | Method | Description |
|----------|--------|-------------|
| Weight | `SetWeight(float)` | Blend weight for this layer (0.0-1.0) |
| Additive | `SetAdditive(bool)` | Whether layer adds to base pose or replaces it |
| Skeleton Mask | `SetSkeletonMask(Ref<SkeletonMask>)` | Limits layer to specific bones |

Sources: [include/RavEngine/AnimatorComponent.hpp:290-298]()

### Layer Playback Control

Each layer has independent playback state:

```cpp
// Start playing the current state
layer->Play();

// Start playing and reset to beginning
layer->Play(true);  // resetPlayhead=true

// Pause playback
layer->Pause();

// Get current state ID
auto currentState = layer->GetCurrentState();
```

Sources: [include/RavEngine/AnimatorComponent.hpp:269-271](), [src/AnimatorComponent.cpp:87-106]()

---

## Transition Blending Implementation

When a transition is active, the layer blends between the source and target states using ozz's `BlendingJob`. The blend weight is controlled by the transition tween's progress.

**Diagram: Transition Blending Process**
```mermaid
graph TD
    TickStart["Layer::Tick(skeleton)"]
    
    CheckPlaying{"isPlaying?"}
    CheckBlending{"isBlending?"}
    
    SampleBoth["Sample both states:<br/>fromState.clip->Sample() â†’ transforms<br/>toState.clip->Sample() â†’ transformsSecondaryBlending"]
    
    StepTween["currentBlendingValue = stateBlend.currentTween.step()"]
    
    SetupLayers["Setup BlendingJob::Layer[2]:<br/>layers[0].weight = 1 - currentBlendingValue<br/>layers[1].weight = currentBlendingValue"]
    
    BlendJob["ozz::animation::BlendingJob::Run()<br/>Blend transforms â†’ output"]
    
    CheckProgress{"tween.progress()<br/>&gt;= 1.0?"}
    
    EndBlending["isBlending = false<br/>Call EndState if animation done"]
    
    SampleSingle["Sample single state:<br/>currentState.clip->Sample() â†’ transforms"]
    
    Return["Return transforms"]
    
    TickStart --> CheckPlaying
    CheckPlaying -->|"No"| Return
    CheckPlaying -->|"Yes"| CheckBlending
    
    CheckBlending -->|"Yes"| StepTween
    CheckBlending -->|"No"| SampleSingle
    
    StepTween --> SampleBoth
    SampleBoth --> SetupLayers
    SetupLayers --> BlendJob
    BlendJob --> CheckProgress
    
    CheckProgress -->|"Yes"| EndBlending
    CheckProgress -->|"No"| Return
    EndBlending --> Return
    
    SampleSingle --> Return
```

Sources: [src/AnimatorComponent.cpp:171-238]()

### Blending Math

During transitions, the blend weight interpolates from 0.0 to 1.0:

- **Layer 0 (source state)**: `weight = 1.0 - currentBlendingValue`
- **Layer 1 (target state)**: `weight = currentBlendingValue`

The tween advances each frame based on the frame time scale:

```cpp
currentBlendingValue = stateBlend.currentTween.step(
    (float)timeScale / stateBlend.currentTween.duration()
);
```

When `tween.progress() >= 1.0`, blending completes and the layer switches to single-state mode.

Sources: [src/AnimatorComponent.cpp:187-209]()

---

## Multi-Layer Blending

The `AnimatorComponent` blends all layers together during its `Tick()` method. Layers are separated into normal and additive categories.

**Diagram: Multi-Layer Blend Process**
```mermaid
graph TD
    AnimTick["AnimatorComponent::Tick(Transform)"]
    
    SetupNormal["Setup normal layers:<br/>For each layer where isAdditive=false<br/>- layer->Tick(skeleton)<br/>- Create BlendingJob::Layer<br/>- Set weight and skeleton mask"]
    
    SetupAdditive["Setup additive layers:<br/>For each layer where isAdditive=true<br/>- layer->Tick(skeleton)<br/>- Create BlendingJob::Layer<br/>- Set weight and skeleton mask"]
    
    BlendAll["ozz::animation::BlendingJob:<br/>- layers = normal layers<br/>- additive_layers = additive layers<br/>- rest_pose = skeleton rest pose<br/>- output = all_transforms"]
    
    LocalToModel["ozz::animation::LocalToModelJob:<br/>Convert local space â†’ model space<br/>all_transforms â†’ models"]
    
    CalcSkinning["Calculate skinning matrices:<br/>skinningmats[i] = pose[i] * bindpose[i]"]
    
    UpdateWorld["GetPose(transform):<br/>Update world-space poses"]
    
    AnimTick --> SetupNormal
    SetupNormal --> SetupAdditive
    SetupAdditive --> BlendAll
    BlendAll --> LocalToModel
    LocalToModel --> CalcSkinning
    CalcSkinning --> UpdateWorld
```

Sources: [src/AnimatorComponent.cpp:108-169](), [src/AnimatorComponent.cpp:138-147]()

This page documents RavEngine's animation blending system, which enables smooth transitions and combinations of multiple animations. The system supports weighted blending, 2D spatial blend trees, layered animation compositing, and state transition blending.

For information about animation state machines and transitions, see [Animation State Machines](#6.2). For the GPU-based skeletal skinning process, see [Skeletal Skinning Pipeline](#6.4). For basic animation components and assets, see [Animation Components and Assets](#6.1).

## Overview

RavEngine's animation blending system is built on top of the Ozz-animation library and provides several blending mechanisms:

- **Blend Trees**: 2D spatial blending where animations are arranged on a plane and blended based on a control point
- **Animation Clips**: Simple weighted blending of multiple animations
- **Layer Blending**: Stacking multiple animation layers with per-layer weights and skeleton masks
- **State Transition Blending**: Smooth blending between animation states during transitions
- **Additive Animations**: Layering additive animations on top of base animations

All blending operations use Ozz's `ozz::animation::BlendingJob` for efficient SIMD-optimized blending.

**Sources**: [include/RavEngine/AnimatorComponent.hpp:42-129](), [include/RavEngine/AnimationAsset.hpp:25-196](), [src/AnimatorComponent.cpp:108-148]()

## Animation Graph Interface

The `IAnimGraphable` interface defines the contract for all animation graph nodes that can be sampled and blended:

```cpp
struct IAnimGraphable {
    virtual bool Sample(
        float t,                                      // Current time
        float start,                                  // Start time
        float speed,                                  // Playback speed
        bool looping,                                 // Loop flag
        ozz::vector<ozz::math::SoaTransform>& output, // Output transforms
        ozz::animation::SamplingJob::Context& cache,  // Sampling cache
        const ozz::animation::Skeleton* skeleton      // Skeleton
    ) const = 0;
};
```

Types that implement `IAnimGraphable`:
- `AnimationAsset`: Pre-computed animation clips loaded from `.rvea` files
- `AnimationAssetSegment`: Subrange of an `AnimationAsset`
- `AnimationClip`: Weighted blend of multiple `IAnimGraphable` nodes
- `AnimBlendTree`: 2D spatial blend of multiple `IAnimGraphable` nodes
- `AnimBlendTree::Node`: Individual node within a blend tree
- `CustomSkeletonAnimation`: Code-driven procedural animation

**Sources**: [include/RavEngine/AnimationAsset.hpp:28-52](), [include/RavEngine/AnimationAsset.hpp:57-196](), [include/RavEngine/AnimatorComponent.hpp:42-129]()

### Animation Graph Hierarchy

```mermaid
graph TD
    IAnimGraphable["IAnimGraphable<br/>interface"]
    
    AnimationAsset["AnimationAsset<br/>Pre-computed clip"]
    AnimationSegment["AnimationAssetSegment<br/>Subrange of clip"]
    AnimationClip["AnimationClip<br/>Weighted blend"]
    BlendTree["AnimBlendTree<br/>2D spatial blend"]
    BlendNode["AnimBlendTree::Node<br/>Tree node wrapper"]
    CustomAnim["CustomSkeletonAnimation<br/>Code-driven"]
    
    IAnimGraphable --> AnimationAsset
    IAnimGraphable --> AnimationSegment
    IAnimGraphable --> AnimationClip
    IAnimGraphable --> BlendTree
    IAnimGraphable --> BlendNode
    IAnimGraphable --> CustomAnim
    
    AnimationSegment -->|references| AnimationAsset
    AnimationClip -->|contains| IAnimGraphable
    BlendTree -->|contains| BlendNode
    BlendNode -->|wraps| IAnimGraphable
    
    State["AnimatorComponent::State<br/>State machine node"]
    State -->|clip| IAnimGraphable
```

**Sources**: [include/RavEngine/AnimationAsset.hpp:28-196](), [include/RavEngine/AnimatorComponent.hpp:42-129](), [include/RavEngine/AnimatorComponent.hpp:144-235]()

## Blend Trees (2D Spatial Blending)

`AnimBlendTree` provides 2D spatial blending where animation nodes are positioned on a normalized 2D plane ([-1,1] on both axes) and blended based on their distance from a movable control point.

### Blend Tree Structure

**Key Classes**:
- `AnimBlendTree`: Container for blend tree nodes ([AnimatorComponent.hpp:42-129]())
- `AnimBlendTree::Node`: Individual node with position and max influence ([AnimatorComponent.hpp:43-61]())
- `clamped_vec2`: 2D vector clamped to [-1,1] range ([AnimatorComponent.hpp:24-36]())

**Node Management**:
```cpp
// Insert/update node at ID
void InsertNode(anim_id_t id, const Node& node);

// Remove node
void DeleteNode(anim_id_t id);

// Get node reference for modification
Node& GetNode(anim_id_t id);

// Set control point position
void SetBlendPos(const clamped_vec2& newPos);
```

**Sources**: [include/RavEngine/AnimatorComponent.hpp:42-129]()

### Blend Tree Sampling Process

```mermaid
graph TD
    Start["AnimBlendTree::Sample()"]
    
    Iterate["Iterate all nodes in tree"]
    SampleNode["Sample node animation<br/>node.Sample()"]
    CalcInfluence["Calculate influence:<br/>1.0 - distance(blend_pos, node.graph_pos)<br/>* node.max_influence"]
    PopulateLayer["Populate BlendingJob::Layer:<br/>layer.transform = node locals<br/>layer.weight = influence"]
    
    SetupBlendJob["Setup ozz::animation::BlendingJob:<br/>- layers array<br/>- rest_pose from skeleton<br/>- output buffer"]
    RunBlendJob["blend_job.Run()<br/>SIMD-optimized blending"]
    OutputResult["Output blended transforms"]
    
    Start --> Iterate
    Iterate --> SampleNode
    SampleNode --> CalcInfluence
    CalcInfluence --> PopulateLayer
    PopulateLayer --> |Next node| Iterate
    PopulateLayer --> |All nodes done| SetupBlendJob
    SetupBlendJob --> RunBlendJob
    RunBlendJob --> OutputResult
```

**Sources**: [src/AnimatorComponent.cpp:342-378]()

### Blend Tree Implementation Details

The influence calculation uses Euclidean distance:
```cpp
float distance(const clamped_vec2& p1, const clamped_vec2& p2) {
    return std::sqrt(std::pow(p2.get_x() - p1.get_x(), 2) + 
                     std::pow(p2.get_y() - p1.get_y(), 2));
}

// In blend tree sampling:
layers[index].weight = 1.0 - distance(blend_pos, sampler.node.graph_pos) 
                            * sampler.node.max_influence;
```

**Constraints**:
- Maximum 64 nodes per blend tree (`kmax_nodes = 64`)
- Node positions clamped to [-1, 1] on both axes
- Control point also clamped to [-1, 1] range
- Blend threshold is 0.1 (configurable in code)

**Sources**: [src/AnimatorComponent.cpp:16-18](), [src/AnimatorComponent.cpp:342-378](), [include/RavEngine/AnimatorComponent.hpp:63]()

## Animation Clips (Weighted Blending)

`AnimationClip` provides simple weighted blending of multiple `IAnimGraphable` nodes with manually specified influences.

### AnimationClip API

```cpp
class AnimationClip : public IAnimGraphable {
    // Add or update animation with influence weight
    void SetAnimationInfluence(Ref<IAnimGraphable> asset, float influence = 1);
    
    // Remove animation
    void RemoveAnimation(Ref<IAnimGraphable> asset);
    
    // Clear all animations
    void Clear();
    
    // Check if empty
    bool IsEmpty() const;
    
    // Sample all animations and blend
    bool Sample(float t, float start, float speed, bool looping, 
                ozz::vector<ozz::math::SoaTransform>&,
                ozz::animation::SamplingJob::Context&,
                const ozz::animation::Skeleton*) const override;
};
```

**Sources**: [include/RavEngine/AnimationAsset.hpp:157-196]()

### AnimationClip Sampling

The `AnimationClip::Sample` implementation samples each child animation and blends them using Ozz's `BlendingJob`:

| Step | Operation | Code Location |
|------|-----------|---------------|
| 1. Iterate animations | For each `IAnimGraphable` in `influence` map | [AnimationAsset.cpp:176-192]() |
| 2. Sample animation | Call `row.first->Sample(...)` into local buffer | [AnimationAsset.cpp:178]() |
| 3. Populate layer | Set `layer.transform` and `layer.weight` | [AnimationAsset.cpp:189-190]() |
| 4. Setup blend job | Create `BlendingJob` with all layers | [AnimationAsset.cpp:194-197]() |
| 5. Run blend | Execute `blend_job.Run()` | [AnimationAsset.cpp:200-202]() |

**Sources**: [src/AnimationAsset.cpp:171-204]()

## Layer Blending

`AnimatorComponent` supports multiple animation layers that are blended together to produce the final pose. Each layer runs its own state machine and can have independent weights, skeleton masks, and additive modes.

### Layer Configuration

```cpp
struct AnimatorComponent::Layer {
    // Weight for this layer (default 1.0)
    void SetWeight(float w);
    float GetWeight() const;
    
    // Skeleton mask (optional per-joint weights)
    void SetSkeletonMask(Ref<SkeletonMask> mask);
    
    // Additive mode
    void SetAdditive(bool additive);
};
```

**Layer Properties**:
- **Weight**: Multiplier for the layer's contribution (0.0 to 1.0+)
- **Skeleton Mask**: Per-joint weights to limit layer influence to specific bones
- **Additive**: Whether the layer is additive or normal blending

**Sources**: [include/RavEngine/AnimatorComponent.hpp:243-300]()

### Layer Blending Pipeline

```mermaid
graph TD
    TickStart["AnimatorComponent::Tick()"]
    
    SetupNormal["Setup normal layers:<br/>Filter isAdditive == false"]
    SetupAdditive["Setup additive layers:<br/>Filter isAdditive == true"]
    
    TickLayer["For each layer:<br/>layer->Tick(skeleton)"]
    PopulateNormal["Populate blend_layers[]:<br/>- layer.transform<br/>- layer.weight<br/>- layer.joint_weights (if mask)"]
    PopulateAdditive["Populate additive_blend_layers[]:<br/>Same structure"]
    
    CreateBlendJob["Create ozz::animation::BlendingJob:<br/>- layers span (normal)<br/>- additive_layers span<br/>- rest_pose<br/>- threshold = 0.1"]
    
    RunBlend["blend_job.Run()<br/>Write to all_transforms"]
    LocalToModel["LocalToModelJob:<br/>Convert SoA local â†’ model space"]
    CreateSkinning["Create skinning matrices:<br/>pose[i] * inverse_bindpose[i]"]
    
    TickStart --> SetupNormal
    SetupNormal --> TickLayer
    TickLayer --> PopulateNormal
    
    TickStart --> SetupAdditive
    SetupAdditive --> TickLayer
    TickLayer --> PopulateAdditive
    
    PopulateNormal --> CreateBlendJob
    PopulateAdditive --> CreateBlendJob
    
    CreateBlendJob --> RunBlend
    RunBlend --> LocalToModel
    LocalToModel --> CreateSkinning
```

**Sources**: [src/AnimatorComponent.cpp:108-169]()

### Layer Blending Implementation

The layer blending occurs in `AnimatorComponent::Tick`:

**Normal vs Additive Separation**:
```cpp
auto setupLayers = [this]<bool isAdditive>(auto&& blend_layers) {
    uint16_t i = 0;
    for(auto& layer : layers) {
        if(layer->isAdditive != isAdditive) {
            continue;  // Filter out wrong type
        }
        layer->Tick(skeleton);
        
        blend_layers[i].transform = ozz::make_span(layer->transforms);
        blend_layers[i].weight = layer->GetWeight();
        
        if (auto mask = layer->GetSkeletonMask()) {
            blend_layers[i].joint_weights = ozz::span(
                mask.value()->mask.data(), 
                mask.value()->mask.size()
            );
        }
        i++;
    }
    return i;
};
```

**Blending Job Setup**:
```cpp
ozz::animation::BlendingJob blend_job;
blend_job.threshold = 0.1f;  // Configurable threshold
blend_job.layers = ozz::span(blend_layers, numLayers);
blend_job.additive_layers = ozz::span(additive_blend_layers, numAdditiveLayers);
blend_job.rest_pose = skeleton->GetSkeleton()->joint_rest_poses();
blend_job.output = make_span(all_transforms);

if (!blend_job.Run()) {
    Debug::Fatal("Blend job failed");
}
```

**Constraints**:
- Maximum 32 layers per `AnimatorComponent` (`kmax_layers = 32`)
- Skeleton masks must match skeleton joint count

**Sources**: [src/AnimatorComponent.cpp:113-148](), [include/RavEngine/AnimatorComponent.hpp:141]()

## State Transition Blending

When transitioning between animation states within a layer, RavEngine blends the source and target states using configurable transition curves.

### Transition Configuration

Transitions are configured on the source state:

```cpp
State& SetTransition(
    anim_id_t target_id,      // Target state ID
    T interpolation,           // Tweeny interpolation type
    decimal duration,          // Transition duration
    Transition::TimeMode mode  // Time handling mode
);
```

**Time Modes**:
- `TimeMode::Blended`: Time carries over from source to target state
- `TimeMode::BeginNew`: Target state time resets to 0

**Sources**: [include/RavEngine/AnimatorComponent.hpp:154-170]()

### State Transition Blending Flow

```mermaid
graph TD
    GotoState["Layer::Goto(newState)"]
    
    CheckTransition{"Has transition<br/>to target?"}
    JustJump["Jump to state directly:<br/>currentState = newState<br/>isBlending = false"]
    
    SetupBlend["Setup blending:<br/>stateBlend.from = currentState<br/>stateBlend.to = newState<br/>isBlending = true"]
    
    CheckTimeMode{"Transition<br/>TimeMode?"}
    CarryTime["BeginNew:<br/>Reset target lastPlayTime"]
    BlendTime["Blended:<br/>Keep target time"]
    
    SeekTween["Seek tween to 0:<br/>stateBlend.currentTween.seek(0)"]
    
    Tick["Layer::Tick()"]
    CheckBlending{"isBlending?"}
    
    SampleBoth["Sample both states:<br/>fromState â†’ transforms<br/>toState â†’ transformsSecondaryBlending"]
    StepTween["Step tween:<br/>currentBlendingValue = tween.step(...)"]
    
    CreateLayers["Create 2 BlendingJob::Layer:<br/>layers[0].weight = 1 - blend value<br/>layers[1].weight = blend value"]
    
    RunBlend["BlendingJob.Run()<br/>Write to transforms"]
    
    CheckComplete{"Tween<br/>complete?"}
    EndBlending["isBlending = false<br/>Call EndState callbacks"]
    
    GotoState --> CheckTransition
    CheckTransition -->|No| JustJump
    CheckTransition -->|Yes| SetupBlend
    
    SetupBlend --> CheckTimeMode
    CheckTimeMode -->|BeginNew| CarryTime
    CheckTimeMode -->|Blended| BlendTime
    
    CarryTime --> SeekTween
    BlendTime --> SeekTween
    SeekTween --> Tick
    
    Tick --> CheckBlending
    CheckBlending -->|No| SingleState["Sample single state"]
    CheckBlending -->|Yes| SampleBoth
    
    SampleBoth --> StepTween
    StepTween --> CreateLayers
    CreateLayers --> RunBlend
    RunBlend --> CheckComplete
    
    CheckComplete -->|Yes| EndBlending
    CheckComplete -->|No| Tick
```

**Sources**: [src/AnimatorComponent.cpp:46-79](), [src/AnimatorComponent.cpp:171-238]()

### Transition Blending Implementation

The transition blending occurs in `AnimatorComponent::Layer::Tick`:

**During Transition**:
```cpp
if (isBlending) {
    auto& fromState = GetStateForID(stateBlend.from);
    auto& toState = GetStateForID(stateBlend.to);
    
    // Update tween
    currentBlendingValue = stateBlend.currentTween.step(
        (float)timeScale / stateBlend.currentTween.duration()
    );
    
    // Sample both states
    fromState.clip->Sample(..., transforms, ...);
    toState.clip->Sample(..., transformsSecondaryBlending, ...);
    
    // Setup blend layers
    layers[0].transform = ozz::make_span(transforms);
    layers[0].weight = 1 - currentBlendingValue;
    layers[1].transform = ozz::make_span(transformsSecondaryBlending);
    layers[1].weight = currentBlendingValue;
    
    // Blend
    ozz::animation::BlendingJob blend_job;
    blend_job.threshold = 0.1f;
    blend_job.layers = layers;
    blend_job.rest_pose = skeleton->GetSkeleton()->joint_rest_poses();
    blend_job.output = make_span(transforms);
    blend_job.Run();
    
    // Check completion
    if (stateBlend.currentTween.progress() >= 1.0) {
        isBlending = false;
    }
}
```

**Sources**: [src/AnimatorComponent.cpp:179-219]()

## Ozz-Animation Integration

RavEngine uses Ozz-animation's `BlendingJob` for all blending operations. This provides SIMD-optimized blending of `SoaTransform` (Structure of Arrays) data.

### BlendingJob Structure

| Field | Type | Purpose |
|-------|------|---------|
| `layers` | `ozz::span<Layer>` | Normal blend layers |
| `additive_layers` | `ozz::span<Layer>` | Additive blend layers |
| `rest_pose` | `ozz::span<SoaTransform>` | Skeleton rest pose (fallback) |
| `output` | `ozz::span<SoaTransform>` | Blended output transforms |
| `threshold` | `float` | Weight threshold for layer inclusion |

**Layer Structure**:
```cpp
struct BlendingJob::Layer {
    ozz::span<const SoaTransform> transform;  // Input transforms
    float weight;                              // Layer weight
    ozz::span<const SimdFloat4> joint_weights; // Per-joint weights (optional)
};
```

**Sources**: [src/AnimatorComponent.cpp:138-147](), [src/AnimatorComponent.cpp:195-219]()

### SoaTransform Layout

Ozz uses a Structure of Arrays (SoA) layout for SIMD efficiency. Each `SoaTransform` contains 4 joints' worth of data:

```
SoaTransform {
    SimdFloat4 translation.x  // x translations for joints 0-3
    SimdFloat4 translation.y  // y translations for joints 0-3
    SimdFloat4 translation.z  // z translations for joints 0-3
    
    SimdFloat4 rotation.x     // Quaternion x for joints 0-3
    SimdFloat4 rotation.y     // Quaternion y for joints 0-3
    SimdFloat4 rotation.z     // Quaternion z for joints 0-3
    SimdFloat4 rotation.w     // Quaternion w for joints 0-3
    
    SimdFloat4 scale.x        // x scales for joints 0-3
    SimdFloat4 scale.y        // y scales for joints 0-3
    SimdFloat4 scale.z        // z scales for joints 0-3
}
```

The number of `SoaTransform` elements needed is `skeleton->num_soa_joints()`, which equals `(num_joints + 3) / 4`.

**Sources**: [src/AnimatorComponent.cpp:256-276](), [include/RavEngine/AnimationAsset.hpp:17-19]()

### Blend Threshold

The blend threshold (default 0.1) determines the minimum weight a layer must have to contribute to the blend. Layers with weights below this threshold are excluded from blending, improving performance.

```cpp
blend_job.threshold = 0.1f;  // TODO: make threshold configurable
```

This threshold appears in:
- Blend tree sampling ([AnimatorComponent.cpp:367]())
- Animation clip sampling ([AnimationAsset.cpp:195]())
- Layer blending ([AnimatorComponent.cpp:139]())
- State transition blending ([AnimatorComponent.cpp:212]())

**Sources**: [src/AnimatorComponent.cpp:139](), [src/AnimatorComponent.cpp:212](), [src/AnimatorComponent.cpp:367](), [src/AnimationAsset.cpp:195]()

### Post-Blending Pipeline

```mermaid
graph LR
    BlendJob["BlendingJob output:<br/>SoaTransform (local space)"]
    
    LocalToModel["LocalToModelJob:<br/>Convert to model space<br/>matrix per joint"]
    
    Skinning["Create skinning matrices:<br/>pose * inverse_bindpose"]
    
    WorldPose["GetPose():<br/>Convert to world space<br/>using entity transform"]
    
    BlendJob --> LocalToModel
    LocalToModel --> Skinning
    Skinning --> WorldPose
```

**Conversion Steps**:
1. **Local to Model**: `ozz::animation::LocalToModelJob` converts local-space SoA transforms to model-space matrices
2. **Skinning Matrices**: Multiply model-space pose by inverse bind pose: `skinningmats[i] = pose[i] * bindpose[i]`
3. **World Space**: Multiply by entity transform for debug visualization and socket attachment

**Sources**: [src/AnimatorComponent.cpp:150-169](), [src/AnimatorComponent.cpp:299-336]()30:T4d09,# Skeletal Skinning Pipeline

## Purpose and Scope

This page documents RavEngine's GPU-based skeletal skinning pipeline, which transforms mesh vertices according to skeletal bone animations. The pipeline uses compute shaders to perform vertex deformation on the GPU, enabling efficient rendering of animated characters and models.

For information about animation state machines and blending, see [Animation State Machines](#6.2). For skeleton and animation asset loading, see [Animation Components and Assets](#6.1). For the overall rendering architecture, see [Rendering Architecture](#4.1).

---

## Overview

The skeletal skinning pipeline transforms static mesh vertices into their animated positions based on bone transformations. This process occurs entirely on the GPU using compute shaders, minimizing CPU-GPU bandwidth and enabling parallel processing of thousands of vertices.

**Key Components:**
- **AnimatorComponent** - Computes bone transformation matrices on CPU
- **SkeletonAsset** - Provides bind pose (rest pose) matrices
- **MeshAssetSkinned** - Contains per-vertex bone weights and indices
- **Skinning Compute Shader** - Performs GPU-side vertex transformation

Sources: [src/RenderEngine_Draw.cpp:475-630](), [include/RavEngine/AnimatorComponent.hpp:132-392](), [include/RavEngine/SkeletonAsset.hpp:15-69]()

---

## Pipeline Architecture

```mermaid

        BlendLayers["Blend Animation Layers"]
        LocalToModel["LocalToModelJob<br/>(Ozz Library)"]
        ComputeSkinMats["Compute Skinning Matrices<br/>pose * inverse_bindpose"]
    end
    
    subgraph "CPU: Prepare GPU Buffers"
        PrepareBuffers["prepareSkeletalMeshBuffers"]
        ResizeBuffers["Resize GPU Buffers if Needed"]
        PrepareIndirect["prepareSkeletalCullingBuffer<br/>Setup Indirect Draw Commands"]
    end
    
    subgraph "CPU-GPU Transfer"

    end
    
    subgraph "GPU: Compute Shader Execution"
        BindBuffers["Bind Input/Output Buffers"]
        DispatchCS["Dispatch skinning_cs_csh<br/>Per-Object, Per-Vertex"]

    end

    end

    SampleAnims --> BlendLayers

    LocalToModel --> ComputeSkinMats
    
    ComputeSkinMats --> PrepareBuffers
    PrepareBuffers --> ResizeBuffers
    ResizeBuffers --> PrepareIndirect
    PrepareIndirect --> CopyMatrices
    
    CopyMatrices --> BindBuffers

```
