## Skinning Matrix Computation

```mermaid
graph LR
    subgraph "Ozz Animation Library"
        SampleJob["SamplingJob<br/>Sample Animation Clip"]
        BlendJob["BlendingJob<br/>Blend Multiple Layers"]
        L2MJob["LocalToModelJob<br/>Local to Model Space"]
    end
    
    subgraph "RavEngine Processing"
        GetPose["models array<br/>(world-space bone transforms)"]
        GetBindPose["skeleton->GetBindposes()<br/>(inverse bind poses)"]
        ComputeSkin["skinningmats[i] =<br/>pose[i] * inverse_bindpose[i]"]
    end
    
    SampleJob --> BlendJob
    BlendJob --> L2MJob
    L2MJob --> GetPose
    GetBindPose --> ComputeSkin
    GetPose --> ComputeSkin
```

**Diagram: Skinning Matrix Computation Flow**

The skinning matrices transform vertices from their bind pose (rest state) to their animated pose. The formula is:

```
skinningMatrix[bone_i] = currentPose[bone_i] * inverseBindPose[bone_i]
```

Where:
- `currentPose[bone_i]` - The bone's current transformation in model space
- `inverseBindPose[bone_i]` - The inverse of the bone's rest pose transformation

This computation happens in `AnimatorComponent::Tick`:

```cpp
// create pose-bindpose skinning matrices
auto& pose = GetLocalPose();
auto& bindpose = skeleton->GetBindposes();
for(int i = 0; i < skinningmats.size(); i++){
    skinningmats[i] = pose[i] * matrix4(bindpose[i]);
}
```

Sources: [src/AnimatorComponent.cpp:161-166](), [include/RavEngine/AnimatorComponent.hpp:387-389]()

---

## GPU Buffer Allocation

Before skinning can occur, the render engine must allocate appropriately-sized GPU buffers. This happens in `prepareSkeletalMeshBuffers`:

```mermaid
graph TD
    CountObjects["Count Total Objects to Skin<br/>totalObjectsToSkin"]
    CountVerts["Count Total Vertices<br/>totalVertsToSkin"]
    CountJoints["Count Total Joints<br/>totalJointsToSkin"]
    
    ResizeShared["Resize Shared Buffers:<br/>sharedSkeletonMatrixBuffer<br/>sharedSkinnedPositionBuffer<br/>etc."]
    
    ResizePerMaterial["Resize Per-Material Buffers:<br/>indirectBuffer<br/>cullingBuffer"]
    
    CountObjects --> CountVerts
    CountObjects --> CountJoints
    CountVerts --> ResizeShared
    CountJoints --> ResizeShared
    CountObjects --> ResizePerMaterial
    
    ResizeShared --> Return["Return skeletalMeshesExist flag"]
    ResizePerMaterial --> Return
```

**Diagram: Buffer Allocation Logic**

The buffer sizes are calculated based on:
- **Per-object data**: Each animated entity needs space in indirect draw and culling buffers
- **Per-vertex data**: Total vertices = sum of all mesh vertex counts * instance counts
- **Per-joint data**: Total joints = sum of all skeleton joint counts * instance counts

Buffer allocation uses power-of-2 sizing to minimize reallocations:

```cpp
auto newSize = closest_power_of<uint32_t>(neededSize, 2);
```

Sources: [src/RenderEngine_Draw.cpp:479-543](), [src/RenderEngine.cpp:486-509]()

---

## Skinning Compute Shader Execution

### Dispatch Parameters

The `poseSkeletalMeshes` function dispatches the skinning compute shader with the following structure:

```cpp
struct SkinningUBO {
    uint32_t numObjects;        // Number of mesh instances
    uint32_t numVertices;       // Vertices per mesh
    uint32_t numBones;          // Joints in skeleton
    uint32_t boneReadOffset;    // Offset in matrix buffer
    uint32_t vertexWriteOffset; // Offset in output buffer
    uint32_t vertexReadOffset;  // Offset in input buffer
};
```

### Workgroup Dimensions

The compute shader is dispatched with:
- **X dimension**: `ceil(numObjects / 8.0)` - Process 8 objects per workgroup
- **Y dimension**: `ceil(numVertices / 32.0)` - Process 32 vertices per workgroup
- **Z dimension**: `1`

Local workgroup size:
- **X**: 8 threads (one per object)
- **Y**: 32 threads (one per vertex)
- **Z**: 1 thread

This means each invocation handles one vertex of one mesh instance.

Sources: [src/RenderEngine_Draw.cpp:577-628](), [include/RavEngine/RenderEngine.hpp:178-186]()

### Buffer Binding Flow

```mermaid
graph TB
    subgraph "Output Buffers (Writable)"
        OutPos["Binding 0:<br/>sharedSkinnedPositionBuffer"]
        OutNorm["Binding 1:<br/>sharedSkinnedNormalBuffer"]
        OutTan["Binding 2:<br/>sharedSkinnedTangentBuffer"]
        OutBitan["Binding 3:<br/>sharedSkinnedBitangentBuffer"]
        OutUV["Binding 4:<br/>sharedSkinnedUV0Buffer"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Input Buffers (Read-Only)"
        InPos["Binding 10:<br/>sharedPositionBuffer"]
        InNorm["Binding 11:<br/>sharedNormalBuffer"]
        InTan["Binding 12:<br/>sharedTangentBuffer"]
        InBitan["Binding 13:<br/>sharedBitangentBuffer"]
        InUV["Binding 14:<br/>sharedUV0Buffer"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Skinning Data (Read-Only)"
        MatBuf["Binding 20:<br/>sharedSkeletonMatrixBuffer"]
        WeightBuf["Binding 21:<br/>mesh->GetWeightsBuffer()"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Compute Shader"
        CS["skinning_cs_csh"]
    end
    
    InPos --> CS
    InNorm --> CS
    InTan --> CS
    InBitan --> CS
    InUV --> CS
    MatBuf --> CS
    WeightBuf --> CS
    
    CS --> OutPos
    CS --> OutNorm
    CS --> OutTan
    CS --> OutBitan
    CS --> OutUV
```

**Diagram: Compute Shader Buffer Bindings**

## Per-Material Command Preparation

Before rendering skinned meshes, indirect draw commands must be prepared. This happens in `prepareSkeletalCullingBuffer`:

```mermaid
graph TD
    BeginPipeline["Begin skinningDrawCallPreparePipeline"]
    
    ForEachMaterial["For Each Material"]
    BindIndirect["Bind Material's indirectBuffer"]
    
    ForEachCommand["For Each Mesh+Skeleton Command"]
    SetupUBO["Setup SkinningPrepareUBO:<br/>- vertexCount<br/>- indexCount<br/>- objectCount<br/>- offsets"]
    
    Dispatch["Dispatch Compute:<br/>ceil(objectCount / 32) workgroups"]

    ForEachMaterial --> BindIndirect

    ForEachCommand --> SetupUBO
    SetupUBO --> Dispatch
    Dispatch --> UpdateOffsets
    UpdateOffsets --> ForEachCommand
```

**Diagram: Indirect Draw Command Setup**

The `skinned_mesh_drawcall_csh` compute shader initializes each `RGL::IndirectIndexedCommand` with:
- `indexCount` - Number of indices in the mesh
- `instanceCount` - Initially 0 (filled by culling pass)
- `indexStart` - Offset into index buffer
- `baseVertex` - Offset into vertex buffer
- `baseInstance` - Instance offset

Sources: [src/RenderEngine_Draw.cpp:546-574](), [include/RavEngine/RenderEngine.hpp:232-240]()

---

## Vertex Transformation Math

Each vertex is transformed by up to 4 bones (as defined by vertex weights). The shader performs:

```
For each vertex v:
    transformedPosition = vec3(0)
    transformedNormal = vec3(0)
    
    For each bone influence i (0 to 3):
        boneIndex = v.boneIndices[i]
        weight = v.boneWeights[i]
        
        if weight > 0:
            skinningMatrix = matrices[object_id * numBones + boneIndex]
            transformedPosition += (skinningMatrix * vec4(v.position, 1.0)).xyz * weight
            transformedNormal += (mat3(skinningMatrix) * v.normal) * weight
    
    output.position = transformedPosition
    output.normal = normalize(transformedNormal)
```

The vertex weights are stored in `VertexWeights` structure:

```cpp
struct VertexWeights {
    uint32_t joint_index[4];  // Bone indices
    float influence[4];        // Bone weights (sum = 1.0)
};
```

Sources: [include/RavEngine/Common3D.hpp]() (implied from vertex weight structure), [src/RenderEngine_Draw.cpp:596-619]()

---

## Memory Layout and Indexing

```mermaid
graph TB
    subgraph "Skinning Matrix Buffer Layout"
        Obj0["Object 0:<br/>matrices[0..numBones-1]"]
        Obj1["Object 1:<br/>matrices[numBones..2*numBones-1]"]
        ObjN["Object N:<br/>matrices[N*numBones..(N+1)*numBones-1]"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Vertex Output Buffer Layout"
        Mesh0Obj0["Mesh0 Object 0:<br/>vertices[0..numVerts-1]"]
        Mesh0Obj1["Mesh0 Object 1:<br/>vertices[numVerts..2*numVerts-1]"]
        Mesh1Obj0["Mesh1 Object 0:<br/>vertices[offset..offset+numVerts-1]"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Indexing Calculation"
        BoneIdx["boneIndex = object_id * numBones + bone_i"]
        VertIdx["vertexIndex = vertexWriteOffset + object_id * numVertices + vertex_i"]
    end
```

**Diagram: Buffer Memory Layout**

The `SkinningUBO` contains offsets that allow the shader to locate data correctly:

| Field | Purpose |
|-------|---------|
| `boneReadOffset` | Starting index in matrix buffer for this batch |
| `vertexReadOffset` | Starting index in input vertex buffers |
| `vertexWriteOffset` | Starting index in output vertex buffers |

These offsets are updated after each mesh is processed to ensure data doesn't overlap.

Sources: [src/RenderEngine_Draw.cpp:598-625](), [include/RavEngine/RenderEngine.hpp:178-186]()

---

## Integration with Rendering Pipeline

After skinning completes, the skinned vertices flow into the main rendering pipeline:

```mermaid
graph LR
    Skinning["Skinning Compute Pass<br/>Write to sharedSkinnedXXXBuffer"]
    
    Culling["GPU Culling Pass<br/>defaultcull.csh"]
    
    DepthPrepass["Depth Prepass<br/>Read skinned vertices"]
    
    MainPass["Main Rendering Pass<br/>Lit/Unlit Materials"]
    
    Skinning --> Culling
    Culling --> DepthPrepass
    DepthPrepass --> MainPass
```

**Diagram: Skinned Mesh Rendering Flow**

The culling pass operates on skinned meshes similarly to static meshes:
- Uses `isSingleInstanceModeAndShadowMode` flag to indicate skinned mesh mode (bit 0 set to 1)
- Each skinned mesh instance gets its own draw call in the indirect buffer
- Frustum and occlusion culling still apply

Sources: [src/RenderEngine_Draw.cpp:1079-1258](), [shaders/defaultcull.csh:186-187]()

---

## Performance Considerations

### Buffer Sizing Strategy

The engine uses power-of-2 sizing for buffers to minimize reallocations:

```cpp
if (!buffer || buffer->getBufferSize() / stride < neededSize) {
    auto newSize = closest_power_of<uint32_t>(neededSize, 2);
    buffer = device->CreateBuffer({newSize, type, stride, access, options});
}
```

This means buffers may be larger than strictly necessary, trading memory for reduced allocation overhead.

### Shared vs. Per-Material Buffers

| Buffer Type | Scope | Purpose |
|-------------|-------|---------|
| Shared (e.g., `sharedSkinnedPositionBuffer`) | All skinned meshes | Stores transformed vertices for all objects |
| Per-Material (e.g., `indirectBuffer`) | Each material instance | Indirect draw commands for meshes using this material |

Shared buffers enable the skinning shader to process all meshes in one or few dispatches, while per-material buffers enable material batching during rendering.

### Workgroup Size Tuning

The dispatch dimensions (8x32x1) are chosen to:
- Process multiple objects in parallel (8 per workgroup)
- Maximize GPU occupancy with 32 vertices per workgroup
- Balance between workgroup granularity and total dispatch count

Sources: [src/RenderEngine.cpp:486-509](), [src/RenderEngine_Draw.cpp:622]()

---

## Error Handling and Validation

The pipeline includes several validation points:

1. **Skeleton-Mesh Compatibility**: Ensured during mesh setup (implied in asset loading)
2. **Buffer Size Validation**: Asserted in debug builds:
   ```cpp
   Debug::Assert(size == GetNumVerts(), "Skin does not have vertex weights for every vertex");
   ```
3. **Matrix Count Validation**: The number of skinning matrices must match `skeleton->num_joints() * numObjects`

Sources: [src/MeshAssetSkinned.cpp:51](), [src/RenderEngine_Draw.cpp:605-607]()

---

## Code Path Summary

### Main Execution Path

1. **`World::Tick`** - Initiates frame
2. **`AnimatorSystem::Tick`** - Processes all animators
3. **`AnimatorComponent::Tick`** - Computes skinning matrices per animator
4. **`RenderEngine::Draw`** - Main rendering entry point
5. **`prepareSkeletalMeshBuffers`** - Allocates/resizes GPU buffers
6. **`prepareSkeletalCullingBuffer`** - Initializes indirect draw commands
7. **`poseSkeletalMeshes`** - Executes skinning compute shader
8. **Culling Pass** - Determines visible skinned meshes
9. **Main Render Pass** - Draws skinned meshes using transformed vertices

|----------|------|-------|
| `AnimatorComponent::Tick` | src/AnimatorComponent.cpp | 108-169 |

RavEngine provides a comprehensive 3D spatial audio system with multi-threaded processing, HRTF-based spatialization, and advanced acoustic simulation. The audio engine supports multiple audio source types, customizable audio spaces for environmental effects, and extensible effect graphs for real-time audio processing.

**Related Pages:**
- For audio asset compilation and packaging, see [Asset Pipeline](#2.2)
- For integration with the ECS and world tick, see [Entity Component System](#3.2)

## Audio System Overview

The RavEngine audio system is built around a dedicated audio thread that processes audio in parallel with the main simulation. The system uses a snapshot-based rendering model to avoid lock contention between threads, and leverages external libraries (Steam Audio, Resonance Audio) for high-quality spatial audio processing.

### Audio System Architecture

```mermaid
graph TB
    subgraph "Main Thread - World"
        World["World"]
        AudioSources["Audio Source Components<br/>AudioSourceComponent<br/>AmbientAudioSourceComponent"]
        AudioSpaces["Audio Space Components<br/>SimpleAudioSpace<br/>GeometryAudioSpace<br/>BoxReverbationAudioSpace"]
        Listener["AudioListener"]
        Assets["AudioAsset<br/>Decoded samples"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Snapshot System"
        CreateSnapshot["World::CreateAudioSnapshot()"]
        Snapshot["AudioSnapshot<br/>sources, ambientSources<br/>simpleAudioSpaces<br/>geometryAudioSpaces<br/>boxAudioSpaces<br/>listenerPos, listenerRot"]
        SwapBuffer["App::SwapRenderAudioSnapshotIfNeeded()"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Audio Thread"
        AudioPlayer["AudioPlayer::Tick()"]
        GetSnapshot["GetRenderAudioSnapshot()"]
        Taskflow["tf::Executor<br/>2 worker threads"]
        SDL["SDL_AudioStream<br/>Device I/O"]
    end
    
    subgraph "External Libraries"
        SteamAudio["Steam Audio<br/>HRTF, Occlusion<br/>Geometry simulation"]
        Resonance["Resonance Audio<br/>Room reverb"]
    end
    
    World --> AudioSources
    World --> AudioSpaces
    World --> Listener
    AudioSources --> Assets
    
    World --> CreateSnapshot
    CreateSnapshot --> Snapshot
    Snapshot --> SwapBuffer
    
    SwapBuffer -.->|Lock-free atomic swap| AudioPlayer
    AudioPlayer --> GetSnapshot
    GetSnapshot --> Taskflow
    
    Taskflow --> SteamAudio
    Taskflow --> Resonance
    Taskflow --> SDL
    
    style AudioPlayer fill:#f9f9f9
    style Snapshot fill:#f9f9f9
    style Taskflow fill:#f9f9f9
```

**Sources:** [src/AudioPlayer.cpp:86-103](), [include/RavEngine/AudioSnapshot.hpp:11-88](), [src/AudioPlayer.cpp:391-424]()

### Key Components

| Component | Purpose | File |
|-----------|---------|------|
| `AudioPlayer` | Main audio engine, runs on dedicated thread | [include/RavEngine/AudioPlayer.hpp:27-141]() |
| `AudioAsset` | Decoded audio sample data in planar float format | [include/RavEngine/AudioSource.hpp:14-57]() |
| `AudioDataProvider` | Interface for providing audio buffers | [include/RavEngine/AudioSource.hpp:61-107]() |

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/AudioPlayer.hpp:1-144](), [include/RavEngine/AudioSource.hpp:1-215](), [include/RavEngine/AudioSnapshot.hpp:1-99]()

## Audio Assets and Loading

### AudioAsset

`AudioAsset` represents decoded audio data stored in planar float format. Audio files are loaded from the virtual filesystem, decoded using libnyquist, and optionally resampled to match the output sample rate (44.1 kHz by default).

```mermaid
graph LR
    File["Audio File<br/>.ogg, .wav<br/>in .rvedata archive"]
    VFS["PhysFS Virtual FS"]
    Load["AudioAsset constructor"]
    Decode["libnyquist decoder"]
    Resample["r8b::CDSPResampler<br/>if sample rate mismatch"]
    Convert["Channel conversion<br/>Monoâ†”Stereo"]
    PlanarData["Planar float samples<br/>PlanarSampleBufferInlineView"]
    
    File --> VFS
    VFS --> Load
    Load --> Decode
    Decode --> Resample
    Resample --> Convert
    Convert --> PlanarData
    
    style PlanarData fill:#f9f9f9
```

**Sources:** [src/AudioSource.cpp:40-115]()

The constructor accepts a file path and desired channel count:

```cpp
AudioAsset(const std::string& name, uint8_t desired_channels = 1)
```

Audio data is stored internally as planar samples (all samples for channel 0, then all samples for channel 1, etc.) accessible via `PlanarSampleBufferInlineView data`. This format is optimized for SIMD processing and matches the internal buffer format used by Steam Audio.

**Key Methods:**
- `GetLength()` - Returns audio duration in seconds
- `GetNChanels()` - Returns number of channels (1 or 2)
- `GetNumSamples()` - Returns sample count per channel
- `GetData()` - Returns raw float pointer to sample data

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/AudioSource.hpp:14-57](), [src/AudioSource.cpp:40-120]()

### Sample Rate and Channel Configuration

The audio system is configured at initialization with:
- Sample rate: 44,100 Hz (`AudioPlayer::SamplesPerSec`)
- Channels: 2 (stereo) (`AudioPlayer::nchannels`)
- Buffer size: 512 samples per channel (`AudioPlayer::buffer_size`)

If loaded audio files don't match these settings, automatic resampling and channel conversion are performed at load time.

**Sources:** [src/AudioPlayer.cpp:428-462](), [include/RavEngine/AudioPlayer.hpp:37-44]()

## Audio Data Providers

### AudioDataProvider Interface

`AudioDataProvider` is an abstract interface for any object that can fill audio buffers. It manages playback state (playing/paused), looping, and volume.

```mermaid
graph TB
    AudioDataProvider["AudioDataProvider<br/>Interface"]
    
    Properties["Properties:<br/>volume: float<br/>loops: bool<br/>isPlaying: bool<br/>renderData: SingleAudioRenderBuffer"]
    
    Methods["Methods:<br/>ProvideBufferData(out_buffer, scratch)<br/>Play() / Pause() / Restart()<br/>SetVolume(vol) / GetVolume()<br/>SetLoop(loop) / IsPlaying()"]
    
    Implementations["Implementations"]
    
    Sampled["SampledAudioDataProvider<br/>Plays AudioAsset<br/>Tracks playhead position"]
    
    Custom["Custom providers<br/>Procedural audio<br/>Streaming, etc."]
    
    AudioDataProvider --> Properties
    AudioDataProvider --> Methods
    AudioDataProvider --> Implementations
    Implementations --> Sampled
    Implementations --> Custom
    
    style AudioDataProvider fill:#f9f9f9
```

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/AudioSource.hpp:61-107]()

### SampledAudioDataProvider

`SampledAudioDataProvider` is the standard implementation that plays back `AudioAsset` data. It maintains a playhead position (`lastPlayTime`) synchronized with the global audio timeline.

**Key Features:**
- Tracks playhead using `GetApp()->GetAudioPlayer()->GetGlobalAudioTime()`
- Handles looping by wrapping playhead modulo sample count
- Applies volume scaling during buffer fill
- Automatically stops non-looping sources when reaching end

**Buffer Filling Process:**
The `ProvideBufferData()` method fills the output buffer with samples from the `AudioAsset`, accounting for the current playhead position:

1. Calculate playhead position based on global audio time
2. Copy samples from asset, applying volume scaling
3. Handle looping or zero-fill when past end
4. Apply effect graph if present

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/AudioSource.hpp:119-149](), [src/AudioSource.cpp:143-180]()

## Audio Source Components

RavEngine provides three types of audio sources for different use cases:

### Audio Source Types

```mermaid
graph TB
    Base["AudioSourceBase<br/>Base class<br/>Holds Ref&lt;AudioDataProvider&gt;"]
    
    Point["AudioSourceComponent<br/>Spatialized point source<br/>Affected by Audio Spaces<br/>ComponentWithOwner"]
    
    Ambient["AmbientAudioSourceComponent<br/>Omnipresent audio<br/>Not spatialized<br/>Not affected by Audio Spaces"]
    
    Instant["InstantaneousAudioSource<br/>Fire-and-forget<br/>Auto-destroyed when finished<br/>Spatialized"]
    
    InstantAmb["InstantaneousAmbientAudioSource<br/>Fire-and-forget<br/>Auto-destroyed when finished<br/>Not spatialized"]
    
    Base --> Point
    Base --> Ambient
    Base --> Instant
    Base --> InstantAmb
    
    style Point fill:#f9f9f9
    style Ambient fill:#f9f9f9
```

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/AudioSource.hpp:154-212]()

### AudioSourceComponent

`AudioSourceComponent` represents a 3D point source attached to an entity. Its world-space position is calculated from the entity's `Transform` component and used for spatialization within audio spaces.

**Usage:**
```cpp
auto audioProvider = New<SampledAudioDataProvider>(audioAsset);
auto source = entity.EmplaceComponent<AudioSourceComponent>(audioProvider);

// Control playback
audioProvider->Play();
audioProvider->SetVolume(0.5f);
audioProvider->SetLoop(true);
```

During world tick, `AudioSourceComponent` instances are collected into the `AudioSnapshot` along with their world positions and passed to the audio thread for spatialization.

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/AudioSource.hpp:178-180](), [src/AudioSource.cpp:23-24]()

### AmbientAudioSourceComponent

`AmbientAudioSourceComponent` plays audio that is not spatialized and not affected by audio spaces. It's suitable for background music, UI sounds, or other omnipresent audio.

**Requirements:**
- Must use an `AudioAsset` with channel count matching output configuration (2 channels for stereo output)
- Not included in spatial audio processing

**Usage:**
```cpp
auto audioProvider = New<SampledAudioDataProvider>(stereoAudioAsset, 2);
auto ambient = world.Emplace<AmbientAudioSourceComponent>(audioProvider);
```

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/AudioSource.hpp:185-187](), [src/AudioSource.cpp:26]()

### Instantaneous Audio Sources

For one-shot sound effects, RavEngine provides fire-and-forget audio sources that automatically clean up when finished:

- `InstantaneousAudioSource` - Spatialized point source at a given world position
- `InstantaneousAmbientAudioSource` - Non-spatialized omnipresent sound

These are created via helper methods on `World` and automatically destroyed when playback completes.

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/AudioSource.hpp:192-211]()

## Audio Listener

`AudioListener` is a marker component that defines the "microphone" position and orientation in the world. There should be exactly one active audio listener per world. The listener's transform is used to calculate relative positions for all spatialized audio sources.

The listener is typically attached to the camera entity:

```cpp
cameraEntity.EmplaceComponent<AudioListener>();
```

The audio snapshot captures the listener's world position and rotation each frame for use in spatialization calculations.

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/AudioSource.hpp:114](), [include/RavEngine/AudioSnapshot.hpp:73-74]()

## Audio Spaces

Audio spaces define regions in the world where specific acoustic processing is applied to audio sources. RavEngine provides three types of audio spaces with increasing complexity and computational cost.

### Audio Space Comparison

| Space Type | Spatialization | Occlusion | Reverb | Library | Use Case |
|------------|---------------|-----------|--------|---------|----------|
| `SimpleAudioSpace` | HRTF binaural | No | No | Steam Audio | Outdoor environments, basic 3D audio |
| `GeometryAudioSpace` | HRTF binaural | Mesh-based | Convolution | Steam Audio | Indoor environments with geometry |
| `BoxReverbationAudioSpace` | Binaural + distance | No | Parametric room | Resonance Audio | Simple reverberant rooms |

### SimpleAudioSpace

`SimpleAudioSpace` provides basic HRTF-based spatialization using Steam Audio's binaural effect. It's the least computationally expensive option and suitable for outdoor or open environments.

```mermaid
graph TB
    Space["SimpleAudioSpace<br/>ComponentWithOwner"]
    RoomData["SimpleAudioSpace::RoomData<br/>sourceRadius<br/>steamAudioData<br/>workingBuffers<br/>accumulationBuffer"]
    
    Process["Per-Source Processing"]
    
    CheckRadius["Is source within<br/>sourceRadius?"]
    GetEffect["Get or create<br/>IPLBinauralEffect<br/>IPLDirectEffect<br/>for source entity"]
    Transform["Transform source position<br/>to listener space"]
    ApplyHRTF["Apply HRTF spatialization<br/>iplBinauralEffectApply()"]
    ApplyAttenuation["Apply distance attenuation<br/>iplDirectEffectApply()"]
    Accumulate["Accumulate to room buffer"]
    
    Space --> RoomData
    RoomData --> Process
    Process --> CheckRadius
    CheckRadius -->|Yes| GetEffect
    CheckRadius -->|No| Skip["Skip source"]
    GetEffect --> Transform
    Transform --> ApplyHRTF
    ApplyHRTF --> ApplyAttenuation
    ApplyAttenuation --> Accumulate
    
    style RoomData fill:#f9f9f9
```

**Configuration:**
```cpp
auto space = entity.EmplaceComponent<SimpleAudioSpace>();
space.SetRadius(20.0f); // Sources within 20 units are processed
```

**Processing Details:**
Each audio source within range is processed independently:
1. Convert source position to listener-relative coordinates
2. Apply HRTF-based binaural spatialization with `IPLBinauralEffect`
3. Apply distance-based attenuation with `IPLDirectEffect`
4. Accumulate spatialized output into room's accumulation buffer

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/AudioSpace.hpp:38-109](), [src/AudioSpace.cpp:21-97](), [src/AudioPlayer.cpp:166-210]()

### GeometryAudioSpace

`GeometryAudioSpace` provides advanced acoustic simulation with geometry-aware occlusion, transmission, and optional reflection/pathing effects. It uses Steam Audio's full simulation engine with mesh-based acoustic analysis.

```mermaid
graph TB
    Space["GeometryAudioSpace<br/>ComponentWithOwner"]
    RoomData["GeometryAudioSpace::RoomData<br/>sourceRadius, meshRadius<br/>steamAudioSimulator<br/>rootScene<br/>steamAudioSourceData<br/>steamAudioMeshData"]
    
    Setup["Initialization"]
    CreateSim["Create IPLSimulator<br/>Direct + Pathing + Reflections"]
    CreateScene["Create IPLScene<br/>Root scene for meshes"]
    
    PerFrame["Per-Frame Processing"]
    ConsiderSources["ConsiderAudioSource()<br/>Add/remove/update<br/>IPLSource instances"]
    ConsiderMeshes["ConsiderMesh()<br/>Add/remove/update<br/>IPLInstancedMesh"]
    Calculate["CalculateRoom()<br/>Set listener transform<br/>Run simulation"]
    Render["RenderAudioSource()<br/>Apply effects per source"]
    
    Effects["Steam Audio Effects Chain"]
    BinauralFX["IPLBinauralEffect<br/>Spatialization"]
    DirectFX["IPLDirectEffect<br/>Occlusion/Transmission"]
    PathFX["IPLPathEffect<br/>Reflections (future)"]
    
    Space --> RoomData
    RoomData --> Setup
    Setup --> CreateSim
    Setup --> CreateScene
    
    RoomData --> PerFrame
    PerFrame --> ConsiderSources
    PerFrame --> ConsiderMeshes
    PerFrame --> Calculate
    Calculate --> Render
    
    Render --> Effects
    Effects --> BinauralFX
    Effects --> DirectFX
    Effects --> PathFX
    
    style RoomData fill:#f9f9f9
    style Effects fill:#f9f9f9
```

**Configuration:**
```cpp
auto space = entity.EmplaceComponent<GeometryAudioSpace>();
space.SetAudioSourceRadius(30.0f);  // Source inclusion radius
space.SetMeshRadius(50.0f);         // Mesh occluder inclusion radius
```

**Simulation Process:**

1. **Source Management** (`ConsiderAudioSource()`): Sources within `sourceRadius` are added to the Steam Audio simulator with `IPLSource` instances. Sources moving out of range are automatically removed.

2. **Mesh Management** (`ConsiderMesh()`): Static mesh components marked as audio occluders within `meshRadius` are added as `IPLInstancedMesh` instances for acoustic geometry.

3. **Simulation** (`CalculateRoom()`): 
   - Set listener position and orientation in room space
   - Commit all queued source/mesh changes with `iplSimulatorCommit()`
   - Run direct sound simulation with `iplSimulatorRunDirect()`
   - Optionally run pathing and reflection simulation (requires probe setup)

4. **Rendering** (`RenderAudioSource()`):
   - Retrieve simulation outputs for each source
   - Apply binaural spatialization
   - Apply direct effects (occlusion/transmission)
   - Apply path effects (reflection/reverb, when configured)

**Coordinate Space Transforms:**
All positions are transformed from world space to room-local space using `invRoomTransform` for simulation, then transformed relative to the listener for final spatialization.

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/AudioSpace.hpp:111-226](), [src/AudioSpace.cpp:133-434](), [src/AudioPlayer.cpp:105-163]()

### BoxReverbationAudioSpace

`BoxReverbationAudioSpace` simulates a rectangular room with parametric reverberation using Resonance Audio. It's efficient for simple reverberant spaces without complex geometry.

```mermaid
graph TB
    Space["BoxReverbationAudioSpace<br/>ComponentWithOwner"]
    RoomData["BoxReverbationAudioSpace::RoomData<br/>audioEngine: ResonanceAudioApi<br/>sourceMap<br/>wallMaterials[6]<br/>workingBuffers"]
    Props["RoomProperties<br/>reflection_scalar<br/>reverb_gain<br/>reverb_time<br/>reverb_brightness"]
    
    Config["Configuration"]
    HalfExts["Set room half-extents<br/>SetHalfExts(vector3)"]
    WallMats["Set wall materials<br/>SetWallMaterial(idx, material)"]
    RoomProps["Set room properties<br/>reflection_scalar, etc."]
    
    Process["Per-Frame Processing"]
    CheckAABB["AABB check:<br/>Is listener in room?"]
    ConsiderSources["ConsiderAudioSource()<br/>Add/update/remove sources"]
    UpdateResonance["Update Resonance API<br/>listener transform<br/>room properties if changed"]
    FillOutput["FillPlanarOutputBuffer()<br/>Get spatialized + reverb output"]
    
    Space --> RoomData
    Space --> Props
    RoomData --> Config
    Config --> HalfExts
    Config --> WallMats
    Config --> RoomProps
    
    RoomData --> Process
    Process --> CheckAABB
    CheckAABB -->|Yes| ConsiderSources
    CheckAABB -->|No| Skip["Skip room"]
    ConsiderSources --> UpdateResonance
    UpdateResonance --> FillOutput
    
    style RoomData fill:#f9f9f9
```

**Configuration:**
```cpp
auto space = entity.EmplaceComponent<BoxReverbationAudioSpace>();
space.SetHalfExts(vector3(10, 3, 10)); // 20x6x20 room

// Set wall materials (6 faces: -X, +X, -Y, +Y, -Z, +Z)
space.SetWallMaterial(0, RoomMat::kConcrete);
space.SetWallMaterial(1, RoomMat::kConcrete);
space.SetWallMaterial(2, RoomMat::kWood);
// ... etc

// Set room properties
auto& props = space.GetRoomProperties();
props.reverb_time = 2.0f;
props.reverb_gain = 0.8f;
```

**Room Properties:**
- `reflection_scalar` - Scales early reflection level
- `reverb_gain` - Overall reverb level
- `reverb_time` - Reverberation decay time (seconds)
- `reverb_brightness` - High-frequency damping

**Wall Materials:**
Resonance Audio provides predefined acoustic materials (e.g., `kConcrete`, `kWood`, `kGlass`) with different absorption characteristics. Each of the 6 box faces can have a different material.

**Processing Details:**
1. Check if listener is inside the axis-aligned bounding box
2. For each source, check if inside room
3. Transform source/listener to room space
4. Calculate room effects gain based on position
5. Update Resonance Audio source properties
6. Process all sources and generate reverberant output

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/AudioSpace.hpp:228-312](), [src/AudioSpaceBoxReverbation.cpp:1-117](), [src/AudioPlayer.cpp:213-243]()

## Audio Effect Graphs

RavEngine supports custom audio processing chains through the `AudioGraphAsset` system. Effect graphs can be applied to individual audio sources or to entire audio spaces.

### AudioGraphAsset Structure

```mermaid
graph LR
    Graph["AudioGraphAsset<br/>nchannels"]
    Filters["LinkedList&lt;AudioFilterLayer&gt;<br/>Effect chain"]
    Layer1["AudioFilterLayer 1<br/>process(in, out)"]
    Layer2["AudioFilterLayer 2<br/>process(in, out)"]
    Layer3["AudioFilterLayer 3<br/>process(in, out)"]
    
    Input["Input Buffer<br/>Planar samples"]
    Scratch["Scratch Buffer<br/>Intermediate storage"]
    Output["Output Buffer<br/>Processed samples"]
    
    Graph --> Filters
    Filters --> Layer1
    Layer1 --> Layer2
    Layer2 --> Layer3
    
    Input --> Layer1
    Layer1 -.->|swap| Scratch
    Scratch --> Layer2
    Layer2 -.->|swap| Input
    Input --> Layer3
    Layer3 -.->|swap| Output
    
    style Graph fill:#f9f9f9
```

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/AudioGraphAsset.hpp:35-59](), [src/AudioGraphAsset.cpp:12-23]()

### Creating Custom Effect Layers

Derive from `AudioFilterLayer` to create custom effects:

```cpp
struct AudioFilterLayer {
    virtual void process(
        const PlanarSampleBufferInlineView& in,
        PlanarSampleBufferInlineView& out
    ) = 0;
};
```

**Example - Gain Effect:**
```cpp
struct AudioGainFilterLayer : public AudioFilterLayer {
    float gain = 1;
    
    void process(
        const PlanarSampleBufferInlineView& in, 
        PlanarSampleBufferInlineView& out
    ) final {
        for (int c = 0; c < in.GetNChannels(); c++) {
            auto channel = in[c];
            for (int i = 0; i < channel.size(); i++) {
                out[c][i] = channel[i] * gain;
            }
        }
    }
};
```

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/AudioGraphAsset.hpp:10-30]()

### Applying Effect Graphs

Effect graphs can be applied to any `AudioGraphComposed` object:

```cpp
// Create graph with appropriate channel count
auto graph = New<AudioGraphAsset>(1); // mono for point sources
graph->filters.emplace_back(std::make_shared<AudioGainFilterLayer>(0.5f));
graph->filters.emplace_back(std::make_shared<MyCustomFilter>());

// Apply to audio provider
audioProvider->SetGraph(graph);

// Or apply to an audio space (affects all sources in space)
audioSpace->GetData()->SetGraph(graph);
```

**Channel Count Considerations:**
- Point source effects: Use 1 channel (mono before spatialization)
- Ambient source effects: Use output channel count (2 for stereo)
- Audio space effects: Use output channel count (2 for stereo)

**Processing Order:**
Effects are processed in insertion order. Each effect reads from one buffer and writes to another, with buffers swapped between stages for cache efficiency.

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/AudioTypes.hpp:114-137](), [src/AudioGraphAsset.cpp:1-30]()

## Audio Buffer Types

RavEngine uses specialized buffer types optimized for parallel audio processing:

### PlanarSampleBufferInlineView

Represents audio samples in planar format where all samples for channel 0 are contiguous, followed by all samples for channel 1, etc. This format is SIMD-friendly and matches Steam Audio's internal representation.

```mermaid
graph LR
    Interleaved["Interleaved Layout<br/>L R L R L R ..."]
    Planar["Planar Layout<br/>L L L ... R R R ..."]
    
    Convert["ImportInterleavedData()"]
    
    View["PlanarSampleBufferInlineView<br/>combined_buffers: span&lt;float&gt;<br/>sizeOfOneChannelInFrames"]
    
    Access["operator[channel]<br/>returns span for channel"]
    
    Interleaved --> Convert
    Convert --> Planar
    Planar --> View
    View --> Access
    
    style View fill:#f9f9f9
```

**Key Methods:**
- `operator[channel]` - Returns `std::span<float>` for a specific channel
- `GetNChannels()` - Returns number of channels
- `GetNumSamples()` - Returns samples per channel
- `sizeOneChannel()` - Returns size of one channel in frames
- `ImportInterleavedData()` - Converts interleaved data to planar format

**Usage:**
```cpp
PlanarSampleBufferInlineView buffer(data, totalSamples, samplesPerChannel);

// Access individual channels
auto leftChannel = buffer[0];
auto rightChannel = buffer[1];

// Process with SIMD
for (size_t i = 0; i < buffer.sizeOneChannel(); i++) {
    leftChannel[i] *= volume;
    rightChannel[i] *= volume;
}
```

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/AudioTypes.hpp:20-95]()

### SingleAudioRenderBuffer

Wraps `PlanarSampleBufferInlineView` with owned storage for audio processing:

```cpp
struct SingleAudioRenderBuffer {
    std::vector<float> dataBuffer;
    std::vector<float> scratchBuffer; // for effects processing
    
    PlanarSampleBufferInlineView GetWritableDataBufferView();
    PlanarSampleBufferInlineView GetWritableScratchBufferView();
    PlanarSampleBufferInlineView GetReadonlyDataBufferView() const;
};
```

Used by `AudioDataProvider` instances and audio spaces to store intermediate processing results.

**Sources:** Referenced in [include/RavEngine/AudioSource.hpp:66]()

## Audio Threading Architecture

The audio system uses a sophisticated multi-threaded architecture to minimize latency and maximize parallelism while avoiding lock contention.

### Thread Model

```mermaid
graph TB
    subgraph "Main Thread"
        WorldTick["World::Tick()"]
        CreateSnap["CreateAudioSnapshot()<br/>Collect sources, spaces, listener"]
        SwapCheck["App::SwapRenderAudioSnapshotIfNeeded()<br/>Check if audio consumed previous"]
        AtomicSwap["Atomic pointer swap<br/>Lock-free exchange"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Audio Thread - Detached"
        AudioLoop["Infinite loop<br/>while audioThreadShouldRun"]
        CheckQueue["SDL_GetAudioStreamQueued()<br/>Backpressure check"]
        GetSnap["GetRenderAudioSnapshot()<br/>Read atomically swapped pointer"]
        Dispatch["audioExecutor.run(audioTaskflow).wait()"]
        PushSDL["SDL_PutAudioStreamData()<br/>Push to device"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Taskflow Workers - 2 Threads"
        Preamble["Preamble Task<br/>Update iterators<br/>Extract listener transform"]
        DataProviders["for_each DataProviders<br/>Fill audio buffers"]
        Ambients["for_each Ambient Sources<br/>Fill audio buffers"]
        SimpleSpaces["for_each Simple Spaces<br/>Spatialize sources"]
        GeomSpaces["for_each Geometry Spaces<br/>Simulate + spatialize"]
        BoxSpaces["for_each Box Spaces<br/>Reverb processing"]
        FinalMix["Final Mix Task<br/>Accumulate + interleave<br/>Clamp to [-1, 1]"]
    end
    
    WorldTick --> CreateSnap
    CreateSnap --> SwapCheck
    SwapCheck --> AtomicSwap
    
    AtomicSwap -.->|Lock-free read| AudioLoop
    AudioLoop --> CheckQueue
    CheckQueue -->|Queue low| GetSnap
    GetSnap --> Dispatch
    
    Dispatch --> Preamble
    Preamble --> DataProviders
    Preamble --> Ambients
    DataProviders --> SimpleSpaces
    DataProviders --> GeomSpaces
    DataProviders --> BoxSpaces
    Ambients --> FinalMix
    SimpleSpaces --> FinalMix
    GeomSpaces --> FinalMix
    BoxSpaces --> FinalMix
    FinalMix --> PushSDL
    
    PushSDL --> AudioLoop
    
    style AtomicSwap fill:#f9f9f9
    style Dispatch fill:#f9f9f9
    style FinalMix fill:#f9f9f9
```

**Sources:** [src/AudioPlayer.cpp:86-103](), [src/AudioPlayer.cpp:391-424](), [src/AudioPlayer.cpp:487-492]()

### Snapshot-Based Rendering

The snapshot system eliminates lock contention by creating immutable copies of audio world state:

1. **Main Thread (World::Tick):**
   - Creates `AudioSnapshot` with current positions, rotations, and references
   - Stores references to `AudioDataProvider`, `AudioSpace::RoomData`, etc.
   - Snapshot contains no raw pointers to game objects

2. **Swap Point:**
   - `App::SwapRenderAudioSnapshotIfNeeded()` checks if audio thread consumed previous snapshot
   - Performs lock-free atomic pointer swap
   - Old snapshot remains accessible to audio thread until next swap

3. **Audio Thread:**
   - Reads snapshot pointer atomically
   - Processes snapshot completely before next iteration
   - Never blocks main thread

**Snapshot Contents:**
```cpp
struct AudioSnapshot {
    UnorderedVector<PointSource> sources;
    UnorderedSet<Ref<AudioDataProvider>> dataProviders;
    UnorderedVector<Ref<AudioDataProvider>> ambientSources;
    
    Vector<SimpleAudioSpaceData> simpleAudioSpaces;
    Vector<GeometryAudioSpaceData> geometryAudioSpaces;
    Vector<BoxReverbationSpaceData> boxAudioSpaces;
    
    Vector<AudioMeshData> audioMeshes;
    
    vector3 listenerPos;
    quaternion listenerRot;
    WeakRef<World> sourceWorld;
};
```

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/AudioSnapshot.hpp:11-88]()

### Taskflow Parallelization

The audio processing pipeline is parallelized using Taskflow with 2 worker threads:

```mermaid
graph TD
    Start["Preamble<br/>PerformAudioTickPreamble()"]
    
    ProviderLoop["for_each dataProviders<br/>doDataProvider lambda"]
    AmbientLoop["for_each ambientSources<br/>doDataProvider lambda"]
    
    SimpleLoop["for_each simpleAudioSpaces<br/>CalculateSimpleAudioSpace()"]
    GeomLoop["for_each geometryAudioSpaces<br/>CalculateGeometryAudioSpace()"]
    BoxLoop["for_each boxAudioSpaces<br/>CalculateBoxAudioSpace()"]
    
    Final["Final Mix<br/>CalculateFinalMix()"]
    
    Start --> ProviderLoop
    Start --> AmbientLoop
    
    ProviderLoop --> SimpleLoop
    ProviderLoop --> GeomLoop
    ProviderLoop --> BoxLoop
    
    AmbientLoop --> Final
    SimpleLoop --> Final
    GeomLoop --> Final
    BoxLoop --> Final
    
    style Start fill:#f9f9f9
    style Final fill:#f9f9f9
```

**Task Dependencies:**
1. **Preamble** executes first, updating iterators and listener transform
2. **Data Provider** and **Ambient** tasks run in parallel after preamble
3. **Audio Space** tasks run in parallel after data providers finish (because they need filled source buffers)
4. **Final Mix** waits for all audio spaces and ambients to complete

**Sources:** [src/AudioPlayer.cpp:391-424]()

### Audio Thread Safety

**Lock-Free Structures:**
- Snapshot swap uses atomic pointer exchange
- `SDL_AudioStream` is internally thread-safe

**Locked Structures:**
- `locked_hashmap` for Steam Audio effect caches (uses `SpinLock`)
- World destruction queues use `moodycamel::ConcurrentQueue`

**Destroyed Entity Handling:**
When entities with audio components are destroyed on the main thread, their IDs are queued in `World::destroyedAudioSources`. The audio thread dequeues these IDs during the preamble and removes associated effect data from audio spaces.

**Sources:** [src/AudioPlayer.cpp:348-389](), [include/RavEngine/AudioSpace.hpp:79]()

## Audio Processing Pipeline

The complete audio processing pipeline from source to output:

### Pipeline Flow

```mermaid
graph TB
    subgraph "1. Data Provider Processing"
        DataProviders["For each AudioDataProvider"]
        FillBuffer["ProvideBufferData()<br/>Fill renderData.dataBuffer<br/>Apply volume, looping"]
        ApplyGraph1["Apply effect graph<br/>if present"]
    end
    
    subgraph "2. Ambient Processing"
        Ambients["For each AmbientAudioSource"]
        FillAmb["ProvideBufferData()<br/>Fill renderData.dataBuffer"]
        ApplyGraph2["Apply effect graph<br/>if present"]
    end
    
    subgraph "3. Audio Space Processing - Parallel"
        Simple["SimpleAudioSpace<br/>HRTF spatialization<br/>Distance attenuation"]
        Geometry["GeometryAudioSpace<br/>Occlusion/Transmission<br/>HRTF spatialization"]
        Box["BoxReverbationAudioSpace<br/>Parametric reverb<br/>Binaural spatialization"]
        
        SimpleAccum["Accumulate to space buffer"]
        GeomAccum["Accumulate to space buffer"]
        BoxOutput["Direct output from Resonance"]
        
        Simple --> SimpleAccum
        Geometry --> GeomAccum
        Box --> BoxOutput
    end
    
    subgraph "4. Final Mix"
        Zero["Zero output buffer<br/>interleavedOutputBuffer"]
        AddAmbient["Additive blend ambients"]
        AddSimple["Additive blend Simple spaces"]
        AddGeom["Additive blend Geometry spaces"]
        AddBox["Additive blend Box spaces"]
        Convert["Planar to interleaved conversion"]
        Clamp["Clamp samples to [-1, 1]"]
    end
    
    subgraph "5. Output"
        SDL["SDL_PutAudioStreamData()<br/>Push to audio device"]
    end
    
    DataProviders --> FillBuffer
    FillBuffer --> ApplyGraph1
    
    Ambients --> FillAmb
    FillAmb --> ApplyGraph2
    
    ApplyGraph1 --> Simple
    ApplyGraph1 --> Geometry
    ApplyGraph1 --> Box
    
    SimpleAccum --> Zero
    GeomAccum --> Zero
    BoxOutput --> Zero
    ApplyGraph2 --> Zero
    
    Zero --> AddAmbient
    AddAmbient --> AddSimple
    AddSimple --> AddGeom
    AddGeom --> AddBox
    AddBox --> Convert
    Convert --> Clamp
    Clamp --> SDL
    
    style Zero fill:#f9f9f9
    style Clamp fill:#f9f9f9
```

**Sources:** [src/AudioPlayer.cpp:245-320](), [src/AudioPlayer.cpp:322-346]()

### Per-Frame Processing Steps

1. **Check Audio Queue** (`SDL_GetAudioStreamQueued`): Verify device queue has space
2. **Swap Snapshot**: Get latest world state from main thread
3. **Preamble**: Extract listener transform, update iterators
4. **Fill Data Provider Buffers**: Each source fills its buffer with mono audio
5. **Fill Ambient Buffers**: Ambient sources fill stereo buffers
6. **Process Audio Spaces**: Spatialize point sources based on listener position
7. **Final Mix**: 
   - Zero output buffer
   - Additively blend all audio space outputs
   - Additively blend ambient sources
   - Convert planar to interleaved format
   - Clamp samples to prevent overflow
8. **Push to SDL**: Submit interleaved buffer to audio device

**Sources:** [src/AudioPlayer.cpp:86-103](), [src/AudioPlayer.cpp:322-346]()

### Additive Blending

All audio sources and spaces are mixed using additive blending:

```cpp
inline void AdditiveBlendSamples(
    PlanarSampleBufferInlineView& A,
    const PlanarSampleBufferInlineView& B
) {
    for (uint8_t c = 0; c < std::min(A.GetNChannels(), B.GetNChannels()); c++) {
        for (size_t i = 0; i < A.sizeOneChannel(); i++) {
            A[c][i] += B[c][i];
        }
    }
}
```

Final clamping prevents overflow:
```cpp
for (int i = 0; i < accumView.size(); i++) {
    accumView[i] = std::clamp(accumView[i], -1.0f, 1.0f);
}
```

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/AudioTypes.hpp:104-111](), [src/AudioPlayer.cpp:313-317]()

## Integration with World and ECS

### World Integration Points

The audio system integrates with the World/ECS through several mechanisms:

```mermaid
        QueryAmbients["Query all AmbientAudioSource"]
        QuerySpaces["Query all audio spaces<br/>Get world transforms"]

    end

    style BuildSnapshot fill:#f9f9f9

```

**Sources:** [src/AudioPlayer.cpp:348-389]()

### Snapshot Creation Process

During world tick, `CreateAudioSnapshot()` collects all audio-related components:

1. **Query Audio Sources**: Find all `AudioSourceComponent` instances, extract world positions and `AudioDataProvider` references
2. **Query Ambient Sources**: Find all `AmbientAudioSourceComponent` instances
3. **Query Audio Spaces**: Find all audio space components, extract world transforms and `RoomData` references
4. **Query Audio Listener**: Find the single `AudioListener` component, extract world transform
5. **Query Audio Mesh Occluders**: For geometry spaces, find mesh components marked as occluders
6. **Build Snapshot**: Populate `AudioSnapshot` structure with collected data

The snapshot uses `Ref<>` smart pointers to shared data (`AudioDataProvider`, `AudioSpace::RoomData`) ensuring data remains valid even if components are destroyed during audio processing.

**Sources:** Referenced through system integration, snapshot structure at [include/RavEngine/AudioSnapshot.hpp:11-88]()

### Component Lifecycle

**Creation:**
Components are emplaced on entities using standard ECS mechanisms:
```cpp
entity.EmplaceComponent<AudioSourceComponent>(audioProvider);
entity.EmplaceComponent<SimpleAudioSpace>();
```

**Destruction:**
When an entity with audio components is destroyed:
1. Component's destructor runs on main thread
2. Entity ID is enqueued in `World::destroyedAudioSources` (lock-free queue)
3. Audio thread dequeues IDs during preamble
4. Audio spaces remove cached effect data for destroyed entities

This deferred cleanup prevents race conditions between main and audio threads.

**Sources:** [src/AudioPlayer.cpp:348-389]()

## External Library Integration

RavEngine integrates three major audio libraries:

### Library Responsibilities

| Library | Purpose | Used By | Key Features |
|---------|---------|---------|--------------|
| **SDL3** | Audio device I/O | `AudioPlayer` | Cross-platform audio output, stream management |
| **Steam Audio** | Spatial audio | Simple/Geometry spaces | HRTF, occlusion, geometry-based propagation |
| **Resonance Audio** | Room acoustics | Box space | Parametric reverb, material-based absorption |

### Steam Audio Integration

Steam Audio provides HRTF-based binaural spatialization and geometry-aware acoustic simulation:

**Initialization** ([src/AudioPlayer.cpp:464-486]()):
```cpp
IPLContextSettings contextSettings{
    .version = STEAMAUDIO_VERSION,
};
iplContextCreate(&contextSettings, &steamAudioContext);

IPLHRTFSettings hrtfSettings{
    .type = IPL_HRTFTYPE_DEFAULT,
    .volume = 1.0
};
iplHRTFCreate(steamAudioContext, &audioSettings, &hrtfSettings, &steamAudioHRTF);
```

**Effect Types:**
- `IPLBinauralEffect` - HRTF-based spatialization
- `IPLDirectEffect` - Distance attenuation, occlusion, transmission
- `IPLPathEffect` - Reflections and reverb (requires probe setup)
- `IPLSource` - Audio source in simulation
- `IPLSimulator` - Acoustic simulation engine
- `IPLScene` - Geometry container for simulation
- `IPLInstancedMesh` - Mesh occluder

**Sources:** [src/AudioPlayer.cpp:464-513](), [src/AudioSpace.cpp:21-97](), [src/AudioSpace.cpp:133-434]()

### Resonance Audio Integration

Resonance Audio provides efficient parametric room reverberation:

**Initialization** ([src/AudioSpaceBoxReverbation.cpp:14]()):
```cpp
audioEngine = vraudio::CreateResonanceAudioApi(
    AudioPlayer::GetNChannels(),
    AudioPlayer::GetBufferSize(),
    AudioPlayer::GetSamplesPerSec()
);
```

**Room Configuration:**
- Set room dimensions
- Assign materials to 6 room faces
- Configure reverb parameters (time, gain, brightness)
- Resonance computes reflection/reverb properties automatically

**Source Management:**
- Create sources with `CreateSoundObjectSource()`
- Set position, rotation, volume per source
- Compute room effects gain based on position
- `FillPlanarOutputBuffer()` generates spatialized + reverberant output

**Sources:** [src/AudioSpaceBoxReverbation.cpp:1-117]()

### SDL3 Audio Stream

SDL3 provides cross-platform audio device output:

**Stream Setup** ([src/AudioPlayer.cpp:433-444]()):
```cpp
SDL_AudioSpec want;
want.freq = 44100;
want.format = SDL_AUDIO_F32;
want.channels = 2;

stream = SDL_OpenAudioDeviceStream(
    SDL_AUDIO_DEVICE_DEFAULT_PLAYBACK,
    &want,
    NULL,
    this
);

SDL_ResumeAudioDevice(SDL_GetAudioStreamDevice(stream));
```

**Output Process:**
1. Check queue size: `SDL_GetAudioStreamQueued(stream)`
2. Process audio if queue is low
3. Push samples: `SDL_PutAudioStreamData(stream, buffer, size)`
4. SDL manages buffering and device synchronization

**Sources:** [src/AudioPlayer.cpp:428-462](), [src/AudioPlayer.cpp:89-100]()

## Configuration and Initialization

### AudioPlayer Initialization

The `AudioPlayer` is initialized during application startup:

```cpp
void AudioPlayer::Init() {
    // Initialize SDL audio subsystem
    SDL_InitSubSystem(SDL_INIT_AUDIO);
    
    // Open audio device stream
    SDL_AudioSpec want = {
        .freq = 44100,
        .format = SDL_AUDIO_F32,
        .channels = 2
    };
    stream = SDL_OpenAudioDeviceStream(
        SDL_AUDIO_DEVICE_DEFAULT_PLAYBACK,
        &want,
        NULL,
        this
    );
    
    // Initialize Steam Audio
    IPLContextSettings contextSettings{ .version = STEAMAUDIO_VERSION };
    iplContextCreate(&contextSettings, &steamAudioContext);
    
    IPLHRTFSettings hrtfSettings{
        .type = IPL_HRTFTYPE_DEFAULT,
        .volume = 1.0
    };
    iplHRTFCreate(steamAudioContext, &audioSettings, &hrtfSettings, &steamAudioHRTF);
    
    // Setup parallel processing graph
    SetupAudioTaskGraph();
    
    // Start audio device
    SDL_ResumeAudioDevice(SDL_GetAudioStreamDevice(stream));
    
    // Launch audio thread
    audioTickThread.emplace([this] {
        while (audioThreadShouldRun) {
            Tick();
        }
    });
    audioTickThread->detach();
}
```

**Sources:** [src/AudioPlayer.cpp:428-493]()

### Static Configuration

Audio system parameters are configured via static constants:

```cpp
static constexpr uint16_t config_buffersize = 512;
static constexpr uint16_t config_samplesPerSec = 44'100;
static constexpr uint32_t config_nchannels = 2;
```

These values determine:
- **Buffer size**: 512 samples per channel (â‰ˆ11.6ms latency at 44.1kHz)
- **Sample rate**: 44,100 Hz
- **Channels**: 2 (stereo output)

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/AudioPlayer.hpp:42-44]()

### Audio Space Initialization

Each audio space type initializes its required libraries during construction:

- **SimpleAudioSpace**: Allocates working buffers
- **GeometryAudioSpace**: Creates IPLSimulator and IPLScene
- **BoxReverbationAudioSpace**: Creates ResonanceAudioApi instance

Audio spaces are automatically registered when attached to entities and included in snapshots during world tick.

**Sources:** [src/AudioSpace.cpp:107-164](), [src/AudioSpaceBoxReverbation.cpp:9-18]()

## Performance Considerations

### Computational Costs

Audio processing cost scales with:

| Factor | Impact | Mitigation |
|--------|--------|------------|
| Number of active sources | Linear | Use radius culling in audio spaces |
| Audio space complexity | High (GeometryAudioSpace) | Use SimpleAudioSpace for outdoor scenes |
| Geometry mesh complexity | High (GeometryAudioSpace) | Use simplified collision meshes |
| Effect graph length | Linear per source | Keep effect chains short |
| Buffer size | Lower = more overhead | 512 samples balances latency/CPU |

### Optimization Strategies

1. **Radius Culling**: Audio spaces only process sources within `sourceRadius`
2. **Lazy Effect Creation**: Steam Audio effects created on-demand per source
3. **SIMD Operations**: Buffer processing uses `#pragma omp simd` for vectorization
4. **Parallel Processing**: Taskflow parallelizes space processing across 2 threads
5. **Lock-Free Snapshot**: Eliminates synchronization overhead between threads
6. **Efficient Buffer Format**: Planar layout enables efficient SIMD processing

**Sources:** [src/AudioPlayer.cpp:391-424](), [src/AudioSpace.cpp:21-434]()

### Memory Management

- Audio buffers allocated per-frame: `buffer_size * nchannels * sizeof(float)` = 4KB
- Steam Audio effect caches: ~10KB per active source
- Resonance Audio sources: ~5KB per source
- Geometry space scene: Scales with mesh complexity

Total memory usage is typically <10MB for moderate scenes with 10-20 active sources.

**Sources:** Memory allocations throughout [src/AudioPlayer.cpp](), [src/AudioSpace.cpp]()32:T4527,# Audio Sources and Playback

## Purpose and Scope

This document covers the loading, storage, and playback of audio in RavEngine. It explains the `AudioAsset` class for audio data storage, the `AudioDataProvider` interface for playback control, and the various audio source components (`AudioSourceComponent`, `AmbientAudioSourceComponent`) that emit audio in the world.

For information about spatial audio processing and audio spaces, see [Spatial Audio and Audio Spaces](#7.2). For details on the audio threading model and rendering architecture, see [Audio System Architecture](#7.3).

---

## AudioAsset

`AudioAsset` loads and stores decoded audio data in a planar float format suitable for real-time playback. Audio is decoded at load time into normalized [-1, 1] float samples.

### Audio Loading Pipeline

```mermaid
graph LR
    SourceFile["Source File<br/>.ogg .wav<br/>VirtualFilesystem"]
    
    Libnyquist["libnyquist<br/>nqr::NyquistIO<br/>Decode audio"]
    
    ResampleCheck{{"Sample rate<br/>match?"}}
    
    Resampler["r8b::CDSPResampler<br/>Resample to 44.1kHz"]
    
    ChannelCheck{{"Channel count<br/>match?"}}
    
    ChannelConvert["Convert channels<br/>MonoToStereo()<br/>StereoToMono()"]
    
    PlanarConvert["Convert to planar<br/>ImportInterleavedData()"]
    
    AudioAssetData["AudioAsset::data<br/>PlanarSampleBufferInlineView"]
    
    SourceFile --> Libnyquist
    Libnyquist --> ResampleCheck
    
    ResampleCheck -->|"No"| Resampler
    ResampleCheck -->|"Yes"| ChannelCheck
    Resampler --> ChannelCheck
    
    ChannelCheck -->|"No"| ChannelConvert
    ChannelCheck -->|"Yes"| PlanarConvert
    ChannelConvert --> PlanarConvert
    
    PlanarConvert --> AudioAssetData
```

**Sources:** [src/AudioSource.cpp:40-115](), [include/RavEngine/AudioSource.hpp:14-57]()

### Constructor and Data Format

The `AudioAsset` constructor performs the following operations:

1. **File Loading**: Reads audio data from the virtual filesystem at `/sounds/{name}` [src/AudioSource.cpp:42-43]()
2. **Decoding**: Uses `nqr::NyquistIO` to decode various formats (OGG, WAV) [src/AudioSource.cpp:47-50]()
3. **Resampling**: If the sample rate doesn't match `AudioPlayer::GetSamplesPerSec()` (44,100 Hz), resamples using `r8b::CDSPResampler` [src/AudioSource.cpp:52-79]()
4. **Channel Conversion**: Converts between mono and stereo as needed [src/AudioSource.cpp:83-104]()
5. **Planar Conversion**: Converts interleaved samples to planar format using `PlanarSampleBufferInlineView::ImportInterleavedData()` [src/AudioSource.cpp:112-114]()

The final data is stored in planar format where each channel is stored contiguously (LLLLL...RRRRR...) rather than interleaved (LRLRLR...).

| Property | Description | Type |
|----------|-------------|------|
| `audiodata` | Raw float array containing audio samples | `const float*` |
| `data` | Planar view of audio data | `PlanarSampleBufferInlineView` |
| `lengthSeconds` | Duration of audio in seconds | `double` |
| `nchannels` | Number of audio channels (1=mono, 2=stereo) | `uint8_t` |

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/AudioSource.hpp:14-57](), [src/AudioSource.cpp:40-120]()

---

## Audio Data Providers

### AudioDataProvider Interface

`AudioDataProvider` is the abstract interface for all audio playback mechanisms. It defines the contract for providing audio samples to the audio system.

| Method | Description |
|--------|-------------|
| `ProvideBufferData(out_buffer, scratchBuffer)` | Fill output buffer with audio samples (pure virtual) |
| `Play()` | Start playback by setting `isPlaying = true` |
| `Pause()` | Stop playback by setting `isPlaying = false` |
| `Restart()` | Reset playhead position (pure virtual) |
| `SetVolume(vol)` | Set volume multiplier |
| `SetLoop(loop)` | Enable/disable looping |
| `IsPlaying()` | Query current playback state |

Each `AudioDataProvider` owns a `SingleAudioRenderBuffer renderData` which stores the rendered audio for consumption by the audio system [include/RavEngine/AudioSource.hpp:66]().

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/AudioSource.hpp:61-107]()

### SampledAudioDataProvider

`SampledAudioDataProvider` is the concrete implementation that plays `AudioAsset` instances with support for looping, volume control, and pause/resume.

#### Playback State Machine

```mermaid
stateDiagram-v2
    [*] --> Stopped
    
    Stopped --> Playing : Play()
    
    Playing --> Paused : Pause()
    Playing --> Stopped : End of audio<br/>(non-looping)
    Playing --> Playing : Loop<br/>(looping)
    
    Paused --> Playing : Play()<br/>(resume from pause point)
    Paused --> Stopped : Restart()
    
    Stopped --> Playing : Play()<br/>(starts from beginning)
```

**Sources:** [src/AudioSource.cpp:124-141]()

#### Playback Implementation

The `ProvideBufferData()` method implements the core playback logic [src/AudioSource.cpp:143-180]():

1. **Calculate Playhead**: Determines sample position based on `globalAudioTime - lastPlayTime` [src/AudioSource.cpp:149-156]()
2. **Handle Looping**: If looping is enabled, wraps playhead using modulo operation [src/AudioSource.cpp:151-152]()
3. **Copy Samples**: Copies samples from `AudioAsset` to output buffer, applying volume [src/AudioSource.cpp:158-178]()
4. **End Detection**: For non-looping sources, fills with zeros after audio ends and sets `isPlaying = false` [src/AudioSource.cpp:160-171]()
5. **Effect Processing**: Applies effect graph via `AudioGraphComposed::Render()` [src/AudioSource.cpp:179]()

The playhead calculation accounts for pause/resume by storing the pause timestamp in `lastPlayTime` [src/AudioSource.cpp:135-140]().

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/AudioSource.hpp:119-149](), [src/AudioSource.cpp:21-180]()

---

## Audio Source Components

### AudioSourceComponent

`AudioSourceComponent` attaches an audio source to an entity for positional 3D audio. The component's world position is used for spatialization by audio spaces (see [Spatial Audio and Audio Spaces](#7.2)).

```cpp
// Example usage (pseudocode)
auto entity = world->Instantiate<Entity>();
auto asset = RavEngine::New<AudioAsset>("explosion.ogg", 1); // mono for 3D audio
auto provider = RavEngine::New<SampledAudioDataProvider>(asset, 1);
auto sourceComponent = entity.EmplaceComponent<AudioSourceComponent>(provider);
provider->SetVolume(0.8f);
provider->Play();
```

| Property | Description |
|----------|-------------|
| Inherits from | `AudioSourceBase`, `ComponentWithOwner`, `Queryable<AudioSourceComponent>` |
| Constructor | `AudioSourceComponent(Entity owner, Ref<AudioDataProvider> provider)` |
| 3D Processing | **Yes** - position used for spatialization |
| Affected by Audio Spaces | **Yes** - processed by SimpleAudioSpace, GeometryAudioSpace, BoxReverbationAudioSpace |

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/AudioSource.hpp:178-180](), [src/AudioSource.cpp:23-24]()

### AmbientAudioSourceComponent

`AmbientAudioSourceComponent` plays non-positional audio that is omnipresent in the scene. It is **not** affected by audio spaces or 3D spatialization.

```cpp
// Example usage (pseudocode)
auto asset = RavEngine::New<AudioAsset>("background_music.ogg", 2); // stereo for ambient
auto provider = RavEngine::New<SampledAudioDataProvider>(asset, 2);
auto ambientSource = world->EmplaceComponent<AmbientAudioSourceComponent>(provider);
provider->SetLoop(true);
provider->Play();
```

| Property | Description |
|----------|-------------|
| Inherits from | `AudioSourceBase`, `Queryable<AmbientAudioSourceComponent>`, `AutoCTTI` |
| Constructor | `AmbientAudioSourceComponent(Ref<AudioDataProvider> provider)` |
| 3D Processing | **No** - played at full volume regardless of listener position |
| Affected by Audio Spaces | **No** - bypasses all spatial processing |
| Typical Use Cases | Background music, UI sounds, narrator voice |

**Note:** Ambient sources should use audio assets with channel count matching `AudioPlayer::GetNChannels()` (typically 2 for stereo output) [src/AudioSource.cpp:34-35]().

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/AudioSource.hpp:185-187](), [src/AudioSource.cpp:26]()

### Comparison Table

| Feature | AudioSourceComponent | AmbientAudioSourceComponent |
|---------|---------------------|----------------------------|
| Attached to Entity | Yes (ComponentWithOwner) | No (world-level component) |
| World Position | Used for 3D audio | Ignored |
| Audio Space Processing | Yes | No |
| Recommended Channels | Mono (1) | Stereo (2) |
| Use Case | 3D sound effects, character voices | Music, UI sounds, ambient loops |

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/AudioSource.hpp:178-187]()

---

## Instantaneous Audio Sources

RavEngine provides "fire-and-forget" audio sources for one-shot sounds that don't require persistent component management.

### InstantaneousAudioSource

Plays a one-shot 3D audio effect at a specific world position. Automatically starts playing on creation and is managed internally by the world.

```cpp
// Example usage (pseudocode)
InstantaneousAudioSource source(audioAsset, vector3(10, 0, 5), 1.0f);
world->PlayInstantaneousAudioSource(source);
```

| Property | Value |
|----------|-------|
| Constructor | `InstantaneousAudioSource(Ref<AudioAsset>, vector3 position, float volume = 1)` |
| Spatial | Yes - position used for 3D audio |
| Audio Spaces | Yes - affected by rooms |
| Lifetime | Automatically destroyed when audio finishes |

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/AudioSource.hpp:192-196](), [src/AudioSource.cpp:28-31]()

### InstantaneousAmbientAudioSource

Plays a one-shot non-spatial audio effect.

```cpp
// Example usage (pseudocode)
InstantaneousAmbientAudioSource source(audioAsset, 0.5f);
world->PlayInstantaneousAmbientAudioSource(source);
```

| Property | Value |
|----------|-------|
| Constructor | `InstantaneousAmbientAudioSource(Ref<AudioAsset>, float volume = 1)` |
| Spatial | No - omnipresent playback |
| Audio Spaces | No - bypasses spatial processing |
| Lifetime | Automatically destroyed when audio finishes |

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/AudioSource.hpp:209-211](), [src/AudioSource.cpp:33-38]()

---

## Playback Control

### Volume Control

Volume is applied as a linear multiplier during sample playback [src/AudioSource.cpp:175]():

```cpp
provider->SetVolume(0.5f);  // 50% volume
provider->SetVolume(1.0f);  // 100% volume (default)
provider->SetVolume(2.0f);  // 200% volume (can amplify)
```

Volume is applied in `ProvideBufferData()` before spatial processing, so audio spaces receive volume-adjusted samples.

### Loop Control

Looping affects the playhead calculation in `ProvideBufferData()` [src/AudioSource.cpp:151-171]():

```cpp
provider->SetLoop(true);   // Continuous playback
provider->SetLoop(false);  // Stop after one play-through
```

When looping is disabled, the source automatically stops (`isPlaying = false`) when reaching the end of the audio data.

### Play/Pause/Restart

| Method | Behavior |
|--------|----------|
| `Play()` | If paused: resumes from pause point by adjusting `lastPlayTime` [src/AudioSource.cpp:124-128]()<br/>If stopped: starts from beginning |
| `Pause()` | Records current time in `lastPlayTime` for resume [src/AudioSource.cpp:135-140]() |
| `Restart()` | Resets `lastPlayTime` to current global time [src/AudioSource.cpp:131-133]() |

**Sources:** [src/AudioSource.cpp:124-141](), [include/RavEngine/AudioSource.hpp:74-85]()

---

## Audio Effect Graphs

Both `SampledAudioDataProvider` and audio spaces support `AudioGraphAsset` for real-time audio processing. Effect graphs can be attached via the `AudioGraphComposed` interface.

### Setting Effect Graphs

```cpp
auto provider = RavEngine::New<SampledAudioDataProvider>(asset, 1);
auto effectGraph = RavEngine::New<AudioGraphAsset>(1); // 1 channel for pre-spatialization

// Add effects (e.g., gain, filters)
effectGraph->filters.push_back(std::make_shared<AudioGainFilterLayer>(0.5f));

provider->SetGraph(effectGraph);
```

### Processing Pipeline

Effect graphs are applied at different stages:

1. **Pre-Spatialization** (on `SampledAudioDataProvider`): Affects raw audio before 3D processing [src/AudioSource.cpp:179]()
2. **Post-Spatialization** (on audio spaces): Affects spatialized output [src/AudioSpace.cpp:95]()

For detailed information on creating custom audio effects, see `AudioGraphAsset` and `AudioFilterLayer` [include/RavEngine/AudioGraphAsset.hpp:7-59]().

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/AudioTypes.hpp:114-137](), [include/RavEngine/AudioGraphAsset.hpp:1-61](), [src/AudioGraphAsset.cpp:1-30]()

## Audio Data Flow

The following diagram shows how audio flows from asset to final output:

```mermaid
graph TB
    Asset["AudioAsset<br/>Planar float data"]
    
    Provider["SampledAudioDataProvider<br/>ProvideBufferData()"]
    
    RenderBuffer["renderData<br/>SingleAudioRenderBuffer"]
    
    EffectGraph["AudioGraphAsset<br/>(optional)"]
    
    Snapshot["AudioSnapshot<br/>Double-buffered"]
    
    AudioSpace["Audio Spaces<br/>3D spatialization"]
    
    FinalMix["AudioPlayer::CalculateFinalMix()<br/>Accumulation"]
    
    SDL["SDL_PutAudioStreamData()"]
    
    Asset --> Provider
    Provider --> EffectGraph
    EffectGraph --> RenderBuffer
    Provider -.->|"no graph"| RenderBuffer
    
    RenderBuffer --> Snapshot
    Snapshot --> AudioSpace
    AudioSpace --> FinalMix
    
    RenderBuffer -.->|"Ambient sources<br/>bypass spaces"| FinalMix
    
    FinalMix --> SDL
```

**Sources:** [src/AudioPlayer.cpp:31-43](), [src/AudioPlayer.cpp:245-320](), [src/AudioSource.cpp:143-180]()

## Buffer Format and Data Types

RavEngine uses two buffer representations internally:

### PlanarSampleBufferInlineView

Organizes multi-channel audio with each channel stored contiguously (LLLL...RRRR...) for efficient SIMD processing.

| Method | Description |
|--------|-------------|
| `operator[](channel)` | Access individual channel data |
| `GetNChannels()` | Number of audio channels |
| `sizeOneChannel()` | Number of samples per channel |
| `ImportInterleavedData()` | Convert interleaved to planar |

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/AudioTypes.hpp:20-95]()

### InterleavedSampleBufferView

Standard interleaved format (LRLRLR...) used for final output to SDL.

| Method | Description |
|--------|-------------|
| `std::span<float>` | Direct array access |
| Used for | Final mix output, external library interfaces |

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/AudioTypes.hpp:13]()

The conversion between formats occurs in `AudioPlayer::CalculateFinalMix()` during the blend operation [src/AudioPlayer.cpp:300-308]().
