## Purpose and Scope

This page documents RavEngine's GPU-driven rendering techniques, which move traditional CPU-side rendering operations to compute shaders for improved performance and parallelism. These techniques enable the engine to efficiently render large numbers of objects by performing culling, skinning, and draw call preparation entirely on the GPU.

For information about the overall rendering pipeline and multi-pass execution, see [Rendering Architecture](#4.1). For details on render data synchronization between CPU and GPU, see [Render Data Synchronization](#9.3).

---

## Overview

RavEngine's GPU-driven architecture offloads the following operations to compute shaders:

| Operation | Compute Pipeline | Purpose |
|-----------|-----------------|---------|
| **Frustum & Occlusion Culling** | `defaultCullingComputePipeline` | Determine object visibility per-camera |
| **LOD Selection** | Integrated into culling pipeline | Select appropriate mesh detail level |
| **Skeletal Skinning** | `skinnedMeshComputePipeline` | Transform vertices by bone matrices |
| **Depth Pyramid** | `depthPyramidPipeline` | Generate hierarchical Z-buffer for occlusion |
| **Light Clustering** | `clusterBuildGridPipeline`, `clusterPopulatePipeline` | Assign lights to 3D grid tiles |
| **Particle Updates** | User-defined compute shaders | Simulate particle lifecycle |

The core principle is to use **Multi-Draw-Indirect (MDI)** commands, where the GPU writes draw parameters into buffers that are immediately consumed by rendering passes, eliminating CPU-GPU synchronization stalls.

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/RenderEngine.hpp:63-365](), [Diagram 3 from architecture overview]()

---

## Multi-Draw-Indirect (MDI) Architecture

### Command Structure

RavEngine organizes drawable objects using the `MDIICommand` and `MDIICommandSkinned` structures, which group entities by material and mesh to minimize state changes:

```mermaid
graph TB
    subgraph "World::RenderData"
        StaticData["staticMeshRenderData<br/>OrderedMap&lt;MaterialSort, MDIICommand&gt;"]
        SkinnedData["skinnedMeshRenderData<br/>OrderedMap&lt;MaterialSort, MDIICommandSkinned&gt;"]
    end
    
    subgraph "MDIICommand Structure"
        Commands["commands: unordered_vector&lt;command&gt;"]
        IndirectBuf["indirectBuffer: RGLBufferPtr"]
        CullingBuf["cullingBuffer: RGLBufferPtr"]
        
        Commands --> Command1["command[0]<br/>mesh: WeakRef&lt;MeshCollectionStatic&gt;<br/>entities: BufferedVRAMSparseSet"]
        Commands --> Command2["command[1]<br/>different mesh<br/>same material"]
    end
    
    subgraph "GPU Buffers"
        IndirectBuf --> GPU_Indirect["Indirect Draw Commands<br/>RGL::IndirectIndexedCommand"]
        CullingBuf --> GPU_IDs["Visible Entity IDs<br/>uint32_t[]"]
    end
    
    StaticData --> Commands
    SkinnedData --> Commands
    
    GPU_Indirect --> DrawCall["GPU: DrawIndexedIndirect"]
    GPU_IDs --> VertexShader["Vertex Shader:<br/>Fetch transform by entity ID"]
```

**Key Components:**

- **`MDIICommand`** [include/RavEngine/World.hpp:334-349](): Holds all static meshes sharing a material
- **`indirectBuffer`**: GPU-writable buffer of `RGL::IndirectIndexedCommand` structures
- **`cullingBuffer`**: GPU-writable buffer of visible entity IDs
- **`entities`**: `BufferedVRAMSparseSet` mapping entity IDs to array indices

The `MaterialSort` key [include/RavEngine/World.hpp:40-66]() ensures materials are rendered in priority order, with the material pointer in the low bits and priority in the high bits of a 128-bit key.

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/World.hpp:334-362](), [src/World.cpp:330-390]()

---

### Indirect Buffer Preparation

Before rendering, compute shaders populate the indirect buffers. For skinned meshes, the `skinningDrawCallPreparePipeline` initializes the indirect commands:

```mermaid
graph LR
    subgraph "CPU: RenderEngine_Draw.cpp:546-574"
        PrepareCall["prepareSkeletalCullingBuffer()"]
    end
    
    subgraph "GPU: skinned_mesh_drawcall_csh"
        ForEachMesh["For each mesh in material"]
        WriteIndirect["Write IndirectIndexedCommand<br/>indexCount = mesh indices<br/>instanceCount = 0<br/>baseInstance = object offset"]
    end
    
    PrepareCall --> ForEachMesh
    ForEachMesh --> WriteIndirect
    WriteIndirect --> IndirectBuf["indirectBuffer<br/>instanceCount starts at 0"]
    
    IndirectBuf --> CullingStage["Culling compute shader<br/>atomicAdd on instanceCount"]
```

The `SkinningPrepareUBO` structure [include/RavEngine/RenderEngine.hpp:232-240]() passes parameters:

- `indexBufferOffset`: Offset into shared index buffer
- `vertexBufferOffset`: Offset into shared vertex buffer  
- `nIndicesInThisMesh`: Number of indices to draw
- `nTotalObjects`: Number of entities with this mesh

After culling increments `instanceCount` via atomics, the indirect buffer is ready for consumption by `DrawIndexedIndirect`.

**Sources:** [src/RenderEngine_Draw.cpp:546-574](), [include/RavEngine/RenderEngine.hpp:232-240]()

---

## Compute-Based Culling

### Culling Pipeline Overview

The `defaultcull_csh` compute shader [shaders/defaultcull.csh:1-315]() performs frustum culling, occlusion culling, and LOD selection in a single pass:

```mermaid
graph TD
    Start["Dispatch: ceil(numObjects / 64) workgroups"]
    
    FindCUBO["Find CUBO instance for thread<br/>Linear search through cubo counts"]
    
    LayerCheck["Check render layers<br/>(cameraRenderLayers & entityLayerMask)"]
    
    AttributeCheck["Check per-object attributes<br/>frustumCullEnabled?<br/>occlusionCullEnabled?<br/>castsShadows?"]
    
    FrustumCull["Frustum Culling<br/>Transform bounding sphere<br/>CullSphere() against 6 planes"]
    
    OcclusionCull["Occlusion Culling<br/>projectWorldSpaceSphere()<br/>Sample depth pyramid<br/>Compare referenceZ >= minDepth"]
    
    LODSelect["LOD Selection<br/>Distance from camera<br/>Select best LOD by 'Price is Right' rules"]
    
    WriteOutput["atomicAdd(indirectBuffer[lodID].instanceCount, 1)<br/>Write entity ID to cullingBuffer"]
    
    Start --> FindCUBO
    FindCUBO --> LayerCheck
    LayerCheck -->|Fail| Bail1[Return]
    LayerCheck -->|Pass| AttributeCheck
    AttributeCheck --> FrustumCull
    FrustumCull -->|Culled| Bail2[Return]
    FrustumCull -->|Visible| OcclusionCull
    OcclusionCull -->|Occluded| Bail3[Return]
    OcclusionCull -->|Visible| LODSelect
    LODSelect --> WriteOutput
```

**Sources:** [shaders/defaultcull.csh:1-315]()

---

### CUBO Structure

The **CUBO** (Culling Uniform Buffer Object) structure [shaders/defaultcull.csh:7-17]() groups culling parameters for each mesh/material combination:

```cpp
struct CUBO {
    uint indirectBufferOffset;           // Start index in indirect buffer
    uint numObjects;                     // Number of entities with this mesh
    uint cullingBufferOffset;            // Start index in culling buffer
    float radius;                        // Bounding sphere radius (pre-transform)
    uint numLODs;                        // Number of LOD levels
    uint idOutputBufferBindlessHandle;   // Bindless handle to output ID buffer
    uint entityIDInputBufferBindlessHandle;  // Bindless handle to entity ID array
    uint indirectOutputBufferBindlessHandle; // Bindless handle to indirect commands
    uint lodDistanceBufferBindlessHandle;    // Bindless handle to LOD distances
};
```

The culling shader receives a `CullingUBO` [include/RavEngine/RenderEngine.hpp:224-231]() with the view-projection matrix, camera position, and render layer mask. Each thread:

1. **Finds its CUBO instance** [shaders/defaultcull.csh:150-164]() via linear search
2. **Fetches its entity ID** from the bindless entity ID buffer
3. **Checks render layers and attributes** [shaders/defaultcull.csh:174-193]()
4. **Performs culling tests** (detailed below)
5. **Atomically increments instance count** and writes entity ID if visible

**Sources:** [shaders/defaultcull.csh:7-17](), [shaders/defaultcull.csh:148-314](), [include/RavEngine/RenderEngine.hpp:224-231]()

---

### Frustum Culling

Frustum culling tests a transformed bounding sphere against six planes extracted from the view-projection matrix:

**Plane Extraction** [shaders/defaultcull.csh:81-92]():
```glsl
void MakeFrustumPlanes(mat4 viewProj, inout vec4 planes[6]) {
    for (uint i = 0; i < 4; ++i) { planes[0][i] = viewProj[i][3] + viewProj[i][0]; }  // left
    for (uint i = 0; i < 4; ++i) { planes[1][i] = viewProj[i][3] - viewProj[i][0]; }  // right
    // ... top, bottom, near, far
    for (uint i = 0; i < planes.length(); i++) {
        planes[i] /= length(planes[i].xyz);  // normalize
    }
}
```

**Sphere Transformation** [shaders/defaultcull.csh:195-214]():
The shader transforms the unit bounding sphere by the model matrix to find the world-space radius:

```glsl
mat3 modelNoTranslate = mat3(model);
vec3 radvecs[] = { vec3(0,0,radius), vec3(0,radius,0), vec3(radius,0,0) };
float radius = 0;
for(uint i = 0; i < radvecs.length(); i++) {
    radvecs[i] = modelNoTranslate * radvecs[i];
    radius = max(radius, length(radvecs[i]));  // Use largest transformed radius
}
vec3 center = (model * vec4(0,0,0,1)).xyz;
```

**Culling Test** [shaders/defaultcull.csh:71-78]():
```glsl
float CullSphere(vec4 vPlanes[6], vec3 vCenter, float fRadius) {
    float dist01 = min(DistanceToPlane(vPlanes[0], vCenter), DistanceToPlane(vPlanes[1], vCenter));
    float dist23 = min(DistanceToPlane(vPlanes[2], vCenter), DistanceToPlane(vPlanes[3], vCenter));
    float dist45 = min(DistanceToPlane(vPlanes[4], vCenter), DistanceToPlane(vPlanes[5], vCenter));
    return min(min(dist01, dist23), dist45) + fRadius;  // > 0 if visible
}
```

Entities can skip frustum culling by clearing bit 0 in their `perObjectFlags` [shaders/defaultcull.csh:181]().

**Sources:** [shaders/defaultcull.csh:81-92](), [shaders/defaultcull.csh:195-218](), [shaders/defaultcull.csh:71-78]()

---

### Occlusion Culling

Occlusion culling uses a **depth pyramid** (hierarchical Z-buffer) to efficiently test if objects are occluded by previously rendered geometry.

**Process** [shaders/defaultcull.csh:220-274]():

1. **Project bounding sphere** to NDC space to find min/max X/Y [shaders/defaultcull.csh:108-145]()
2. **Calculate screen-space dimensions** in pixels
3. **Select mip level** matching bounding box size: `ceil(log2(max(width, height))) - 1`
4. **Sample depth pyramid** at the four corners of the bounding box
5. **Compare** `referenceZ >= minDepth` (using reverse-Z, so greater = closer)

**Depth Pyramid Sampling** [shaders/defaultcull.csh:255-270]():
```glsl
vec2 ndcCorners[] = {
    vec2(projected.minX, projected.maxY),  // top left
    vec2(projected.maxX, projected.maxY),  // top right
    vec2(projected.maxX, projected.minY),  // bottom right
    vec2(projected.minX, projected.minY),  // bottom left
};

for(uint i = 0; i < ndcCorners.length(); i++) {
    ndcCorners[i] = (ndcCorners[i] + 1) * 0.5;      // [-1,1] to [0,1]
    ndcCorners[i].y = 1 - ndcCorners[i].y;          // flip Y
    float depth = textureLod(sampler2D(depthPyramid, depthPyramidSampler), ndcCorners[i], miplevel).x;
    minDepth = min(minDepth, depth);
}
```

On platforms without reduction samplers (Metal, WebGPU), the shader manually samples four texels and takes the minimum [shaders/defaultcull.csh:257-266]().

Objects intersecting the near plane (`referenceZ > 1`) are considered visible [shaders/defaultcull.csh:229]().

**Sources:** [shaders/defaultcull.csh:220-274](), [shaders/defaultcull.csh:108-145]()

---

### LOD Selection

LOD (Level of Detail) selection uses squared distance from camera and "Price is Right" rules [shaders/defaultcull.csh:276-303]():

```glsl
float distFromCamera = distSquared(worldSpacePos, ubo.camPos);
float currentBest = lodDistanceBuffer[0];

for(uint i = 0; i < cubo.numLODs; i++) {
    float minDisplayableDistForThisLOD = lodDistanceBuffer[i];
    minDisplayableDistForThisLOD *= minDisplayableDistForThisLOD;  // square it
    
    // Use LOD if distance > LOD's threshold AND threshold > current best
    if (distFromCamera > minDisplayableDistForThisLOD && minDisplayableDistForThisLOD > currentBest) {
        lodID = i;
        currentBest = minDisplayableDistForThisLOD;
    }
}
```

The selected `lodID` determines which indirect draw command receives the entity:

```glsl
const uint indirectBufferIdx = cubo.indirectBufferOffset + lodID;
uint idx = atomicAdd(indirectBuffer[indirectBufferIdx].instanceCount, 1);
```

**Sources:** [shaders/defaultcull.csh:276-313]()

---

## Depth Pyramid Generation

### Purpose

The depth pyramid is a mipmap chain of the depth buffer where each mip level stores the **minimum depth** (farthest surface) of a 2x2 quad from the previous level. This enables efficient hierarchical occlusion culling by allowing the culling shader to sample at a mip level matching the object's screen-space size.

**Format:** `RGL::TextureFormat::R32_Float` [include/RavEngine/RenderEngine.hpp:144]()

**Generation:** After the depth prepass, the `depthPyramidPipeline` compute shader [src/RenderEngine.cpp:1217-1224]() builds the pyramid in multiple dispatches, one per mip level.

```mermaid
graph TD
    DepthPrepass["Depth Prepass<br/>Opaque geometry writes depth<br/>depthFunction = Greater"]
    
    subgraph "Depth Pyramid Generation"
        Mip0["Mip 0: Copy from depth buffer<br/>depthPyramidCopyPipeline"]
        Mip1["Mip 1: Sample Mip 0 (2x2)<br/>depthPyramidPipeline<br/>Find minimum depth"]
        Mip2["Mip 2: Sample Mip 1 (2x2)"]
        MipN["Mip N: Continue until 1x1"]
        
        Mip0 --> Mip1
        Mip1 --> Mip2
        Mip2 --> MipN
    end
    
    OcclusionCull["Occlusion Culling<br/>Sample pyramid at matching mip level"]
    
    DepthPrepass --> Mip0
    MipN --> OcclusionCull
```

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/RenderEngine.hpp:144](), [src/RenderEngine.cpp:1217-1224]()

---

### Generation Process

The depth pyramid generation occurs in `RenderEngine::Draw` after the depth prepass [src/RenderEngine_Draw.cpp:1208-1269]():

**Step 1: Copy Base Level** [src/RenderEngine_Draw.cpp:1208-1234]()
```cpp
// Copy depth buffer to pyramid mip 0 using a fullscreen pass
depthPyramidCopyPass->SetAttachmentTexture(0, depthPyramidView);
mainCommandBuffer->BeginRendering(depthPyramidCopyPass);
mainCommandBuffer->SetViewport(fullSizeViewport);
mainCommandBuffer->BindRenderPipeline(depthPyramidCopyPipeline);
mainCommandBuffer->SetVertexSampler(depthPyramidSampler, 0);
mainCommandBuffer->SetVertexTexture(depthTextureView, 1);
mainCommandBuffer->SetVertexBytes(PyramidCopyUBO{.size = dim.width}, 0);
mainCommandBuffer->Draw(3);  // fullscreen triangle
mainCommandBuffer->EndRendering();
```

**Step 2: Build Mip Chain** [src/RenderEngine_Draw.cpp:1236-1269]()
```cpp
mainCommandBuffer->BeginCompute(depthPyramidPipeline);
for (uint8_t mip = 1; mip < depthPyramid.numMips; mip++) {
    uint32_t dimDivisor = std::pow(2, mip);
    dim_t<uint32_t> mipSize = {
        .width = dim.width / dimDivisor,
        .height = dim.height / dimDivisor
    };
    
    // Bind output mip level for writing
    auto outputView = depthPyramid.GetMipView(mip);
    mainCommandBuffer->BindComputeStorageTexture(outputView, 0);
    
    // Sample previous mip level
    auto inputView = depthPyramid.GetMipView(mip - 1);
    mainCommandBuffer->BindComputeSampler(depthPyramidSampler, 2);
    mainCommandBuffer->BindComputeTexture(inputView, 1);
    
    // Dispatch: one thread per output pixel
    mainCommandBuffer->DispatchCompute(
        std::ceil(mipSize.width / 32.0),
        std::ceil(mipSize.height / 32.0),
        1, 32, 32, 1
    );
}
mainCommandBuffer->EndCompute();
```

The `depthPyramidSampler` uses `RGL::SamplerReductionMode::Minimum` [src/RenderEngine.cpp:323-331]() to automatically return the minimum of sampled texels on platforms that support it (Vulkan, DirectX 12). On platforms without reduction samplers, the culling shader performs manual min-reduction [shaders/defaultcull.csh:257-266]().

**Sources:** [src/RenderEngine_Draw.cpp:1208-1269](), [src/RenderEngine.cpp:323-331]()

---

## GPU Resource Management

### BufferedVRAMVector and BufferedVRAMSparseSet

RavEngine uses specialized containers to efficiently synchronize data from CPU to GPU each frame. These containers maintain **staging buffers** on the host and **private buffers** on the device.

```mermaid
graph LR
    subgraph "Host Side"
        HostData["CPU Data<br/>std::vector or SparseSet"]
        StagingBuffer["Staging Buffer<br/>Shared/Mappable Memory"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Device Side"
        PrivateBuffer["Private Buffer<br/>GPU-only Memory"]
        Shader["Compute/Vertex Shaders<br/>Read private buffer"]
    end
    
    HostData -->|Write| StagingBuffer
    StagingBuffer -->|CopyBuffer| PrivateBuffer
    PrivateBuffer --> Shader
```

**BufferedVRAMVector** [include/RavEngine/BufferedVRAMVector.hpp](): Manages a contiguous array on GPU
- **Usage:** Transform matrices, light data, render layers
- **Example:** `worldTransforms` [include/RavEngine/World.hpp:440]()

**BufferedVRAMSparseSet** [include/RavEngine/VRAMSparseSet.hpp](): Manages a sparse set on GPU with O(1) lookups
- **Usage:** Per-light data, per-material entity lists
- **Example:** `directionalLightData` [include/RavEngine/World.hpp:421]()

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/World.hpp:419-449]()

---

### Synchronization Strategy

Synchronization occurs in `World::Tick` during the render tasks phase [src/World.cpp:69-73]():

```mermaid
sequenceDiagram
    participant CPU as World::Tick
    participant Task as Render Tasks (async)
    participant CB as transformSyncCommandBuffer
    participant GPU as GPU Queue
    
    CPU->>Task: executor.run(renderTasks)
    Task->>Task: Update dirty transforms
    Task->>Task: Update dirty lights
    Task->>CB: EncodeSync() for each buffer
    CB->>CB: CopyBuffer: staging â†’ private
    Task->>GPU: Commit transformSyncCommandBuffer
    GPU->>GPU: Execute copies
    Note over GPU: Guaranteed to complete before<br/>mainCommandBuffer (same queue)
    CPU->>CPU: Wait for render tasks
    CPU->>GPU: Submit mainCommandBuffer
```

**EncodeSync Pattern** [src/RenderEngine_Draw.cpp:113-147]():

Each buffered container calls `EncodeSync()` if dirty:
```cpp
bool transformSyncCommandBufferNeedsCommit = false;
wrd.worldTransforms.EncodeSync(
    device, 
    transformSyncCommandBuffer, 
    gcbuffer,  // callback to garbage collect old buffers
    transformSyncCommandBufferNeedsCommit
);
```

If any buffer needs synchronization, the command buffer is committed [src/RenderEngine_Draw.cpp:296-303]():
```cpp
if (transformSyncCommandBufferNeedsCommit) {
    transformSyncCommandBuffer->End();
    transformSyncCommandBuffer->Commit(config);
    // No fence needed - same-queue ordering guarantees completion
}
```

This approach minimizes synchronization overhead by:
1. **Batching** all buffer copies into one command buffer
2. **Using queue ordering** instead of explicit fences
3. **Only syncing dirty data** via change tracking

**Sources:** [src/RenderEngine_Draw.cpp:113-304](), [src/World.cpp:69-73]()

---

## Compute Shader Skinning

### Overview

Skeletal animation transforms vertices by bone matrices entirely on the GPU using the `skinnedMeshComputePipeline` [src/RenderEngine.cpp:1053-1059](). This eliminates CPU-side skinning and enables efficient instancing of animated characters.

```mermaid
graph LR
    subgraph "CPU: World::Tick"
        AnimatorSystem["AnimatorSystem<br/>Calculate bone matrices<br/>Store in AnimatorComponent"]
    end
    
    subgraph "CPU: RenderEngine::Draw"
        PrepareBuffers["Resize skinning buffers<br/>Write bone matrices to<br/>sharedSkeletonMatrixBuffer"]
        EncodeSkinning["Encode skinning compute pass<br/>poseSkeletalMeshes()"]
    end
    
    subgraph "GPU: skinning_cs_csh"
        ReadBones["Read bone matrices<br/>Read vertex weights"]
        Transform["Transform each vertex:<br/>position, normal, tangent, etc."]
        WriteOutput["Write to shared vertex buffers<br/>sharedSkinnedPositionBuffer, etc."]
    end
    
    subgraph "Rendering"
        Culling["Culling compute shader<br/>Tests skinned meshes"]
        DrawIndirect["DrawIndexedIndirect<br/>Uses skinned vertex buffers"]
    end
    
    AnimatorSystem --> PrepareBuffers
    PrepareBuffers --> EncodeSkinning
    EncodeSkinning --> ReadBones
    ReadBones --> Transform
    Transform --> WriteOutput
    WriteOutput --> Culling
    Culling --> DrawIndirect
```

**Sources:** [src/RenderEngine.cpp:1053-1059](), [src/RenderEngine_Draw.cpp:577-630]()

---

### Skinning Pipeline

**Step 1: Prepare Buffers** [src/RenderEngine_Draw.cpp:479-544]()

Before skinning, `prepareSkeletalMeshBuffers()` resizes GPU buffers:
- **`sharedSkeletonMatrixBuffer`**: All bone matrices (stride: `sizeof(matrix4)`)
- **`sharedSkinnedPositionBuffer`**: Skinned vertex positions (writable storage buffer)
- **`sharedSkinnedNormalBuffer`**, `sharedSkinnedTangentBuffer`, etc.: Other vertex attributes
- **`indirectBuffer`** per material: Draw commands
- **`cullingBuffer`** per material: Visible entity IDs

The buffers are sized for `totalJointsToSkin` and `totalVertsToSkin` across all skinned meshes.

**Step 2: Write Bone Matrices** [src/RenderEngine_Draw.cpp:598-627]()

For each mesh, the engine writes bone matrices to the staging buffer:
```cpp
std::span<mat_t> matbufMem{
    static_cast<mat_t*>(sharedSkeletonMatrixBuffer->GetMappedDataPtr()), 
    sharedSkeletonMatrixBuffer->getBufferSize() / sizeof(mat_t)
};

for (const auto& ownerid : command.entities.GetReverseMap()) {
    auto& animator = worldOwning->GetComponent<AnimatorComponent>({ownerid, ...});
    const auto& skinningMats = animator.GetSkinningMats();
    std::copy(skinningMats.begin(), skinningMats.end(), 
              (matbufMem.begin() + subo.boneReadOffset) + object_id * skinningMats.size());
    object_id++;
}
```

**Step 3: Dispatch Skinning** [src/RenderEngine_Draw.cpp:577-630]()

The `poseSkeletalMeshes()` function dispatches compute work:
```cpp
mainCommandBuffer->BeginCompute(skinnedMeshComputePipeline);
mainCommandBuffer->BindComputeBuffer(sharedSkinnedPositionBuffer, 0);  // output
mainCommandBuffer->BindComputeBuffer(sharedPositionBuffer, 10);        // input (base pose)
mainCommandBuffer->BindComputeBuffer(sharedSkeletonMatrixBuffer, 20);  // bone matrices
mainCommandBuffer->BindComputeBuffer(mesh->GetWeightsBuffer(), 21);    // bone weights

SkinningUBO subo{
    .numObjects = entities.DenseSize(),
    .numVertices = mesh->GetNumVerts(),
    .numBones = skeleton->GetSkeleton()->num_joints(),
    .boneReadOffset = ...,
    .vertexWriteOffset = ...,
    .vertexReadOffset = mesh->GetAllocation().getVertexRangeStart()
};
mainCommandBuffer->SetComputeBytes(subo, 0);
mainCommandBuffer->DispatchCompute(
    std::ceil(subo.numObjects / 8.0),
    std::ceil(subo.numVertices / 32.0),
    1, 8, 32, 1
);
```

**Dispatch dimensions:** `(numObjects/8, numVertices/32, 1)` with `(8, 32, 1)` threads per workgroup, so each thread processes one vertex for one object instance.

**Sources:** [src/RenderEngine_Draw.cpp:479-630]()

---

### Skinning Shader

The `skinning_cs_csh` shader [src/RenderEngine.cpp:974-1059]() transforms vertices:

```glsl
layout(local_size_x = 8, local_size_y = 32, local_size_z = 1) in;
void main() {
    uint objectID = gl_GlobalInvocationID.x;
    uint vertexID = gl_GlobalInvocationID.y;
    
    if (objectID >= ubo.numObjects || vertexID >= ubo.numVertices) return;
    
    uint inputVertexIdx = ubo.vertexReadOffset + vertexID;
    uint outputVertexIdx = ubo.vertexWriteOffset + objectID * ubo.numVertices + vertexID;
    
    // Read base pose vertex
    vec3 position = positionBuffer[inputVertexIdx];
    vec3 normal = normalBuffer[inputVertexIdx];
    
    // Read bone weights
    vec4 weights = weightBuffer[vertexID].weights;
    uvec4 joints = weightBuffer[vertexID].joints;
    
    // Transform by weighted bone matrices
    vec3 skinnedPos = vec3(0);
    vec3 skinnedNormal = vec3(0);
    for (int i = 0; i < 4; i++) {
        if (weights[i] > 0) {
            uint boneIdx = ubo.boneReadOffset + objectID * ubo.numBones + joints[i];
            mat4 boneMatrix = boneMatrixBuffer[boneIdx];
            skinnedPos += weights[i] * (boneMatrix * vec4(position, 1.0)).xyz;
            skinnedNormal += weights[i] * mat3(boneMatrix) * normal;
        }
    }
    
    // Write output
    skinnedPositionBuffer[outputVertexIdx] = skinnedPos;
    skinnedNormalBuffer[outputVertexIdx] = normalize(skinnedNormal);
}
```

Each object instance gets a full copy of the skinned vertices in the output buffer. During rendering, the vertex shader fetches the entity ID from `cullingBuffer` and uses it to index into the transform buffer, while vertex attributes come from the per-instance offset in the skinned buffers.

**Sources:** [src/RenderEngine.cpp:974-1059]()

---

## Clustered Forward+ Lighting

### Overview

RavEngine uses **Clustered Forward+ rendering** to efficiently handle large numbers of dynamic lights. The view frustum is subdivided into a 3D grid of clusters (default: 12Ã—12Ã—24 = 3,456 clusters), and lights are assigned to clusters in a compute shader. During the main lighting pass, the pixel shader only evaluates lights affecting its cluster.

```mermaid
graph TD
    BuildGrid["Compute: Build Cluster Grid<br/>cluster_build_grid_csh<br/>Calculate AABB per cluster"]
    
    AssignLights["Compute: Assign Lights to Clusters<br/>cluster_assign_lights_csh<br/>For each light:<br/>  Test sphere-AABB intersection<br/>  Add light index to cluster"]
    
    Rendering["Fragment Shader:<br/>Calculate cluster index from depth<br/>Iterate lights in cluster<br/>Accumulate lighting"]
    
    BuildGrid --> AssignLights
    AssignLights --> Rendering
```

**Sources:** [src/RenderEngine.cpp:922-971](), [include/RavEngine/RenderEngine.hpp:47-61]()

---

### Cluster Grid Structure

The cluster grid divides view space using a logarithmic Z distribution for better precision near the camera.

**Cluster Definition** [include/RavEngine/RenderEngine.hpp:53-60]():
```cpp
struct Cluster {
    glm::vec3 minPoint;
    glm::vec3 maxPoint;
    uint32_t pointLightCount;
    uint32_t spotLightCount;
    uint32_t pointLightIndices[CLUSTER_MAX_POINTS];  // typically 50
    uint32_t spotLightIndices[CLUSTER_MAX_SPOTS];    // typically 50
};
```

**Buffer:** `lightClusterBuffer` [src/RenderEngine.cpp:839-845]() holds 3,456 clusters.

**Grid Dimensions** [include/RavEngine/RenderEngine.hpp:48-51]():
```cpp
constexpr static uint32_t gridSizeX = 12;
constexpr static uint32_t gridSizeY = 12;
constexpr static uint32_t gridSizeZ = 24;
constexpr static uint32_t numClusters = 12 * 12 * 24;  // 3,456
```

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/RenderEngine.hpp:47-61](), [src/RenderEngine.cpp:839-845]()

---

### Cluster Building

**Step 1: Build Grid** [src/RenderEngine_Draw.cpp:1387-1414]()

The `clusterBuildGridPipeline` computes the AABB for each cluster:

```cpp
mainCommandBuffer->BeginCompute(clusterBuildGridPipeline);
mainCommandBuffer->BindComputeBuffer(lightClusterBuffer, 0);

GridBuildUBO gridUBO{
    .invProj = glm::inverse(camData.projOnly),
    .gridSize = {Clustered::gridSizeX, Clustered::gridSizeY, Clustered::gridSizeZ},
    .zNear = camData.zNearFar[0],
    .screenDim = {collection.pixelDimensions.width, collection.pixelDimensions.height},
    .zFar = camData.zNearFar[1]
};
mainCommandBuffer->SetComputeBytes(gridUBO, 0);

mainCommandBuffer->DispatchCompute(
    Clustered::gridSizeX,
    Clustered::gridSizeY,
    Clustered::gridSizeZ,
    1, 1, 1
);
```

Each thread computes one cluster's min/max bounds in view space using the inverse projection matrix.

**Step 2: Assign Lights** [src/RenderEngine_Draw.cpp:1416-1443]()

The `clusterPopulatePipeline` iterates all lights and tests sphere-AABB intersection:

```cpp
mainCommandBuffer->BeginCompute(clusterPopulatePipeline);
mainCommandBuffer->BindComputeBuffer(lightClusterBuffer, 0);
mainCommandBuffer->BindComputeBuffer(pointLightPrivateBuffer, 1);
mainCommandBuffer->BindComputeBuffer(spotLightPrivateBuffer, 2);

GridAssignUBO assignUBO{
    .viewMat = camData.viewOnly,
    .pointLightCount = pointLightCount,
    .spotLightCount = spotLightCount
};
mainCommandBuffer->SetComputeBytes(assignUBO, 0);

mainCommandBuffer->DispatchCompute(numClusters, 1, 1, 256, 1, 1);
```

This shader uses 256 threads per workgroup, with each thread processing multiple clusters. For each light:
1. Transform light position to view space
2. Test against all cluster AABBs
3. Atomically add light index to matching clusters (if not full)

**Sources:** [src/RenderEngine_Draw.cpp:1387-1443]()

---

### Fragment Shader Integration

During the main lit pass, fragment shaders:

1. **Calculate cluster index** from screen position and depth:
   ```glsl
   uint clusterX = uint(gl_FragCoord.x / screenWidth * gridSizeX);
   uint clusterY = uint(gl_FragCoord.y / screenHeight * gridSizeY);
   float linearDepth = ... // convert depth to linear
   uint clusterZ = uint(log(linearDepth / zNear) / log(zFar / zNear) * gridSizeZ);
   uint clusterIndex = clusterX + clusterY * gridSizeX + clusterZ * gridSizeX * gridSizeY;
   ```

2. **Iterate lights in cluster**:
   ```glsl
   Cluster cluster = clusterBuffer[clusterIndex];
   vec3 lighting = vec3(0);
   for (uint i = 0; i < cluster.pointLightCount; i++) {
       uint lightIndex = cluster.pointLightIndices[i];
       PointLight light = pointLightBuffer[lightIndex];
       lighting += evaluatePointLight(light, worldPos, normal);
   }
   ```

This reduces the lighting complexity from O(numLights) to O(lightsPerCluster), typically reducing thousands of lights to tens per pixel.

**Sources:** [Diagram 3 from architecture overview]()

---

## Complete Pipeline Flow

The following diagram shows the complete GPU-driven rendering pipeline execution:

```mermaid
graph TB
    Start["RenderEngine::Draw<br/>src/RenderEngine_Draw.cpp:98"]
    
    SyncBuffers["Sync GPU Buffers<br/>worldTransforms, lights, meshData<br/>transformSyncCommandBuffer<br/>Lines 113-304"]
    
    SkinningPrep["Prepare Skinned Mesh Buffers<br/>prepareSkeletalMeshBuffers()<br/>Lines 479-544"]
    
    SkinningDrawCallPrep["Prepare Skinning Indirect Buffer<br/>prepareSkeletalCullingBuffer()<br/>skinned_mesh_drawcall_csh<br/>Lines 546-574"]
    
    PoseSkinned["Compute: Pose Skinned Meshes<br/>poseSkeletalMeshes()<br/>skinning_cs_csh<br/>Lines 577-630"]
    
    TickParticles["Compute: Tick Particles<br/>User update shaders<br/>Lines 632-757"]
    
    CameraLoop["For Each Camera<br/>Lines 759-2390"]

    ClusterGrid["Compute: Build Light Clusters<br/>cluster_build_grid_csh<br/>Lines 1387-1414"]
    
    ClusterAssign["Compute: Assign Lights to Clusters<br/>cluster_assign_lights_csh<br/>Lines 1416-1443"]
    
    CullOpaque["Compute: Cull Opaque Objects<br/>defaultcull_csh<br/>Frustum + Occlusion + LOD<br/>Lines 1445-1516"]
    
    Shadows["Pass: Shadow Map Rendering<br/>Directional/Point/Spot<br/>Depth-only<br/>Lines 1518-1764"]
    
    MainOpaque["Pass: Main Opaque Rendering<br/>Lit/Unlit materials<br/>depthFunction = Equal<br/>Clustered lighting<br/>Lines 1766-1954"]
    
    Skybox["Pass: Skybox<br/>Lines 1956-1986"]
    
    CullTransparent["Compute: Cull Transparent Objects<br/>defaultcull_csh<br/>Lines 1988-2044"]
    
    Transparent["Pass: Transparent Rendering<br/>Order-Independent Transparency<br/>Multi-Layer Alpha Blending<br/>Lines 2046-2176"]
    
    PostProcess["Pass: Post-Processing<br/>SSAO/GTAO, SSGI, Bloom, etc.<br/>Lines 2178-2352"]
    
    GUI["Pass: GUI Rendering<br/>RmlUi contexts<br/>Lines 2354-2390"]
    
    Submit["Submit Command Buffer<br/>mainCommandBuffer->End()<br/>mainCommandBuffer->Commit()"]
    
    Start --> SyncBuffers
    SyncBuffers --> SkinningPrep
    SkinningPrep --> SkinningDrawCallPrep
    SkinningDrawCallPrep --> PoseSkinned
    PoseSkinned --> TickParticles
    TickParticles --> CameraLoop
    
    CameraLoop --> DepthPrepass
    DepthPrepass --> DepthPyramid
    DepthPyramid --> ClusterGrid
    ClusterGrid --> ClusterAssign
    ClusterAssign --> CullOpaque
    CullOpaque --> Shadows
    Shadows --> MainOpaque
    MainOpaque --> Skybox
    Skybox --> CullTransparent
    CullTransparent --> Transparent
    Transparent --> PostProcess
    PostProcess --> GUI
    
    GUI --> CameraLoop
    CameraLoop --> Submit
```

**Key Observations:**

1. **Compute-heavy front-end:** Skinning, particle updates, and culling happen before any rendering
2. **Depth-first ordering:** Depth prepass â†’ pyramid â†’ culling enables early-Z optimization
3. **Per-camera clustering:** Light clustering runs per viewport for split-screen/VR support
4. **Separate transparent culling:** Transparent objects are culled after opaque rendering completes
5. **No CPU stalls:** All draw parameters are GPU-generated; CPU only submits one command buffer

**Sources:** [src/RenderEngine_Draw.cpp:98-2390]()

---

## Performance Considerations

### Advantages

| Technique | Benefit |
|-----------|---------|
| **Indirect Rendering** | Eliminates CPU-side draw call submission overhead |
| **GPU Culling** | Massively parallel, avoids CPU-GPU readback stalls |
| **Depth Pyramid** | Efficient hierarchical occlusion testing |
| **Compute Skinning** | Eliminates CPU skinning bottleneck, enables instancing |
| **Clustered Lighting** | O(lightsPerCluster) instead of O(numLights) |
| **Bindless Resources** | Reduces descriptor set management overhead |

### Trade-offs

- **Memory:** Requires large GPU buffers (shared vertex/index buffers, indirect buffers)
- **Buffer resizing:** Reallocation may cause frame stutter [src/RenderEngine.cpp:1061-1194]()
- **Debugging:** GPU-side logic is harder to debug than CPU-side
- **Platform support:** Some features (reduction samplers, bindless) have fallbacks

**Sources:** [src/RenderEngine.cpp:1061-1194]()

---

## Purpose and Scope

This document covers RavEngine's render data synchronization system, which bridges the Entity-Component-System (ECS) world representation with GPU-friendly data structures. The system maintains parallel, optimized copies of component data specifically formatted for efficient GPU consumption, and handles the asynchronous transfer of changes from the main simulation thread to rendering resources.

For information about the overall rendering pipeline execution, see [Rendering Architecture](#4.1). For GPU-driven culling techniques that consume this synchronized data, see [GPU-Driven Rendering Techniques](#9.2). For the ECS architecture that produces the source data, see [Entity Component System](#3.2).

---

## Overview

RavEngine's ECS design uses sparse sets for flexible component storage on the CPU side, but GPUs require contiguous, tightly-packed data layouts for optimal performance. The render data synchronization system solves this impedance mismatch by:

- Maintaining **parallel GPU-resident copies** of frequently-accessed component data (transforms, lights, material assignments)
- Using **dirty flags** to track changes and minimize unnecessary data transfers
- Employing **double-buffered structures** to avoid GPU stalls during updates
- Organizing mesh rendering commands into **Multi-Draw Indirect (MDI)** structures grouped by material for batch rendering
- Executing synchronization **asynchronously** via command buffers to overlap with GPU work

This architecture allows the simulation to proceed independently while the rendering system consumes a consistent snapshot of world state.

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/World.hpp:418-449](), [src/World.cpp:310-521](), [src/RenderEngine_Draw.cpp:98-304]()

---

## Core Data Structures

### World::RenderData Structure

```mermaid
classDiagram
    class World_RenderData {
        +BufferedVRAMSparseSet~DirLightUploadData~ directionalLightData
        +BufferedVRAMSparseSet~AmbientLightUploadData~ ambientLightData
        +BufferedVRAMSparseSet~PointLightUploadData~ pointLightData
        +BufferedVRAMSparseSet~SpotLightDataUpload~ spotLightData
        +BufferedVRAMVector~DirLightUploadDataPassVarying~ directionalLightPassVarying
        +BufferedVRAMVector~renderlayer_t~ renderLayers
        +BufferedVRAMVector~perobject_t~ perObjectAttributes
        +BufferedVRAMVector~matrix4~ worldTransforms
        +OrderedMap~MaterialSort,MDIICommand~ staticMeshRenderData
        +OrderedMap~MaterialSort,MDIICommandSkinned~ skinnedMeshRenderData
        +SharedBufferPool stagingBufferPool
    }
    
    class BufferedVRAMVector {
        -RGLBufferPtr privateBuffer
        -RGLBufferPtr stagingBuffer
        -vector~T~ hostData
        -dirty flags
        +EncodeSync()
        +SetValueAt()
        +GetValueAtForWriting()
    }
    
    class BufferedVRAMSparseSet {
        -RGLBufferPtr privateBuffer
        -RGLBufferPtr stagingBuffer
        -SparseSet~T~ hostData
        -dirty tracking
        +EncodeSync()
        +Emplace()
        +GetForSparseIndexForWriting()
    }
    
    class MDIICommand {
        +RGLBufferPtr indirectBuffer
        +RGLBufferPtr cullingBuffer
        +vector~command~ commands
    }
    
    class MDIICommand_command {
        +WeakRef~MeshCollectionStatic~ mesh
        +BufferedVRAMSparseSet~entity_id_t~ entities
    }
    
    World_RenderData *-- BufferedVRAMVector
    World_RenderData *-- BufferedVRAMSparseSet
    World_RenderData *-- MDIICommand
    MDIICommand *-- MDIICommand_command
```

**Description of World::RenderData Components**

The `World::RenderData` structure ([include/RavEngine/World.hpp:418-449]()) contains all GPU-synchronized rendering state:

| Member | Type | Purpose |
|--------|------|---------|
| `directionalLightData` | `BufferedVRAMSparseSet<DirLightUploadData>` | Directional light properties indexed by entity ID |
| `ambientLightData` | `BufferedVRAMSparseSet<AmbientLightUploadData>` | Ambient/environment light data |
| `pointLightData` | `BufferedVRAMSparseSet<PointLightUploadData>` | Point light positions, colors, shadow matrices |
| `spotLightData` | `BufferedVRAMSparseSet<SpotLightDataUpload>` | Spot light transforms and parameters |
| `directionalLightPassVarying` | `BufferedVRAMVector<DirLightUploadDataPassVarying>` | Per-camera shadow matrices for cascaded shadow maps |
| `renderLayers` | `BufferedVRAMVector<renderlayer_t>` | Layer masks for culling, indexed by entity ID |
| `perObjectAttributes` | `BufferedVRAMVector<perobject_t>` | Per-entity rendering flags (frustum culling, shadows) |
| `worldTransforms` | `BufferedVRAMVector<matrix4>` | World-space transform matrices indexed by entity ID |
| `staticMeshRenderData` | `OrderedMap<MaterialSort, MDIICommand>` | Static mesh draw commands grouped by material |
| `skinnedMeshRenderData` | `OrderedMap<MaterialSort, MDIICommandSkinned>` | Skinned mesh draw commands with skeleton references |

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/World.hpp:418-449](), [include/RavEngine/World.hpp:334-362]()

### Buffered VRAM Containers

```mermaid
graph TB
    subgraph BufferedVRAMVector["BufferedVRAMVector&lt;T&gt;"]
        HostVec["Host-side vector&lt;T&gt;<br/>CPU-accessible"]
        StagingVec["Staging Buffer<br/>RGL::BufferAccess::Shared"]
        PrivateVec["Private Buffer<br/>RGL::BufferAccess::Private<br/>GPU-optimal"]
    end
    
    subgraph BufferedVRAMSparseSet["BufferedVRAMSparseSet&lt;Index,T&gt;"]
        HostSparse["Host-side SparseSet<br/>Sparse index mapping"]
        StagingSparse["Staging Buffer<br/>Dense packed"]
        PrivateSparse["Private Buffer<br/>GPU-side dense array"]
    end
    
    CPUWrite["CPU writes"] --> HostVec
    CPUWrite2["CPU writes"] --> HostSparse
    HostVec -->|"SetValueAt()<br/>marks dirty"| HostVec
    HostSparse -->|"Emplace()<br/>GetForWriting()"| HostSparse
    
    HostVec -->|"EncodeSync()"| StagingVec
    StagingVec -->|"Copy Command"| PrivateVec
    
    HostSparse -->|"EncodeSync()"| StagingSparse
    StagingSparse -->|"Copy Command"| PrivateSparse
    
    PrivateVec -->|"Shader binding"| GPU["GPU Shader Access"]
    PrivateSparse -->|"Shader binding"| GPU
    
    style HostVec fill:#f9f9f9
    style HostSparse fill:#f9f9f9
    style StagingVec fill:#fff9e6
    style StagingSparse fill:#fff9e6
    style PrivateVec fill:#e6f7ff
    style PrivateSparse fill:#e6f7ff
```

**BufferedVRAMVector and BufferedVRAMSparseSet**

These template containers implement triple-buffering for CPU-to-GPU data transfer:

1. **Host-side data**: Standard C++ containers (`std::vector` or sparse set) for CPU manipulation
2. **Staging buffer**: `RGL::BufferAccess::Shared` memory visible to both CPU and GPU, used for uploading
3. **Private buffer**: `RGL::BufferAccess::Private` GPU-local memory for optimal shader access

The `EncodeSync()` method ([src/RenderEngine_Draw.cpp:120-146]()) conditionally copies modified data from host to staging, then encodes a GPU copy from staging to private buffer. This avoids blocking the CPU on GPU operations.

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/World.hpp:418-449](), [src/RenderEngine_Draw.cpp:110-304]()

---

## Synchronization Pipeline

### Overall Synchronization Flow

```mermaid
sequenceDiagram
    participant ECS as "ECS Components<br/>(Transform, Lights, etc.)"
    participant Task as "Render Tasks<br/>(Taskflow graph)"
    participant Sync as "EncodeSync<br/>(transformSyncCommandBuffer)"
    participant GPU as "GPU Private Buffers"
    participant Render as "RenderEngine::Draw"
    
    Note over ECS: Component modifications<br/>mark dirty flags
    
    Task->>Task: World::Tick() PostTick phase
    activate Task
    Task->>Task: Execute renderTasks graph
    
    Task->>ECS: updateInvalidatedDirs()
    activate ECS
    ECS->>ECS: Check Transform.isTickDirty
    ECS->>ECS: Update renderData light structs
    ECS-->>Task: Complete
    deactivate ECS
    
    Task->>ECS: updateRenderDataStaticMesh()
    activate ECS
    ECS->>ECS: Filter dirty transforms
    ECS->>ECS: Write worldTransforms
    ECS-->>Task: Complete
    deactivate ECS
    
    deactivate Task
    
    Note over Task,Sync: After all task updates complete
    
    Render->>Sync: Begin Draw()
    activate Sync
    
    Sync->>Sync: worldTransforms.EncodeSync()
    Sync->>Sync: directionalLightData.EncodeSync()
    Sync->>Sync: pointLightData.EncodeSync()
    Sync->>Sync: [all other buffers].EncodeSync()
    
    Sync->>GPU: transformSyncCommandBuffer.End()
    Sync->>GPU: Commit(transformSyncCommandBuffer)
    
    deactivate Sync
    
    Note over GPU: Async GPU copy operations
    
    Render->>Render: Continue with rendering passes
```

**Synchronization Phases**

The synchronization process occurs in two distinct phases:

1. **Task Graph Phase** ([src/World.cpp:310-521]()): During `World::Tick()`, the `renderTasks` task graph executes in parallel, updating `renderData` structures based on dirty flags. These tasks run on the main thread after ECS systems complete.

2. **Command Buffer Phase** ([src/RenderEngine_Draw.cpp:110-146]()): At the start of `RenderEngine::Draw()`, `EncodeSync()` is called on all buffered structures. If any data changed, the method:
   - Copies host data to staging buffers
   - Encodes GPU-side buffer copies into `transformSyncCommandBuffer`
   - Commits the command buffer asynchronously

The `transformSyncCommandBuffer` is committed without waiting for a fence because command buffers on the same queue execute in submission order ([src/RenderEngine_Draw.cpp:296-303]()).

**Sources:** [src/World.cpp:310-521](), [src/RenderEngine_Draw.cpp:98-304]()

---

### EncodeSync Implementation Details

```mermaid
flowchart TD
    Start["EncodeSync(device, commandBuffer, gcCallback, needsCommit)"] --> CheckDirty{"Data marked dirty?"}
    
    CheckDirty -->|No| Return["Return (no-op)"]
    CheckDirty -->|Yes| CopyToStaging["Copy host data â†’ staging buffer<br/>(memcpy to mapped memory)"]
    
    CopyToStaging --> CheckPrivate{"Private buffer exists<br/>and correct size?"}
    
    CheckPrivate -->|No| CreatePrivate["device.CreateBuffer()<br/>Private GPU-only buffer"]
    CheckPrivate -->|Yes| ReusePrivate["Reuse existing private buffer"]
    
    CreatePrivate --> GCOld["gcCallback(oldPrivateBuffer)"]
    GCOld --> EncodeCopy
    ReusePrivate --> EncodeCopy
    
    EncodeCopy["commandBuffer.CopyBufferToBuffer()<br/>(staging â†’ private)"]
    EncodeCopy --> SetNeedsCommit["needsCommit = true"]
    SetNeedsCommit --> ClearDirty["Clear dirty flag"]
    ClearDirty --> Return
    
    style Start fill:#e1f5ff
    style EncodeCopy fill:#ffe1e1
    style Return fill:#e1ffe1
```

**EncodeSync Process**

The `EncodeSync()` method implements lazy GPU buffer allocation and conditional synchronization:

1. **Dirty Check**: If no data changed since last sync, return immediately
2. **Staging Update**: Copy host data to the CPU-visible staging buffer via `memcpy`
3. **Private Buffer Management**:
   - If the private buffer doesn't exist or is the wrong size, create a new one
   - Old buffers are enqueued for garbage collection via `gcCallback` to avoid use-after-free
4. **GPU Copy**: Encode a `CopyBufferToBuffer` command from staging to private
5. **Commit Flag**: Set `needsCommit` reference parameter to signal the command buffer needs submission

After all `EncodeSync()` calls, if any set `needsCommit` to true, the command buffer is ended and committed ([src/RenderEngine_Draw.cpp:296-303]()).

**Sources:** [src/RenderEngine_Draw.cpp:113-146](), [src/RenderEngine_Draw.cpp:296-303]()

---

## Per-Component Synchronization

### Transform Synchronization

```mermaid
flowchart LR
    subgraph ECS["ECS Component Storage"]
        Transform["Transform Component<br/>isTickDirty flag<br/>worldMatrix cache"]
    end
    
    subgraph RenderTasks["Render Tasks (Taskflow)"]
        ResizeBuffer["resizeBuffer task<br/>Ensure worldTransforms size"]
        UpdateMeshes["updateRenderDataStaticMesh<br/>updateRenderDataSkinnedMesh<br/>Filter dirty transforms"]
    end
    
    subgraph RenderData["World::RenderData"]
        WorldTransforms["worldTransforms<br/>BufferedVRAMVector&lt;matrix4&gt;<br/>Indexed by entity ID"]
    end
    
    subgraph GPU["GPU Buffers"]
        PrivateTransforms["Private Transform Buffer<br/>Bound to vertex shaders"]
    end
    
    Transform -->|"ClearTickDirty()"| UpdateMeshes
    ResizeBuffer --> UpdateMeshes
    UpdateMeshes -->|"SetValueAt(entityID, matrix)"| WorldTransforms
    WorldTransforms -->|"EncodeSync()"| PrivateTransforms
    
    style Transform fill:#fff5e1
    style UpdateMeshes fill:#ffe1e1
    style WorldTransforms fill:#e1f5ff
    style PrivateTransforms fill:#f5e1ff
```

**Transform Update Process**

Transforms are synchronized through a multi-step process ([src/World.cpp:354-390]()):

1. **Resize Phase**: The `resizeBuffer` task ([src/World.cpp:316-328]()) ensures `worldTransforms` has capacity for all entities (including newly created ones)
2. **Filter Phase**: Tasks like `updateRenderDataStaticMesh` ([src/World.cpp:354-365]()) filter entities with dirty transforms:
   ```cpp
   Filter([](const StaticMesh& sm, Transform& trns) {
       if (trns.isTickDirty && sm.GetEnabled()) {
           renderData.worldTransforms.SetValueAt(ownerID.id, trns.GetWorldMatrix());
           trns.ClearTickDirty();
       }
   });
   ```
3. **Write Phase**: Updated matrices are written to `worldTransforms` using entity ID as the index
4. **Sync Phase**: During `RenderEngine::Draw()`, `worldTransforms.EncodeSync()` uploads changes ([src/RenderEngine_Draw.cpp:120]())

The `worldTransforms` buffer is indexed directly by entity ID, avoiding indirection during rendering. This wastes some VRAM for non-rendered entities but provides O(1) lookup in shaders.

**Sources:** [src/World.cpp:316-328](), [src/World.cpp:354-390](), [src/RenderEngine_Draw.cpp:120]()

---

### Light Synchronization

```mermaid
graph TB
    subgraph Components["Light Components"]
        DirLight["DirectionalLight<br/>isInvalidated() flag"]
        PointLight["PointLight<br/>isInvalidated() flag"]
        SpotLight["SpotLight<br/>isInvalidated() flag"]
        AmbLight["AmbientLight"]
        LightTransform["Transform<br/>isTickDirty"]
    end
    
    subgraph RenderTasks["Render Task Graph"]
        UpdateDirs["updateInvalidatedDirs<br/>Check dirty + invalidated"]
        UpdatePoints["updateInvalidatedPoints<br/>Transform + color changes"]
        UpdateSpots["updateInvalidatedSpots<br/>View/proj matrices"]
        UpdateAmbients["updateInvalidatedAmbients<br/>Environment maps"]
    end
    
    subgraph RenderData["BufferedVRAMSparseSet Storage"]
        DirData["directionalLightData<br/>DirLightUploadData"]
        PointData["pointLightData<br/>PointLightUploadData"]
        SpotData["spotLightData<br/>SpotLightDataUpload"]
        AmbData["ambientLightData<br/>AmbientLightUploadData"]
    end
    
    DirLight --> UpdateDirs
    LightTransform --> UpdateDirs
    UpdateDirs -->|"GetForSparseIndexForWriting()"| DirData
    
    PointLight --> UpdatePoints
    UpdatePoints -->|"Update position, viewMats"| PointData
    
    SpotLight --> UpdateSpots
    UpdateSpots -->|"Update worldTransform, lightViewProj"| SpotData
    
    AmbLight --> UpdateAmbients
    UpdateAmbients -->|"Update color, skybox bindless IDs"| AmbData
    
    DirData -->|"EncodeSync()"| DirGPU["GPU Light SSBO"]
    PointData -->|"EncodeSync()"| PointGPU["GPU Light SSBO"]
    SpotData -->|"EncodeSync()"| SpotGPU["GPU Light SSBO"]
    AmbData -->|"EncodeSync()"| AmbGPU["GPU Light SSBO"]
    
    style UpdateDirs fill:#ffe1e1
    style DirData fill:#e1f5ff
```

**Light Update Strategy**

Lights use two separate dirty flags ([src/World.cpp:392-520]()):

- **Transform dirty** (`Transform.isTickDirty`): Position/rotation changed
- **Light invalidated** (`light.isInvalidated()`): Color, intensity, shadow settings changed

Each light type has a dedicated render task that checks both flags:

| Light Type | Task Function | Updates |
|------------|---------------|---------|
| Directional | `updateInvalidatedDirs` ([src/World.cpp:392-427]()) | Direction vector, color, intensity, shadow cascade matrices, bindless texture indices |
| Point | `updateInvalidatedPoints` ([src/World.cpp:464-499]()) | Position, 6 view matrices (cubemap faces), color, intensity, projection matrix |
| Spot | `updateInvalidatedSpots` ([src/World.cpp:429-462]()) | World transform, view-projection matrix, cone angles, color, intensity |
| Ambient | `updateInvalidatedAmbients` ([src/World.cpp:501-520]()) | Color, intensity, environment map bindless handles, irradiance map handles |

Light data is stored in `BufferedVRAMSparseSet` structures indexed by entity ID, allowing efficient sparse updates. The `GetForSparseIndexForWriting()` method provides direct write access to the GPU upload structure.

**Sources:** [src/World.cpp:392-520](), [include/RavEngine/World.hpp:364-416]()

---

### Directional Light Shadow Cascade Computation

The directional light synchronization includes a complex shadow cascade calculation ([src/RenderEngine_Draw.cpp:149-294]()) that computes view-projection matrices for cascaded shadow mapping:

1. **Frustum Subdivision**: For each camera, the view frustum is split into cascades based on `DirectionalLight.shadowCascades` array
2. **Frustum Corner Extraction**: World-space corners of each cascade frustum are computed via inverse view-projection transform
3. **Light-Space Bounding**: An orthographic projection is fitted to tightly bound the frustum corners in light space
4. **Matrix Storage**: Resulting light view-projection matrices are written to:
   - `directionalLightPassVarying` (GPU-visible, per-camera-per-light)
   - `directionalLightPassVaryingHostOnly` (CPU-only, for debug visualization)

This computation runs before the main `EncodeSync()` phase and is synchronized separately ([src/RenderEngine_Draw.cpp:293]()).

**Sources:** [src/RenderEngine_Draw.cpp:149-294]()

---

## Multi-Draw Indirect (MDI) Data Synchronization

### MDI Command Structure

```mermaid
classDiagram
    class OrderedMap_staticMeshRenderData {
        <<map MaterialSort to MDIICommand>>
    }
    
    class MaterialSort {
        +Ref~MaterialInstance~ mat
        +operator<() : sorts by priority then pointer
    }
    
    class MDIICommand {
        +RGLBufferPtr indirectBuffer
        +RGLBufferPtr cullingBuffer
        +RGLBufferPtr indirectStagingBuffer
        +RGLBufferPtr cuboBuffer
        +RGLBufferPtr cuboStagingBuffer
        +vector~command~ commands
    }
    
    class MDIICommand_command {
        +WeakRef~MeshCollectionStatic~ mesh
        +BufferedVRAMSparseSet~entity_id_t~ entities
        +entities.SetValueAt(entityID, entityID)
    }
    
    class IndirectBuffer {
        indexCount : uint32
        instanceCount : uint32
        indexStart : uint32
        baseVertex : uint32
        baseInstance : uint32
    }
    
    class CullingBuffer {
        entity_id_t[] : visible entity IDs
    }
    
    OrderedMap_staticMeshRenderData *-- MaterialSort
    OrderedMap_staticMeshRenderData *-- MDIICommand
    MDIICommand *-- MDIICommand_command
    MDIICommand *-- IndirectBuffer
    MDIICommand *-- CullingBuffer
    
    MDIICommand_command --> MeshCollectionStatic
```

**MDI Data Organization**

Static and skinned meshes are organized into Multi-Draw Indirect structures ([include/RavEngine/World.hpp:334-362]()) to minimize draw calls:

1. **Material Grouping**: The `staticMeshRenderData` and `skinnedMeshRenderData` maps use `MaterialSort` as keys, grouping all entities with the same material together
2. **Mesh Subdivision**: Within each material group, `MDIICommand.commands` is a vector where each entry represents entities sharing the same mesh asset
3. **Entity Tracking**: Each `command` contains a `BufferedVRAMSparseSet<entity_id_t>` that stores which entities use this mesh-material combination
4. **Indirect Buffers**: GPU-side `indirectBuffer` contains draw command parameters, and `cullingBuffer` stores visible entity IDs after GPU culling

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/World.hpp:334-362](), [include/RavEngine/World.hpp:40-76]()

---

### MDI Synchronization Process

```mermaid
sequenceDiagram
    participant SM as "StaticMesh Component"
    participant Task as "updateRenderDataStaticMesh"
    participant Entities as "command.entities<br/>(BufferedVRAMSparseSet)"
    participant EncSync as "EncodeSync Phase"
    participant GPU as "GPU Entity ID Buffer"
    
    Note over SM: Mesh added/material changed
    
    SM->>Task: Filter(StaticMesh, Transform)
    activate Task
    
    Task->>Task: Find or create MDIICommand<br/>for material
    Task->>Task: Find or create command<br/>for mesh within material group
    
    Task->>Entities: entities.Emplace(entityID, entityID)
    Note over Entities: Sparse set maps entity ID<br/>to itself for membership
    
    deactivate Task
    
    Note over Task,EncSync: Later, during Draw()
    
    EncSync->>Entities: entities.EncodeSync()
    activate Entities
    
    Entities->>Entities: Copy dense entity IDs<br/>to staging buffer
    Entities->>GPU: CopyBufferToBuffer<br/>(staging â†’ private)
    
    deactivate Entities
    
    Note over GPU: GPU culling shader reads<br/>entity IDs from private buffer
```

**MDI Entity Synchronization**

The `entities` field in each `MDIICommand.command` ([include/RavEngine/World.hpp:342-346]()) uses `BufferedVRAMSparseSet<entity_id_t, entity_id_t>` where both index and value are entity IDs. This design allows:

- **Sparse Membership**: O(1) insertion/removal as entities are added/destroyed
- **Dense GPU Access**: GPU shaders receive a tightly-packed array of entity IDs for culling ([shaders/defaultcull.csh:170]())
- **Automatic Sync**: When an entity's mesh or material changes, the old and new `entities` sets are updated, and `EncodeSync()` handles GPU upload

The synchronization occurs during the mesh update tasks ([src/World.cpp:354-378]()):

```cpp
updateRenderDataGeneric(ptrForTemplate, renderData.staticMeshRenderData, 
    [](auto& sm) { return sm.GetMesh(); },
    [](auto& row, auto& meshToUpdate) {
        return std::find_if(row.commands.begin(), row.commands.end(), 
            [&](const auto& value) {
                return value.mesh.lock() == meshToUpdate;
            });
    });
```

During `RenderEngine::Draw()`, each `command.entities` is synchronized via its `EncodeSync()` method ([src/RenderEngine_Draw.cpp:131-146]()):

```cpp
for(auto& [mat, command] : wrd.staticMeshRenderData) {
    for(auto& draw : command.commands) {
        draw.entities.EncodeSync(device, transformSyncCommandBuffer, 
                                  gcbuffer, transformSyncCommandBufferNeedsCommit);
    }
}
```

**Sources:** [include/RavEngine/World.hpp:334-362](), [src/World.cpp:330-390](), [src/RenderEngine_Draw.cpp:131-146]()

---

## Render Layer and Per-Object Attribute Synchronization

### Render Layer System

```mermaid
graph LR
    subgraph EntityCreation["Entity Creation"]
        CreateEntity["CreateEntity()"]
    end
    
    subgraph Setup["SetupPerEntityRenderData"]
        AllocRL["renderLayers.Resize(entityID+1)"]
        AllocPO["perObjectAttributes.Resize(entityID+1)"]
        InitRL["renderLayers[entityID] = ALL_LAYERS"]
        InitPO["perObjectAttributes[entityID] = ALL_ATTRIBUTES"]
    end
    
    subgraph API["Public API"]
        SetLayer["SetEntityRenderlayer(entityID, layers)"]
        SetAttrib["SetEntityAttributes(entityID, attributes)"]
    end
    
    subgraph Sync["Synchronization"]
        EncodeRL["renderLayers.EncodeSync()"]
        EncodePO["perObjectAttributes.EncodeSync()"]
    end
    
    subgraph GPUCull["GPU Culling Shader"]
        ReadRL["renderLayerBuffer[entityID]"]
        ReadPO["perObjectFlags[entityID]"]
        CheckLayer["cameraRenderLayers & entityLayerMask"]
        CheckAttribs["Check frustum/occlusion/shadow flags"]
    end
    
    CreateEntity --> AllocRL
    AllocRL --> AllocPO
    AllocPO --> InitRL
    InitRL --> InitPO
    
    InitPO --> SetLayer
    InitPO --> SetAttrib
    
    SetLayer --> EncodeRL
    SetAttrib --> EncodePO
    
    EncodeRL --> ReadRL
    EncodePO --> ReadPO
    
    ReadRL --> CheckLayer
    ReadPO --> CheckAttribs
    
    style AllocRL fill:#fff5e1
    style EncodeRL fill:#e1f5ff
    style CheckLayer fill:#ffe1e1
```

**Render Layers and Attributes**

Each entity has associated metadata stored in `BufferedVRAMVector` structures indexed by entity ID ([include/RavEngine/World.hpp:434-436]()):

- **Render Layers** (`renderlayer_t`): 32-bit bitmask determining which cameras can see this entity
- **Per-Object Attributes** (`perobject_t`): 16-bit flags controlling culling behavior:
  - Bit 0: Frustum culling enabled (if 0, skip frustum test)
  - Bit 1: Occlusion culling enabled (if 0, skip occlusion test)
  - Bit 2: Casts shadows (if 1, render in shadow passes)

These are initialized in `SetupPerEntityRenderData()` ([src/World.cpp:531-541]()) when an entity is created:

```cpp
renderLayers.SetValueAt(localID.id, ALL_LAYERS);       // Visible to all cameras by default
perObjectAttributes.SetValueAt(localID.id, ALL_ATTRIBUTES); // All culling enabled by default
```

The GPU culling shader ([shaders/defaultcull.csh:174-193]()) reads these values:

```glsl
const uint entityLayerMask = renderLayerBuffer[entityID];
if ((cameraRenderLayers & entityLayerMask) == 0) {
    return;  // Not visible to this camera
}

uint16_t attributeBitmask = perObjectFlags[entityID];
const bool skipFrustumCulling = !bool(attributeBitmask & 1);
const bool skipOcclusionCulling = !bool(attributeBitmask & (1 << 1));
const bool castsShadows = bool(attributeBitmask & (1 << 2));
```

Synchronization occurs during `RenderEngine::Draw()` ([src/RenderEngine_Draw.cpp:128-129]()):

```cpp
wrd.renderLayers.EncodeSync(device, transformSyncCommandBuffer, gcbuffer, transformSyncCommandBufferNeedsCommit);
wrd.perObjectAttributes.EncodeSync(device, transformSyncCommandBuffer, gcbuffer, transformSyncCommandBufferNeedsCommit);
```

**Sources:** [src/World.cpp:531-550](), [include/RavEngine/World.hpp:434-436](), [shaders/defaultcull.csh:174-193](), [src/RenderEngine_Draw.cpp:128-129]()

## Task Graph Integration

### Render Task Graph Structure

```mermaid
graph TB
    subgraph MasterTasks["World::masterTasks"]
        ECSMod["ECS Task Module"]
        RenderMod["Render Task Module"]
    end
    
    subgraph RenderTasks["renderTasks (Taskflow)"]
        ResizeBuf["resizeBuffer<br/>Ensure worldTransforms capacity"]
        
        UpdateDirs["updateInvalidatedDirs<br/>Directional lights"]
        UpdateSpots["updateInvalidatedSpots<br/>Spot lights"]
        UpdatePoints["updateInvalidatedPoints<br/>Point lights"]
        UpdateAmb["updateInvalidatedAmbients<br/>Ambient lights"]
        
        UpdateStatic["updateRenderDataStaticMesh<br/>Static mesh transforms"]
        UpdateSkinned["updateRenderDataSkinnedMesh<br/>Skinned mesh transforms"]
        UpdateParticles["updateParticleSystems<br/>Particle emitter transforms"]
    end
    
    subgraph Execution["Execution Order"]
        TickECS["World::TickECS()"]
        ExecuteRender["executor.run(renderTasks).wait()"]
        DrawStart["RenderEngine::Draw()"]
    end
    
    ECSMod --> RenderMod
    RenderMod --> ResizeBuf
    
    ResizeBuf --> UpdateDirs
    ResizeBuf --> UpdateSpots
    ResizeBuf --> UpdatePoints
    ResizeBuf --> UpdateAmb
    ResizeBuf --> UpdateStatic
    ResizeBuf --> UpdateSkinned
    ResizeBuf --> UpdateParticles
    
    UpdateDirs --> UpdateStatic
    UpdateDirs --> UpdateSkinned
    UpdateSpots --> UpdateStatic
    UpdateSpots --> UpdateSkinned
    UpdatePoints --> UpdateStatic
    UpdatePoints --> UpdateSkinned
    
    TickECS --> ExecuteRender
    ExecuteRender --> DrawStart
    
    style ResizeBuf fill:#fff5e1
    style UpdateDirs fill:#ffe1e1
    style UpdateStatic fill:#e1f5ff
    style ExecuteRender fill:#f5e1ff
```

**Task Graph Execution**

The render synchronization tasks ([src/World.cpp:310-521]()) form a Taskflow directed acyclic graph (DAG) executed during `World::Tick()`:

1. **Setup Phase**: `resizeBuffer` task ensures all `BufferedVRAMVector` structures have sufficient capacity ([src/World.cpp:316-328]())

2. **Light Update Phase**: Light update tasks run in parallel, but all must complete before mesh updates because mesh tasks clear the `Transform.isTickDirty` flag ([src/World.cpp:392-520]())

3. **Mesh Update Phase**: Static mesh, skinned mesh, and particle emitter updates run in parallel after light updates complete ([src/World.cpp:354-390]())

4. **Execution**: During `World::Tick()`, after ECS systems complete, the engine executes:
   ```cpp
   executor.run(renderTasks).wait();  // Blocks until all render tasks complete
   ```

5. **Draw Phase**: Once render tasks finish, `RenderEngine::Draw()` begins and calls `EncodeSync()` on all buffered structures

The task graph ensures:
- Parallel execution where possible (light updates, mesh updates within their phase)
- Correct dependency ordering (lights before meshes, resize before all updates)
- Completion before rendering begins

**Sources:** [src/World.cpp:310-521](), [src/World.cpp:54-74]()

---

## Garbage Collection and Resource Management

### Buffer Garbage Collection

```mermaid
flowchart TD
    Start["EncodeSync creates new buffer"] --> OldBuffer{"Old private buffer exists?"}
    
    OldBuffer -->|Yes| Enqueue["gcCallback(oldBuffer)<br/>Enqueue to gcBuffers"]
    OldBuffer -->|No| UseNew["Use new buffer immediately"]
    
    Enqueue --> InUse["Old buffer may still be<br/>in use by GPU"]
    UseNew --> Return["Return from EncodeSync"]
    
    InUse --> NextFrame["Next frame Draw() begins"]
    NextFrame --> Destroy["DestroyUnusedResources()"]
    
    Destroy --> TryDequeue["gcBuffers.try_dequeue(buffer)"]
    TryDequeue --> CheckFence{"GPU finished with buffer?"}
    
    CheckFence -->|No| ReEnqueue["Enqueue back to gcBuffers<br/>Try again next frame"]
    CheckFence -->|Yes| Release["Buffer destructor called<br/>GPU memory freed"]
    
    ReEnqueue --> NextFrame
    Release --> Return
    
    style Enqueue fill:#ffe1e1
    style Destroy fill:#e1f5ff
    style Release fill:#e1ffe1
```

**Deferred Buffer Destruction**

When `EncodeSync()` creates a new private buffer (due to resize), the old buffer cannot be immediately destroyed because it may still be referenced by in-flight GPU commands. The garbage collection system ([src/RenderEngine.cpp:1352-1385]()) solves this:

1. **Enqueue**: `EncodeSync()` calls the `gcCallback` lambda ([src/RenderEngine_Draw.cpp:116-118]()):
   ```cpp
   auto gcbuffer = [this](RGLBufferPtr oldPrivateBuffer) {
       gcBuffers.enqueue(oldPrivateBuffer);
   };
   ```

2. **Defer**: Old buffers remain in the `gcBuffers` concurrent queue until the GPU finishes using them

3. **Destroy**: At the start of each `RenderEngine::Draw()`, `DestroyUnusedResources()` attempts to dequeue and destroy buffers:
   ```cpp
   RGLBufferPtr buffer;
   while (gcBuffers.try_dequeue(buffer)) {
       // Buffer shared_ptr goes out of scope, destructor called
   }
   ```

4. **Fence**: RGL internally tracks command buffer completion, so buffer destructors only execute after GPU commands complete

This lock-free queue approach avoids stalling the CPU while ensuring GPU resources are not freed prematurely.

**Sources:** [src/RenderEngine_Draw.cpp:104](), [src/RenderEngine_Draw.cpp:116-118](), [include/RavEngine/RenderEngine.hpp:311-314]()

---

## Summary

The render data synchronization system bridges RavEngine's flexible ECS architecture with GPU-optimal data layouts through:

- **Buffered containers** (`BufferedVRAMVector`, `BufferedVRAMSparseSet`) that maintain host-side, staging, and private GPU copies
- **Dirty tracking** at the component level (transforms, lights) to minimize unnecessary transfers
- **Task-based updates** that run in parallel during `World::Tick()` to prepare render data
- **Asynchronous GPU copies** via command buffers that overlap with rendering
- **Material-grouped MDI structures** that organize mesh rendering for batch efficiency
- **Deferred garbage collection** to safely destroy GPU resources after in-flight commands complete

This architecture allows simulation and rendering to proceed independently while maintaining a consistent, high-performance snapshot of world state for GPU consumption.

**Sources:** [src/World.cpp:310-521](), [src/RenderEngine_Draw.cpp:98-304](), [include/RavEngine/World.hpp:418-449]()3c:T5f53,# Cross-Platform Build System

## Purpose and Scope

This document describes RavEngine's CMake-based cross-platform build system, which supports native and cross-compilation for multiple target platforms including Windows (Win32/UWP), macOS, iOS, tvOS, visionOS, Linux, Android, and Emscripten. The build system handles platform detection, host tool compilation for cross-compilation scenarios, asset processing, shader compilation, and dependency management.

For information about the runtime asset loading system, see [Asset Pipeline](#2.2). For details on shader compilation specifics, see [Materials and Shaders](#4.2). For graphics API abstraction, see [RGL Graphics Abstraction Layer](#9.1).

## Cross-Compilation Architecture

RavEngine's build system distinguishes between the **host platform** (where compilation occurs) and the **target platform** (where the application runs). When these differ, the build system uses a two-stage process:

```mermaid
graph TD
    DetectCrossComp["Cross-Compilation Detection<br/>[CMakeLists.txt:80-99]"]
    
    DetectCrossComp --> IsNative{Native Build?}
    DetectCrossComp --> IsCross{Cross-Compile?}
    
    IsNative -->|Yes| BuildToolsInline["Build host tools inline<br/>protoc, rglc, flatc, rvesc, etc.<br/>[CMakeLists.txt:178-181]"]
    
    IsCross -->|Yes| ConfigureHostTools["Configure host tools project<br/>deps/host-tools/<br/>[CMakeLists.txt:142-149]"]
    
    ConfigureHostTools --> BuildHostTools["Build host tools<br/>Native executables<br/>[CMakeLists.txt:163-169]"]
    
    BuildHostTools --> SetToolPaths["Set tool paths<br/>PROTOC_CMD, rglc_path,<br/>RVESC_PATH, etc.<br/>[CMakeLists.txt:107-126]"]
    
    BuildToolsInline --> CompileAssets["Asset Compilation Phase"]
    SetToolPaths --> CompileAssets
    
    CompileAssets --> CompileShaders["Shader Compilation<br/>Target platform bytecode"]
    CompileAssets --> CompileMeshes["Mesh Import<br/>.rvem format"]
    CompileAssets --> CompileAnims["Animation/Skeleton Import<br/>.rvea/.rves format"]
    
    CompileShaders --> PackResources["pack_resources()<br/>Create .rvedata archive"]
    CompileMeshes --> PackResources
    CompileAnims --> PackResources
    
    PackResources --> CompileTarget["Compile Target Executable<br/>Link with processed assets"]
```

The `RVE_CROSSCOMP` variable tracks whether cross-compilation is active, determined by `CMAKE_CROSSCOMPILING` or Visual Studio's platform selection:

[CMakeLists.txt:80-99]()

**Sources:** [CMakeLists.txt:80-99](), [CMakeLists.txt:102-181](), [deps/host-tools/CMakeLists.txt:1-76]()

### Host Tools Directory Structure

When cross-compiling, host tools are built in a separate directory hierarchy:

| Tool | Purpose | Output Path (Ninja/Make) | Output Path (VS) |
|------|---------|---------------------------|------------------|
| `protoc` | Protocol buffer compiler | `host-tools/protobuf/protoc` | `host-tools/protobuf/Release/protoc.exe` |
| `rglc` | RGL shader compiler | `host-tools/RGL/rglc` | `host-tools/RGL/Release/rglc.exe` |
| `flatc` | FlatBuffers compiler | `host-tools/flatc/flatc` | `host-tools/flatc/Release/flatc.exe` |
| `rvesc` | RavEngine shader compiler | `host-tools/RVESC/rvesc` | `host-tools/RVESC/Release/rvesc.exe` |
| `rvemc` | Mesh compiler | `host-tools/rvemc/rvemc` | `host-tools/rvemc/Release/rvemc.exe` |
| `rveac` | Animation compiler | `host-tools/rveac/rveac` | `host-tools/rveac/Release/rveac.exe` |
| `rveskc` | Skeleton compiler | `host-tools/rveskc/rveskc` | `host-tools/rveskc/Release/rveskc.exe` |

[CMakeLists.txt:107-126]()

**Sources:** [CMakeLists.txt:102-157](), [deps/host-tools/CMakeLists.txt:1-76]()

### Host Compiler Selection

When cross-compiling from Linux or macOS to Emscripten/Android, the build system ensures host tools use native compilers rather than cross-compilers:

[CMakeLists.txt:128-132]()

The `LINUX_HOST_CC` and `LINUX_HOST_CXX` variables force the use of system `cc`/`c++` for host tools while the main project uses the NDK or Emscripten toolchain.

**Sources:** [CMakeLists.txt:128-143]()

## Host Tools

RavEngine includes several host tools that process assets at build time. These tools are built natively on the host platform, even when cross-compiling:

```mermaid

        RVEMC["rvemc<br/>Mesh Compiler<br/>OBJ/FBX â†’ .rvem<br/>[tools/rvemc/]"]
        RVESKC["rveskc<br/>Skeleton Compiler<br/>FBX â†’ .rves<br/>[tools/rveskc/]"]
        RVEAC["rveac<br/>Animation Compiler<br/>FBX â†’ .rvea<br/>[tools/rveac/]"]
        RVESC["rvesc<br/>Shader Compiler<br/>GLSL â†’ Platform bytecode<br/>[tools/rvesc/]"]
        
        RVEMC --> ImportLib
        RVESKC --> ImportLib
        RVEAC --> ImportLib
        
        RVEMC --> Assimp["Assimp<br/>3D model importer"]
        RVESKC --> Assimp
        RVEAC --> Assimp
        
        RVEMC --> MeshOpt["meshoptimizer<br/>Mesh optimization"]
        
        RVESC --> RGLC["librglc<br/>RGL shader compiler"]

        ImportLib --> FMT["fmt<br/>String formatting"]

    end

```

**Sources:** [cmake/importers.cmake:1-37](), [cmake/rvesc.cmake:1-17](), [deps/host-tools/CMakeLists.txt:1-76]()

### rve_importlib

The `rve_importlib` library provides shared functionality for asset importers:

[cmake/importers.cmake:1-9]()

This library uses **Assimp** for loading 3D model formats and provides common mesh processing utilities. It targets C++20 and links against Assimp, fmt, glm, and zlib.

**Sources:** [cmake/importers.cmake:1-9](), [deps/host-tools/CMakeLists.txt:52-72]()

### Mesh Compiler (rvemc)

The `rvemc` tool converts source mesh files (OBJ, FBX, etc.) into optimized `.rvem` format:

[cmake/importers.cmake:29-30]()

It reads configuration files (`.json`) that specify input mesh files and options, then produces optimized binary mesh data with vertex/index buffers. The tool uses **meshoptimizer** for vertex cache optimization, overdraw reduction, and vertex encoding.

**Integration with build system:**

[cmake/pack_resources.cmake:122-144]()

**Sources:** [cmake/importers.cmake:29-30](), [cmake/pack_resources.cmake:122-144]()

### Skeleton Compiler (rveskc)

The `rveskc` tool extracts skeletal hierarchies from 3D model files and converts them to Ozz-animation's `.rves` format:

[cmake/importers.cmake:32-33]()

[cmake/pack_resources.cmake:146-162]()

**Sources:** [cmake/importers.cmake:32-33](), [cmake/pack_resources.cmake:146-162]()

### Animation Compiler (rveac)

The `rveac` tool imports animation data and compiles it to compressed `.rvea` format using Ozz-animation:

[cmake/importers.cmake:35-36]()

[cmake/pack_resources.cmake:164-180]()

**Sources:** [cmake/importers.cmake:35-36](), [cmake/pack_resources.cmake:164-180]()

### Shader Compiler (rvesc)

The `rvesc` tool compiles GLSL shaders to platform-specific bytecode (SPIR-V, DXIL, Metal IR):

[cmake/rvesc.cmake:9-15]()

RVESC embeds common shader includes using **CMRC** (CMake Resource Compiler) and depends on `librglc` from the RGL library for cross-API shader compilation. See [Materials and Shaders](#4.2) for runtime shader usage.

**Sources:** [cmake/rvesc.cmake:1-17](), [deps/host-tools/CMakeLists.txt:33-49]()

### Protocol Buffer Compiler (protoc)

Used by GameNetworkingSockets for network message serialization. The build system configures protobuf to skip building `protoc` when cross-compiling:

[CMakeLists.txt:401-405]()

Custom `protobuf_generate` function in GameNetworkingSockets uses the cross-compilation-aware `PROTOC_CMD` variable:

[deps/GameNetworkingSockets/CMakeLists.txt:166-173]()

**Sources:** [CMakeLists.txt:401-426](), [deps/GameNetworkingSockets/CMakeLists.txt:42-184]()

### FlatBuffers Compiler (flatc)

Used by Steam Audio for spatial audio data structures. Built as part of host tools when cross-compiling:

[deps/host-tools/CMakeLists.txt:28-31]()

**Sources:** [deps/host-tools/CMakeLists.txt:28-31]()

### RGL Compiler (rglc)

The RGL shader compiler is part of the RGL graphics library. When cross-compiling, it's built in the host tools directory:

[deps/host-tools/CMakeLists.txt:11-19]()

The `RGL_SKIP_BACKEND_CHECK` option allows building `rglc` without graphics SDK dependencies since it only needs the compiler, not the runtime.

**Sources:** [deps/host-tools/CMakeLists.txt:11-19](), [CMakeLists.txt:355-366]()

## Platform Detection and Configuration

RavEngine detects the target platform and configures platform-specific settings accordingly:

```mermaid
graph TD
    DetectPlatform["Platform Detection<br/>[CMakeLists.txt:36-93]"]
    
    DetectPlatform --> IsApple{APPLE?}
    DetectPlatform --> IsWindows{WIN32?}
    DetectPlatform --> IsLinux{LINUX?}
    DetectPlatform --> IsAndroid{ANDROID?}
    DetectPlatform --> IsEmscripten{EMSCRIPTEN?}
    
    IsApple -->|Yes| CheckApplePlatform{CMAKE_SYSTEM_NAME}
    CheckApplePlatform --> MacOS["macOS<br/>Metal backend<br/>x86_64 + arm64"]
    CheckApplePlatform --> iOS["iOS<br/>Metal backend<br/>aarch64"]
    CheckApplePlatform --> tvOS["tvOS<br/>Metal backend<br/>aarch64"]
    CheckApplePlatform --> visionOS["visionOS<br/>Metal backend<br/>aarch64"]
    
    IsWindows -->|Yes| CheckWindowsMode{Mode}
    CheckWindowsMode --> Win32["Win32<br/>DX12 + Vulkan<br/>x64 + ARM64"]
    CheckWindowsMode --> UWP["UWP/GDK<br/>DX12 + Vulkan<br/>x64"]
    
    IsLinux -->|Yes| LinuxPlatform["Linux<br/>Vulkan backend<br/>x86_64 + aarch64"]
    
    IsAndroid -->|Yes| AndroidPlatform["Android<br/>Vulkan backend<br/>armeabi-v7a, arm64-v8a<br/>x86, x86_64"]
    
    IsEmscripten -->|Yes| WebPlatform["Emscripten<br/>WebGPU backend<br/>wasm"]
    
    MacOS --> SetDefines["Platform Defines<br/>Compiler Flags<br/>Link Libraries"]

    tvOS --> SetDefines
    visionOS --> SetDefines
    Win32 --> SetDefines
    UWP --> SetDefines
    LinuxPlatform --> SetDefines

    WebPlatform --> SetDefines
```

## Build Configuration Options

RavEngine exposes several CMake options to customize builds:

| Option | Type | Default | Description |
|--------|------|---------|-------------|
| `RAVENGINE_BUILD_TESTS` | OPTION | OFF | Build unit tests and test applications |
| `RAVENGINE_SERVER` | OPTION | Tests value | Build as headless server (no graphics/audio) |
| `RAVENGINE_ASSETS_DIR` | STRING | `${CMAKE_BINARY_DIR}` | Directory for output `.rvedata` archives |
| `RAVENGINE_MSVC_FAST_DEBUG_ITERATORS` | OPTION | ON | Disable iterator debugging in MSVC Debug builds |
| `RAVENGINE_PROFILE_ALL_BUILDS` | OPTION | OFF | Enable Tracy profiling in all configurations |
| `RAVENGINE_MSVC_DEBUG_ALL_BUILDS` | OPTION | OFF | Enable debug symbols in all MSVC configurations |

[CMakeLists.txt:17-21]()

[CMakeLists.txt:23-31]()

**Sources:** [CMakeLists.txt:17-31](), [CMakeLists.txt:891-896]()

## Generator Support

RavEngine supports multiple CMake generators per platform:

| Platform | Generators | Notes |
|----------|-----------|-------|
| macOS, iOS, tvOS, visionOS | Xcode | Primary generator for Apple platforms |
| Windows | Visual Studio 2022, Ninja | VS for IDE integration, Ninja for CI/CD |
| Linux | Ninja, Unix Makefiles | Ninja recommended for faster builds |
| Android | Ninja, Unix Makefiles, Android Studio | Ninja for command-line, AS for IDE |
| Emscripten | Ninja, Unix Makefiles | Requires `emcmake` wrapper |

The build system detects the generator and adjusts tool paths:
